# ChravelApp 30-Persona Synthetic User Testing — Full Persona Reports (2026-06-11)

> ⚠️ **Synthetic research.** Every persona, answer, score, and quote below is simulated. Evidence labels: [OBSERVED] = grounded in UI/code/docs; [SIMULATED RISK] = plausible reaction inferred from observed behavior; [HYPOTHESIS] = needs real users. See README.md and evidence-delta.md.

## Persona 1: Denise Walker — Consumer / Youth Soccer Team Mom (Weekend Tournament Coordinator)

### A. Profile
- **Name:** Denise Walker
- **Age range:** 38–45
- **Location/timezone:** Columbus, OH (America/New_York)
- **Industry/role:** Part-time dental office manager; volunteer "team mom" for U12 girls soccer
- **Tech comfort:** Medium — fluent in iMessage, TeamSnap, GroupMe; wary of new apps that ask for too much
- **Platform:** iOS (iPhone 13), occasionally the family iPad
- **Group size:** 14 families (~30 people counting siblings) for a weekend tournament in Cincinnati
- **Planning style:** Spreadsheet-brain in a group-chat world; sends the same reminder three times
- **Current tools:** TeamSnap (roster/schedule), GroupMe (parents chat), iMessage (side chats), shared iCloud album (photos)
- **Main pain points:** Schedule changes buried in GroupMe; "who's bringing snacks/canopy" never assigned; parents who never answer; keeping kids' names/faces off public links
- **Budget sensitivity:** High — she already resents TeamSnap's upsell banners; anything she pays for comes out of her own pocket, not team dues
- **Why adopt Chravel:** One place where the Saturday schedule, the snack list, and the hotel info live together instead of across four apps
- **Why reject Chravel:** If it's a fifth app the other 13 families won't install; if photos of kids feel less private than the iCloud album she controls; if anything costs money

### B. Jobs-to-Be-Done
1. When the tournament bracket drops on Thursday night, I want to get game times in front of all 14 families at once, so I can stop answering "what time Saturday?" twelve separate times.
2. When game times change mid-tournament, I want everyone to see the updated time in one authoritative place, so nobody shows up to an empty field.
3. When we need canopy/snacks/cooler/first-aid covered, I want to assign tasks to specific parents with due dates, so the same three moms don't carry everything.
4. When I share a link with the team, I want to control exactly who can join and see the kids' info, so a forwarded link doesn't expose my roster to strangers.
5. When the weekend is over, I want to settle the shared hotel-block snack run without chasing Venmo requests, so I'm not the team's collections agent.
6. When a parent never responds, I want to see who has and hasn't seen the plan, so I can call exactly the right person.

### C. Screener Answers
| Question | Answer |
|---|---|
| Group trips last 12 months | 4+ (tournament weekends count, right?) |
| Typical group size | 16+ |
| Main tools | TeamSnap, GroupMe, iMessage, shared iCloud album |
| Primary device | iOS |
| 45-min call? | Maybe — Sunday evening only |
| Role in group | Primary planner |
| Pro-ops responsibility | Yes, I own logistics (nobody pays me for it though) |

### D. Full Survey Answers

**About you.** I'm Denise, two kids, the older one plays travel soccer. Somewhere along the way I became "team mom," which means I run the parents' GroupMe, the snack signup, and the hotel block email thread. I didn't ask for the job, it just happened to me.

**Most recent group trip.** Memorial Day tournament in Cincinnati. What kicked it off: the club posted the bracket and suddenly 14 families needed the same hotel near the fields. Who was involved: every family, the coach (who answers nothing), and me. Most frustrating: Saturday's 9 AM game got moved to 7:45 AM Friday night and I had to post it in GroupMe, text the four parents who mute GroupMe, AND email two grandparents. Three channels for one fact. What went well: the iCloud album — everyone dumps photos in and it just works, I'll be honest. Apps used: TeamSnap (official schedule), GroupMe (chat), iMessage (the moms' side chat where decisions actually happen), iCloud album, and Marriott's app. So five. What happened after the first plan: the bracket changed twice and I basically re-sent everything each time.

**Planning workflow.** Idea → the club tells us. Booked → I negotiate a hotel block over email and post the code. During → I live on my phone refreshing the tournament app and relaying. Post → I total up the team snack/water/ice receipts and ask for $12 a family, and four families take three weeks to pay. Where decisions stick: the moms' iMessage chat — 8 of 14 families are in it, which is the problem. Non-responders: two dads I have to text individually, every time. Example thread: 75 GroupMe messages about whether to do a team dinner; resolution: no decision, families did their own thing.

**Feature areas.**
- *Create/Invite:* I'd make "Cincy Memorial Day Tournament" and send one link. The approval toggle matters a lot to me — I saw it has "Require approval to join" and a 7-day expiry, that's exactly what I'd want before kids' names go in anything.
- *Places:* Hotel + the two field complexes pinned would honestly stop half the Saturday-morning texts.
- *Calendar/Itinerary:* This is the whole job. Game times, warm-up times, team dinner. The day view with times and locations looked like exactly what I retype into GroupMe every Friday.
- *Polls/Decisions:* Team dinner yes/no with a deadline would have saved 75 messages.
- *Tasks:* Snack/canopy/cooler assignments with names attached. Yes. This is the feature I'd switch for.
- *Smart Import:* I'd paste the tournament schedule email and the hotel confirmation. If it actually puts games on the calendar, that's Friday night back.
- *AI Concierge:* I guess I'd ask "restaurants near the fields that take a party of 30 with kids"? Honestly I'd probably just Google it. I don't need a chatbot, I need the schedule to be right.
- *AI Trust:* The first time it tells me a wrong game time or invents a restaurant, I'm done forever. With kids' logistics there is no "close enough."
- *Settings priorities:* Who can see the member list, who can join, turning OFF notifications I don't need. I don't want 14 families getting pinged every time someone uploads a photo.

**Money.** Collecting: Venmo requests for $12/family, and I eat the cost when someone's "Venmo is acting up." Reimbursement talk is awkward — I'm asking other moms for money for snacks I already bought. Plan changes get communicated three ways (see above). Is there always one planner: yes, me, and one mom who helps. Hotels: the club suggests, I pick the block, families book on their own. Restaurants: chaos, usually no group decision. Conversations live in GroupMe officially and iMessage actually.

**Willingness to pay.** **Free only.** I'm a volunteer. I already think TeamSnap squeezes the club. If Chravel's free tier covers a calendar, tasks, and chat for one tournament at a time, that's me. If a tournament weekend hits a paywall mid-weekend I will be loudly annoyed in the parking lot.

**Ratings (1–5).**
- Likelihood to use for next trip: **3** — depends entirely on whether other parents will tap one link
- Clarity of what the app does: **4** — "group chat travel app" plus the trip cards made sense immediately
- Time saved (expected): **4** — calendar + tasks replaces my Friday-night retype ritual
- AI trust: **2** — I didn't see it be wrong, I just don't lean on chatbots for kids' schedules
- Would invite others: **4** — inviting is the whole point or it's useless to me
- Mobile usability: **3** — fine, but tabs scroll sideways and Tasks is at the far end where I'd never find it
- Web usability: **4** — the calendar page on desktop was genuinely clear
- Pricing fit: **3** — free tier looks survivable for me; I'll never pay so the rest is moot
- NPS-style sentiment: **3** — would say "worth a try" to another team mom, not "you have to get this"

**Wrap-up.** Change one thing: let people see the weekend schedule from the link without creating an account — half my parents will not make another login. What makes me recommend: if one tournament goes by with zero "what time is the game?" texts. Anything else: please don't ever show kids' photos on a public preview page. Follow-up call: Maybe.

### E. Web Flow Walkthrough
- **Discovery/landing:** The hero is an actual product dashboard with six sample trips, and the subtitle literally lists "Team Travel" and "Local Community Clubs" — I felt named. [OBSERVED — `desktop-01`] The trip cards showing People/Days/Places counts read clearly even to a non-techie. [OBSERVED — `desktop-01`]
- **Pricing impression:** "Start free. Upgrade when your trip gets serious." / "Free works forever—upgrade only when you need more" is the only pricing framing that works on a volunteer. [OBSERVED — `desktop-22`] The "Why Upgrade?" bullets are traveler-flavored (lose receipts, $1,000 trips) — none of them speak to a team mom, which is fine because she won't upgrade. [OBSERVED — `desktop-22`]
- **Signup:** Clean sign-in/sign-up card, Google and Apple buttons; she'd use Apple. [OBSERVED — `desktop-04`] Whether 13 other families complete signup is the real funnel risk — invitees get a trip preview but must fully join because guests have zero resource access. [OBSERVED — `src/types/permissionMatrix.generated.ts:44-50`] [SIMULATED RISK — for a 14-family group, every non-signup is a hole in the plan's reach]
- **Trip creation:** Required fields (title, dates, timezone) map fine to a tournament weekend. [OBSERVED — ground truth §4] Free tier allows 3 active trips; a fall season with 4 overlapping tournament weekends would force archiving or a paywall. [OBSERVED — `src/billing/entitlements.ts:245-252`] [SIMULATED RISK — she'd perceive this as "the app stopped working in October"]
- **Feature usage:** The demo calendar — month grid plus "Events for Thursday, Jun 11" with times, locations, and edit/delete — is precisely her game-day artifact. [OBSERVED — `desktop2-02`] Tasks tab exists in the strip; assignment + due dates + filters are implemented. [OBSERVED — `desktop2-02` tab strip; ground truth §6]
- **Invite modal:** Require-approval toggle, 7-day expiry, max-uses limit, regenerate — this is her child-safety checklist in one modal. [OBSERVED — `desktop2-11`] But the default helper text "Anyone with the link can use it until it expires or is turned off" describes exactly the forwarded-link scenario she fears unless she flips toggles. [OBSERVED — `desktop2-11`] [SIMULATED RISK — safe defaults matter more than safe options for this persona]
- **Web positives:** Calendar clarity [OBSERVED — `desktop2-02`]; pending-join-request banner ("2 pending requests to review") visible right in the trip header gives her gatekeeper visibility. [OBSERVED — `desktop2-02`]
- **Web pain points:** Desktop trip surfaces logged a "Maximum update depth exceeded" loop ~10×/tab during the harvest — at minimum a perf/jank smell on the exact pages she'd live on. [OBSERVED — `desktop-harvest2-log.json` steps 3–13 (R2)] No kid/COPPA-specific privacy posture is articulated anywhere on the landing page. [HYPOTHESIS — whether this blocks team adoption needs real parent interviews]

### F. Mobile / PWA Flow Walkthrough
- **First impression:** Mobile landing leads with "Login or Signup" and "Less Chaos, More Coordination" — legible, uncluttered. [OBSERVED — `mobile-01`]
- **Navigation:** In-trip navigation is a horizontally scrolling tab strip (Chat, Calendar, Concierge, …) with no bottom nav bar on mobile web; Tasks — her #1 feature — is off-screen to the right on first load. [OBSERVED — `mobile2-01`, `mobile2-05`; evidence-delta "Notable non-defect observations"] [SIMULATED RISK — she may never discover Tasks unscaffolded]
- **Chat/input:** Chat bubbles with author names and timestamps, urgent red callouts (weather alert, lobby time) visually pop — that's her "9 AM sharp" message rendered better than GroupMe does it. [OBSERVED — `mobile2-01`] Subtabs Messages/Broadcasts/Pinned/Search exist; Pinned is where her hotel code would live. [OBSERVED — `mobile2-01`]
- **Forms/modals:** Payments form on mobile is one column, big targets, summary cards (You Owe / You're Owed / Net) up top. [OBSERVED — `mobile2-05`]
- **Invite link flow:** Link + copy + share verified in demo; real join completion is auth-gated and untestable here. [OBSERVED — `desktop2-11`] [HYPOTHESIS — completion rate for low-motivation parents]
- **Perceived speed:** Mobile demo pages fired continuous React duplicate-key warnings (~150/step, 5,940 total in pass 2) from `MobileGroupCalendar`'s weekday-letter keys, and the calendar stays mounted re-rendering while on other tabs — on her mid-cycle iPhone this is battery and jank risk on game day. [OBSERVED — `src/components/mobile/MobileGroupCalendar.tsx:525`; `mobile-harvest2-log.json` (R1)]
- **Thumb reach/tap targets:** Bottom-anchored "Add Payment Request" and chat input are thumb-friendly. [OBSERVED — `mobile2-05`, `mobile2-01`]
- **Mobile positives:** Payment status chips (Pending/Settled) are glanceable. [OBSERVED — `mobile2-05`]
- **Mobile pain points:** Tab strip overflow burying Tasks/Polls [OBSERVED — `mobile2-05` shows Payments/Places/Polls/T… truncated]; calendar render storm [OBSERVED — R1]; trip title truncates to "Spring Break Cancun 2…" leaving little context. [OBSERVED — `mobile2-01`]

### H. Emotional Reaction
- **Impressed by:** The calendar day view and the invite-approval controls — "someone here has met a forwarded link."
- **Confused by:** Why Tasks, the thing she'd come for, is the last tab she'd find on a phone.
- **Annoyed by:** The idea of convincing 13 families to create accounts; any cap that could trip mid-weekend.
- **Would abandon when:** The third parent says "I'm not downloading another app," or the first wrong/duplicated calendar entry appears.
- **Would invite others?** Yes — inviting IS the product for her; a solo team-mom Chravel is worthless.
- **[SYNTHETIC QUOTE]** "If one link gets all fourteen families the right game time on Saturday, I'll forgive a lot. But the day it tells a grandma the wrong field, we're back to GroupMe forever."

### I. Conversion Scores
- **Activation:** 7/10 — landing → demo → calendar is a straight line to her job-to-be-done
- **Invite likelihood:** 8/10 — she must invite to get any value at all
- **Day-7 retention:** 5/10 — depends on whether the other families joined; solo usage decays fast
- **Paid conversion:** 1/10 — volunteer, free-only, on principle
- **NPS-style:** +15 — cautious recommender to other team moms if one weekend goes well
- **Would they pay?** No.
- **What would they pay?** $0; might tolerate the club paying a team plan she never sees
- **Feature creating willingness to pay:** None personally; Tasks+Calendar create advocacy, not revenue
- **Limit/CTA that triggers upgrade:** 3-active-trips cap in a 4-tournament month — but it triggers churn, not upgrade
- **CTA that would annoy her:** Any AI-upsell mid-weekend ("Unlimited AI assistance") — she didn't come for AI

### J. Top 5 Fixes for This Persona
1. Fix the mobile calendar duplicate-key render storm and keep inactive tab components unmounted, because Denise lives on the Calendar tab on a mid-tier iPhone during tournaments and continuous re-renders cause jank/battery drain at her highest-stakes moment. (`src/components/mobile/MobileGroupCalendar.tsx:525`, `MobileTripTabs`)
2. Add a read-only itinerary preview for invitees pre-signup, because consumer_guest has zero resource access and Denise fails at "get 14 families seeing the schedule" when half won't create accounts, causing the whole plan to stay in GroupMe. (`src/types/permissionMatrix.generated.ts:44-50`, `src/pages/JoinTrip.tsx`)
3. Ship safe-by-default invite presets (approval ON, expiry ON for family/team trips), because Denise fails at "share without exposing kids' info" when defaults read "Anyone with the link can use it," causing privacy-driven rejection. (`InviteModal`, `desktop2-11`)
4. Make the mobile in-trip tab strip wrap or reorder per trip type, because Denise failed to even see Tasks/Polls without horizontal scrolling, causing her #1 feature to go undiscovered. (`mobile2-01`/`mobile2-05`; `src/pages/MobileTripDetail.tsx`)
5. Auto-exclude past-dated trips from the 3-active-trip free cap, because Denise's fall season hits the cap by October, causing a "the app stopped working" perception in a free-only segment where the cap converts nobody. (`src/billing/entitlements.ts:245-252`)

### K. Confidence
- **Level:** Medium
- **Directly observed:** Landing positioning, pricing copy, auth UI, demo calendar/payments/invite modal at both viewports, mobile tab-strip reality, R1/R2 defect logs, entitlement and permission code.
- **Needs real-user validation:** Whether parents complete signup from an invite link; whether Smart Import nails a real tournament email; whether iCloud-album loyalty actually blocks Media adoption; COPPA/privacy expectations.
- **Beta interview question:** "Walk me through the last time a game time changed after 8 PM — every app you opened and every person you individually texted."

## Persona 2: Marcus Tran — Consumer / AAU Volleyball Parent Coordinator (Multi-City Tournament Season)

### A. Profile
- **Name:** Marcus Tran
- **Age range:** 40–50
- **Location/timezone:** San Jose, CA (America/Los_Angeles)
- **Industry/role:** QA lead at a networking-hardware company; volunteer travel coordinator for a 16U AAU volleyball club
- **Tech comfort:** Medium — methodical, reads settings screens, files bug reports for fun; not an early adopter
- **Platform:** **Android** (Pixel 8) — this matters: he checks the Play Store before trusting any app
- **Group size:** 11 players' families (~25 adults) across a season: Reno, Anaheim, Las Vegas, Phoenix
- **Planning style:** Spreadsheet master copy + WhatsApp broadcast; treats every tournament like a release cycle
- **Current tools:** Google Sheets (hotel blocks, carpools), WhatsApp (two groups: announcements + chatter), SportsEngine (club schedule), Gmail
- **Main pain points:** Hotel-block deadlines nobody meets; carpool seats reshuffling at 6 AM; bracket/schedule changes mid-tournament reaching only half the parents; announcement messages drowned by 60 emoji replies
- **Budget sensitivity:** Medium — won't subscribe annually for a seasonal problem, but a per-season price is rational to him
- **Why adopt Chravel:** A broadcast channel parents can't bury, plus a schedule that updates once for everyone
- **Why reject Chravel:** Second-class Android experience (no Play Store app), any sloppiness around kids' data, or a subscription-only pricing model for a 4-month season

### B. Jobs-to-Be-Done
1. When the hotel block deadline is 10 days out, I want to broadcast it with visibility into who's seen it, so I stop losing block rates to procrastinators.
2. When pool play reseeds Saturday night, I want to update one schedule that every family is already watching, so Sunday morning isn't a text-relay race.
3. When carpools shuffle, I want seat assignments visible and editable in one place, so kids aren't standing in a parking lot at 6 AM.
4. When the season has four cities, I want one structure per tournament without paying year-round, so the cost matches the four months I actually coordinate.
5. When I share anything about a youth team, I want join-approval and link expiry by default, so a reposted link never exposes 16-year-olds' whereabouts.
6. When I'm evaluating an app on Android, I want it to feel native-grade installed from my browser, so I'm not the coordinator who recommended a janky webpage.

### C. Screener Answers
| Question | Answer |
|---|---|
| Group trips last 12 months | 4+ |
| Typical group size | 16+ |
| Main tools | Google Sheets, WhatsApp, SportsEngine, Gmail |
| Primary device | Android |
| 45-min call? | Yes — I have opinions and a spreadsheet to show you |
| Role in group | Primary planner |
| Pro-ops responsibility | Yes, I own logistics |

### D. Full Survey Answers

**About you.** Marcus, QA lead, two daughters, the older plays 16U club volleyball. I run travel for 11 families because I made one good spreadsheet in 2024 and was never released from duty.

**Most recent group trip.** Las Vegas Classic, three days, 11 families. Kicked off when the club posted the schedule six weeks out. Involved: me, an assistant-coach who forwards everything, and 22 parents with wildly different responsiveness. Most frustrating: the bracket reseeded Saturday 9 PM; I updated the sheet, posted in WhatsApp announcements, and still had two families at the wrong court Sunday because the message was 40 emojis deep by morning. What went well: my hotel-block tracker — color-coded, booked/not-booked — but I built that myself and it answers nothing on its own. Apps used: Sheets, WhatsApp ×2 groups, SportsEngine, Gmail, Google Maps pins. Six, effectively. After the first plan: three revisions, each one a full re-broadcast.

**Planning workflow.** Idea → club calendar drops in August. Booked → I negotiate the block, post the booking link with a deadline, then chase. During → I'm courtside refreshing AES/SportsEngine and relaying changes. Post → I reconcile gas-split money for carpools, which takes two weeks. Decisions stick in: WhatsApp announcements (in theory), my sheet (in practice). Non-responders: a known list of four; I text them directly, every single time. Example doc: my "LV Classic Master" sheet — tabs for hotel, carpools, schedule, food — 9 of 22 parents ever opened it.

**Feature areas.**
- *Create/Invite:* One trip per tournament, link with **require-approval ON** — I saw that toggle and the expiry and max-uses options; that's the right control surface for a youth team. I'd still want approval to be the default, not something I remember to flip four times a season.
- *Places:* Pin the convention center, the hotel, and a protein-heavy breakfast spot. Useful, not decisive.
- *Calendar/Itinerary:* Decisive. Court assignments change; one authoritative calendar with edit-in-place beats my sheet because parents are already in the app where the chat is.
- *Polls/Decisions:* Carpool departure 6:00 vs 6:30 — poll with a close time. Yes.
- *Tasks:* Snack rotation, scorekeeping duty, tent setup. I'd use it; I currently shame people via spreadsheet column.
- *Smart Import:* I'd paste the AES schedule email and the Marriott block confirmation. If it parses court times correctly I'd be impressed; if it duplicates rows on a retry I'd file a bug — I read that the import retry path isn't fully idempotent, and as a QA guy that's exactly where I'd poke.
- *AI Concierge:* "Cheapest 10-room block within 15 min of the venue under $150/night" — if it answers with real options and links, fine. I'd verify everything anyway.
- *AI Trust:* Made-up specifics kill it — a hallucinated hotel rate or wrong court time, once, and AI is decoration. Also: 11 families' data better not be training anything.
- *Settings priorities:* Notification control per trip, who-can-join, data/privacy posture for minors, and whether the PWA actually pushes notifications on Android.

**Pro/Events branch.** I looked at what Broadcasts means here — the consumer demo trip already shows a Broadcasts subtab in chat, and the Pro tier has role-targeted broadcasts with delivery tracking. Delivery tracking is the feature: I don't need to send, I need to know who hasn't seen. "Professional-grade" to me = audit trail of who saw what when. Control vs automation: control. Trust comes from the app showing its work.

**Money.** Collecting: gas splits and shared-cooler costs over Venmo/Zelle, reconciled in my sheet. Reimbursement discussion happens publicly in WhatsApp, which is awkward. Plan changes: announced 2–3 times across channels. One planner: yes, me. Hotels: I decide block, families book individually. Restaurants: the team eats where the poll I run in WhatsApp says. Conversations live: WhatsApp, with the sheet as constitution.

**Willingness to pay.** **Per-trip** — really per-season. A 90-day pass at $74.99 covering Frequent Chraveler features would map almost exactly onto a season leg, and I'd pitch the club to reimburse it. A $19.99/mo annual subscription for a 4-month problem is how you lose me; I cancel things, it's a hobby.

**Ratings (1–5).**
- Likelihood next trip: **3** — pilot one tournament, full season only if Android holds up
- Clarity: **4** — landing told me exactly what it is; "Team Travel" in the hero helped
- Time saved: **4** — calendar + broadcasts + tasks collapses three of my six tools
- AI trust: **3** — confirm-before-write design is correct; outputs unproven
- Would invite: **4** — useless solo; but I won't invite 22 parents until I've QA'd it myself
- Mobile usability: **3** — competent web app on my Pixel, but I can tell it's web, and the no-bottom-nav scrolling tab strip is un-Android
- Web usability: **4** — desktop demo was solid; that's where I'd do season setup
- Pricing fit: **3** — Trip Pass concept fits; the fact I had to find it under upgrade copy doesn't
- NPS sentiment: **3** — recommend with caveats, Android caveats first

**Wrap-up.** Change one thing: ship a real Android presence — or at minimum an "install this PWA" flow that doesn't make me explain what a PWA is to 22 parents. Recommend when: a mid-tournament schedule change reaches every family with zero side-texts. Anything else: your demo had broken images on some surfaces — looked like blocked image hosts; sweat the details, coordinators notice. Follow-up: Yes.

### H. Emotional Reaction
- **Impressed by:** Invite gatekeeping controls; the confirm-before-write AI design; calendar edit-in-place.
- **Confused by:** Where the Android app is — and why the feature built for announcement-heavy coordinators (tracked broadcasts) lives in a $49 Pro tier.
- **Annoyed by:** Broken demo images and 401 console noise during his evaluation — "if the demo isn't QA'd, what is?"
- **Would abandon when:** Android PWA push proves unreliable for a schedule change, or the render jank makes courtside use feel cheap.
- **Would invite others?** Yes, after a one-tournament solo pilot — he doesn't stake his coordinator reputation on unverified software.
- **[SYNTHETIC QUOTE]** "I don't need the app to be magic. I need it to tell me which four families haven't seen the 7:45 AM court change — and to not stutter on my phone while it does it."

### I. Conversion Scores
- **Activation:** 6/10 — strong landing fit, but the Android/PWA gap and account-required wall slow his pilot
- **Invite likelihood:** 7/10 — inevitable if the pilot passes; he invites 22 people at once or none
- **Day-7 retention:** 6/10 — between tournaments usage dips; during one it's daily
- **Paid conversion:** 6/10 — genuinely would buy a 90-day pass framed as a season pass
- **NPS-style:** +10 — recommender with an asterisk shaped like a robot (Android)
- **Would they pay?** Yes — once per season.
- **What would they pay?** $74.99/90 days, ideally club-reimbursed; never $199/yr
- **Feature creating willingness to pay:** Tracked broadcasts/read-visibility + unlimited splits for a season
- **Limit/CTA that triggers upgrade:** Hitting the 3-split cap mid-tournament with the Trip Pass offer present
- **CTA that would annoy him:** "Start free trial" of a monthly subscription when he's asked for a seasonal product

### J. Top 5 Fixes for This Persona
1. Add an explicit Android/PWA story (landing copy + in-browser install prompt flow), because Marcus failed at "trust the platform" the moment the Play Store came up empty, causing pre-use trust downgrade for every Android coordinator. (`public/manifest.json` exists; no `android/` dir; `src/components/landing/FullPageLanding.tsx`)
2. Bring read/delivery visibility ("seen by N") to consumer-trip broadcasts or chat announcements, because Marcus failed at "know who missed the court change" — his core JTBD — causing him to keep WhatsApp + manual chasing. (`src/features/chat/`; Pro-only delivery tracking per ground truth §6)
3. Fix the mobile duplicate-key render storm and stop mounting the calendar on other tabs, because courtside mobile use is his primary context and continuous re-renders degrade exactly that. (`src/components/mobile/MobileGroupCalendar.tsx:525`)
4. Default require-approval ON (or trip-type-based safe presets) for invite links, because Marcus must remember to flip it four times a season for a youth team, and one forgotten toggle is a privacy incident. (`InviteModal`, `desktop2-11`)
5. Reconcile the Pro-trial and Explorer-trip-limit drift between docs/marketing and `FEATURE_LIMITS`, because Marcus (a QA lead) will catch "1 free Pro trial" vs `free: 0` and "unlimited trips" vs `explorer: 10`, causing exactly the credibility damage that loses methodical evaluators. (`src/billing/entitlements.ts:245-260`)

### K. Confidence
- **Level:** Medium
- **Directly observed:** Landing/pricing copy, demo trip surfaces at both viewports, invite modal controls, chat Broadcasts subtab, entitlements code, absence of Android platform dir, R1/R4/R5 defect logs.
- **Needs real-user validation:** Android PWA push reliability, Smart Import accuracy on real AES/SportsEngine emails, whether parents adopt without a store-listed app, Trip Pass appeal framed as season pass.
- **Beta interview question:** "When the bracket reseeded at 9 PM, how did you confirm each family actually saw the change — and what would 'confirmed' need to look like in an app for you to stop double-texting?"

## Persona 3: Jessica Romano — Consumer / Bachelorette Maid of Honor (Nashville Weekend)

### A. Profile
- **Name:** Jessica Romano
- **Age range:** 27–32
- **Location/timezone:** Chicago, IL (America/Chicago)
- **Industry/role:** Senior marketing manager at a DTC beauty brand; maid of honor, self-appointed CEO of this bachelorette
- **Tech comfort:** High — lives in Notion, Canva, Partiful, TikTok; zero patience for slow software
- **Platform:** iOS (iPhone 15 Pro), everything mobile-first
- **Group size:** 9 girls, Nashville, 3 nights
- **Planning style:** Aesthetic-forward command-and-control; builds the vibe deck before the budget
- **Current tools:** iMessage group (chaos), Partiful (invites), Google Sheet (costs nobody opens), Venmo (requests, then re-requests), Canva (itinerary graphic), shared Apple album
- **Main pain points:** Chasing 8 Venmo payments across 3 deposits; the group can't pick a dinner spot in under 200 messages; one bridesmaid never answers anything; itinerary lives as a JPEG that's outdated by Friday
- **Budget sensitivity:** Low for this trip — it's the wedding, money flows; but a *recurring subscription* for a one-weekend job is dead on arrival
- **Why adopt Chravel:** One gorgeous link that holds the itinerary, the polls, the photo dump, and the money math — and makes her look organized
- **Why reject Chravel:** If it's slow, ugly on her phone, or makes the girls do homework to join; if the free tier embarrasses her mid-planning

### B. Jobs-to-Be-Done
1. When I'm collecting 3 rounds of deposits from 8 girls, I want every charge, split, and who-paid status in one ledger, so I stop being the Venmo bill collector at 11 PM.
2. When the group needs to pick Saturday dinner, I want a poll with a deadline that auto-closes, so a decision exists by Tuesday instead of a 200-message spiral.
3. When the itinerary changes, I want one live link instead of re-exporting a Canva JPEG, so nobody screenshots an outdated plan.
4. When the weekend happens, I want every photo and video in one place the bride can cry over later, so memories don't die in 9 camera rolls.
5. When I send the girls anything, I want it to look expensive, so the planning matches the brand of the weekend.
6. When I ask an AI for outfit themes or a private-dining spot for 9, I want answers that aren't the same listicle Google gives everyone, so it's actually worth asking.

### C. Screener Answers
| Question | Answer |
|---|---|
| Group trips last 12 months | 2–3 (bachelorette, girls' ski weekend, a wedding) |
| Typical group size | 9–15 |
| Main tools | iMessage, Partiful, Venmo, Google Sheets, Canva |
| Primary device | iOS |
| 45-min call? | Maybe — make it 20 and I'm in |
| Role in group | Primary planner |
| Pro-ops responsibility | Yes, I own logistics (the bride is on a need-to-know basis) |

### D. Full Survey Answers

**About you.** Jess, 29, marketing. I'm the friend who plans. MOH for my college roommate's wedding, which means I'm running a 9-person Nashville weekend with a spreadsheet nobody reads and a Venmo history that looks like money laundering.

**Most recent group trip.** This bachelorette, in progress. Kicked off when the bride picked Nashville and a date. Involved: 9 girls including one who answers in 6–10 business days. Most frustrating: deposits — Airbnb, the boat thing, dinner — three separate splits, eight people each, some paid, some "wait what was this for?" I have a Notes-app ledger like an animal. What went well: the vibe — my Canva itinerary slaps, the girls got hyped. Apps used: iMessage, Partiful, Venmo, Sheets, Canva, Apple album, Airbnb, OpenTable. Eight. After the first plan: dinner venue changed twice, the JPEG itinerary became a lie, and I re-sent it with "FINAL_v3."

**Planning workflow.** Idea → bride's vision board. Booked → I book everything, front the money, split it. During → I'm the human itinerary, answering "what time is the boat" while in a cowboy hat. Post → photo-collection begging, then one final Venmo sweep. Decisions stick in: nowhere — that's the problem. iMessage threads about dinner get to 200 messages and a poll I make in there gets buried. Non-responders: I DM her, then the bride DMs her, then we book without her. Example thread: "Saturday dinner" — 212 messages, four restaurants, zero decisions, I picked one and announced it.

**Feature areas.**
- *Create/Invite:* One trip, one link, send it with a sparkle emoji. The invite modal with the short link looked clean. If a single girl gets stuck making an account, I will hear about it forever.
- *Places:* Pin the Airbnb, Broadway bars, brunch — and the map view for the Uber-splitting question of how far things are. Yes.
- *Calendar/Itinerary:* Live itinerary that updates in place = no more FINAL_v3.jpeg. The day view with times and venue names is exactly my Canva layout, but functional.
- *Polls/Decisions:* THE feature. Dinner poll, auto-close Tuesday 8 PM, anonymous off — I want names so I can apply pressure. The demo trip had polls right in the tabs.
- *Tasks:* "Bring the sashes," "own the playlist," "decorate Friday." Cute, useful, secondary.
- *Smart Import:* I'd paste the Airbnb confirmation, OpenTable reservations, and the pedal-tavern email. If they land on the calendar correctly I'd actually scream (good scream).
- *AI Concierge:* "Private dining for 9 in Nashville, fun not stuffy, under $80/head" and "bachelorette outfit theme ideas that aren't cowboy-core." If it gives me the same Top-10 list as every TikTok, never again.
- *AI Trust:* Generic answers break it instantly. Also if it "saves" something to my itinerary wrong — I saw it asks before saving, which, smart.
- *Settings priorities:* Notifications that don't blow up 9 phones at 8 AM; making sure the bride can be in the trip but blind to the surprise-party parts (can I even do that?).

**Money.** Collecting: I front everything and Venmo-request in waves; there's always one ghost. Reimbursement discussion: public-ish in the group chat because shame works. Plan changes: I announce in iMessage and update the JPEG (lol). One planner: always, me. Hotels/restaurants: the group "decides" by exhaustion; I decide by deadline. Conversations live in iMessage and they will not fully leave it — Chravel has to coexist, not replace.

**Willingness to pay.** **Per-trip.** The $39.99 Trip Pass for 45 days is exactly shaped like a bachelorette: I'd expense it to the group ($5/girl, nobody blinks). $9.99/month forever for a weekend? No. And hear me — the free tier's **3 splits per trip** is insulting for this use case; I have three splits before anyone boards a plane. That cap alone forces the pass, which I guess is the point, but it better tell me upfront and not at split #4 on a Friday.

**Ratings (1–5).**
- Likelihood next trip: **4** — if the girls join easily, I'm running the whole weekend in it
- Clarity: **5** — "The Group Chat Travel App" + the demo dashboard hero; got it in 5 seconds
- Time saved: **4** — polls with deadlines + a live itinerary kill my two biggest time sinks
- AI trust: **3** — the ask-before-saving card is the right instinct; quality unproven
- Would invite: **5** — the product IS the invite
- Mobile usability: **4** — gorgeous dark/gold, glanceable payments; the sideways tab scroll is the one cheap-feeling thing
- Web usability: **4** — fine, but I'd touch the web app twice total
- Pricing fit: **3** — Trip Pass = perfect shape; 3-split free cap = rude
- NPS sentiment: **4** — I'd post it in my group chats if weekend one goes clean

**Wrap-up.** Change one thing: free tier split cap — at least let one trip breathe before the paywall. Recommend when: the dinner poll closes itself Tuesday and nobody argues. Anything else: the demo photos were broken in spots — for an app selling vibes, broken images are a crime. Follow-up: Yes, if it's quick.

### H. Emotional Reaction
- **Impressed by:** The payments ledger with per-head math and pending/settled states; the live itinerary day view; the fact the demo had a bachelorette trip in it.
- **Confused by:** Why Polls — the group-decision feature in a group-decision app — is hiding off-screen on mobile.
- **Annoyed by:** The 3-split free cap ("I have three splits before the flights"); broken demo images; any rumor of jank.
- **Would abandon when:** A bridesmaid says the link "didn't work" twice, or the app stutters during the weekend in front of the girls.
- **Would invite others?** Emphatically — and publicly. She's a megaphone if it works and a megaphone if it doesn't.
- **[SYNTHETIC QUOTE]** "This is my Canva itinerary, my Venmo ledger, and my dinner poll in one link that actually looks expensive — but if it hits me with a paywall at split number four on a Friday night, I will simply die, and then post about it."

### I. Conversion Scores
- **Activation:** 8/10 — instant comprehension, perfect use-case match, high energy to set up tonight
- **Invite likelihood:** 9/10 — the product is delivered via invite; she invites within the hour
- **Day-7 retention:** 7/10 — planning frenzy sustains daily use through the wedding cycle
- **Paid conversion:** 7/10 — Trip Pass is shaped exactly like her problem and she's not price-sensitive for THIS trip
- **NPS-style:** +35 — high advocacy potential, contingent on a clean first weekend
- **Would they pay?** Yes — one-time.
- **What would they pay?** $39.99 Trip Pass, split across the group without thinking twice
- **Feature creating willingness to pay:** Unlimited splits + media headroom + PDF keepsake for the bride
- **Limit/CTA that triggers upgrade:** Split cap at deposit time WITH the Trip Pass offered inline (timing is everything)
- **CTA that would annoy her:** A monthly-subscription pitch ("$9.99/mo") for a 3-night event; any upsell mid-weekend

### J. Top 5 Fixes for This Persona
1. Fix the CSP image-host block breaking demo/mock imagery, because Jessica evaluates on aesthetics first and failed at "be impressed by the demo" when tiles rendered broken, causing first-impression loss in the most shareable segment. (R4 — CSP allowlist vs `images.unsplash.com` mock hosts)
2. Resolve the desktop consumer-trip "Maximum update depth exceeded" loop and the mobile re-render storm, because perceived speed is her #1 churn trigger and both defects fire on her core surfaces. (R2 `desktop-harvest2-log.json` steps 3–13; R1 `MobileGroupCalendar.tsx:525`)
3. Move the split-cap paywall moment to trip setup (offer the Trip Pass when a date-bounded trip with 5+ members is created), because Jessica failed at "collect deposit #2" when the cap landed mid-collection, converting a willing payer into an angry one. (`src/billing/entitlements.ts:272-279`; `TripPassModal.tsx`)
4. Add a pre-signup itinerary/cover teaser at the invite link, because her slowest bridesmaid failed at "just see the plan," causing the whole group to fall back to iMessage screenshots. (`src/pages/JoinTrip.tsx`; `permissionMatrix.generated.ts:44-50`)
5. Pin active polls as a persistent chat banner until closed, because the group failed at "decide dinner" when the poll scrolled away — the decision feature must live where the arguing happens. (`src/components/poll/`, `src/features/chat/`)

### K. Confidence
- **Level:** High (for this segment's observable surfaces) — the consumer demo trip is literally her use case
- **Directly observed:** Landing + bachelorette demo card, payments ledger at both viewports, invite modal, calendar day view, split-cap enforcement code, R1/R2/R4 defects.
- **Needs real-user validation:** AI recommendation quality for taste-based queries; group join-completion rate among 9 invitees; whether expense-in-chat reduces Venmo chasing in practice; Trip Pass purchase timing.
- **Beta interview question:** "Show me your actual Venmo request history for the last group trip you planned — at which exact moment would you have paid $40 to make that stop?"

## Persona 4: Derek Okafor — Consumer / Guys' Golf Birthday Trip Planner (Atlanta → Scottsdale)

### A. Profile
- **Name:** Derek Okafor
- **Age range:** 33–40
- **Location/timezone:** Atlanta, GA (America/New_York)
- **Industry/role:** Commercial insurance broker; default planner of the annual guys' golf trip, this year his own 35th-birthday edition
- **Tech comfort:** Medium — competent, utilitarian; uses apps that work and deletes ones that nag
- **Platform:** iOS (iPhone 14)
- **Group size:** 8 guys, 4 nights, Scottsdale, 3 rounds of golf
- **Planning style:** Reluctant dictator — asks for input twice, then books and tells everyone what they owe
- **Current tools:** iMessage group, GroupMe (legacy, half-dead), Venmo, a Google Doc nobody edits but him, GolfNow/course websites, Vrbo
- **Main pain points:** Nobody responds to anything; tee times need real deposits weeks out; the group decides nothing ("I'm easy" ×8); collecting $200/head happens in three painful waves
- **Budget sensitivity:** Medium — happily drops $300 on a round, deeply allergic to subscriptions; reviews his credit card for "$9.99/mo" parasites quarterly
- **Why adopt Chravel:** Polls with deadlines + a payment ledger that does the chasing math + one calendar nobody can claim they didn't see
- **Why reject Chravel:** If it's another app the guys won't open; if anything smells like a recurring charge; if setup takes longer than his Google Doc

### B. Jobs-to-Be-Done
1. When I need $250/head for the house deposit by Friday, I want one payment request with per-head math and visible paid/unpaid status, so the group's peer pressure replaces my nagging.
2. When I float two tee-time options, I want a poll that closes itself Wednesday, so "I'm easy" stops being an answer and a booking happens.
3. When the itinerary is set, I want one schedule everyone sees with times and courses, so nobody texts me "what time Saturday?" from the hotel lobby.
4. When the trip is over, I want the final who-owes-who math done for me, so settling up doesn't take three weeks and one awkward call.
5. When I plan one trip a year, I want to pay once or never, so I'm not subscribed to my own birthday.
6. When the guys won't respond, I want to see who's seen the plan, so I know whether to repost or to call Mike directly.

### C. Screener Answers
| Question | Answer |
|---|---|
| Group trips last 12 months | 1 (this one; 2 if you count the Auburn tailgate weekend) |
| Typical group size | 5–8 |
| Main tools | iMessage, Venmo, Google Docs, Vrbo, GolfNow |
| Primary device | iOS |
| 45-min call? | No — 15 minutes, tops, and I'll be walking somewhere |
| Role in group | Primary planner |
| Pro-ops responsibility | Yes, I own logistics (by attrition) |

### D. Full Survey Answers

**About you.** Derek, 35 next month, insurance broker. I plan the golf trip because the one year I didn't, we ended up at a course none of us could break 100 on and a house with five beds for eight men. Never again.

**Most recent group trip.** This Scottsdale trip, planning now. Kicked off: my birthday landing on a long weekend. Involved: 8 guys — two respond instantly, four within a week, two are functionally unreachable until they show up at the airport. Most frustrating: tee times. TPC-adjacent courses want deposits 60 days out, which means I need eight commitments and eight payments before anyone's emotionally ready to commit. I fronted $400 last year and got the last $50 back in November. What went well: the trip itself — we always have a great time, which is why nobody learns. Apps used: iMessage, Venmo, Google Doc, Vrbo, GolfNow, Delta app. Six. After the first plan: one guy dropped, splits all changed, I redid the math by hand in Notes.

**Planning workflow.** Idea → me, in January. Booked → I pick the house from three options I pre-screen, "vote" happens (it doesn't), I book. During → I'm the tee-time alarm clock. Post → the Venmo sweep, wave one gets five guys, wave two gets two, wave three is a phone call. Decisions stick: nowhere. The thread produces eight thumbs-up reactions and zero information. Non-responders: two chronic; I text them separately with deadlines I made up. Example: "Friday course: We-Ko-Pa or Troon North?" — 11 replies, nine were jokes, I booked We-Ko-Pa.

**Feature areas.**
- *Create/Invite:* One trip, one link. If joining takes more than a minute, three of my guys will simply not do it, and then the app holds five-eighths of a trip, which is worthless. That's my single biggest fear with this thing.
- *Places:* Pin the house, the courses, a steakhouse. Mildly useful; I know Scottsdale.
- *Calendar/Itinerary:* Yes — tee times with course names and "be in the lobby at 6:40" notes. The day view I saw with times and locations is exactly the artifact I rebuild in the Doc every year.
- *Polls/Decisions:* The feature I'd come for. Two options, deadline Wednesday 8 PM, auto-close, names visible. "I'm easy" becomes a non-vote and I book with a clear conscience.
- *Tasks:* "Bring the speaker," "you own Saturday dinner res," "rent the second SUV." Useful, low bar.
- *Smart Import:* I'd paste the Vrbo confirmation and GolfNow tee-time emails. If those land on the calendar with correct times, that's genuinely most of my setup done.
- *AI Concierge:* "Fourth course option near North Scottsdale under $200 green fees" or "steakhouse for 8 with a private table Saturday." I'd try it twice. If it recommends some tourist trap, I'm done — I trust my group chat's one golf-snob more than any AI.
- *AI Trust:* Wrong specifics (price, distance, "this course allows eightsomes" nonsense). Also any AI that touches my bookings without asking — saw it asks first, good.
- *Settings priorities:* Notifications minimal; nobody in this group wants pings. Payment visibility — who paid — matters more than any setting.

**Money.** Collecting: I front the house + first deposits, then Venmo-request in waves. Reimbursement discussion: public in the thread, names named after wave two. Plan changes: I announce; the calendar is whatever my last text said, which is the problem. One planner: yes, always, me. Hotels/restaurants: group "decides" hotels by me offering three and booking my favorite; restaurants decided day-of by whoever's loudest. Conversations live: iMessage, exclusively. Chravel has to be where the FACTS live; the jokes will stay in iMessage and that's fine.

**Willingness to pay.** **Per-trip.** I'd pay $30–40 once if it visibly saved me the Venmo waves and the tee-time panic — call it a trip expense and split it, fine, that's $5 a guy. A subscription for one trip a year is a hard no on principle; I cancel gym memberships for sport. And the free tier capping splits at three is real: house, two course deposits — I'm at the cap before dinner exists. If the app shows me that wall with a one-time pass next to it, fair enough. If it shows me a monthly plan, I screenshot it and roast it in the group chat.

**Ratings (1–5).**
- Likelihood next trip: **3** — strong if the guys join; dead if they don't
- Clarity: **4** — landing made sense fast; "For Friend & Family trips" plus a golf-trip card in the demo, message received
- Time saved: **4** — polls + payment ledger directly attack my two time sinks
- AI trust: **2** — golf recs are taste + insider knowledge; I default to skeptical
- Would invite: **4** — mandatory; the app without the guys is a fancier Google Doc
- Mobile usability: **4** — payments screen was glanceable; tab scrolling is whatever, I'd learn it
- Web usability: **3** — fine; I'd set up on web once and live on the phone
- Pricing fit: **3** — Trip Pass is the right shape, the split cap placement decides whether it feels fair or like a toll booth
- NPS sentiment: **3** — would recommend to other trip-dads with "it worked for us" energy if it works

**Wrap-up.** Change one thing: let my guys see the itinerary and poll from the link before making an account — every signup hurdle costs me one guy. Recommend when: deposit collection happens in one wave instead of three. Anything else: don't add AI to things that don't need it; I need eight humans to answer one question, that's not an AI problem. Follow-up: Maybe (15 minutes).

1. (`src/types/permissionMatrix.generated.ts:44-50`, `src/pages/JoinTrip.tsx`)
2. Surface the 3-split cap status BEFORE the first split and pair the wall with the Trip Pass inline, because Derek hits the cap at house + two deposits and a mid-collection paywall converts a willing one-time payer into a vocal detractor. (`src/billing/entitlements.ts:272-279`; `TripPassModal.tsx`; delta D4)
3. Add seen-by/read counts on pinned messages and polls, because Derek failed at "know whether Mike saw the tee time" — the non-responder problem is his root pain and the app currently can't answer it. (`src/features/chat/`)
4. Fix the desktop setState loop and mobile render storm on trip tabs, because Derek's tolerance for "laggy" is one bad session before he calls the whole thing overbuilt. (R2 `desktop-harvest2-log.json`; R1 `MobileGroupCalendar.tsx:525`)
5. Replace raw edge-function error copy on the demo trip gate with human language, because skeptical evaluators on hotel wifi failed at "trust the polish" when shown "Failed to send a request to the Edge Function" at a signup moment. (R3 — `src/pages/DemoTripGate.tsx`)

### K. Confidence
- **Level:** Medium-High — payments and polls surfaces were directly observed; his core risk (group adoption) is inherently unobservable in this environment
- **Directly observed:** Landing/pricing framing, payments create + ledger at both viewports, calendar day view, invite modal, split-cap enforcement code, R1/R2/R3 defects.
- **Needs real-user validation:** Invite→join completion among low-motivation male friend groups; whether ledger visibility actually accelerates payment waves; Trip Pass conversion at the cap moment.
- **Beta interview question:** "Last trip: how many separate Venmo requests did you send, over how many weeks — and what's the maximum one-time fee that whole ordeal was worth to you?"


---

## Persona 5: Amanda & Tyler Brooks — Consumer (Events mode) / Destination Wedding Couple (Tulum Wedding Weekend)

### A. Profile
- **Name:** Amanda & Tyler Brooks (Amanda drives; Tyler approves and pays)
- **Age range:** 28–35
- **Location/timezone:** Denver, CO (America/Denver)
- **Industry/role:** Amanda: UX researcher at a healthtech startup; Tyler: structural engineer. Co-planning their own 60-guest destination wedding weekend in Tulum (welcome party, ceremony, recovery brunch, optional cenote day)
- **Tech comfort:** Medium-high — Amanda evaluates software professionally; Tyler reads the pricing page twice
- **Platform:** Mixed — Amanda iOS + desktop web (planning happens on a laptop); guests are iOS/Android/web/everything
- **Group size:** 60 invited guests across 3 generations, ~15 in the wedding party with real logistics
- **Planning style:** Amanda runs a Notion wedding hub; weekly planning hour on Sundays; a wedding planner on the ground in Mexico
- **Current tools:** Zola (registry + RSVP website), Notion, WhatsApp (wedding party), email blasts to guests, Google Sheets (room blocks), WithJoy considered
- **Main pain points:** 60 guests with wildly different tech ability who must know times/shuttles/dress codes; RSVP for sub-events (who's coming to the cenote day?); the same five questions asked sixty times; keeping grandma informed without an app
- **Budget sensitivity:** Low for the wedding line-item — they will happily pay real money once for something polished; zero appetite for the couple's tools becoming a subscription
- **Why adopt Chravel:** One beautiful hub for the whole weekend — itinerary, shuttle times, polls for the cenote day, photo pooling from 60 phones — that makes them look like they hired a second planner
- **Why reject Chravel:** If 60 guests (including parents' friends in their 60s) must each create an account to see the shuttle time, it's disqualified on day one — the guest experience IS the product for them

### B. Jobs-to-Be-Done
1. When 60 guests need the weekend schedule, I want a single link that shows times/locations/dress codes WITHOUT requiring an account, so my 64-year-old aunt isn't locked out of her own niece's wedding logistics.
2. When sub-events have capacity (cenote tour, welcome dinner), I want RSVP-style headcounts per event, so I can give the planner real numbers two weeks out.
3. When the shuttle time changes, I want to broadcast once to all guests and know it reached them, so nobody's stranded at the resort lobby.
4. When the weekend ends, I want every guest's photos pooled in one place, so we're not begging in a WhatsApp thread for months.
5. When I hand guests anything, I want it polished enough to match $40k of wedding, so the logistics feel like part of the experience — including a printable/PDF itinerary for the non-app generation.
6. When we pay for a tool for one weekend, I want to pay once at a price that reflects a wedding (not a monthly app habit), so the cost matches the event.

### C. Screener Answers
| Question | Answer |
|---|---|
| Group trips last 12 months | 2–3 (wedding scouting trip, bach trips adjacent) |
| Typical group size | 16+ (60 for the wedding itself) |
| Main tools | Zola, Notion, WhatsApp, Google Sheets, email |
| Primary device | Both (Amanda iOS + desktop; guests = everything) |
| 45-min call? | Yes — Amanda does user interviews for a living; turnabout is fair play |
| Role in group | Primary planner (couple), with a hired on-the-ground planner |
| Pro-ops responsibility | Yes, we own logistics |

### D. Full Survey Answers

**About you.** Amanda, 31, UX researcher; Tyler, 33, engineer. Getting married in Tulum next spring, 60 guests, three days of programming. I have a Notion hub with 14 pages and a recurring nightmare where the shuttle leaves without my grandmother.

**Most recent group trip.** The wedding-scouting trip, 6 people (us + both sets of parents). Kicked off by the venue shortlist. Most frustrating: relaying the same itinerary across iMessage (my family), WhatsApp (his family), and a printed PDF (his dad). Three formats, one schedule, constant drift. What went well: the Notion hub for US — but I can't send 60 guests into Notion; I tried with the wedding party and got back "it wants me to make an account?" Apps used: Notion, WhatsApp, iMessage, Google Sheets, Zola, email. Six, for six people. The wedding multiplies this by ten. After the first plan: venue changed once, both moms re-asked every question already answered in the doc.

**Planning workflow.** Idea → us + Pinterest. Booked → planner-in-Tulum executes, we coordinate guests. During → I'm terrified of being the help desk in a white dress; the goal is for the schedule to answer questions so I don't. Post → photo collection (the wedding party WhatsApp produced 400 photos last wedding I was in; my parents' friends produced zero because they weren't in it). Decisions stick: in our weekly Sunday session; guest-facing info sticks in the Zola site, which guests forget exists. Non-responders: RSVP chasing is a part-time job — currently done by my mom calling people. Example doc: the "Tulum Weekend Master" sheet — room blocks, shuttle manifests, dietary restrictions.

**Feature areas.**
- *Create/Invite:* This is where I'm both most excited and most worried. Events mode with RSVP states and agenda is the right shape. But I read the link flow as: guest taps link → sees a preview → must create an account to see anything more. For my guests that's a funnel cliff. My aunt will not OAuth into anything.
- *Places:* Venue, three hotels, the cenote, the brunch spot, with distances — genuinely useful for guests booking their own rooms.
- *Calendar/Itinerary:* The core artifact. The day view with times, venues, and notes ("VIP table reserved") is exactly the welcome-packet card I was going to design by hand. If guests can see THIS, half my problem is solved.
- *Polls/Decisions:* "Cenote day: in or out?" as a poll = my sub-event headcount. Also "brunch: 10 or 11?" for the wedding party.
- *Tasks:* Wedding party only — "pick up welcome bags," "own the speaker," "shuttle marshal."
- *Smart Import:* I'd paste the resort room-block confirmation, flight manifests people email me, and the planner's run-of-show PDF. If the run-of-show lands on the calendar, I cry tears of joy.
- *AI Concierge:* Guests asking "what's the dress code Saturday?" or "when's the last shuttle?" and getting the RIGHT answer from trip context — that's the dream; it makes the app the help desk instead of me. I'd also ask it "restaurants near the venue for guest free-night."
- *AI Trust:* If it tells one guest the wrong shuttle time, the damage is a stranded grandmother and I will never forgive software in my life. Wedding logistics is zero-fault-tolerance. The confirm-before-saving design is right; the answers need to be grounded in MY itinerary, not vibes.
- *Settings priorities:* Who can post vs view (guests should mostly view), notification control so 60 people aren't pinged about wedding-party tasks, and a printable/PDF export for the non-digital contingent.

**Pro/Events branch.** "Professional-grade" for us means: guest-facing polish (it looks like part of the wedding brand), reliability (zero wrong times, ever), and visibility (RSVP counts, broadcast delivery). Control vs automation: control with receipts — I want to push the broadcast, and then see it arrived. What creates trust: the app never showing a guest stale or partial information, and never making a 60-year-old debug a login.

**Money.** Collecting: we're not splitting wedding costs with guests; minor wedding-party splits (bach remnants, welcome-bag supplies) only — so payment features are nearly irrelevant to this event. Reimbursement: n/a at scale. Plan-change communication: currently email blast + WhatsApp + moms-as-routers; a tracked broadcast replaces all three. One planner: two of us + a pro. How the group decides: it doesn't — we decide, guests RSVP. Conversations live: everywhere, which is the disease Chravel would need to cure.

**Willingness to pay.** **$30+ one-time (per-event), happily more.** We'd pay $75–150 for one event done perfectly — that's less than the welcome bags cost. What we will NOT do is parse "Frequent Chraveler $19.99/mo" to figure out which subscription unlocks a wedding. I see events are free for the first 3 — so our wedding is technically $0, which is great and slightly suspicious — but PDF export needs a paid tier anyway, and there's no "Wedding/Event Pass" SKU shaped like us. Trip Pass at $74.99/90d is the closest thing and it's labeled like a backpacker product.

**Ratings (1–5).**
- Likelihood next trip/event: **3** — desperate for this to work; blocked entirely by the guest-account wall
- Clarity: **4** — landing communicates fast; Events as a distinct mode took digging to understand
- Time saved: **4** — IF guests self-serve answers, it's tens of hours; if they can't, it's zero
- AI trust: **3** — right guardrails, unproven answers, zero-fault domain
- Would invite: **5** — the entire use case is inviting 60 people
- Mobile usability: **4** — guest-side mobile views looked clean in demo
- Web usability: **4** — Amanda would run the whole event from desktop; demo desktop was solid
- Pricing fit: **2** — free events are generous but the SKU shaped like a wedding doesn't exist, and PDF export paywalls the politest feature
- NPS sentiment: **3** — enthusiastic about the shape, blocked on the one structural thing

**Wrap-up.** Change one thing: guest view-without-account. Nothing else matters until that exists. What makes us recommend: a guest's mom saying "that wedding app was so easy." Anything else: weddings are the most viral event category on earth — every guest is a future couple or knows one; the guest experience is your growth loop, not the planner experience. Follow-up: Yes.

### E. Web Flow Walkthrough
- **Discovery/landing:** Hero names "Friend & Family trips… & Anybody Organizing a Group" and the demo grid includes "The Tyler's Tie The Knot — Bali" (a wedding!) and "Cameron Knight's Dubai Birthday" — Amanda sees weddings are a first-class citizen. [OBSERVED — `desktop-01`, `desktop-06`]
- **Mode discovery:** Top nav in the demo dashboard shows an "Events" section distinct from My Trips/Pro — the right mental model exists, but nothing on the marketing landing explains what Events mode adds (RSVP, agenda, broadcasts). [OBSERVED — `desktop-06`; ground truth §6 Events] [SIMULATED RISK — couples self-select into a regular trip and miss RSVP features]
- **Signup/onboarding (couple side):** Clean auth, Google/Apple, fine for the two of them. [OBSERVED — `desktop-04`]
- **The structural finding (guest side):** `consumer_guest` has read=false on every resource — an invitee who doesn't fully join sees nothing beyond the invite preview (name, dates, cover, member count). For a 60-guest wedding spanning three generations, the mandatory account-per-guest model is the adoption decision, and it currently fails them. [OBSERVED — `src/types/permissionMatrix.generated.ts:44-50` (D15); ground truth §5] [SIMULATED RISK — 20–40% of older guests never complete signup; the couple reverts to email + the moms]
- **Event creation:** Events are NOT immediately paywalled — Free/Explorer get 3 lifetime events, so the wedding itself costs $0 to create; advertised attendee caps (100) have no enforcement call sites, so 60 guests technically fit even on Free. [OBSERVED — `src/billing/entitlements.ts:296-306`; ground truth §4]
- **Feature usage:** Calendar day view with times/venues/notes is the welcome-packet artifact. [OBSERVED — `desktop2-02`] Event surfaces (agenda/tasks/polls/calendar) rendered with rich data in the demo's Netflix Joke Fest event. [OBSERVED — evidence-delta L2, `desktop-13..15` per index] Invite modal's require-approval OFF + no-expiry is actually correct for a wedding link. [OBSERVED — `desktop2-11`]
- **PDF itinerary:** Free tier has `pdf_export: 0` — the printable itinerary for grandma requires Explorer+ ($9.99/mo) or a pass; the politeness feature is paywalled while the event itself is free, a strange inversion for this persona. [OBSERVED — `src/billing/entitlements.ts:280-287`]
- **Pricing reaction:** "Start free. Upgrade when your trip gets serious" — their event is the MOST serious and yet no SKU is labeled for it; Tyler reads Free/Explorer/FC/Pro and finds no "wedding" anywhere. [OBSERVED — `desktop-22`; ground truth §7] [SIMULATED RISK — high-WTP couple bounces to WithJoy for legibility, not capability]
- **Web positives:** Demo polish at desktop sells the "second planner" fantasy [OBSERVED — `desktop-06`, L2]; pending-request review banner gives the couple gatekeeping. [OBSERVED — `desktop2-02`]
- **Web pain points:** R2 setState loop on trip-tab interaction [OBSERVED — R2]; raw "Failed to send a request to the Edge Function" copy possible at the demo-gate conversion moment — their guests on resort wifi WILL hit flaky-network states. [OBSERVED — R3, `src/pages/DemoTripGate.tsx`]

### F. Mobile / PWA Flow Walkthrough
- **First impression (guest's-eye view):** Mobile landing is elegant; "Login or Signup" as the only CTA confirms the account wall starts at the front door. [OBSERVED — `mobile-01`]
- **Navigation clarity:** Horizontal scrolling tab strip, no bottom nav on mobile web; 8 tabs is a lot for a guest who needs exactly two (Calendar, Chat) — wedding guests would face wedding-party clutter (Tasks, Payments, Polls). [OBSERVED — `mobile2-01`, `mobile2-05`] [SIMULATED RISK — older guests get lost in planner-grade UI]
- **Chat/input usability:** Urgent red broadcast-style messages ("Meeting at hotel lobby at 9 AM sharp") are exactly shuttle-change material and visually unmissable. [OBSERVED — `mobile2-01`] Broadcasts subtab exists in chat. [OBSERVED — `mobile2-01`]
- **Forms/modals:** Mobile forms are single-column with large targets — manageable for less-technical guests IF they get in. [OBSERVED — `mobile2-05`]
- **Invite link flow:** Short link + copy + no-expiry option suits a save-the-date email blast. [OBSERVED — `desktop2-11`] Join completion across 60 mixed-platform guests is the great unknown. [HYPOTHESIS]
- **Perceived speed:** The mobile duplicate-key render storm fires on every trip surface including event pages (component stack confirms `MobileGroupCalendar` inside event mobile pages too) — guests' older devices amplify this. [OBSERVED — R1, `MobileGroupCalendar.tsx:525`; delta notes it affects consumer, pro AND event mobile pages]
- **Thumb reach/tap targets:** Generally good; bottom-anchored CTAs. [OBSERVED — `mobile2-05`]
- **Notification scale risk:** Notification fanout blocks the INSERT transaction at scale; 60 guests is modest, but a broadcast to all guests during the wedding weekend leans on exactly the unbatched path flagged in the audit. [OBSERVED — NOTIFICATION_AUDIT.md via ground truth §10.4] [SIMULATED RISK at 60; real risk at their friends' 200-person wedding]
- **Mobile positives:** Glanceable cards, strong urgent-message styling, premium feel that matches a wedding brand. [OBSERVED — `mobile2-01`, `mobile-01`]
- **Mobile pain points:** Tab overflow [OBSERVED — `mobile2-05`]; title truncation would eat "Amanda & Tyler's Wedding Week…" [OBSERVED — `mobile2-01` pattern]; no guest-simplified view exists. [SIMULATED RISK]

### G. Feature-by-Feature Findings
| Feature | Expected goal | Tried | What happened | Positive | Friction | Bug/UX issue | Evidence | Severity 1–5 | Revenue impact | Retention impact | Recommended fix |

| Create event | Wedding weekend with agenda + RSVP | Read code + demo event | 3 lifetime free events; RSVP states + agenda exist; 100-cap unenforced | Wedding costs $0 to create | Free generosity is invisible pre-signup | Advertised caps have no enforcement call sites | [OBSERVED] `entitlements.ts:296-306`; ground truth §4, §6 | 2 | Medium | Medium | Say "your first event is free" out loud in marketing |

| Places/Basecamp | Venue/hotels/cenote with distances | Docs/demo | Saved places + basecamp distances | Guests self-serve "how far is X" | None major | None | [OBSERVED] ground truth §6 | 2 | Low | Medium | Guest-visible places list in read-only view |

| AI Concierge | Guests self-serve "when's the shuttle?" | Not live-testable | Trip-context Q&A among 18 query classes; confirm-before-write | The help-desk-in-a-white-dress savior, if grounded | Wrong answer = stranded grandmother; zero tolerance | Preference injection on irrelevant queries documented | [OBSERVED] ground truth §6, §10; [HYPOTHESIS] grounding accuracy | 4 | Medium | High | Hard-ground guest Q&A to itinerary data; refuse rather than guess |
| Payments | Barely relevant (wedding-party odds and ends) | Demo payments | Full split ledger exists | Fine for welcome-bag splits | Irrelevant at guest scale; adds tab clutter | None | [OBSERVED] `desktop2-05` | 1 | Low | Low | Hide Payments tab for event guests by default |
| Media | Pool 60 phones' photos | Demo surfaces + docs | Hub with grid/lightbox; iOS share-sheet ingestion | The post-wedding photo dream | 500 MB free cap is absurd for a wedding (one ceremony video) | Demo tiles broken via CSP block | [OBSERVED] ground truth §6; `entitlements.ts:261-271`; R4 | 4 | High | High | Event-scoped storage add-on; fix CSP demo images |

| Permissions/roles | Guests view, party contributes, we admin | Read permission matrix | event_organizer full; event_attendee read-only exists | The role model fits weddings well | Mapping invitees → attendee role requires full join | None | [OBSERVED] `permissionMatrix.generated.ts` (event roles); D15 | 3 | Medium | High | Auto-assign event invitees to attendee role with view access pre-join |
| Pricing/upgrade | Pay once, labeled for weddings | Pricing + billing code | Free event + paid PDF export + no event-shaped SKU | First event free = generous | High-WTP couple can't find what to buy; PDF paywalled | None | [OBSERVED] `desktop-22`; `entitlements.ts:280-306`; ground truth §7 | 4 | High | Medium | Ship an "Event Pass" SKU (~$99 one-time: PDF, storage, broadcasts, delivery counts) |

### H. Emotional Reaction
- **Impressed by:** The demo's event surfaces and the calendar day view — "this is the welcome packet, alive"; first-event-free generosity; urgent broadcast styling.
- **Confused by:** What Events mode actually includes vs a regular trip (invisible on marketing); which tier a wedding is supposed to buy.
- **Annoyed by:** The guest account wall — Amanda, professionally: "you built a B2C2C product and put a registration gate on the second C."
- **Would abandon when:** The first test guest (Tyler's dad) fails to get past the invite preview — they'd know within one week of trying.
- **Would invite others?** It's the entire use case — 60 invites or nothing. And every wedding guest is a future event organizer; they understand they ARE the growth loop.
- **[SYNTHETIC QUOTE]** "We'd pay a hundred dollars tonight for this exact app — if my aunt can tap the link and see the shuttle time without creating an account. She can't, so we can't."

### I. Conversion Scores
- **Activation:** 5/10 — strong pull, but the guest-wall discovery happens in week one and stalls everything
- **Invite likelihood:** 9/10 — structurally maximal (60 invites); gated on the wall
- **Day-7 retention:** 6/10 — Amanda would keep building the itinerary while deciding; the decision comes fast
- **Paid conversion:** 5/10 — highest WTP in the batch with no SKU shaped like them; money left on the table
- **NPS-style:** 0 — perfectly torn: evangelist features, disqualifying guest model
- **Would they pay?** Yes — eagerly, once, if the guest experience works.
- **What would they pay?** $75–150 one-time per event; $0/month
- **Feature creating willingness to pay:** Guest-facing polish bundle — PDF itinerary, storage for wedding media, tracked broadcasts
- **Limit/CTA that triggers upgrade:** PDF export gate (they'd pay instantly for the printable itinerary)
- **CTA that would annoy them:** "Frequent Chraveler $19.99/mo" as the answer to "I'm having a wedding" — subscription branding for a once-in-a-lifetime event

### J. Top 5 Fixes for This Persona
1. Add a tokenized, read-only guest view (itinerary, places, agenda) at the invite link with no account required, because Amanda & Tyler failed at "let 60 mixed-ability guests see the schedule" — consumer_guest has zero resource access — causing outright disqualification of the highest-WTP, highest-virality consumer segment. (`src/types/permissionMatrix.generated.ts:44-50`; `src/pages/JoinTrip.tsx`)
2. Ship an event-shaped one-time SKU (Event Pass: PDF export + media storage + broadcast delivery counts), because the couple failed at "figure out what to buy" on a subscription-framed pricing page, causing $100+ of willing spend to bounce. (`src/billing/config.ts`; `PricingSection.tsx`, `desktop-22`)
3. Surface delivery/read counts on event broadcasts below Pro tier, because the couple failed at "confirm the shuttle change reached everyone," which is the single moment of truth for wedding logistics. (ground truth §6 Pro broadcasts; `src/features/chat/`)
4. Add role-scoped tab visibility and notification defaults for event guests (Calendar/Chat/Places only; broadcasts-only pings), because guests failed at "find the schedule" inside planner-grade 8-tab UI, causing help-desk regression to the couple. (`src/pages/MobileTripDetail.tsx`; `NotificationsDialog.tsx`)
5. Fix the mobile render storm before event-scale usage (it fires on event mobile pages too) and batch notification fanout, because 60 guests on older devices during a wedding weekend hit both the R1 perf defect and the unbatched fanout path simultaneously. (`src/components/mobile/MobileGroupCalendar.tsx:525`; NOTIFICATION_AUDIT.md)

### K. Confidence
- **Level:** Medium — the disqualifying finding (D15 guest access) is code-verified and High confidence; everything about guest behavior at scale is unobserved
- **Directly observed:** Wedding card in demo grid, Events nav, event demo surfaces, invite modal options, calendar artifact, permission matrix, entitlements (events free ×3, PDF gated), R1/R3/R4 defects, notification fanout audit.
- **Needs real-user validation:** Guest signup completion across age cohorts; whether invite-preview-only is truly a cliff or merely friction; Event Pass price sensitivity; AI grounding quality on "when's the shuttle" queries.
- **Beta interview question:** "Send your real save-the-date list a test link to a sample event: what percentage of guests over 55 make it past the sign-up screen without calling you?"

# Synthetic Persona Study — Batch 2 (Personas 6–10, Consumer segment)
Study: 2026-06-11 30-persona study · Evidence: `evidence-delta.md` (overrides 2026-06-09 ground truth) · Screenshots: `docs/research/synthetic-user-testing/2026-06-11-30-persona-study/screenshots/`

---

## Persona 6: Gloria Jenkins — Consumer / Family Reunion Planner

### A. Profile
- **Name:** Gloria Jenkins
- **Age range:** 58–65
- **Location/timezone:** Memphis, TN / Central (CT)
- **Industry/role:** Retired school administrator; volunteer church events coordinator; the family's designated reunion planner
- **Tech comfort:** LOW — comfortable with Facebook, texting, and printing things out; suspicious of "another app"
- **Platform:** Android phone (Samsung, large-font mode on) + desktop-first (does real planning on the family computer)
- **Group size:** ~35 family members across 4 generations (great-aunts to grandbabies)
- **Planning style:** One binder, one Facebook group, one phone tree. Decisions made by calling the elders first.
- **Current tools:** Facebook group, group texts, email chains nobody reads, a paper sign-up sheet at church, Walmart photo prints
- **Main pain points:** Aunts who only use Facebook; uncles who don't read email; collecting headcounts and t-shirt sizes from 35 people; nobody knows the latest version of the schedule
- **Budget sensitivity:** Very high — reunion money goes to the venue and the fish fry, not software. **Free only.**
- **Why adopt Chravel:** One link where the whole family can see the schedule, the hotel, and the photos — instead of 4 channels and a phone tree
- **Why reject Chravel:** If Aunt Bernice has to create an account with a password to see the schedule, Gloria is back to Facebook by Sunday

### B. Jobs-to-Be-Done
1. When I am planning the Jenkins family reunion, I want one place with the schedule, hotel, and headcount, so I can stop repeating myself on three different phone calls.
2. When I send the invite out, I want my low-tech relatives to open one link and see everything, so I can include the elders without teaching them a new app.
3. When the schedule changes (and it will), I want everybody to see the same updated version, so I can stop hearing "well, the email said 2 o'clock."
4. When we're picking the reunion weekend, I want a simple vote everyone can tap, so I can settle the date without a phone tree.
5. When the reunion is over, I want all the photos in one place, so I can get prints made for the elders who aren't on Facebook.
6. When I'm reading on my phone at night, I want text I can actually see, so I can use the app without fetching my reading glasses.

### C. Screener Answers
| Question | Answer |
|---|---|
| Trips last 12 months | 1 (reunion) + 1 church trip |
