| 45-min call? | Yes — "I've got time and opinions" |
| Role in group | Primary planner |
| Pro-ops responsibility | Yes, I own logistics |

### D. Full Survey Answers

**About you.** I'm Gloria, I'm 61, retired from Shelby County Schools, and I have run the Jenkins family reunion for eleven years. Thirty-five people, four generations, three states. I keep a binder.

**Most recent/next group trip.** Next reunion is summer 2027 in Memphis — we rotate cities and it's our turn. What kicked it off: my cousin Denise said "let's do Gatlinburg" in the Facebook group and forty comments later we still hadn't picked a weekend. Who's involved: everybody — but really me, Denise, and my brother Ray do the work. Most frustrating: getting answers. I post in Facebook, the aunties see it. I email, the uncles don't read it. I text, the kids answer and the elders don't. Same announcement, four channels, and somebody STILL shows up at the wrong time. What went well last time: the matching t-shirts and the Saturday banquet — because I confirmed every single person by phone. Apps used: Facebook (the group), Messages, Gmail, and my niece set up a Google Sheet that exactly four people opened. That's 4 apps and a binder. After the first plan: it changed twice and I had to re-announce on every channel both times.

**Planning workflow.** Idea comes at the previous reunion. Then: pick the weekend (two months of back-and-forth), block hotel rooms, plan the banquet, collect $45 per family for the hall, chase t-shirt sizes. During the trip I am the information desk. After, I mail photo prints to the elders. Where decisions stick: picking dates — everybody has a conflict and nobody says so until you've booked. Non-responders: I call them. That's the only thing that works. Example thread: the 2025 t-shirt size thread in Facebook had 87 comments and I still ordered two wrong sizes.

**Feature areas.**
- *Create/Invite:* Making the trip looked simple enough on the computer. But here's my question and it's the only question that matters: when Aunt Bernice, who is 78 and uses Facebook on a tablet, taps my link — does she see the schedule, or does she see a sign-up form? Because if it's a sign-up form, she's calling me, and I'm back to being the information desk.
- *Places:* I liked that the hotel sits right at the top with the address — "Trip Base Camp" is a funny name for the Holiday Inn but the idea is right. The Get Directions box is something I'd actually use for the older drivers.
- *Calendar/Itinerary:* This would be my schedule — Friday meet-and-greet, Saturday banquet, Sunday church. But I need to PRINT it. The elders want paper on the refrigerator. I'm told printing the trip to PDF costs money on the free plan, and that's backwards — the free plan is the one with the grandmothers on it.
- *Polls/Decisions:* Now THIS I like. "Which weekend works?" with three options and everybody taps one. If that works on Bernice's tablet, that alone beats two months of Facebook comments.
- *Tasks:* I'd assign Ray the grills and Denise the banquet hall and it'd be in writing for once.
- *Smart Import:* I'd paste the hotel confirmation email. If it puts the address and dates in by itself, fine, but I'd check its work.
- *AI Concierge:* I'd ask "what's a restaurant near the hotel that seats 35 and takes a reservation." I would not let it change my schedule without asking me first.
- *AI Trust:* It breaks the first time it tells one of my relatives something different than what I announced. One schedule, one truth.
- *Settings priorities:* Make the words bigger. And if there's a way to make the screen white instead of black, show me where, because this black screen with gray writing is hard on my eyes.

**Money.** I collect $45 per family for the hall — cash, checks, and my niece's Venmo for the young ones. I track it on paper. Reimbursement talk is simple in my family: you pay me before the reunion or you hear about it at the reunion. Plan changes get announced on every channel and STILL missed. Is there one planner? Yes. Me. How the group decides: the elders pick the city, I pick everything else. Conversations live on Facebook and the phone.

**Willingness to pay.** **Free only.** It's a family reunion, not a business. If the app needs $9.99 a month from me, I'll need it to also fry the fish.

**Ratings (1–5).**
- Likelihood to use for next trip: **3** — depends entirely on whether the elders can open the link without me driving to their houses.
- Clarity: **3** — the computer version made sense; the dark screen and small gray words did not.
- Time saved: **4** — IF the family actually gets in, this replaces four channels.
- AI trust: **2** — I don't trust anything I can't double-check against my binder.
- Would invite others: **3** — I'd try it on the planning committee (me, Denise, Ray) first.
- Mobile usability: **2** — small words, dark screen, and my phone got warm poking around the sample trip.
- Web usability: **3** — fine on the computer, which is where I'd live anyway.
- Pricing fit: **4** — free covers a reunion if the free plan keeps letting 35 people in.
- Overall sentiment: **3** — good idea, but it wasn't built with Bernice in mind.

**Wrap-up.** Change one thing: let people I invite SEE the trip before they make an account. What makes me recommend it: one reunion where nobody calls me asking what time the banquet is. Anything else: y'all should sell a big-print mode like the phones have. Follow-up call: **Yes.**

### F. Mobile / PWA Flow Walkthrough
- **First impression:** Same black-and-gold on my Android. Pretty, the way a jewelry store is pretty. Hard to read, the way a jewelry store is dimly lit. [OBSERVED palette — `mobile-22`; readability for 60+ eyes SIMULATED RISK]
- **Navigation:** Inside a trip there's a row of tabs across the top you swipe sideways (Media, Payments, Places...). There is no big bottom row of buttons like my other apps in the mobile-web demo — my relatives will not discover tabs that are off-screen to the right. [OBSERVED — `mobile2-04` tab strip; evidence-delta "Notable non-defect observations"]
- **Chat/input:** Bubbles are legible; the red announcement bubbles stand out, which I like for "banquet moved to 6 PM." [OBSERVED — desktop2-01 equivalent; mobile chat per delta L2]
- **Forms/modals:** The signup form on a phone is the same dark form. My concern is my relatives, not me. [OBSERVED — `mobile-05` per delta L4; impact SIMULATED RISK]
- **Invite link flow:** The killer issue. The invite preview shows trip name and dates before signing in — good. But to see ANYTHING more, my relatives must create an account, verify an email, and join — because guests have no access to any resource: `consumer_guest: { '*': { read: false ... } }`. For four generations of Jenkinses, that's not onboarding, that's a door. [OBSERVED — `src/types/permissionMatrix.generated.ts:44-51` (D15); family abandonment rate HYPOTHESIS]
- **Perceived speed:** The demo moved fine, but my phone warmed up and the screen stuttered now and then on the trip pages — the study found the app re-renders a calendar constantly in the background on every mobile trip surface. [OBSERVED — R1, `MobileGroupCalendar.tsx:525`, ~5,940 duplicate-key warnings in mobile pass 2]
- **Thumb reach/tap targets:** Buttons are big enough; the storage meter and filter chips on Media were clear. [OBSERVED — `mobile2-04`]
- **Mobile positives:** Take Photo / Upload buttons are huge and obvious — photo collection from the family might actually work. Storage meter is plain English (127 MB of 500 MB). [OBSERVED — `mobile2-04`]
- **Mobile pain points:** dark theme + small gray secondary text; sideways tab strip; account wall on invite; 500 MB fills fast with 35 people's reunion photos. [OBSERVED limit — `entitlements.ts:265`; fill-rate SIMULATED RISK]

### H. Emotional Reaction
- **Impressed by:** The polls page, the hotel/directions page, and the honesty of showing the real app on the landing page.
- **Confused by:** Why the schedule I can see free on screen costs money the moment I want it on paper; what "Base Camp" means; where the tabs went on the phone.
- **Annoyed by:** Gray writing on a black screen everywhere, all the time, with the light switch hidden in settings.
- **Would abandon when:** The third relative calls saying "it wants me to make an account" — that's the moment I post the schedule back on Facebook.
- **Would invite others?** The planning committee, yes. All 35? Only after one of the aunties survives the join flow unassisted.
- **[SYNTHETIC QUOTE]:** "It's a beautiful app, baby, but my family doesn't need beautiful — they need big print, one link, and no passwords."

### I. Conversion Scores
- **Activation:** 4/10 — she'll build the trip on desktop, but activation = her family joining, and the account wall sits in front of it.
- **Invite likelihood:** 4/10 — committee yes, full family only after a guest view exists.
- **Day-7 retention:** 4/10 — reunion planning is bursty; she returns when the family does.
- **Paid conversion:** 1/10 — free only, on principle.
- **NPS-style:** −10 — likes the idea, can't deploy it to her actual users (the elders).
- **Would they pay?** No.
- **What would they pay?** $0 — "the reunion budget buys fish, not software."
- **Feature creating willingness to pay:** None for her; printable PDF is the only paid feature she covets, and she resents that it's the one she needs.
- **Limit/CTA that triggers upgrade:** 500 MB storage during photo-sharing weekend — and she'd sooner delete videos than pay.
- **CTA that would annoy them:** "Start Free Trial" popups mid-planning; anything implying her trip "got serious" so she owes money.

### J. Top 5 Fixes for This Persona
1. **Add a read-only guest view for valid invite-token holders** because Gloria failed at her core task — getting 78-year-old relatives to the schedule — at the `consumer_guest` zero-access wall (`src/types/permissionMatrix.generated.ts:44-51`), causing reversion to Facebook for the whole 35-person group.
2. **Give the Free tier limited PDF/print export (1–3 per trip)** because Gloria's elders need paper and `pdf_export.free: 0` (`src/billing/entitlements.ts:280-286`) paywalls the one output her lowest-tech members depend on, causing the schedule to live outside Chravel anyway.
3. **Surface light mode + text size during onboarding (and respect OS font scaling)** because the dark-default theme (`src/hooks/useTheme.ts:15-16`) with low-contrast secondary text makes reading hard for 55+ users who will never find the toggle in `ConsumerGeneralSettings.tsx`, causing day-one abandonment by exactly her demographic.
4. **Auto-skip the 10-screen onboarding carousel for users arriving via invite link** because relatives joining Gloria's trip face `OnboardingCarousel.tsx`'s 10 screens before the thing they came for, causing join-funnel drop-off she has to mop up by phone.
5. **Make cash/check manual settlement a first-class, prominent path in Payments** because Gloria's family pays in cash and checks, and a Venmo-deeplink-centered settle-up (`src/components/payments/SettlePaymentDialog.tsx`) reads as "not for us," causing the money tracking to stay on paper.

### K. Confidence
- **Level:** Medium.
- **Directly observed:** Landing/pricing/auth/demo surfaces at both viewports (`desktop-01`, `desktop-19`, `desktop-05`, `desktop2-06/07/08`, `mobile2-04`, `mobile-22`); guest zero-access (D15); PDF export Free=0; dark-default theme; mobile render-storm (R1).
- **Needs real-user validation:** Whether 60–80-year-old invitees actually complete account creation + email verification; real readability failure rates on the dark theme; whether polls survive first contact with a tablet-using great-aunt.
- **Beta interview question:** "Walk me through the last time you got a relative over 70 to use a new app — what was the exact step where they called you instead?"

## Persona 7: Tyler Nguyen — Consumer / College Spring Break Group Planner

### A. Profile
- **Name:** Tyler Nguyen
- **Age range:** 19–22
- **Location/timezone:** Austin, TX / Central (CT)
- **Industry/role:** Junior at UT Austin (RTF major); the guy in the group chat who actually books things
- **Tech comfort:** HIGH — but zero patience; if a page takes 3 seconds he's gone
- **Platform:** iPhone only. The laptop is for essays.
- **Group size:** 12 students (core 6 + the maybes)
- **Planning style:** Chaos until two weeks out, then panic-booking. All decisions happen in iMessage with fire emojis as votes.
- **Current tools:** iMessage, Venmo, Zelle, Splitwise (one guy insists), Google Maps pins, a shared Note titled "SPRING BREAK???"
- **Main pain points:** 12 people, 3 commit early, 5 commit late, 4 ghost; collecting money; the Airbnb link dying in the scroll; nobody reads the Note
- **Budget sensitivity:** Extreme — broke. Splits a $7 queso. **Free only, forever.**
- **Why adopt Chravel:** It's free, he can try it without signing up, and polls might end the "where are we even going" debate
- **Why reject Chravel:** Any paywall, any forced signup before value, any friction his flakiest friend can't survive

### B. Jobs-to-Be-Done
1. When the group chat starts saying "spring break??", I want to throw options into a poll, so I can get a real decision instead of 200 messages and zero commitments.
2. When I find the Airbnb, I want it saved somewhere permanent, so I can stop scrolling iMessage for a link from three weeks ago.
3. When I front the deposit, I want everyone to see exactly what they owe me, so I can stop being the venmo-request villain.
4. When people ghost on decisions, I want the poll to just close and pick, so I can book before prices go up.
5. When I try a new app, I want to see it working before I make an account, so I can decide in 30 seconds whether it's worth my time.

### C. Screener Answers
| Question | Answer |
|---|---|
| Trips last 12 months | 2–3 (spring break, ACL camping, one road trip) |
| Typical group size | 9–15 |
| Main tools | iMessage, Venmo/Zelle, Splitwise, Notes app |
| Primary device | iOS |
| 45-min call? | No — "45 minutes?? I'll do 10" |
| Role in group | Primary planner |
| Pro-ops responsibility | Yes, I own logistics (by default, nobody else will) |

### D. Full Survey Answers

**About you.** Tyler, 20, UT Austin. I'm the friend who books the Airbnb and then spends six weeks getting paid back $83 at a time.

**Most recent/next group trip.** South Padre, spring break, 12 of us. Kicked off when someone posted a TikTok of the beach house in the group chat. Who's involved: 6 actual humans and 6 "I'm down"s who were not, in fact, down. Most frustrating: the headcount. The Airbnb cost depended on headcount, the headcount depended on price, infinite loop, I just booked and prayed. Went well: the trip itself, once we physically arrived everything was great. Apps: iMessage (everything), Venmo (money), Zelle (the two guys whose Venmo is "broken"), Splitwise (Dev made us), Google Maps, Notes. So like 6 apps. After the first plan: two people dropped, one added his girlfriend, and the room math broke twice.

**Planning workflow.** Idea → 300 messages → I make a Note nobody reads → I book → I send Venmo requests → I send them again → trip → after the trip the chat dies for 4 months. Where decisions stick: literally choosing anything. Dates was a 3-week argument. Non-responders: we just say "silence = you're in for $250" and that works honestly. Example: our "SPRING BREAK???" Note has the 2024 plan still in it because nobody updates it.

**Feature areas.**
- *Create/Invite:* Making a trip looked fast. The invite has to be one link I drop in iMessage and people are IN. If my flakiest friend has to verify an email he will simply not go on the trip.
- *Places:* Saving the Airbnb + the beach + the taco spot in one place instead of pinned messages — yeah that's useful. The "base camp" thing where it does distances from the house is lowkey sick.
- *Calendar/Itinerary:* We don't really do itineraries. Maybe "check-in 4 PM" and "boat day Tuesday." Two events max.
- *Polls/Decisions:* The actual killer feature. "South Padre vs Gulf Shores vs New Orleans" with a close date so it just DECIDES. The Leading badge is exactly the peer pressure we need.
- *Tasks:* "Bring speaker" assigned to Marcus with a due date is funny and also necessary.
- *Smart Import:* I'd paste the Airbnb confirmation email. If it pulls check-in time and address automatically, respect.
- *AI Concierge:* "Cheapest place to feed 12 people near the house" and "what's free to do in South Padre." 10 free questions per person per trip is honestly plenty — that's like 120 questions across the group, we're not writing a thesis.
- *AI Trust:* It breaks if it recommends some tourist-trap $$$ place. We can smell a sponsored answer.
- *Settings priorities:* Notifications OFF by default for everything except polls and money. The chat already exists, it's called iMessage.

**Money.** I front it, the app splits it, people pay me on Venmo. The Venmo deeplink thing is genuinely the correct feature — no in-app wallet nonsense, just open Venmo pre-filled. Reimbursement discussion: "pay me by Friday or you're sleeping on the floor." Plan changes: I post in the chat; 8 see it, 4 ask me the same question the next day. One planner? Me. Always me. Hotels/restaurants get decided by vibes and whoever yells loudest — polls would fix this. Conversations live in iMessage and will continue to live in iMessage; Chravel has to be the planning layer, not the chat replacement.

**Willingness to pay.** **Free only.** I'm a student. $9.99/month is two Chipotle entrees. If the app stops being free at any point mid-trip I will simply screenshot everything and leave. BUT — and I'm being honest — if it saved the trip in a real way, a one-time $5 from the whole group split 12 ways? Maybe. Monthly? Never.

**Ratings (1–5).**
- Likelihood to use for next trip: **4** — the try-before-signup demo sold me; polls + split tracking is exactly our problem.
- Clarity: **4** — I never had to think. Except finding tabs on mobile (sideways scroll, weird).
- Time saved: **4** — one poll replaces three weeks of arguing.
- AI trust: **3** — useful for "what's near us," wouldn't trust it for taste.
- Would invite: **4** — drops the link in the chat tonight, but if two people bounce off signup, the whole experiment dies.
- Mobile usability: **3** — looks great, but the demo trip made my phone stutter a bit and the tab strip hides half the features off-screen.
- Web usability: **4** — fine on the rare laptop session.
- Pricing fit: **3** — free tier is genuinely usable (huge), but the upgrade nags better stay out of my face during the trip.
- Overall sentiment: **4** — best free option I've seen, retention is gonna be their problem not mine.

**Wrap-up.** Change one thing: let people vote in a poll from the invite link WITHOUT making an account — that's the whole funnel right there. Recommend trigger: the first time a poll ends an argument. Anything else: the app dies in my dock April 1st when the trip ends, that's not hate, that's just what trips are. Follow-up: **Maybe** (if it's 10 min).

### E. Web Flow Walkthrough
- **Discovery/landing:** Opened the link, and the landing page IS the app — live demo dashboard with real-looking trips, zero "Book a Demo" garbage. This is the single best decision they made: I evaluated the entire product in 90 seconds without giving an email. [OBSERVED — `desktop-01`; demo depth per delta L2]
- **How it works:** "Why Juggle a Dozen Apps for One Trip?" — called out. That's literally my six apps. [OBSERVED — `desktop-19`]
- **Signup:** Apple button at the top — one tap, no password, this is the only acceptable signup in 2026. [OBSERVED — `desktop-05` shows Apple/Google OAuth] Email verification after = where I lose my flaky friends. [SIMULATED RISK — auth not live-testable per evidence-delta]
- **Trip creation:** Looked like 30 seconds of work. Fine. [OBSERVED — ground truth §4; not live-tested]
- **Feature usage:** Polls with vote counts and the "Leading" badge — perfect, ship nothing else. [OBSERVED — `desktop2-07`] Concierge suggests "Split last night's dinner $240 four ways and log it" — okay that's actually our life. [OBSERVED — `desktop2-03`] Chat looks like a full chat app; we won't use it, iMessage exists, but broadcasts for "LEAVING AT 9" are valid. [OBSERVED — `desktop2-01`]
- **Pricing reaction:** "Free works forever—upgrade only when you need more" — correct answer. "Trips can easily exceed $1,000. Your memories are worth more than a Trip Pass" — bro my trip budget IS $250, this copy is for people with jobs. [OBSERVED — `mobile-22`]
- **Web positives:** demo-first landing (massive), free tier with real limits I'll never hit (3 trips? I plan 2 a year), Venmo deeplink instead of some in-app wallet. [OBSERVED — `entitlements.ts:245-252`; ground truth §6 payments]
- **Web pain points:** the desktop demo trip threw repeated "Maximum update depth exceeded" loops on tab clicks per the harvest log — didn't crash for me but that's the kind of thing that becomes a frozen tab on a hotel wifi. [OBSERVED — R2, `desktop-harvest2-log.json` steps 3–13]

### F. Mobile / PWA Flow Walkthrough
- **First impression:** Looks like a real iOS app, dark mode native energy, gold accents. For once a web app that doesn't feel like a tax form. [OBSERVED — `mobile2-04`, `mobile-22`]
- **Navigation clarity:** Tab strip scrolls sideways across the top of the trip (Media | Payments | Places | ...) and there's no bottom tab bar on mobile web — half my group will never find Polls because it's off-screen right. iOS users expect bottom tabs; thumb has to travel to the top. [OBSERVED — `mobile2-04` tab strip; delta non-defect observation re: no bottom nav]
- **Chat/input:** Input bar with @ mentions at the bottom where it belongs. [OBSERVED — delta L2, mobile2-01]
- **Forms/modals:** Signup form is thumb-fine. [OBSERVED — `mobile-05` per delta L4]
- **Invite link flow:** Link → preview → CREATE ACCOUNT → verify email → join. That's four steps and my group's completion rate on four steps is maybe 60%. The preview (name, dates, "starts in X days") is good bait though. [OBSERVED flow — ground truth §5; drop-off rate HYPOTHESIS]
- **Perceived speed:** Mostly snappy, but the trip pages run a hidden calendar that re-renders constantly even when you're on other tabs — thousands of duplicate-key warnings in the harvest. On my friends' three-year-old phones with 47 open Safari tabs, that's jank and battery drain. [OBSERVED — R1, `MobileGroupCalendar.tsx:525`, 5,940 warnings in mobile pass 2; battery impact SIMULATED RISK]
- **Thumb reach/tap targets:** Take Photo / Upload are huge. Storage meter (127/500 MB, 25.4%) is clear — but 12 people posting beach videos will hit 500 MB by day 2, and the quota is advisory-only so it'll be confusing when it "still works." [OBSERVED — `mobile2-04`, `entitlements.ts:265`, register §10.7; fill-rate SIMULATED RISK]
- **Mobile positives:** demo works fully on phone, media UX is clean, payments tab exists where the money argument happens.
- **Mobile pain points:** no bottom nav, off-screen tabs, render jank (R1), account-wall invites.

### G. Feature-by-Feature Findings

| Feature | Expected goal | Tried | What happened | Positive | Friction | Bug/UX issue | Evidence | Severity 1–5 | Revenue impact | Retention impact | Recommended fix |
|---|---|---|---|---|---|---|---|---|---|---|---|
| Marketing/positioning | Know in 30s if it's worth it | Viewed landing | Landing = live demo app; evaluated everything pre-signup | Try-before-signup is elite; zero gatekeeping | "Memories worth more than a Trip Pass" copy targets people with money | None | [OBSERVED] `desktop-01`, `mobile-22` | 1 | Low | Low | Keep demo-first forever; add a student-budget pricing voice |
| Signup/onboarding | One tap in | Viewed auth | Apple/Google OAuth front and center; 10-screen carousel after (skippable) | Apple sign-in = no password | Email verification + 10 onboarding screens between my friends and the trip | None | [OBSERVED] `desktop-05`; D13; drop-off [SIMULATED RISK] | 3 | Low | High | Invite-link joiners skip carousel entirely, land in the trip |
| Create trip | 30-second setup | Demo + code review | Title/dates/timezone; fast | Minimal required fields | None real | None | [OBSERVED] ground truth §4 | 1 | Low | Low | — |

| Calendar/Itinerary | Two events max | Viewed demo | Full calendar views exist | More than enough | Overkill for vibes-based trips | None | [OBSERVED] delta L2 | 1 | Low | Low | — |

| Polls | End the destination argument | Viewed demo | Options, live counts, Leading badge, auto-close exists | THE feature; auto-close = forced decision | Voting requires full account (see Invite) | None | [OBSERVED] `desktop2-07`; poll config ground truth §6 | 1 | Low | High | Tokenized guest voting — this is the viral loop |
| Tasks | Assign "bring speaker" | Viewed demo | Tasks, due dates, filters | Public accountability for Marcus | None | None | [OBSERVED] `desktop2-08` | 1 | Low | Low | — |

| AI Concierge | Cheap eats for 12 | Viewed demo prompts | Group-aware prompts incl. splitting dinners; 10 free queries/user/trip | Free limit is genuinely fine (120 group-wide) | Tourist-trap answers would kill trust instantly | Upgrade link on limit still routes to /settings not checkout | [OBSERVED] `desktop2-03`, `entitlements.ts:237-244`, D2 `AIConciergeChat.tsx:52-53`; answer quality [HYPOTHESIS] | 2 | Medium | Low | Fix limit-wall upgrade URL; keep free limit per-user |
| Payments | See who owes me | Viewed demo + code | Equal split, who-owes-whom, Venmo deeplink; Free = 3 splits/trip | Venmo deeplink is the correct architecture | **3 splits per trip is a joke for spring break** — Airbnb + gas + groceries and we're capped on day 1; we'd bail to Splitwise | Cap enforced with typed error + upsell (D3) | [OBSERVED] `entitlements.ts:272-279`, D3; bail-to-Splitwise [SIMULATED RISK] | 4 | High | High | Raise free splits to ~10/trip; charge for receipts/exports instead |
| Media | Beach pics in one place | Viewed mobile demo | Grid, filters, 500 MB meter | Clean, fast, obvious upload | 12 people × videos = cap by day 2 | Quota advisory-only → inconsistent enforcement confusion | [OBSERVED] `mobile2-04`, register §10.7 | 3 | Medium | Medium | Compress video by default; clear "what happens at cap" copy |
| Settings/notifications | Mute everything except money | Code review | Per-trip mute now exists (D11) | Mute shipped | Notification defaults unknown; my group will get spammed and leave | None | [OBSERVED] D11 `useTripNotificationMute.ts:26-94`; defaults [HYPOTHESIS] | 2 | Low | Medium | Default-quiet for consumer trips: polls + payments only |
| Pricing/upgrade | Never see a paywall | Viewed pricing + demo | Free tier real; upsells exist at limit moments | "Free works forever" is true to the config | Mid-trip upsell modal would be instant screenshot-and-roast material | None observed in demo flow | [OBSERVED] `mobile-22`, D4; mid-trip nag tolerance [SIMULATED RISK] | 2 | Medium | High | Suppress upgrade modals during active trip dates |
| Performance (mobile) | Not melt my phone | Harvest evidence | Hidden calendar re-renders constantly on all mobile trip tabs | App mostly feels fast | Stutter + battery on older phones | Duplicate-key render storm, 5,940 warnings | [OBSERVED] R1 `MobileGroupCalendar.tsx:525` | 3 | Low | Medium | Fix weekday keys; unmount inactive tab components |

### H. Emotional Reaction
- **Impressed by:** Landing page = the actual app. No email gate, no demo-call nonsense. Also polls and the Venmo deeplink.
- **Confused by:** Where the rest of the tabs went on mobile (off-screen right), and what happens when storage hits the cap.
- **Annoyed by:** The idea of any group member hitting a signup wall; the "$1,000 trip" upsell copy aimed at adults with salaries; 3 free payment splits.
- **Would abandon when:** Two friends fail to join from the link, OR an upgrade modal appears mid-trip. Either one and we're back in iMessage like nothing happened.
- **Would invite others?** Yes — tonight, it's free and the demo is shareable. But the invite IS the test; the funnel decides, not me.
- **[SYNTHETIC QUOTE]:** "The landing page just let me use the whole app with zero signup — that's the most respect a website has ever shown me. Now make the invite link work the same way and you've got all 12 of us."

### I. Conversion Scores
- **Activation:** 9/10 — demo-to-trip-creation is frictionless for HIM; he's activated already.
- **Invite likelihood:** 8/10 — link goes in the chat immediately; cost of trying is zero.
- **Day-7 retention:** 6/10 — high during the 6 weeks pre-trip, then a cliff.
- **Paid conversion:** 1/10 — structurally broke; Free-only forever.
- **NPS-style:** +20 — genuinely enthusiastic, with loud caveats about invites and split caps.
- **Would they pay?** No (monthly never; a one-time group-split $5 "maybe").
- **What would they pay?** $0/mo; theoretical $0.50/head one-time.
- **Feature creating willingness to pay:** None personally — polls and splits must stay free or he leaves.
- **Limit/CTA that triggers upgrade:** 3 splits/trip — but it triggers EXIT to Splitwise, not upgrade. That's the danger.
- **CTA that would annoy them:** Any modal during the trip; "your memories are worth more than a Trip Pass."

### J. Top 5 Fixes for This Persona
1. **Add tokenized guest poll-voting and itinerary viewing from invite links** because Tyler failed at his core loop — getting 12 flaky students past the account+verify wall (`src/types/permissionMatrix.generated.ts:44-51`, `src/pages/JoinTrip.tsx`) — causing group-adoption collapse back to iMessage.
2. **Raise the Free payment-split cap from 3/trip to ~10/trip** because a single spring break (Airbnb, gas, groceries, boat day) exhausts `payment_splitting.free: 3` (`src/billing/entitlements.ts:272-279`) on day 1, causing migration to Splitwise instead of upgrade — the cap monetizes a user with $0 WTP and loses the group.
3. **Suppress upgrade modals during active trip dates** because a paywall interrupt mid-trip is Tyler's stated screenshot-and-quit trigger, causing public churn in the exact group-viral moment; gate via trip date range in `PlusUpsellModal.tsx` display logic.
4. **Fix the mobile background-calendar render storm** (`src/components/mobile/MobileGroupCalendar.tsx:525` duplicate keys + stays mounted on other tabs, R1) because perceived stutter and battery drain on older student phones erodes the "fast and free" positioning that won him over.
5. **Route concierge limit-wall CTA to checkout instead of `/settings`** (`src/components/AIConciergeChat.tsx:52-53`, D2) because even non-payers like Tyler judge the product by coherent dead-ends, and his richer friends (the Priyas) hit this exact wall ready to pay.

### K. Confidence
- **Level:** High for funnel/limit findings (config + screenshots), Medium for behavior.
- **Directly observed:** Demo-first landing (`desktop-01`), polls/concierge/tasks surfaces (`desktop2-03/07/08`), media meter (`mobile2-04`), pricing copy (`mobile-22`), split/AI/trip limits (`entitlements.ts`), R1/R2 performance defects, D15 guest access.
- **Needs real-user validation:** Actual invite-funnel completion rate for college groups; whether 3-split cap drives upgrade or exit; post-trip churn curve.
- **Beta interview question:** "Show me the last group trip chat — at what exact message did planning stall, and what would have had to happen for all 12 people to tap one link and vote?"


---

## Persona 8: Priya Sharma — Consumer / Girls' Luxury Trip Planner

### A. Profile
- **Name:** Priya Sharma
- **Age range:** 30–38
- **Location/timezone:** New York, NY / Eastern (ET)
- **Industry/role:** Brand strategy director at a beauty conglomerate; plans the annual girls' trip like a product launch
- **Tech comfort:** HIGH — lives in Notion, Resy, American Express app, Flighty; judges software like she judges hotels
- **Platform:** iPhone 16 Pro (primary), MacBook for the planning doc
- **Group size:** 6 women, friends since business school
- **Planning style:** Curated. Mood board first, then a shortlist of three destinations with a POV on each, then she "facilitates" the group to the right answer
- **Current tools:** Notion doc with embedded maps, iMessage group, Resy/OpenTable, Google Flights, a travel agent for the big one, Splitwise (reluctantly — "it's ugly")
- **Main pain points:** Her curation lives in Notion where nobody comments; restaurant decisions decided too late for good reservations; the aesthetic chaos of juggling ugly apps
- **Budget sensitivity:** Low for herself, moderate optics with the group. **Clear subscription candidate.**
- **Why adopt Chravel:** A single beautiful surface where her curation IS the trip — places, itinerary, polls — and an AI that does the first-pass research
- **Why reject Chravel:** Visible jank, broken images, mediocre AI recommendations. One rough edge and it's "cute idea, not ready," said in a group chat she influences

### B. Jobs-to-Be-Done
1. When I'm pitching this year's destination, I want my shortlist presented beautifully with places and context, so I can get the group aligned in one session instead of three weeks.
2. When I curate restaurants, I want them saved with my notes next to the itinerary, so I can book the 8 PM table before it's gone.
3. When the group needs to decide, I want an elegant poll inside the trip, so I can drive consensus without seeming like a dictator.
4. When I research, I want the AI to do the first 80% at my taste level, so I can spend my time on the final 20% that makes the trip mine.
5. When I share the plan, I want it to look like a Condé Nast itinerary, so I can maintain the standard the group expects of me.

### C. Screener Answers
| Question | Answer |
|---|---|
| Trips last 12 months | 4+ (girls' trip, two couples' trips, one solo) |
| Typical group size | 5–8 |
| Main tools | Notion, iMessage, Resy, Google Flights, Splitwise |
| Primary device | iOS |
| 45-min call? | Maybe — "send the questions first" |
| Role in group | Primary planner |
| Pro-ops responsibility | Yes, I own logistics |

### D. Full Survey Answers

**About you.** Priya, 34, brand strategy in beauty, Manhattan. I plan our annual girls' trip the way I'd run a launch: positioning, shortlist, decision gates, flawless execution. Last year was Mallorca. This year I'm pushing Kyoto.

**Most recent/next group trip.** Kyoto, October, six of us. Kicked off in January when I dropped three destination one-pagers into the group chat — yes, one-pagers, I make them in Notion. Most frustrating: I produce a beautiful document and the decisions still happen in a 400-message iMessage thread where my embedded map becomes a blue link nobody taps. Went well: my restaurant matrix — every dinner booked 30 days out, zero "where should we eat" moments. Apps: Notion, iMessage, Resy, OpenTable, Google Flights, Flighty, Splitwise, Pinterest for the mood board. Eight, embarrassingly. After the first plan: one drop-out, one budget renegotiation, re-curated the hotel from a riad-style place to one with a pool — the Notion doc went through nine versions.

**Planning workflow.** Mood board (Pinterest) → destination one-pagers (Notion) → group decision (iMessage chaos) → flights individually booked → I take hotels and dinners → shared doc → during the trip I'm the concierge → after, I make the album. Where decisions stick: budget — nobody wants to say a number, so I float tiers. Non-responders: one friend reads everything, answers nothing; I DM her directly. Example doc: my Kyoto Notion has 40 places, each with one-line POV ("go for the yuba, skip the matcha flight").

**Feature areas.**
- *Create/Invite:* The trip card with a cover photo matters more than you'd think — if the trip looks beautiful the group takes it seriously. Crop control on the cover: noted and appreciated.
- *Places:* The closest thing to my Notion system I've seen in a travel app. Base Camp as the hotel anchor with distances — that's how I think ("12 minutes from the hotel" is the only distance metric that matters). I need my one-line POV on every saved place, and I need places to feel curated, not like a Google Maps dump.
- *Calendar/Itinerary:* Day-by-day with places attached is the dream. The PDF Recap idea is genuinely chic if the export is beautiful — if it's a default-font data dump, I'd rather die.
- *Polls/Decisions:* Elegant solution to my dictator problem. "Three hotels, vote by Friday" with the Leading badge doing my lobbying for me.
- *Tasks:* Light use — "book your flight by March 1" assigned to all six.
- *Smart Import:* I'd paste hotel confirmations and the Resy emails. If it builds the itinerary from my inbox, that's hours back.
- *AI Concierge:* The test: "omakase in Kyoto under ¥30,000, counter seats six, somewhere my group chat hasn't already seen on TikTok." If it gives me the three obvious tourist answers, I close the tab forever. I want Tatler-level specificity — names, why, how hard to book.
- *AI Trust:* Broken by generic answers, by recommending a place that closed in 2024, or by it touching my itinerary without asking. The confirm-before-save card is the right instinct.
- *Settings priorities:* Aesthetic control of what the group sees; notification discipline (I do not want six pings when six people vote).

**Money.** I front hotels and dinners; the group settles by Venmo or Zelle within days — my friends are not the chasing type. Splitwise works but offends me visually. Equal split is fine for the villa; dinners are sometimes "whoever didn't drink pays less," so custom splits matter. Plan changes: I announce in iMessage with a one-line rationale. One planner? Me, with a deputy CFO friend who double-checks the math. Hotels/restaurants: I present three options, the group "chooses" — note the quotes. Conversations live in iMessage; my docs live in Notion; the gap between them is exactly where Chravel could live.

**Willingness to pay.** **$15–30/month.** I pay for Notion, Flighty Pro, and three streaming tiers I forgot about. If Chravel replaces the Notion-doc-plus-chaos workflow and the AI actually researches at my level, $19.99 Frequent Chraveler is nothing — unlimited AI plus the polish tier features. I'd start with Explorer at $9.99 and upgrade the first time I hit the AI ceiling mid-curation, which would take approximately one evening.

**Ratings (1–5).**
- Likelihood to use next trip: **4** — Kyoto becomes the pilot; the Notion doc stays as backup, dual-running.
- Clarity: **4** — information architecture is genuinely good; tab strip on mobile is the weak spot.
- Time saved: **4** — Smart Import plus AI first-pass research is hours per trip, if quality holds.
- AI trust: **3** — the confirm-card pattern earns trust; recommendation quality is entirely unproven to me.
- Would invite: **4** — inviting five women with high standards; the app gets exactly one first impression.
- Mobile usability: **3** — gorgeous, but I felt the stutter on the trip pages, and I notice everything.
- Web usability: **5** — the desktop experience is legitimately premium.
- Pricing fit: **4** — Explorer/FC pricing is rational for what it claims; Trip Pass framing is clever.
- Overall sentiment: **4** — the rare travel app whose taste level matches mine; execution gaps are fixable, taste isn't.

**Wrap-up.** Change one thing: notes/POV on saved places — my curation is annotations, not pins. Recommend trigger: one flawless trip where the group says "this was so organized" and I say "I know." Anything else: fix the broken images in the demo; nothing undermines a luxury aesthetic like a gray rectangle where a photo should be. Follow-up: **Yes**, if scheduled efficiently.

### E. Web Flow Walkthrough
- **Discovery/landing:** Dark, gold, confident. The landing being a live product demo signals the team has taste AND nerve — you only demo what you're proud of. [OBSERVED — `desktop-01`] The dark/gold system carries through pricing and auth without drift; as a brand person, the consistency is the tell. [OBSERVED — `desktop-05`, `mobile-22`]
- **How it works:** "Less Chaos, More Coordination" with the accordion — clean hierarchy, restrained. [OBSERVED — `desktop-19`]
- **Signup:** The auth modal is genuinely beautiful — gold CTA, proper spacing, Apple/Google priority. This screen would survive a design crit at my office. [OBSERVED — `desktop-05`]
- **Trip creation:** Cover photo with crop modal = the team understands that trips are objects of desire, not database rows. [OBSERVED — ground truth §4; not live-tested]
- **Feature usage:** Places/Base Camp is my favorite surface — hotel anchored top-left, private personal base camp, directions box. [OBSERVED — `desktop2-06`] Polls are clean, though the poll bars render in blue/orange/green gradients that fight the gold system — a small thing, which is exactly the kind of thing I notice. [OBSERVED — `desktop2-07` bar colors vs. gold accent system] Concierge's suggested prompts are practical but pedestrian ("find 5 great hotels") — the copy should flex taste, not utility. [OBSERVED — `desktop2-03`; rec quality HYPOTHESIS]
- **Pricing reaction:** "Start free. Upgrade when your trip gets serious." — good line; my trips start serious. Explorer→FC ladder maps to my usage; unlimited AI is the FC hook for me. [OBSERVED — `mobile-22`, `entitlements.ts:237-244`]
- **Web positives:** design system coherence, Places architecture, confirm-before-write AI pattern, PDF Recap concept.
- **Web pain points:** The demo threw "Maximum update depth exceeded" loops across consumer-trip tabs (worst on Pinned) — I didn't see a crash, but I saw the hesitation, and hesitation is jank. [OBSERVED — R2, `desktop-harvest2-log.json` steps 3–13] Demo imagery blocked by the app's own CSP — broken/blank images in a product whose pitch is aesthetic control. Unforgivable in a first impression. [OBSERVED — R4, 20 blocked `images.unsplash.com` loads, `desktop-harvest2-log.json`]

### F. Mobile / PWA Flow Walkthrough
- **First impression:** It photographs well, which matters — this app will appear in my group chat as screenshots. [OBSERVED — `mobile2-04`]
- **Navigation clarity:** The horizontal tab strip is the one mass-market compromise — tabs hide off-screen and there's no bottom nav on mobile web. I found everything; two of my friends would not. [OBSERVED — `mobile2-04`; delta non-defect note]
- **Chat/input:** Fine; we'll stay in iMessage, but in-trip chat for logistics keeps the planning artifacts out of our real conversation, which I actually want.
- **Forms/modals:** Consistent with desktop; no drift I could catch from the captures. [OBSERVED — delta L4]
- **Invite link flow:** Preview-then-account. My friends will convert — they're not Tyler's flakes — but five separate email verifications for one trip is beneath the experience tier this app is selling. [OBSERVED flow — ground truth §5; friend conversion HYPOTHESIS]
- **Perceived speed:** Here's my problem. The mobile trip pages run a constantly re-rendering calendar in the background — ~150 duplicate-key warnings per step, nearly 6,000 across the session — and it reads as micro-stutter while browsing. On a 16 Pro. Luxury is the absence of friction; this is friction. [OBSERVED — R1, `MobileGroupCalendar.tsx:525`; component stays mounted across tabs per delta]
- **Thumb reach/tap targets:** Buttons generous, media grid lovely, storage meter legible. [OBSERVED — `mobile2-04`]
- **Mobile positives:** the aesthetic survives the small screen; media hub is genuinely elegant; demo depth on phone.
- **Mobile pain points:** R1 stutter, off-screen tabs, and any broken demo imagery (R4) lands twice as hard on mobile where images ARE the interface.

| Payments | Settle without ugliness | Viewed demo + code | Equal/custom splits, who-owes-whom, Venmo deeplink | Prettier than Splitwise (her bar) | Custom splits ("non-drinkers pay less") essential — present per ground truth | None | [OBSERVED] ground truth §6; custom-split UX [HYPOTHESIS] | 2 | Medium | Low | — |
| Media | The album, beautifully | Viewed mobile demo | Grid + lightbox + filters | Genuinely elegant grid | 500 MB free is one dinner's photos for 6 women | Demo images broken by CSP — gray boxes in a luxury pitch | [OBSERVED] `mobile2-04`; R4 CSP blocks; `entitlements.ts:265` | 3 | High | Medium | Fix CSP allowlist for demo assets; storage upsell here is the natural Explorer trigger |
| Settings/notifications | Quiet, controlled | Code review | Per-trip mute exists (D11); categories | Mute shipped | Six votes = six pings would be gauche | Batching absent per register §10.4 | [OBSERVED] D11; batching gap register §10.4 | 2 | Low | Medium | Digest/batch poll + payment notifications |
| Pricing/upgrade | Rational premium ladder | Viewed pricing | Free→Explorer→FC; Trip Pass one-time; AI limits 10/25/∞ | FC = unlimited AI maps exactly to her usage | Concierge limit-wall CTA routes to /settings, not checkout — fumbles HER exact conversion moment | Broken upgrade path at peak intent | [OBSERVED] D2 `AIConciergeChat.tsx:52-53`, `useConciergeUsage.ts:310-368` | 4 | High | Medium | Limit wall → direct checkout with tier preselected |
| Performance | Zero jank, ever | Harvest evidence | Mobile render storm (R1); desktop setState loops (R2) | Desktop mostly composed | Micro-stutter on her primary device | R1 duplicate keys; R2 max-update-depth ×129 | [OBSERVED] R1 `MobileGroupCalendar.tsx:525`; R2 harvest log | 4 | High | High | Fix R1 keys + unmount; profile and pin R2 before premium push |

### H. Emotional Reaction
- **Impressed by:** The design system's discipline — landing to auth to trip without a single off-brand screen; Base Camp distances; confirm-before-write AI.
- **Confused by:** Why saved places have no notes field; why a luxury-positioned app ships a demo with broken images.
- **Annoyed by:** The mobile stutter she can feel but her friends can't name; poll colors off-palette; the upgrade wall that points at settings instead of taking her money.
- **Would abandon when:** The AI returns the three most obvious tourist restaurants in Kyoto, or a friend screenshots a janky/broken-image moment into the group chat.
- **Would invite others?** Yes — but understand: her invite is an endorsement, and she protects her endorsements. One flawless dry-run first.
- **[SYNTHETIC QUOTE]:** "This is the first travel app that dresses the way I plan — now it has to walk in the heels: no stutter, no gray-box images, and an AI that knows the difference between a recommendation and a search result."

### I. Conversion Scores
- **Activation:** 8/10 — she'll build the Kyoto trip this week as a dual-run with Notion.
- **Invite likelihood:** 7/10 — high, but deliberately staged after personal QA.
- **Day-7 retention:** 7/10 — curation is a daily hobby for her between trips.
- **Paid conversion:** 8/10 — the clearest subscription candidate in this batch; pays for tools that flatter her workflow.
- **NPS-style:** +30 — advocate-in-waiting, contingent on polish.
- **Would they pay?** Yes.
- **What would they pay?** $9.99 Explorer immediately; $19.99 Frequent Chraveler the first evening she hits 25 AI queries mid-curation.
- **Feature creating willingness to pay:** Unlimited AI concierge at her quality bar + beautiful PDF itinerary export + storage for the album.
- **Limit/CTA that triggers upgrade:** The 25-query Explorer AI ceiling during a curation session (10 on Free she'd blow through in an hour).
- **CTA that would annoy them:** The limit-wall that routes to `/settings` — peak intent, fumbled; also any upsell visible to her INVITED friends.

### J. Top 5 Fixes for This Persona
1. **Fix the mobile render storm** (`src/components/mobile/MobileGroupCalendar.tsx:525` duplicate weekday keys; component stays mounted re-rendering across tabs — R1) because Priya perceives micro-stutter as a quality verdict on her primary device, causing the premium segment's silent exit before any paywall is reached.
2. **Fix the demo-image CSP block** (R4 — app CSP refuses `images.unsplash.com`, 20 failed loads) because broken images in the first-impression demo directly contradict the aesthetic positioning that converts this persona, causing "cute idea, not ready" verdicts in high-influence group chats.
3. **Add per-place notes/POV to Places** because Priya failed to map her core curation behavior (annotated shortlists) onto saved places (`desktop2-06` shows no note affordance), causing her to keep the Notion doc — and whoever keeps the doc keeps the workflow.
4. **Route AI limit walls to checkout with tier preselected** (currently `upgradeUrl: '/settings'`, `src/components/AIConciergeChat.tsx:52-53`, D2) because her highest-intent moment — out of queries mid-curation — dead-ends in a settings page, causing lost conversions from the segment with the highest WTP.
5. **Tune the consumer concierge for taste-tier recommendation quality (specificity, freshness, source confidence)** because generic answers are her stated one-strike churn trigger ([HYPOTHESIS — needs live test], `src/features/concierge/`), causing loss of exactly the users who'd pay for unlimited queries.

### K. Confidence
- **Level:** Medium-High.
- **Directly observed:** Design-system coherence across `desktop-01/05/19`, `desktop2-01/03/06/07/08`, `mobile2-04`, `mobile-22`; R1/R2 performance defects; R4 CSP image failures; AI limits and upgrade-URL gap (D2); Places surface lacking note affordance.
- **Needs real-user validation:** AI recommendation quality at the taste tier (the make-or-break); whether her friends convert through invite verification; PDF export aesthetics.
- **Beta interview question:** "Ask the concierge for a restaurant recommendation in a city you know deeply — then tell me the exact moment in its answer where you decided to trust it or dismiss it."

## Persona 9: Mike & Karen Delgado — Consumer / Couples-Group Annual Trip Planners

### A. Profile
- **Name:** Mike & Karen Delgado (they plan as a unit; Karen drives the apps, Mike drives the spreadsheet)
- **Age range:** 45–55
- **Location/timezone:** Phoenix, AZ / Mountain (MST, no DST — "the timezone field actually matters to us")
- **Industry/role:** Mike: commercial insurance broker; Karen: hospital administrator. Co-chairs of the annual four-couples trip (the "Crew Trip," 14 years running)
- **Tech comfort:** MEDIUM — competent with mainstream apps, no patience for hidden gestures
- **Platform:** Mixed — Karen iPhone, Mike Android, planning on a shared iPad and Mike's work laptop
- **Group size:** 8 adults (4 couples)
- **Planning style:** Democratic to a fault. Everything is a group decision; nothing ever gets decided. Mike maintains "the spreadsheet."
- **Current tools:** One giant group text (8 people, 3 platforms, reactions don't sync), email for "official" stuff, Mike's Excel budget, Zelle/Venmo mix, TripAdvisor links
- **Main pain points:** Decision deadlock — where, when, budget tier; one couple always books late; settling money couple-to-couple while every app thinks in individuals
- **Budget sensitivity:** Moderate. Will pay for value but hate subscriptions on principle ("we have enough monthly bills"). **Prefer per-trip.**
- **Why adopt Chravel:** Polls with deadlines could end the six-week destination debate; one place for the plan across iPhone/Android
- **Why reject Chravel:** If money can't be tracked by couple, or if one of the eight can't figure out the app, it becomes the ninth thing Mike maintains

### B. Jobs-to-Be-Done
1. When the four couples start the annual where-to-go debate, I want a vote with a deadline, so I can book the house before the good weeks are gone.
2. When we're picking dates, I want everyone's conflicts visible in one place, so I can stop merging four couples' calendars by text.
3. When I front the house deposit, I want to track who owes what BY COUPLE, so I can send one number to each household instead of arguing over eight.
4. When plans change mid-trip, I want one announcement everyone actually sees, so I can stop the iPhone/Android telephone game.
5. When the trip ends, I want the budget reconciled in days not months, so I can stop being the guy who emails about $63 in October.

### C. Screener Answers
| Question | Answer |
|---|---|
| Trips last 12 months | 2–3 (Crew Trip, one family wedding, a long weekend) |
| Typical group size | 5–8 |
| Main tools | Group text, email, Excel, Zelle/Venmo, TripAdvisor |
| Primary device | Both (iPhone + Android household) |
| 45-min call? | Yes — "Karen will do the talking, I'll do the complaining" |
| Role in group | Co-planner (the two of us share it) |
| Pro-ops responsibility | Shared responsibility |

### D. Full Survey Answers

**About you.** Mike, 52, insurance, and Karen, 49, hospital admin. Phoenix. We've co-run the Crew Trip — four couples, college friends — for fourteen years. Mike has a spreadsheet with fourteen tabs. Karen has opinions about the spreadsheet.

**Most recent/next group trip.** Next: a lake house somewhere, fall 2026 — "somewhere" because we are currently six weeks into deciding between Tahoe, Coeur d'Alene, and the Ozarks. Kicked off at last year's trip dinner — "same time next year!" — then nothing for eight months. Who's involved: all 8, in theory; in practice the Delgados propose and the group disposes... slowly. Most frustrating: decision deadlock. Karen: "We had a 96-message thread about WHICH WEEK. Not which place. Which week." Went well last year: the house itself (booked early for once) and the meal-night rotation. Apps: group text (the big one), email, Excel, Zelle, Venmo, TripAdvisor, one couple insists on a shared Google Doc nobody else edits. Six-ish. After the first plan: the late couple confirmed at the deadline+10 days, which re-opened the bedroom assignments, which re-opened the cost split. Every year.

**Planning workflow.** Idea (at the previous trip) → 8 months of silence → Delgados propose 3 options → 6 weeks of debate → book → Mike builds the budget tab → deposits via Zelle/Venmo → trip → 2 months of settling up. Where decisions stick: where AND when AND budget tier — the trifecta. One couple wants luxury, one wants value, two abstain until it's "whatever you guys think" and then complain. Non-responders: the Hendersons. Every year. We now book refundable and tell them their deadline. Example thread: the WHICH WEEK thread — 96 messages, 4 polls Karen improvised with emoji reactions that don't sync between iPhone and Android, decision finally made on a phone call.

**Feature areas.**
- *Create/Invite:* Eight adults, two platforms — the invite must work identically on iPhone and Android. Web app actually helps us there.
- *Places:* The house as Base Camp with driving distances — Mike: "that's the first thing I compute manually every year, restaurants within 20 minutes of the house."
- *Calendar/Itinerary:* Meal-night rotation and the boat reservation. Medium use.
- *Polls/Decisions:* THE feature. Karen: "A poll with a real deadline that CLOSES is the marriage counselor this group needs." Destination poll, week poll, budget-tier poll — that's our entire bottleneck, instrumented.
- *Tasks:* "Hendersons: confirm by June 1" as an assigned task with a due date is passive-aggressive perfection.
- *Smart Import:* The VRBO confirmation email. If the house, dates, and cancellation deadline land in the trip automatically, Mike retires a spreadsheet tab.
- *AI Concierge:* "Restaurants within 20 minutes of the house that take a party of 8" and "what's the cancellation deadline again?" Practical questions, not inspiration.
- *AI Trust:* Broken if it answers about the wrong trip or invents a reservation detail. Mike: "I verify everything against the confirmation email anyway. I'm in insurance."
- *Settings priorities:* Notifications that respect that 8 adults have jobs — digest, not drip.

**Money.** The core issue. We operate in COUPLES. The house splits four ways, not eight. Dinners split by couple. Mike fronts the deposit; each couple Zelles him a quarter. Every expense app wants to split by individual and we end up with Karen-owes and Mike-owes as separate line items for the same household — it doubles the bookkeeping. Reimbursement discussion: civil but eternal; the October "$63 email" is a running joke. Plan changes: Karen posts in the group text AND emails "official" changes; one platform always garbles it. One planner? One planner-COUPLE. Hotels: we propose 3, group votes (slowly). Restaurants: decided day-of, badly. Conversations live in the group text, which Android-vs-iPhone makes worse — a neutral web app is genuinely appealing.

**Willingness to pay.** **Per-trip.** Mike: "I will not add a monthly line item for an annual trip. But $39.99 once, for the trip window, split four ways? That's ten bucks a couple — less than one round of drinks, and I'd expense the chaos it removes." The Trip Pass is the first pricing we've seen that matches how normal adults take trips. A subscription would need us traveling 4+ times a year, which we don't.

**Ratings (1–5).**
- Likelihood to use next trip: **4** — polls alone justify the pilot; this year's destination vote happens in Chravel.
- Clarity: **3** — desktop clear; mobile tab strip lost Mike twice ("where did Payments go?" — off-screen right).
- Time saved: **4** — six weeks of deadlock compressed to two poll deadlines is the whole pitch.
- AI trust: **3** — fine for restaurant lookups; verify anything contractual.
- Would invite: **4** — the other three couples, with a Karen-authored "how to join" text.
- Mobile usability: **3** — works on both platforms (the point), but top tab strip + occasional stutter on Karen's iPhone.
- Web usability: **4** — the iPad/laptop experience is where we'd actually plan.
- Pricing fit: **3** — Trip Pass concept: great. But the $39.99 pass is Explorer-tier, and Explorer still caps splits at 10/trip — a 9-day, 8-person trip logs 25+ expenses. The pass that fits our trip cadence doesn't fit our trip SIZE.
- Overall sentiment: **3.5 → call it 4** — Karen: "first app that's shaped like our actual problem." Mike: "the money model thinks in individuals; we're four households."

**Wrap-up.** Change one thing: split by couple/household, not just by person. Recommend trigger: the destination poll closing on time WITHOUT a phone call. Anything else: Mike keeps the spreadsheet for one more year regardless ("trust, then verify, then retire the tab"). Follow-up: **Yes.**

### E. Web Flow Walkthrough
- **Discovery/landing:** The demo dashboard with sample trips made it concrete immediately — Karen: "it's a group chat with a filing system, got it." The 'For Friend & Family trips' line covers us. [OBSERVED — `desktop-01`] The dozen-apps section is literally our stack. [OBSERVED — `desktop-19`]
- **Signup:** Clean; Google button works for both of us. Eight adults will manage, with one "how to join" text from Karen. [OBSERVED — `desktop-05`; group completion SIMULATED RISK]
- **Trip creation:** Title/dates/timezone — and we noticed the timezone field with approval (Arizona doesn't do DST; calendar apps burn us annually). [OBSERVED — ground truth §4]
- **Feature usage:** Polls are exactly as hoped — counts, percentages, the "Leading" badge applying gentle public pressure, and auto-close exists in the poll config. Karen wants to frame this screen. [OBSERVED — `desktop2-07`; auto-close per ground truth §6] Places with the house as Base Camp + Get Directions = Mike's manual distance math, automated. [OBSERVED — `desktop2-06`] Tasks with due dates handles the Hendersons. [OBSERVED — `desktop2-08`]
- **Pricing reaction:** "Start free. Upgrade when your trip gets serious" — fine. The Trip Pass ($39.99/45d Explorer) is the first travel-app pricing that matches annual-trip reality. But: Explorer caps payment splits at 10/trip and our trip logs 25+ shared expenses — the pass priced for us doesn't cover our usage; the $74.99 FC pass does, at nearly double. [OBSERVED — `mobile-22`; `entitlements.ts:272-279`; Trip Pass tiers per spec/ground truth §7]
- **Web positives:** polls, base camp distances, platform-neutral (the Android/iPhone wall finally irrelevant), timezone-aware trips, who-owes-whom summary.
- **Web pain points:** per-person-only split math (next section); desktop demo showed setState loops on tab interaction per the harvest log — felt like occasional hesitation, tolerable but noticed. [OBSERVED — R2, `desktop-harvest2-log.json`]

### F. Mobile / PWA Flow Walkthrough
- **First impression:** Dark and fancy — Karen likes it; Mike turned the brightness up. Readable for late-40s eyes, mostly, though gray-on-black secondary text is borderline. [OBSERVED palette — `mobile2-04`; readability SIMULATED RISK]
- **Navigation clarity:** The top tab strip scrolls horizontally and several tabs sit off-screen — Mike genuinely lost Payments on first pass. No bottom nav on mobile web. For medium-tech 50-somethings, off-screen tabs are invisible tabs. [OBSERVED — `mobile2-04`; delta non-defect note]
- **Chat/input:** Fine. The red URGENT broadcast style is perfect for "boat leaves at 10, not 10:15." [OBSERVED — `desktop2-01` equivalent]
- **Forms/modals:** Workable on both phones; the shared iPad is our real planning surface anyway.
- **Invite link flow:** Preview then account creation. Six of eight will sail through; the Hendersons will need the Karen text. Acceptable — for adults, unlike Gloria's elders. [OBSERVED flow — ground truth §5; completion HYPOTHESIS]
- **Perceived speed:** Karen's iPhone showed intermittent stutter on trip pages — the background-calendar re-render issue is real and registered even with medium-tech users as "it hiccups." [OBSERVED — R1, `MobileGroupCalendar.tsx:525`]
- **Thumb reach/tap targets:** Generous buttons, clear storage meter. [OBSERVED — `mobile2-04`]
- **Mobile positives:** identical app both platforms (the headline for us); media meter in plain numbers; payments visible on phone where the money conversation happens.
- **Mobile pain points:** off-screen tabs, R1 stutter, dark-theme contrast for older eyes.

### H. Emotional Reaction
- **Impressed by:** Polls with deadlines (Karen audibly said "finally"), the house-as-Base-Camp distances, and a pricing model — Trip Pass — that respects people who take one big trip a year.
- **Confused by:** Where the off-screen mobile tabs went; why an app this group-oriented thinks money in individuals; "Base Camp."
- **Annoyed by:** The prospect of explaining to the group why the expense report shows Karen and Mike as separate debtors for the same household; the iPhone hiccups.
- **Would abandon when:** The first settlement round produces MORE confusion than Mike's spreadsheet — money is the trust moment; fumble it once and Excel wins forever.
- **Would invite others?** Yes — the other three couples this season, with Karen running onboarding like the hospital trains nurses: one text, three steps, no improvising.
- **[SYNTHETIC QUOTE]:** "Fourteen years we've argued for six weeks about where to go. A poll with a deadline fixes my marriage's group chat — now fix the math so my wife and I are one wallet, the way we've been since 1999."

### I. Conversion Scores
- **Activation:** 7/10 — they'll pilot the destination poll this season; real activation is all 8 joined.
- **Invite likelihood:** 6/10 — definite but managed; one couple needs hand-holding.
- **Day-7 retention:** 6/10 — strong in planning season, dormant the other 8 months (that's the cadence, not churn).
- **Paid conversion:** 6/10 — Trip Pass is genuinely attractive; the split-cap mismatch and couple-math gap are the two blockers.
- **NPS-style:** +10 — warm, conditional on the money experience.
- **Would they pay?** Yes — once per trip.
- **What would they pay?** $39.99 Trip Pass split across four couples ("$10 a couple"); $74.99 only grudgingly if the split cap forces it.
- **Feature creating willingness to pay:** Polls-with-deadline + frictionless couple-based settlement (the second doesn't exist yet).
- **Limit/CTA that triggers upgrade:** 10-split Explorer cap mid-trip — though it risks triggering "back to Excel" instead of the FC pass.
- **CTA that would annoy them:** Monthly subscription nudges ("we have enough monthly bills"); any upsell while a poll is open.

### J. Top 5 Fixes for This Persona
1. **Add household/couple grouping to payment splits** because the Delgados' core money model — four couples, not eight individuals — has no representation in the data model (`splitParticipants: string[]` in `src/components/payments/PaymentInput.tsx:32-33`; equal per-person division at `src/hooks/usePaymentSplits.ts:63`), causing double bookkeeping and a fallback to Mike's Excel at the exact trust moment.
2. **Uncap (or raise to 25+) payment splits on Trip Passes** because the $39.99 Explorer-tier pass — the SKU built for this persona — carries Explorer's 10-split cap (`src/billing/entitlements.ts:272-279`) that a 9-day 8-person trip exhausts mid-week, causing either a resentful $74.99 upsell or abandonment of payment tracking.
3. **Add guest poll-voting from invite tokens** because the Delgados' first-value moment is the destination poll, which currently requires all 8 adults to complete account+verification first (`permissionMatrix.generated.ts:44-51`, D15), causing the killer feature to arrive after the adoption hurdle instead of before it.
4. **Make the mobile in-trip tab strip discoverable (scroll affordance/overflow indicator or bottom nav)** because Mike lost the Payments tab off-screen right on first use (`mobile2-04`; delta non-defect note), causing medium-tech users to believe features don't exist.
5. **Offer a 60–90 day window on the entry Trip Pass** because annual-trip planning starts 8+ weeks out and the 45-day Explorer pass forces buying either too late to plan or too early to cover the trip, causing the best-fit SKU to misfit its best-fit customer (pricing per ground truth §7).

### K. Confidence
- **Level:** High on the payments-model findings (code-verified), Medium on adoption behavior.
- **Directly observed:** Per-person-only split architecture (`usePaymentSplits.ts:63`, `PaymentInput.tsx:32-33`, `paymentService.ts:490-491`); split caps per tier; polls/places/tasks surfaces (`desktop2-06/07/08`); Trip Pass pricing and reachability (D4); mobile tab strip (`mobile2-04`); R1/R2 performance notes.
- **Needs real-user validation:** Whether couple-workaround splits (one spouse per couple) cause real confusion or are fine in practice; group completion rate across 8 mixed-platform adults; whether poll deadlines actually end deadlock or just relocate it.
- **Beta interview question:** "Open your last trip's expense record — walk me through how you'd want $2,400 of house, gas, and grocery costs to appear if the app understood 'couples,' and where last year's process actually broke."

## Persona 10: Sam Rivera — Consumer / Solo Organizer ("Planner Martyr")

### A. Profile
- **Name:** Sam Rivera
- **Age range:** 29–36
- **Location/timezone:** Seattle, WA / Pacific (PT)
- **Industry/role:** Senior product operations manager at a logistics SaaS company; the friend who plans EVERYTHING — ski weekends, bachelor parties, the annual cabin trip, his sister's birthday in Palm Springs
- **Tech comfort:** HIGH — power user; keyboard shortcuts, automations, three task managers evaluated per year
- **Platform:** iPhone + desktop (genuinely both; plans at a desk, executes from a phone)
- **Group size:** 5–10 friends depending on the trip; 3–4 trips in flight at any time
- **Planning style:** Systematic and resentful. Builds the perfect plan, then spends 80% of the effort chasing humans to acknowledge it.
- **Current tools:** Notion (the trip doc), iMessage, Partiful for invites, Splitwise, Google Sheets flight tracker, TripIt for his own bookings, Reminders app for nag schedules
- **Main pain points:** Chasing people. "Did you book your flight?" ×7. No way to know who's even SEEN the plan. He is the single point of failure for every trip in his friend group.
- **Budget sensitivity:** Low — pays for 9 SaaS tools personally; expects software to earn it
- **Why adopt Chravel:** Tasks with assignment and automatic nagging would outsource the worst part of his life; AI for grunt-work research; one home for 4 concurrent trips
- **Why reject Chravel:** If his friends won't join, he's just maintaining the plan in one more app — the tool is only as good as its weakest adopter

### B. Jobs-to-Be-Done
1. When I assign "book your flight by Friday" to a friend, I want the app to remind THEM automatically, so I can stop being the human cron job of my friend group.
2. When I publish the itinerary, I want to see who has actually looked at it, so I can chase only the people who genuinely haven't engaged.
3. When I'm running four trips at once, I want them in one dashboard with separate everything, so I can context-switch without dropping balls.
4. When I need the boring research done (transfer times, rental car options, group dinner availability), I want the AI to produce a first draft, so I can spend my effort on judgment, not lookup.
5. When the group needs to decide, I want a poll that closes itself, so the decision happens even when I'm not pushing it.
6. When a friend joins my trip, I want the join to take under a minute, so my system doesn't die at the adoption step like the last three tools did.

### D. Full Survey Answers

**About you.** Sam, 32, product ops in Seattle. In my friend group I am the infrastructure. Six trips last year, planned all six, was thanked for two. I'm not bitter, I'm SYSTEMATIZED about being bitter.

**Most recent/next group trip.** Next: Whistler cabin in January, 8 people. Also currently in flight: a bachelor party (Nashville, 10 guys), my sister's Palm Springs birthday (6), and a maybe-Japan trip (4). That's four concurrent trips, which matters later. Kicked off: I posted three cabin options with a price-per-head breakdown — I always arrive with options, never questions. Most frustrating: I assigned everyone ONE task — book your own flight — and then sent 11 individual "did you book?" texts over three weeks. Eleven. I counted, because of course I track my nags in Reminders. Went well: the trip itself runs flawlessly because of the spreadsheet nobody reads. Apps: Notion, iMessage, Partiful, Splitwise, TripIt, Sheets, Reminders — 7, plus Google Maps lists. After the first plan: two flight changes, one drop-out, and the room assignment redo, all absorbed by me, silently, like a load balancer.

**Planning workflow.** Idea → I produce a Notion doc with options → group "discusses" (reacts with emojis, decides nothing) → I force a decision → I book the shared stuff → I assign individual bookings → THE CHASING (3 weeks, 80% of total effort) → trip executes off my doc → I do the Splitwise reconciliation → nobody opens the doc again. Where decisions stick: they don't stick, they STALL — any decision requiring 8 humans to express a preference. Non-responders: tracked in a literal spreadsheet column called "nagged (n)". Example: my Whistler doc has a tab named "WHO STILL HASN'T BOOKED" in red.

**Feature areas.**
- *Create/Invite:* Speed matters less than my friends' completion rate. Partiful wins my invites today because nobody needs an account to RSVP. That's the bar.
- *Places:* Saved spots with distances from the cabin — useful, replaces my Google Maps list.
- *Calendar/Itinerary:* My Notion doc, structured. If Smart Import builds it from confirmation emails, even better.
- *Polls/Decisions:* Auto-close is the feature. Decisions should have deadlines that execute themselves.
- *Tasks:* THE feature. Multi-assign, due dates, an overdue filter — I saw the bones of my dream. But the dream is: I assign "book flight," and the APP nags them at T-7, T-3, T-1, escalating tone, while I sleep. If I still have to do the reminding manually, it's just my Reminders app with extra steps.
- *Smart Import:* Everything. Airbnb confirmations, flight emails, the lift-ticket PDF, OpenTable confirmations. I'd forward my whole trip inbox at it.
- *AI Concierge:* "Compare rental car vs two Ubers for 8 people Whistler weekend," "restaurants near base camp that take 10 on a Saturday," "build a day-by-day skeleton from our calendar." Grunt work. I keep the judgment.
- *AI Trust:* Broken by confidently wrong logistics (a closed restaurant, wrong transfer time). Repaired by citations and the confirm-before-write card — which is the correct pattern, full credit.
- *Settings priorities:* Granular notification control per trip (I have FOUR), and visibility into what my members have/haven't seen.

**Money.** I front everything shared, Splitwise the rest. Venmo deeplink settle is correct — don't build a wallet. Reimbursement discussion: my group is good about money, terrible about ACTIONS; money isn't my pain, acknowledgment is. Plan changes: announced in iMessage, written into Notion, and still someone shows up not knowing. Is there one planner: there is ONLY one planner, hi. Hotels/restaurants: I propose, they emoji, I decide. Conversations live in iMessage; the SYSTEM lives wherever I maintain it — the question is whether Chravel can become the system of record my friends actually open.

**Willingness to pay.** **$15–30/month.** I pay for Notion, TripIt Pro, and Superhuman; I am exactly the demographic. Frequent Chraveler at $19.99 is priced for me almost insultingly precisely: I run 4+ concurrent trips (Free caps at 3 active — I hit that wall in week one), and unlimited AI queries matter because grunt-work research is exactly what I'd hammer. I'd pay TODAY if — and this is the entire deal — my friends join from a link without friction. I'm not paying $240/year to be alone in a nicer Notion.

**Ratings (1–5).**
- Likelihood to use next trip: **5** — Whistler gets piloted this month; I migrate fast when tools deserve it.
- Clarity: **4** — strong IA; I found everything; minor mobile tab-overflow quibble.
- Time saved: **5** — IF task nagging is automatic; 4 without it; the delta IS the product for me.
- AI trust: **4** — confirm-before-write earns real trust; quality TBD.
- Would invite: **5** — inviting is literally the use case.
- Mobile usability: **4** — good, with perceptible trip-page stutter that I'd file a bug about.
- Web usability: **5** — desktop is excellent, and I plan at a desk.
- Pricing fit: **4** — FC is correctly priced for me; the 3-trip free cap is an aggressive but fair trigger.
- Overall sentiment: **5** — first consumer travel tool that takes the ORGANIZER seriously.

**Wrap-up.** Change one thing: automatic task reminders with escalation — the app should chase, not me. Recommend trigger: the first trip where I send zero "did you book?" texts. Anything else: add "seen by" on itinerary/announcements; read receipts on plans would end 50% of my chasing. Follow-up: **Yes** — "I'll bring a doc."

### E. Web Flow Walkthrough
- **Discovery/landing:** Demo-as-landing is exactly how I evaluate tools — I had the full feature map in two minutes without an email gate. Respect. [OBSERVED — `desktop-01`] The "dozen apps" section lists my literal stack. [OBSERVED — `desktop-19`]
- **Signup:** OAuth-first, clean. For ME, frictionless. For my friends, the account+verify wall before any trip access is the same disease that killed my last two tool migrations — guests have zero resource access until full membership. [OBSERVED — `desktop-05`; D15 `permissionMatrix.generated.ts:44-51`]
- **Trip creation:** Fast enough; I'd create four trips immediately — and hit the Free cap at three (`trip_creation.free: 3`), which honestly is a well-placed paywall: it catches exactly the power users like me. [OBSERVED — `entitlements.ts:245-252`]
- **Feature usage:** Tasks: filters (All/Open/Completed), due dates, sort — solid skeleton, and `task_assigned` notifications exist in the service layer. But I searched the codebase pattern for due-date reminders and found no `task_due`/reminder type — assignment pings once at creation; nobody chases the overdue. The hardest 80% of my job remains manual. [OBSERVED — `desktop2-08`; `notificationService.ts:572-578` has task_assigned; no due-date reminder type found in `src/components/todo/` or notification types] Concierge: suggested prompts are my actual queries ("find 5 hotels near base camp," "what's on our calendar"), group-aware, confirm-before-write. [OBSERVED — `desktop2-03`] Polls auto-close: decision infrastructure, finally. [OBSERVED — `desktop2-07`; ground truth §6]
- **Pricing reaction:** FC $19.99 = unlimited trips + unlimited AI + (nominally) voice. Correctly priced for me. One asterisk: the "voice concierge" entitlement currently means dictation-only — the realtime path is disabled product-wide. Sell me what exists; I read changelogs. [OBSERVED — `mobile-22`; D8 `voiceProductPath.ts:1`]
- **Web positives:** demo-first evaluation, tasks/polls/concierge architecture, PDF Recap for the post-trip artifact, 3-trip cap as honest upgrade trigger.
- **Web pain points:** no automated task chasing; no plan-level read receipts; the desktop demo's "Maximum update depth exceeded" loops on tab interaction (129 across the walk) — as a product ops person, an uncaught render loop in the demo is a tell about QA maturity. [OBSERVED — R2, `desktop-harvest2-log.json` steps 3–13]

### F. Mobile / PWA Flow Walkthrough
- **First impression:** Premium, fast-feeling, real app energy in Safari. [OBSERVED — `mobile2-04`]
- **Navigation clarity:** Horizontal top tab strip with overflow off-screen; no bottom nav on mobile web. I'm fine; my groups' least-engaged member — the exact person I need to reach — is not. [OBSERVED — `mobile2-04`; delta non-defect note]

My adoption math: 8 invitees × ~80% per-step completion = I'm chasing two people about SIGNUP before I can chase them about flights. [OBSERVED flow — ground truth §5; completion math SIMULATED RISK]

- **Mobile pain points:** R1 jank, off-screen tabs for low-engagement members, invite funnel length.
