### H. Emotional Reaction
- **Impressed by:** The whole organizer toolkit existing in one place — tasks with assignment, polls that close themselves, group-aware AI with a confirm card, per-trip mute. Someone on this team has BEEN the planner.
- **Confused by:** Why tasks ping once at assignment and then go silent forever — the overdue filter shows me the fire but hands me no extinguisher.
- **Annoyed by:** The invite funnel being three steps longer than Partiful; the demo's render-loop console noise; "voice concierge" meaning dictation.
- **Would abandon when:** Two of eight friends stall at signup — the moment the tool needs ME to chase people INTO it, it has reproduced my problem with extra steps.
- **Would invite others?** Emphatically yes — inviting IS the product for him. He will personally walk all 8 through it once. Only once.
- **[SYNTHETIC QUOTE]:** "I sent eleven 'did you book your flight?' texts last trip. Eleven. Build the version where the app sends them and I'll pay the $19.99 before you finish the sentence — but if my friends can't get in from one link, I'm just lonely in a prettier Notion."

### I. Conversion Scores
- **Activation:** 9/10 — creates trips day one; activation is instant for him personally.
- **Invite likelihood:** 8/10 — guaranteed attempts; the funnel decides the outcome.
- **Day-7 retention:** 8/10 — four concurrent trips = daily organizer sessions.
- **Paid conversion:** 9/10 — highest in batch; FC is shaped exactly like his life, and the 3-trip cap finds him in week one.
- **NPS-style:** +40 — enthusiastic with surgical complaints.
- **Would they pay?** Yes.
- **What would they pay?** $19.99/mo Frequent Chraveler (annual $199 if the Whistler pilot succeeds).
- **Feature creating willingness to pay:** Unlimited active trips + unlimited AI; would pay MORE for automated task chasing — the feature that doesn't exist yet.
- **Limit/CTA that triggers upgrade:** The 4th active trip against `trip_creation.free: 3` — clean, legitimate, immediate.
- **CTA that would annoy them:** Overselling ("voice concierge" = dictation); any upsell shown to his invited friends.

### J. Top 5 Fixes for This Persona
1. **Build automated task reminders with escalation (T-7/T-3/T-1, overdue pings to the assignee)** because Sam's defining pain — manual chasing — survives intact: `task_assigned` fires once at creation (`src/services/notificationService.ts:572-578`) and no due-date reminder type exists in the notification enum (`src/lib/notifications/contentBuilder.ts:23`) or `src/components/todo/`, causing the product to miss its single highest-WTP feature for this persona.
2. **Add no-account guest access (view itinerary, RSVP, vote) from invite links** because Sam's adoption math dies at the account+verify wall (`src/types/permissionMatrix.generated.ts:44-51`, D15) where Partiful — his current bar — needs no account, causing tool migration failure regardless of his own enthusiasm.
3. **Add "seen by" indicators on broadcasts and itinerary updates** because Sam cannot distinguish friends-who-saw from friends-who-ghosted (no seen-by surface in `desktop2-01` chat or itinerary views), causing him to over-nag the innocent and under-nag the guilty — read-receipt infra already exists in chat per ground truth §10.
4. **Surface non-voters on polls with a one-tap nudge** because auto-close (the feature he loves, `desktop2-07`) currently closes on whoever showed up, causing decisions that re-litigate when the silent third complains — "Hasn't voted: ..." converts his chasing into one tap.
5. **Route the 4th-trip and AI limit walls directly to FC checkout** because his conversion moments are precisely located (`trip_creation.free: 3` at `entitlements.ts:245-252`; concierge wall still routes to `/settings` per D2 `AIConciergeChat.tsx:52-53`), causing the cleanest paid conversion in the consumer segment to depend on him navigating to billing manually.

### K. Confidence
- **Level:** High.
- **Directly observed:** Tasks/polls/concierge surfaces (`desktop2-03/07/08`), task-notification architecture and the missing reminder type (code-verified), trip/AI caps (`entitlements.ts`), guest zero-access (D15), dictation-only voice (D8), R1/R2 performance defects, invite flow structure (ground truth §5).
- **Needs real-user validation:** Whether automated reminders actually change assignee behavior (vs. being ignored like his texts); real invite-funnel completion for 30-something friend groups; whether he'd sustain FC after trip season ends.
- **Beta interview question:** "Pull up your reminders or sent texts from your last trip — how many nags did you send, to whom, and which single one would you most want the app to have sent for you?"

## Persona 11: Dan Kowalski — Pro / NFL Team Travel Logistics Coordinator

### A. Profile
- **Name:** Dan Kowalski
- **Age range:** 45–55
- **Location/timezone:** Philadelphia, PA (ET)
- **Industry/role:** NFL franchise — Director of Team Travel & Logistics; 22 years in pro sports ops
- **Tech comfort:** High on ops tooling (TMC portals, charter manifest systems, Excel macros), skeptical of consumer apps
- **Platform:** Desktop-first (two monitors at the facility) + iPhone on game weekends
- **Group size:** ~180-person traveling party (53-man roster + practice squad, coaches, training, equipment, video, PR, security, front office)
- **Planning style:** Military-grade advance work — charter manifests locked T-72h, TSA known-crewmember coordination, hotel contracts negotiated annually, per-diem distribution per CBA rules
- **Current tools:** Excel (manifest master), Outlook, TripSource/TMC portal, charter operator portal, team app (custom), DocuSign for hotel contracts, printed itinerary books
- **Main pain points:** Last-minute manifest changes (injury moves, practice-squad elevations), per-diem reconciliation across union rules, communicating gate/bus/lobby changes to 180 people who don't read email
- **Budget sensitivity:** Low at the price level, HIGH at the procurement level — anything touching team data goes through legal, security review, and an MSA
- **Why adopt Chravel:** Broadcasts + role channels + roster in one place could replace the "text-tree" chaos on travel days
- **Why reject Chravel:** Real Pro trips ship with zero structured ops data (roster/rooms/schedule/per-diem/settlement all empty arrays); no SSO, no audit logs, no DPA — a non-starter for an NFL club today

### B. Jobs-to-Be-Done
1. When I am building the charter manifest for an away game, I want one source of truth for the 180-person party with roles and seat/room assignments, so I can stop reconciling four spreadsheets at midnight.
2. When the gate or bus time changes on a travel day, I want to broadcast to the whole party — and to position groups separately — so I can prove everyone was notified.
3. When the league or the union asks for per-diem records, I want exportable, auditable distribution logs, so I can answer in hours not weeks.
4. When a practice-squad player is elevated Saturday at 4pm, I want to update the manifest, rooming list, and per-diem in one motion, so nothing falls through.
5. When legal asks who can see player medical and travel data, I want role-based access with an audit trail, so I can pass our security review.
6. When I evaluate any new vendor, I want SSO, a DPA, and procurement-grade invoicing, so the deal can actually close.

### C. Screener Answers
| Question | Answer |
|---|---|
| Trips last 12 months | 4+ (10 away games + preseason + international game) |
| Typical group size | 16+ (180-person traveling party) |
| Main tools | Excel, Outlook, TMC portal, charter operator portal, DocuSign |
| Primary device | Desktop-first |
| 45-min call? | Yes — if you bring product and security people |
| Role in group | Primary planner |
| Pro-ops responsibility | Yes, I own logistics |

### D. Full Survey Answers

**About you.** Dan Kowalski, Philadelphia. I run team travel for an NFL club. Charter air, hotels, buses, security, per-diem, TSA coordination for 180 people, ten-plus times a season. I've done this for two decades. My tolerance for software that "almost works" is zero, because my failure mode is a Pro Bowler standing at the wrong gate.

**Most recent/next group trip.** Next one is a Week 1 away game. Kicked off the moment the schedule dropped in May — hotel contracts were actually signed last winter. Involved: me, my coordinator, the TMC, charter operator, hotel CSM, equipment manager, security director. Most frustrating: Saturday roster moves blowing up the manifest and rooming list after the hotel's cutoff. What went well: our charter operator's portal handles the manifest changes cleanly. Apps used: Excel, Outlook, charter portal, TMC portal, the team's internal app for player comms, group texts for the stuff that can't wait. Call it 6–7 systems. After first plan: the plan is never done — it's a living manifest until wheels-up.

**Planning workflow.** Idea→booked is annual: contracts in winter, schedules in May, advance packets per game two weeks out. During: travel-day command via text trees and bus captains. Post: per-diem reconciliation and invoice audit. Decisions stick in email chains with the TMC. Non-responders: players don't read anything — position coaches chase them. Example doc: the "travel grid," a 14-tab Excel workbook that I am honestly embarrassed still runs an NFL operation.

**Feature areas.**
- *Create/Invite:* Fine for a club staffer to set up. The "Require approval to join" toggle and max-uses on invite links is the right instinct [OBSERVED — desktop2-11 per evidence log L3]. But 180 invites need bulk roster import from a CSV, not link-sharing.
- *Places:* Marginal for us — we go stadium, hotel, airport. Basecamp-as-hotel could anchor bus timing, mildly useful.
- *Calendar/Itinerary:* The demo's day-sheet style schedule is what travel day looks like [OBSERVED — desktop-08 demo data]. But I created the equivalent of a real Pro trip in my head and the schedule is an empty array — `roster: []`, `roomAssignments: []`, `schedule: []`, `perDiem` zeroed [OBSERVED — src/utils/tripConverter.ts:118-130, evidence-delta D7].
- *Polls/Decisions:* Not how an NFL travel party works. Nobody votes on the bus time.
- *Tasks:* Could track advance checklists. My Excel does this fine.
- *Smart Import (what I'd paste):* Charter manifests (PDF), hotel rooming list exports (CSV), TSA crew docs. If it parsed a 180-row manifest reliably I'd pay attention [HYPOTHESIS — parse quality on operational PDFs untested; Smart Import replay idempotency only partially tested per ground truth §10.8 — duplicate rows in a manifest is a fireable offense].
- *AI Concierge (what I'd ask):* "Who hasn't been assigned a room for Sunday?" "Which players are on the early bus?" Cross-referencing questions. Not restaurant recs.
- *AI Trust (what breaks it):* One wrong answer about a manifest. Also: AI that writes to the itinerary without an approval chain. The pending-action confirm card is the right idea [OBSERVED — ground truth §6].
- *Settings priorities:* Role-based permissions, audit logs, SSO/SAML, data retention controls, DPA. I see roles [OBSERVED — desktop-09 Create Role/Manage Roles], but no audit log surface anywhere I looked [SIMULATED RISK].

**Pro/Events branch.** Professional-grade means: it works at 5am in a hotel ballroom with 180 people and no Wi-Fi, every change is logged, access is provisioned through our identity provider, and there's a phone number to call when it breaks. Control vs automation: control, always — automation proposes, a human commits. What creates trust: SOC 2 report, a DPA, named account rep, references from another club, and real data in the product — the demo's 57-member Beyoncé roster with role chips and an org chart is genuinely the right shape [OBSERVED — desktop-09, desktop2-18], but when I learned real trips start from empty arrays with per-diem/settlement/medical/compliance stubbed [OBSERVED — tripConverter.ts:118-130], the conversation ended. You showed me a furnished model home and the real house has no plumbing.

**Money.** We don't split expenses — the club pays, players get per-diem cash/cards per CBA. The Payments tab's "You Owe / You Are Owed" framing is consumer-shaped, not club-shaped [OBSERVED — desktop2-14]. Reimbursement discussion: handled by accounting against receipts. Plan changes: broadcast + bus captains + position coaches. One planner? Yes — me, with one deputy. Hotels/restaurants: I decide hotels off contract; players' dinner is their business. Conversations live in email (record) and texts (speed).

**Willingness to pay.** Team plan (Enterprise, custom). Pricing isn't the issue — $99/mo is a rounding error against one charter. The issue is there's nothing behind the Pro tier for my use case yet, and the trial CTA is a `mailto:` link [OBSERVED — src/components/conversion/PricingSection.tsx:140,158,173], which tells me the Pro motion isn't built either. I'd never self-serve anyway; procurement runs the paper.

**Ratings (1–5).**
- Likelihood to use on next trip: **1** — empty ops surfaces on real trips; can't run a season on it.
- Clarity: **4** — demo communicates the vision extremely well.
- Time saved: **1** — today it would add a system without removing one.
- AI trust: **2** — confirm-card pattern is right; no audit trail behind it.
- Would invite others: **2** — I'd show a colleague the demo as "watch this space."
- Mobile usability: **3** — clean chat on iPhone [OBSERVED — mobile-08]; I live on desktop.
- Web usability: **4** — the Pro layout with tabs + roster header is well organized [OBSERVED — desktop-08].
- Pricing fit: **2** — tiers exist, but Enterprise (the only tier with compliance/approvals) is a mailto.
- NPS-style sentiment: **2** — low-neutral. Call me when it's real.

**Wrap-up.** Change one thing: make a real Pro trip able to hold a roster, rooming list, and schedule — imported from CSV — instead of empty arrays. Recommend when: SSO + audit logs + DPA + manifest import exist and another team vouches. Anything else: the demo is the best sales deck you have; just stop letting it write checks the product can't cash. Follow-up: Yes — with product and security folks on the call.

### E. Web Flow Walkthrough
- **Discovery/landing:** "The Group Chat Travel App ... Team Travel, Touring Crews" — the headline names my category, which is rare [OBSERVED — evidence log L1, desktop-01]. The interactive demo-dashboard hero is more convincing than screenshots.
- **Signup/onboarding:** Auth renders email + Google/Apple [OBSERVED — desktop-04/05]. No SSO/SAML option anywhere — immediate enterprise red flag [OBSERVED — absence on auth surfaces; SIMULATED RISK for procurement].
- **Pro trip exploration:** The Beyoncé touring demo is impressive: 57-member header, role chips (Artists, Performers, Tour Manager, Crew), Invite/PDF Recap/Leave Trip actions [OBSERVED — desktop-08]. Team tab: Create Role, Manage Roles, Requests, Grid/Org Chart toggle, role-count filter chips, dietary flags on cards — that's a real roster concept [OBSERVED — desktop-09]. Then the tell: the Team tab title says "Tour Crew — 5 members" while the header says 57 [OBSERVED — desktop-09 vs header; mobile shows 57: mobile2-18] — mock data stitched from two sources. And the corporate demo (Eli Lilly retreat, 32 executives) reuses the identical consumer chat transcript — "Room 502," "split an Uber" [OBSERVED — desktop-12 shows the same messages as desktop-08]. An ops buyer notices recycled set dressing.
- **The dealbreaker:** Real Pro trips convert with `roster: []`, `roomAssignments: []`, `schedule: []`, `settlement: []`, `medical: []`, `compliance: []` [OBSERVED — src/utils/tripConverter.ts:118-130; evidence-delta D7 "honest surfaces" hide the placeholder tabs on real trips]. Demo ≠ product.
- **Pricing reaction:** Grid is legible; Enterprise lists approvals/QuickBooks/compliance [OBSERVED — ground truth §7] — but compliance data structures are stubbed [OBSERVED — D7], so Enterprise sells features that don't hold data yet [SIMULATED RISK]. Pro trial = `mailto:` [OBSERVED — PricingSection.tsx:140,158,173].
- **Web positives:** Information architecture, role model, broadcast/channel separation, PDF Recap with privacy line ("Emails and phone numbers hidden") [OBSERVED — desktop2-21].
- **Web pain points:** No SSO, no audit-log surface, no bulk import, member-count inconsistency, consumer-shaped Payments on a Pro trip [OBSERVED — desktop2-14], demo-vs-real gap.

### F. Mobile / PWA Flow Walkthrough
- **First impression:** Compact pro header (trip name, cities, member count) with a clear "Demo Mode" banner — honest labeling, good [OBSERVED — mobile-08].
- **Navigation:** Horizontal scrolling tab strip, not a bottom nav [OBSERVED — mobile-08; evidence-delta non-defect note]. On a game-day sideline I'd want one-thumb reach to Broadcasts; a scrolling strip buries it.
- **Chat/input:** Message bubbles, mention hint, mic-dictation and attach buttons all reachable [OBSERVED — mobile-08]. Fine for travel-day triage.
- **Team tab on mobile:** Full roster controls survive on a 390px screen — Create Role, Manage Roles, Requests, filter chips with counts (Artists 1, Crew 33, Performers 17) [OBSERVED — mobile2-18]. Genuinely good density work.
- **Forms/modals:** Not deeply exercised on mobile in this environment [HYPOTHESIS].
- **Invite link flow:** Untestable live (backend blocked) [SIMULATED RISK — per evidence-delta environment limits].
- **Perceived speed:** A documented duplicate-key render storm fires continuously on mobile trip surfaces (~150 warnings/step, 2,528 during pro chat-channels) from `MobileGroupCalendar.tsx:525` weekday keys [OBSERVED — evidence-delta R1]. At 180 members and a season of message volume, mobile perf headroom worries me [SIMULATED RISK].
- **Mobile positives:** Roster density, demo-mode banner, reachable composer.
- **Mobile pain points:** No bottom nav for critical tabs; render-storm perf smell; my deputies would live on this during travel days and it needs to be bulletproof.

### H. Emotional Reaction
- **Impressed by:** The Pro demo's information architecture — roster with roles, org chart, channels split by function, broadcasts with urgency styling. Someone on this team understands touring/team ops [OBSERVED — desktop-08/09, desktop2-19/20].
- **Confused by:** Why the corporate retreat demo shows the same "Room 502 / split an Uber" chat as the Beyoncé tour [OBSERVED — desktop-12 vs desktop-08]; why the Team panel says 5 when the header says 57 [OBSERVED — desktop-09].
- **Annoyed by:** Realizing the entire ops layer — roster, rooms, schedule, per-diem, medical, compliance — is empty arrays on real trips [OBSERVED — tripConverter.ts:118-130]. I spent 40 minutes evaluating a movie set.
- **Would abandon when:** The first real trip I create has none of what the demo showed. Immediately.
- **Would invite others?** Not to use it — I'd forward the demo to a colleague with "keep an eye on these guys."
- **[SYNTHETIC QUOTE]:** "You built the most convincing brochure in team travel. Now build the product in the brochure, get me SSO and an audit log, and call me — I answer my phone."

### I. Conversion Scores
- **Activation:** 2/10 — would create one real Pro trip, see empty ops, stop.
- **Invite likelihood:** 2/10 — demo-forwarding only.
- **Day-7 retention:** 1/10 — nothing to run a season on yet.
- **Paid conversion:** 2/10 — enterprise intent exists, product doesn't.
- **NPS-style:** −10 — low-neutral; vision earns it back from negative.
- **Would they pay?** Not today; yes at Enterprise when ops data layer + SSO + audit exist.
- **What would they pay?** Enterprise custom — five figures/season is normal for club software.
- **Feature creating willingness to pay:** Manifest/roster import with role-based access and broadcast ack tracking.
- **Limit/CTA that triggers upgrade:** None — he'd never hit a usage limit before hitting the capability wall.
- **CTA that would annoy them:** "Start Free Trial" mailto link on a $99 tier — signals the sales motion isn't real [OBSERVED — PricingSection.tsx:140,158].

### J. Top 5 Fixes for This Persona
1. Replace the empty-array Pro ops conversion with a real data layer (roster, room assignments, schedule, per-diem) populated via CSV/manifest import, because Dan evaluated the demo (desktop-08/09), created the mental real trip, and found `src/utils/tripConverter.ts:118-130` returns nothing — instant disqualification.
2. Add SAML/OIDC SSO and an admin audit log, because Dan's security review fails any tool with only email/Google/Apple auth (desktop-04/05) and no change history, blocking all NFL procurement.
3. Add broadcast read/ack receipts with export, because Dan's job is proving 180 people were notified of the gate change; desktop2-19 shows the message but no delivery accountability surface.
4. Build bulk member provisioning (CSV roster invite, later SCIM), because link-based invites (desktop2-11 pattern) cannot onboard a 180-person traveling party per game week.
5. Reconcile demo data inconsistencies (Team panel "5 members" vs 57-member header, desktop-09; recycled consumer chat in the corporate demo, desktop-12), because ops buyers read sloppy demo data as sloppy engineering.

### K. Confidence
- **Level:** High on the demo-vs-real gap (code-verified at tripConverter.ts:118-130) and UI observations; Medium on enterprise requirements blocking (industry-standard but persona-inferred).
- **Directly observed:** Pro demo surfaces (desktop-08/09, desktop2-14/18/19/20/21, desktop-12, mobile-08, mobile2-18), empty ops conversion code, mailto Pro CTAs, dictation-only voice.
- **Needs real-user validation:** Whether NFL-tier buyers would pilot a comms-only subset (broadcasts + channels) before the ops layer exists.
- **Beta interview question:** "If broadcasts, role channels, and roster import worked today but per-diem and compliance didn't, would you run one road trip on it alongside your current stack — and what would make you stop?"

## Persona 12: Alicia Burch — Pro / NBA Team Travel Operations Coordinator

### A. Profile
- **Name:** Alicia Burch
- **Age range:** 35–45
- **Location/timezone:** Dallas, TX (CT)
- **Industry/role:** NBA franchise — Manager, Team Travel Operations; runs 41 road games plus preseason
- **Tech comfort:** High — lives in Slack, Teams, TripIt Pro, airline ops portals; will try anything that kills a spreadsheet
- **Platform:** iPhone (travel days) + laptop (planning days)
- **Group size:** ~45-person traveling party (players, coaches, performance staff, equipment, broadcast, security, PR)
- **Planning style:** Rolling two-week advance windows; everything re-planned constantly — schedule churn is the job (flexed game times, back-to-backs, weather reroutes)
- **Current tools:** Excel rooming lists, Outlook, charter operator portal, hotel CSM emails, GroupMe for the party, Slack for staff, TripIt
- **Main pain points:** Schedule churn ripples (one flex game = new charter slot, hotel dates, bus times, per-diem day count); telling 45 people the bus moved 30 minutes and knowing who saw it; rooming lists living in five inboxes
- **Budget sensitivity:** Medium — she has a department card and can expense $99/mo without drama; bigger commitments need her VP
- **Why adopt Chravel:** Broadcasts + role channels map exactly to how she already segments comms; per-trip mute means her phone survives the season
- **Why reject Chravel:** Real Pro trips have no roster/rooms/schedule data layer yet; no charter/flight integration; she won't hand-retype what lives in the charter portal

### B. Jobs-to-Be-Done
1. When the league flexes a game time, I want to update one schedule and have every member's view and notifications update, so I don't send 45 corrective texts.
2. When I post "bus at 10:15 not 10:45," I want to broadcast to everyone but discuss logistics only with ops staff, so players aren't buried in staff chatter.
3. When the hotel asks for the rooming list, I want to export it from the same roster the team sees, so there's one truth instead of five attachments.
4. When I'm boarding a charter at midnight, I want to do everything one-handed on my phone, so the laptop stays in the bag.
5. When it's a back-to-back, I want trip-level notification control, so tomorrow's trip doesn't wake me during tonight's game.
6. When the charter operator changes tail numbers or slots, I want it to flow into the trip automatically, so I'm not the human API between portals.

### C. Screener Answers
| Question | Answer |
|---|---|
| Trips last 12 months | 4+ (41 road games — laughs) |
| Typical group size | 16+ (45-person party) |
| Main tools | Excel, Outlook, GroupMe, Slack, charter portal, TripIt |
| Primary device | iOS (iPhone on the road, laptop at the facility) |
| 45-min call? | Yes |
| Role in group | Primary planner |
| Pro-ops responsibility | Yes, I own logistics |

### D. Full Survey Answers

**About you.** Alicia, Dallas. I coordinate team travel for an NBA club — 41 road games, charters, hotels, buses, rooming lists, per-diem days. My season is one long re-plan. If your product can't survive a schedule change at 11pm, it can't survive me.

**Most recent/next group trip.** A four-game road swing — west coast back-to-back then through Denver. Kicked off when the league schedule dropped; rebuilt twice since (one game flexed for national TV). Involved: me, ops assistant, charter operator, four hotel CSMs, equipment manager. Most frustrating: the flex — new wheels-up time, hotel late checkout renegotiated, bus grid redone, and then telling 45 people in a GroupMe where half of them have it muted. What went well: charter ops were flawless; my rooming-list template is battle-tested. Apps: Excel, Outlook, GroupMe, Slack, charter portal, TripIt, plus texts — 7. After first plan: the plan changed before the first flight. Always does.

**Planning workflow.** Idea→booked: schedule release → charter slots → hotel contracts → rolling 2-week advances. During: I'm mission control from seat 1A — broadcast changes, chase stragglers, fix rooms at the front desk. Post: per-diem day-count reconciliation, invoice checks. Decisions stick in email; speed happens in texts; the gap between those two is where things get lost. Non-responders: two veterans who treat every group thread as spam — their position coach is my delivery mechanism. Example thread: a 62-message GroupMe spiral about one bus time. Sixty-two.

**Feature areas.**
- *Create/Invite:* Easy. Approval-to-join toggle matters — I can't have a fan with a leaked link inside team comms [OBSERVED — invite modal per evidence log L3].
- *Places:* Basecamp = hotel anchoring distances is actually useful for bus timing. Mild.
- *Calendar/Itinerary:* Demo's schedule view reads like a day sheet [OBSERVED — desktop-08 demo]. Real trips: `schedule: []` [OBSERVED — src/utils/tripConverter.ts:120, D7]. I will not hand-type 41 games of itinerary. Import or nothing.
- *Polls:* Staff dinner picks, maybe. Players don't vote.
- *Tasks:* Advance checklists per city — yes, I'd use this. Assignment + due dates is enough [OBSERVED — ground truth §6].
- *Smart Import (what I'd paste):* Charter operator confirmations (PDF), hotel rooming list (CSV), league schedule (ICS). If pasting the charter PDF builds my day sheet, that's the moment I'm sold [HYPOTHESIS — parse quality on charter/ops PDFs untested].
- *AI Concierge (what I'd ask):* "What time is the bus to the arena in Denver?" — because if the team can self-serve answers, my phone stops buzzing. Also "who's missing a room assignment?"
- *AI Trust (what breaks it):* Confidently wrong bus time, once. And AI writes without the confirm card — the "Save to Trip?" gate is the right call [OBSERVED — ground truth §6].
- *Settings priorities:* Per-trip mute is THE one — and you actually shipped it [OBSERVED — D11, src/hooks/useTripNotificationMute.ts:26-94]. With 5+ active trip shells in a season, blanket notifications would kill me.

**Pro/Events branch.** Professional-grade means: change-resilient (edits propagate, nobody's looking at a stale version), role-aware (players see player things), and accountable (I can see who got the broadcast). Control vs automation: automate the ripple (schedule change updates everyone's view), but I commit the change. Trust comes from: reliability during churn, delivery receipts, and the vendor understanding that my data already lives in the charter portal and the league system — meet me there with integrations. The demo's channels (#production 25, #security 20) and broadcasts with urgency styling are genuinely my mental model [OBSERVED — desktop2-20, desktop2-19]; GroupMe has neither.

**Money.** Club pays; I track per-diem day counts, not splits. The "You Owe / You Are Owed" Payments framing is for friend trips, not team ops [OBSERVED — desktop2-14]. Reimbursements go through accounting. Plan-change comms: broadcast + targeted channel + read receipts ideally. One planner: me. Hotels: contracted; restaurants: people's own business. Conversations live in GroupMe/Slack/texts — three places, which is the disease Chravel could cure.

**Willingness to pay.** Team plan — Growth $99/mo on the department card is defensible if real trips get the ops surfaces. I'd start a pilot on one road swing. Per-seat pricing above that needs my VP. (Aside: I went to start the trial and the button is an email link [OBSERVED — PricingSection.tsx:140,158, D9]. I almost closed the tab — self-serve or I pilot something else.)

**Ratings (1–5).**
- Likelihood next trip: **2** — would pilot comms-only today; ops gap blocks real adoption.
- Clarity: **4** — channels/broadcasts/roster concepts land instantly.
- Time saved: **2** — today, comms only; with schedule import it's a 4.
- AI trust: **3** — confirm card helps; needs to prove itself on bus times.
- Would invite: **3** — I'd pull my ops assistant into a pilot.
- Mobile usability: **3** — chat works one-handed [OBSERVED — mobile-08]; tab strip means scrolling to reach Team/Broadcasts [OBSERVED — mobile2-18 nav].
- Web usability: **4** — Pro layout is clean and dense in the right ways [OBSERVED — desktop-08/09].
- Pricing fit: **3** — Growth price is fine; what's behind it isn't there yet, and no self-serve.
- NPS sentiment: **3** — genuinely hopeful; closest thing to my workflow I've seen in a consumer-grade package.

**Wrap-up.** Change one thing: schedule + rooming-list import on real Pro trips — kill the hand-typing. Recommend if: one road swing runs end-to-end on it without me opening GroupMe. Anything else: per-trip mute shipping tells me someone there actually travels — do flight integration next. Follow-up: Yes.

### J. Top 5 Fixes for This Persona

3. Surface broadcast delivery/read receipts in the Broadcasts UI, because her core job is proving 45 people saw the bus change; desktop2-19 shows the message with no accountability layer (ground truth §6 claims tracking exists — expose it).
4. Fix the mobile render storm (`src/components/mobile/MobileGroupCalendar.tsx:525` duplicate weekday keys; keep the calendar from re-rendering while unmounted-from-view), because her season is lived on an iPhone and R1 shows 2,500+ warnings/step on pro chat surfaces — battery and jank risk.

## Persona 13: Coach Marcus Webb — Pro / University Basketball Travel Coordinator (Duke)

### A. Profile
- **Name:** Marcus Webb ("Coach Webb" to everyone)
- **Age range:** 38–48
- **Location/timezone:** Durham, NC (ET)
- **Industry/role:** Director of Basketball Operations, Duke University men's basketball — travel, compliance documentation, recruiting-travel logistics
- **Tech comfort:** Medium-high — fluent in Teamworks, ARMS-style compliance software, Excel, the university's Concur instance; suspicious of anything that can't export to PDF for an auditor
- **Platform:** iPhone primarily; office laptop for compliance paperwork
- **Group size:** ~25 travel party (15 players, coaches, athletic trainers, managers, SID) + compliance officers reviewing everything after the fact
- **Planning style:** NCAA-rule-shaped — every meal, per-diem dollar, and hotel night is documentable; recruiting travel has its own ruleset and calendars
- **Current tools:** Teamworks (roster/itinerary), Excel per-diem logs, Concur, Outlook, GroupMe for the team, compliance office's document portal
- **Main pain points:** Producing per-diem and travel records for compliance audits; recruiting-travel rules (who can travel, when, contact periods); duplicate data entry between Teamworks, Concur, and compliance docs
- **Budget sensitivity:** Medium-high — it's not his money but it's a PO process; no credit-card self-serve, ever; athletic department procurement + an addendum from university counsel
- **Why adopt Chravel:** Roster/roles + broadcasts is cleaner than GroupMe; per-trip records that export could feed compliance files
- **Why reject Chravel:** Compliance features are Enterprise-only on the pricing grid AND the compliance data structure is an empty stub in code — a double gap; plus university procurement can't buy a mailto link

### B. Jobs-to-Be-Done
1. When we travel for an away game, I want the itinerary, roster, and per-diem log in one exportable record, so the compliance office gets one clean file instead of five.
2. When compliance audits a season, I want per-trip documentation I can produce in minutes, so I'm not reconstructing meal receipts from March in July.
3. When recruiting travel happens, I want role-restricted visibility (coaches see recruit logistics, players don't), so we stay inside NCAA contact rules.
4. When the bus time changes, I want one broadcast that 25 people actually see, so the trainers aren't relaying messages.
5. When procurement evaluates a tool, I want a quote, a W-9, and a data agreement on letterhead, so the PO can actually be cut.
6. When a freshman loses the itinerary, I want him to find it himself in the app, so my phone isn't the team's help desk.

|---|---|

| 45-min call? | Maybe — depends if you can talk compliance |

### D. Full Survey Answers

**About you.** Marcus Webb, Director of Basketball Operations at Duke. I run team travel and the paperwork that proves we ran it by the book. In college athletics the trip isn't over when we land — it's over when compliance signs off on the file.

**Most recent/next group trip.** ACC road game at Virginia. Kicked off when the conference schedule locked. Involved: me, an assistant, our Teamworks admin, the hotel, charter bus company, compliance officer (after the fact, always after the fact). Most frustrating: building the per-diem documentation twice — once to distribute, once in the format compliance wants. What went well: Teamworks push got everyone to the bus on time for once. Apps used: Teamworks, Excel, Concur, Outlook, GroupMe — 5, plus the compliance portal makes 6. After first plan: travel itself is routine; the records tail drags for weeks.

**Planning workflow.** Idea→booked: schedule release → bus/charter booking → hotel block → Teamworks itinerary → per-diem prep. During: broadcasts and bed checks. Post: receipts, per-diem logs, compliance file. Decisions stick in email with compliance cc'd. Non-responders: freshmen, reliably — the team managers chase them. Example doc: my per-diem spreadsheet, formatted to the compliance office's template, which is itself formatted to an NCAA interpretation from 2019.

**Feature areas.**
- *Create/Invite:* Approval-to-join is mandatory for us — and it exists [OBSERVED — invite modal, evidence log L3]. Student-athletes can't be in channels with boosters; controlled membership matters.
- *Places:* Low value. We know where Cameron is.
- *Calendar/Itinerary:* The demo's structured schedule is the Teamworks itinerary concept [OBSERVED — desktop-08 demo]. Real Pro trips: `schedule: []` and — this is the one that stings — `compliance: []` and `perDiem` zeroed out [OBSERVED — src/utils/tripConverter.ts:118-130, D7]. The data structure for my job exists in the type system and holds nothing.
- *Polls:* Team meal choices, fine. Marginal.
- *Tasks:* Managers' game-day checklist — usable [OBSERVED — ground truth §6].
- *Smart Import (what I'd paste):* Hotel folios, bus confirmations, the conference schedule ICS, per-diem receipts. If imports build the compliance file as a byproduct of running the trip — that's the dream [HYPOTHESIS — untested parse quality; replay idempotency partially tested per §10.8, and duplicated expense rows in a compliance file is how you end up in an NCAA inquiry].
- *AI Concierge (what I'd ask):* "Generate the per-diem summary for the Virginia trip." "Who hasn't submitted receipts?" Administrative deflection, not restaurant tips.
- *AI Trust (what breaks it):* Anything fabricated in a document that goes to compliance. One hallucinated dollar amount and I'm done forever. The confirm-before-write card is necessary but not sufficient [OBSERVED — ground truth §6].
- *Settings priorities:* Role permissions (recruiting info away from players), export controls, and who-can-see-what documentation I can show counsel [SIMULATED RISK — permission matrix exists per ground truth §8, but no user-facing permissions documentation surface observed].

**Pro/Events branch.** Professional-grade means: defensible. Every record exportable, every access role-scoped, every change traceable. Control vs automation: automation for assembly (collect receipts, build the file), human sign-off for anything with my name on it. Trust comes from: PDF exports that match what compliance expects, a data agreement the university will sign, and FERPA-aware handling of student-athlete data [SIMULATED RISK — no FERPA/education posture observed anywhere in product surfaces]. The PDF Recap modal got my attention — section checkboxes, "Emails and phone numbers hidden. Chat and AI history never included." [OBSERVED — desktop2-21]. That privacy line is the most procurement-literate sentence in the product. But "1 Free Export per trip" on the same modal [OBSERVED — desktop2-21] tells me exports are a metered upsell, and the audit-grade version of my life is gated to a tier — Enterprise — whose compliance features are simultaneously stubbed in code [OBSERVED — ground truth §7 row "Approvals/QuickBooks/compliance: Enterprise only" + tripConverter.ts:130 `compliance: []`]. You're charging top-tier for an empty array. That's the double gap.

**Money.** No splitting — university funds, per-diem per policy, receipts to Concur. The consumer owe/owed Payments tab is a different sport [OBSERVED — desktop2-14]. Reimbursement: through Concur, never an app deeplink — Venmo settle-up [OBSERVED — ground truth §6] is actually a compliance hazard in my world; boosters Venmo-ing players is a headline. Plan-change comms: broadcast + managers. One planner: me. Hotels: I book per athletic-department contract. Conversations live in GroupMe (team) and email (record).

**Willingness to pay.** Team plan via PO — but realistically this is an athletic-department procurement at Enterprise tier, and there's no path: the Enterprise CTA is `mailto:billing@chravelapp.com` [OBSERVED — src/components/conversion/PricingSection.tsx:173]. I can't attach a mailto to a purchase requisition. Get a quote generator, a W-9 on a vendor page, and invoicing, or university money can't reach you. Personally? I wouldn't pay out of pocket; this is a department tool or nothing.

### I. Conversion Scores
- **Activation:** 3/10 — comms pilot plausible; core job untouched.
- **Invite likelihood:** 4/10 — managers/assistants only.

- **NPS-style:** −5 — respectful skeptic.

- **Feature creating willingness to pay:** Per-diem + compliance record export that matches audit templates.
- **Limit/CTA that triggers upgrade:** Export metering ("1 Free Export per trip") would force the tier question on trip two [OBSERVED — desktop2-21].
- **CTA that would annoy them:** "Start Free Trial" mailto — universities don't email for trials, they cut POs [OBSERVED — PricingSection.tsx:140].

### J. Top 5 Fixes for This Persona
1. Build the per-diem/compliance data layer behind the existing types (populate what `src/utils/tripConverter.ts:121-130` stubs), because Coach Webb's purchase driver is audit documentation and today Enterprise sells an empty array — a credibility and revenue blocker.
2. Add a procurement path — quote request form, invoicing, vendor docs — replacing the Enterprise `mailto:` (`src/components/conversion/PricingSection.tsx:173`), because university POs cannot attach to an email link; this gap zeroes an entire buyer class.
3. Make PDF Recap exports unlimited on Pro/Enterprise tiers (currently "1 Free Export per trip," desktop2-21), because metering the audit artifact penalizes exactly the compliance use case the tier ladder claims to serve.
4. Add broadcast read/ack receipts with export, because bed-check-grade accountability ("all 25 saw the 7am bus change") is table stakes for team ops and desktop2-19 shows no delivery proof.
5. Suppress Venmo settle-up deeplinks on Pro/Sports trips (ground truth §6 payments), because peer-to-peer money movement around student-athletes is an NCAA compliance hazard the product currently invites by default.

### K. Confidence
- **Level:** Medium-High — the double gap (tier gating + stubbed data) is fully code/doc-verified; NCAA-specific requirements are persona-inferred.
- **Directly observed:** desktop-08/09, desktop2-14/18/19/21, mobile-08, mobile2-18; tripConverter.ts:118-130; PricingSection.tsx:140,173; pricing grid (§7); permission matrix (§8).
- **Needs real-user validation:** Whether college programs would pilot comms-only alongside Teamworks; actual compliance-office export format requirements; FERPA posture demands.
- **Beta interview question:** "Show me the exact file you hand the compliance office after a road trip — if Chravel generated 80% of it automatically, what's in the missing 20% that would still keep you in Excel?"

## Persona 14: Linda Park — Pro / Middle & High School Athletic Director

### A. Profile
- **Name:** Linda Park
- **Age range:** 48–58
- **Location/timezone:** Sacramento, CA (PT)
- **Industry/role:** Athletic Director for a public middle/high school — 8 teams, roughly 20 kids each, plus coaches, parent volunteers, and bus drivers
- **Tech comfort:** Low-medium — comfortable with email, Google Sheets, and the district's student-information system after years of practice; learns new apps reluctantly and only if coaches and parents will too
- **Platform:** Desktop-first (school office PC); personal iPhone for sideline emergencies
- **Group size:** 8 teams × ~20 students + 2–3 coaches each + parents on the comms tree
- **Planning style:** Season-calendar driven; permission slips, bus requisitions through the district transportation office, emergency contact binders, parent phone trees
- **Current tools:** Email, paper permission slips, Google Sheets rosters, Remind (one coach uses it), district SIS, a laminated emergency-contact binder in every team bag
- **Main pain points:** Parents not getting bus-time changes; chasing permission slips; emergency contacts living in a binder; every coach communicating differently (Remind, group text, email, nothing)
- **Budget sensitivity:** EXTREME — a $49/month subscription is a school-board line item; anything above free-ish needs a requisition, a vote, and a fiscal-year cycle
- **Why adopt Chravel:** Broadcasts to parents per team would end the phone tree; one place for schedules instead of eight
- **Why reject Chravel:** Price is structurally impossible; minors' data with no visible FERPA/COPPA posture; her actual fit might be free consumer trips, not Pro at all

### B. Jobs-to-Be-Done
1. When a bus time changes at 1pm on game day, I want every parent of that team notified in one step, so no seventh-grader is standing alone in a parking lot at 6pm.
2. When a new season starts, I want each team's schedule entered once and visible to families, so coaches stop maintaining eight different systems.
3. When we take minors off campus, I want emergency contacts and medical flags accessible to the coach on the sideline, so the binder isn't the single point of failure.
4. When I adopt any tool touching students, I want clear minors-privacy answers (FERPA/COPPA), so I can defend it to the district and to parents.
5. When the district reviews spending, I want the tool to be free or nearly free, so it survives the budget cycle.
6. When parents ask "where's the game and what time," I want them self-serving the answer, so coaches coach instead of answering texts.

### C. Screener Answers
| Question | Answer |
|---|---|
| Trips last 12 months | 4+ (league away games all season, 8 teams) |
| Typical group size | 16+ (team + coaches + parent drivers) |
| Main tools | Email, Google Sheets, paper slips, Remind (one team), district SIS |
| Primary device | Desktop-first |
| 45-min call? | Maybe — after 3pm when the buses are gone |
| Role in group | Primary planner |
| Pro-ops responsibility | Yes, I own logistics |

### D. Full Survey Answers

**About you.** Linda Park, athletic director at a public school in Sacramento. Eight teams, about 160 kids, two seasons each, and every away game involves a bus requisition, permission slips, and praying the parents read the email. I am not a "power user" of anything except patience.

**Most recent/next group trip.** Girls' volleyball away match, 40 minutes out. Kicked off by the league schedule in August. Involved: me, the coach, the district transportation office, 14 families. Most frustrating: the bus came back early and four parents didn't see the pickup-time email — I sat in the lot with the kids for an hour. What went well: the coach's Remind group got most parents instantly; that contrast is exactly why I'm looking at apps. Apps used: email, Remind, a Google Sheet, paper slips — call it 4, but really the system is "Linda." After first plan: every game repeats the same scramble.

**Planning workflow.** Idea→booked: league sets the schedule; I requisition buses for the season in one batch; slips go home on paper. During: coach texts me, I email parents, the office calls anyone unreachable. Post: incident reports if anything happened, slip filing. Decisions stick in email. Non-responders: the same five families every season — for them we go to phone calls. Example doc: my master Google Sheet — eight tabs, one per team, color-coded since 2019.

**Feature areas.**
- *Create/Invite:* I'd need eight trips (one per team-season). Here's my problem: that's eight separate setups, and on a free account I get **3 active trips** [OBSERVED — ground truth §7 free limits]. My structure breaks the free tier on day one.
- *Places:* Schools and gyms. Marginal — though parents asking "where is Ridgeview Middle?" would love a map link [OBSERVED — Places exists, ground truth §6].
- *Calendar/Itinerary:* One season schedule per team that parents can see — this is honestly most of what I need [OBSERVED — calendar with month/list views, §6].
- *Polls:* Team dinner after the championship, sure. Not core.
- *Tasks:* Permission slip tracking! If "turned in slip" could be a task per kid... though I suspect that's not what tasks are for. What I actually need is a form with a signature [SIMULATED RISK — no permission-slip/waiver primitive exists in the product].
- *Smart Import (what I'd paste):* The league's schedule PDF and my Google Sheet roster. If those imported, setup goes from a weekend to an hour [HYPOTHESIS — parse quality untested].
- *AI Concierge (what I'd ask):* Honestly? Probably nothing at first. Maybe "what time is the bus Friday." I'd worry the kids ask it silly things — is there a way to see what it tells them? [SIMULATED RISK — no guardian/visibility controls for minors observed].
- *AI Trust (what breaks it):* AI talking to children unsupervised. Full stop. That's a parent phone call I don't want.
- *Settings priorities:* Who can see the kids' info. Emergency contacts visible to coaches only, not other parents. And the broadcasts — those red announcement messages [OBSERVED — desktop2-19] — that's the bus-change problem solved, if parents can receive without being full chatty members.

**Pro/Events branch.** Professional-grade for me isn't roles and org charts — it's: minors' data handled defensibly, parents reachable without being drowned in chat, and a paper trail when something goes wrong. Control vs automation: I want almost no automation — schools run on explicit human approvals. What creates trust: a privacy policy I can forward to the district counsel, COPPA/FERPA language, references from other schools, and a price that doesn't require a board vote. I watched the demo's Team tab with roles and the broadcast stream [OBSERVED — desktop-09, desktop2-19] and thought: that's a varsity version of my phone tree. But the demo is a Beyoncé tour with 57 adults [OBSERVED — desktop-08]; nothing in the product mentions minors, guardians, or schools — the "School" Pro category exists in trip creation [OBSERVED — ground truth §4 categories] but there's no kid-safety layer behind it [OBSERVED — no guardian/consent surfaces anywhere in observed UI; tripConverter `medical: []` stub at src/utils/tripConverter.ts:129].

**Money.** We don't split costs in-app — boosters and the district budget pay; parents pay fees through the district portal. Venmo links between school staff and families? Absolutely not, that's a district-policy violation waiting to happen [OBSERVED that settle-up = Venmo deeplink, ground truth §6; SIMULATED RISK for school context]. Reimbursements: district forms. Plan-change comms: this is THE job — today email + Remind + prayer; broadcasts would replace all of it. One planner: me plus eight coaches. Hotels/restaurants: rare (playoffs only). Conversations live in email and whatever each coach improvised.

**Willingness to pay.** Free only — personally and structurally. Pro Starter at $49/month is $588/year, which in district terms is a purchase order, a vendor approval, and a fight. Honest answer: the right product for me might be **eight free consumer trips** (one per team), except free caps at 3 active trips [OBSERVED — §7], pro features like broadcasts are Pro-tier-gated [OBSERVED — §7 channels/roster Pro-only], and consumer trips don't have broadcasts at all on the tiers I could afford. There is no SKU shaped like a school. If you made a $10–15/month "Community/School" tier with broadcasts, read-only parent membership, and 10 trips — I'd find that in the booster budget tomorrow.

**Ratings (1–5).**
- Likelihood next trip: **2** — I'd try one team as a pilot on free; the 3-trip cap stops the rollout.
- Clarity: **3** — I understood it, but it took me a while; nine tabs is a lot for a volleyball parent.
- Time saved: **3** — broadcasts + shared calendar would genuinely save hours weekly.
- AI trust: **2** — not with children, not yet, not without controls.
- Would invite: **3** — coaches first; parents only after the privacy answer.
- Mobile usability: **3** — sideline phone use looked fine [OBSERVED — mobile-08]; small text worries me for our older volunteers.
- Web usability: **4** — the desktop layout is clear and I live on desktop [OBSERVED — desktop-08].
- Pricing fit: **1** — no affordable tier fits a school's shape.
- NPS sentiment: **3** — I want this to exist for schools; it doesn't yet.

**Wrap-up.** Change one thing: a school-shaped plan — affordable, multi-team, broadcasts included, minors-privacy documented. What makes me recommend: another AD saying "we ran a season on it and the parents loved it." Anything else: please, a permission-slip feature — whoever builds that owns this market. Follow-up: Yes — schools never get asked.

### E. Web Flow Walkthrough
- **Discovery/landing:** "For Friend & Family trips, Team Travel... & Anybody Organizing a Group" — I'm technically in "anybody," which is the problem; schools aren't named [OBSERVED — desktop-01 hero copy, L1]. The pricing line "Free works forever—upgrade only when you need more" [OBSERVED — L1] set an expectation the Pro gating immediately breaks for me.
- **Signup/onboarding:** Email signup fine [OBSERVED — desktop-04/05]. A 10-screen carousel [OBSERVED — D13] — I'd skip by screen three; my coaches would skip by two.
- **Trip creation:** "School" is a Pro category [OBSERVED — ground truth §4] — but Pro trip creation gates to Frequent Chraveler $19.99/mo after one free trial [OBSERVED — §4, §7]. So the product names my segment and prices it out in the same modal.
- **Feature usage:** Broadcasts demo — the "URGENT: Flight departure gate changed" red message [OBSERVED — desktop2-19] is my bus-change message with different nouns. Team tab roles [OBSERVED — desktop-09] could map to Coaches/Parents/Players. Requests/approval queue [OBSERVED — desktop-09] matters — I cannot have strangers joining a kids' team chat [OBSERVED — require-approval exists, L3].
- **Pricing reaction:** $49 Starter = board approval = no. The math nobody at Chravel did: 8 teams × free consumer trips would serve me better than one Pro sub, except the 3-active-trip cap and broadcast gating make both paths fail [OBSERVED — §7]. SKU-fit failure, not a price-sensitivity whine.
- **Web positives:** Legible layout, broadcasts concept, approval-gated joins, shared calendar.
- **Web pain points:** No school story, no minors-privacy posture [SIMULATED RISK], Pro gating on the one feature (broadcasts) my use case is built on, demo full of pop stars instead of anything I recognize [OBSERVED — desktop-08].

### F. Mobile / PWA Flow Walkthrough
- **First impression:** Clean, dark, modern — honestly more polished than anything the district buys [OBSERVED — mobile-08]. The dark theme at a sunny 3pm game might be hard to read [HYPOTHESIS].
- **Navigation:** Horizontal tab strip with many tabs [OBSERVED — mobile-08; evidence-delta note — no bottom nav]. For a parent who only ever needs Calendar and announcements, eight-plus tabs is noise; they'd get lost finding Broadcasts [SIMULATED RISK].
- **Chat/input:** Fine for coaches; for parents I'd disable chat entirely if I could — broadcast-only membership is the school model [SIMULATED RISK — read-only roles exist for pro_viewer per §8, which is close].
- **Forms/modals:** Roster admin on phone worked in demo [OBSERVED — mobile2-18]; I'd do setup on my office PC regardless.
- **Invite link flow:** Sending links to 160 families needs approval gating (exists [OBSERVED — L3]) — but guests have zero access until they fully join [OBSERVED — D15, permissionMatrix.generated.ts:44-50], meaning every parent must create an account just to see a bus time. Half my families won't. The preview page helps, joining is still an account wall [SIMULATED RISK].
- **Perceived speed:** The mobile render storm (R1, MobileGroupCalendar.tsx:525) [OBSERVED — evidence-delta R1] — on parents' five-year-old Androids, jank means "the app is broken" and they go back to ignoring email.
- **Mobile positives:** Polish, demo banner honesty, readable chat.
- **Mobile pain points:** Account wall for low-intent parents, tab overload, no large-text/simple mode for older volunteers [HYPOTHESIS].

### H. Emotional Reaction
- **Impressed by:** The broadcast stream — I showed the screenshot to a coach and she said "that's Remind but inside the schedule app" [OBSERVED — desktop2-19]. The polish overall; this looks nicer than anything we use.
- **Confused by:** Whether kids are even allowed on it — terms, ages, guardian consent — nothing says [SIMULATED RISK — no minors posture observed]. Also which of the nine tabs a parent is supposed to care about.
- **Annoyed by:** Being named as a category ("School") and then priced like a touring rock band [OBSERVED — §4 categories, §7 tiers]. "Free works forever" until you need the one feature that matters [OBSERVED — L1 copy vs §7 gating].
- **Would abandon when:** The pilot team's parents hit the account wall and half never join — back to email for those families means email for everyone [OBSERVED — D15 guest zero-access].
- **Would invite others?** Coaches yes; the district, not until there's a privacy page I can forward.
- **[SYNTHETIC QUOTE]:** "I don't need an org chart for a middle-school volleyball team. I need every parent to know the bus moved to 5:15, and I need it to cost less than the postage we spend on permission slips."

### I. Conversion Scores
- **Activation:** 3/10 — one-team free pilot, then structural walls (trip cap, broadcast gating).
- **Invite likelihood:** 4/10 — coaches yes; parent rollout stalls at the account wall.
- **Day-7 retention:** 3/10 — email inertia wins unless parents adopt fast.
- **Paid conversion:** 1/10 — no SKU a school can buy.
- **NPS-style:** 0 — wants to love it; product isn't shaped for her.
- **Would they pay?** Booster funds could do $10–15/mo for a school-shaped tier; $49 Pro, never.
- **What would they pay?** $120–180/yr from boosters, free preferred.
- **Feature creating willingness to pay:** Broadcasts-to-parents + multi-team trips + minors-privacy documentation.
- **Limit/CTA that triggers upgrade:** 3-active-trip cap on team #4 — except it triggers abandonment, not upgrade, at her budget [OBSERVED — §7].
- **CTA that would annoy them:** A 14-day trial countdown on a tool holding kids' emergency contacts — schools can't sprint procurement [OBSERVED — trial framing per §7 paywall surfaces].

### J. Top 5 Fixes for This Persona
1. Add a Community/School SKU (~$10–15/mo or free with limits: multi-team trips, broadcasts, read-only parent role), because Linda's segment is named in `CreateTripModal` Pro categories but the cheapest broadcast-capable path is $49/mo Pro Starter — a structural SKU-fit failure that loses every K-12 org.
2. Add read-only/guardian membership that doesn't require full account-gated joining (relax `consumer_guest` zero-access for announcement/calendar viewing, `src/types/permissionMatrix.generated.ts:44-50`), because parent adoption dies at the account wall and her rollout fails on the five unreachable families.
3. Publish a minors-privacy page (age policy, guardian consent, COPPA/FERPA stance, AI-access controls per trip), because Linda cannot pilot a tool holding children's data without something to forward to district counsel — currently nothing in the product addresses minors [SIMULATED RISK].
4. Add SMS/email fallback delivery for broadcasts, because the bus-change job (desktop2-19) only works if it reaches app-less parents; in-app-only announcements recreate her phone-tree problem.
5. Build permission-slip/waiver collection (form + e-sign + per-kid tracking), because it's the single highest-frequency artifact in school travel and no current primitive (tasks, polls, media) holds it — whoever ships this owns the segment.

### K. Confidence
- **Level:** Medium — pricing/gating walls are fully observed; school-specific needs (slips, FERPA, parent behavior) are persona-inferred and need field validation.
- **Directly observed:** Pricing grid + free caps (§7), Pro gating of broadcasts/roster, School category (§4), broadcast UI (desktop2-19), approval-gated invites (L3), guest zero-access (D15), demo surfaces (desktop-08/09, mobile-08).
- **Needs real-user validation:** Parent account-creation tolerance; district procurement thresholds; whether boosters fund tools; consent-workflow requirements.
- **Beta interview question:** "If parents could see schedules and receive announcements without creating an account, and it cost your boosters $12 a month for all eight teams — what's still missing before you'd retire the phone tree?"

## Persona 15: Jamie Sutton — Pro / Tour Manager for a Touring Comedian

### A. Profile
- **Name:** Jamie Sutton
- **Age range:** 30–40
- **Location/timezone:** Los Angeles when home, which is never (40 club dates a year, every US timezone)
- **Industry/role:** Tour manager for a mid-level touring comedian — advances, settlements, travel, day sheets, merch counts, "everything that isn't the 75 minutes on stage"
- **Tech comfort:** High scrappiness, zero patience — iMessage, Google Sheets on a phone, PDF mark-ups, Splice-together workflows; will master any tool in one night if it earns its place
- **Platform:** iPhone ONLY. The laptop lives in the backpack and comes out for settlements, maybe.
- **Group size:** Party of 6 — comedian, opener, Jamie, merch person, occasional security, occasional photographer
- **Planning style:** Day-sheet-driven. Every day is: lobby call, travel, soundcheck, doors, set times, settlement, hotel. Built from venue advance PDFs that arrive in 40 different formats.
- **Current tools:** iMessage group, Google Sheets master grid, venue PDFs in Files app, Google Maps, Southwest/Delta apps, Venmo for tips/floats, TripIt for flights
- **Main pain points:** Re-typing venue advance PDFs into the day sheet; "what time is lobby call" asked six times a day; schedule changes mid-leg propagating to nobody; everything lives in Jamie's head and Jamie's phone
- **Budget sensitivity:** High but pragmatic — $49/mo comes out of tour budget if it demonstrably kills the spreadsheet; prefers per-tour pricing because tours are lumpy (8 weeks on, 6 weeks off)
- **Why adopt Chravel:** The touring demo IS the job — day-sheet schedule, roles, broadcasts, one chat; Smart Import of venue PDFs would be life-changing
- **Why reject Chravel:** Created a real Pro trip in his head and the schedule is empty — back to re-typing, so why switch from Sheets; no per-tour pass for Pro

### B. Jobs-to-Be-Done
1. When a venue sends the advance PDF, I want it to become tomorrow's day sheet automatically, so I stop re-typing lobby calls at 1am.
2. When anyone in the party asks "what time," I want the app to answer instead of me, so I can do settlements in peace.
3. When the set time moves 30 minutes, I want one edit to update everyone's schedule and ping them, so the opener isn't in the green room while doors open.
4. When we're between legs, I want to pause paying, so the tool's cost matches the tour's rhythm.
5. When the tour ends, I want a clean record of every date (schedule, expenses, contacts), so next year's advance starts from something.
6. When I'm doing all of this, I want it on a phone with one thumb in a loading dock with one bar of LTE, so it works where the job happens.

### C. Screener Answers
| Question | Answer |
|---|---|
| Trips last 12 months | 4+ (40 club dates across ~6 legs) |
| Typical group size | 5–8 (party of 6) |
| Main tools | iMessage, Google Sheets, venue PDFs, TripIt, Venmo |
| Primary device | iOS (iPhone only — the laptop is for settlements) |
| 45-min call? | Maybe — text me first, I'm probably in a van |
| Role in group | Primary planner |
| Pro-ops responsibility | Yes, I own logistics |

### D. Full Survey Answers

**About you.** Jamie. I tour-manage a comedian — 40 dates a year, clubs and small theaters. I'm the advance, the day sheet, the travel desk, the settlement, and the lost-and-found. My office is an iPhone and a van.

**Most recent/next group trip.** Mid a 12-date midwest leg right now. Kicked off when the agent confirmed routing. Involved: me, the agent's assistant, six venues' ops contacts, the party of six. Most frustrating: six venue advances in six formats — one's a beautiful PDF, one's an email thread, one's a phone call I had to transcribe. All of it re-typed into my Sheets grid. What went well: my grid template is honed — color-coded, one row per date, everybody has the link. Apps used: iMessage, Sheets, Files (PDFs), TripIt, Maps, Venmo, airline apps — 7-ish. After first plan: the plan mutates daily; the grid is alive until the leg ends.

**Planning workflow.** Idea→booked: agent routes, I advance each date 2 weeks out — tech specs, hospitality, lobby calls, settlements terms. During: morning broadcast in iMessage ("Lobby 11:15, wheels 11:30"), then real-time chaos management. Post: settlement recap, expenses to the business manager. Decisions stick in iMessage and die there — scrollback is my filing system, which is insane. Non-responders: the comedian, famously, who then asks the question that was answered in the thread. Example doc: the grid. 14 columns. Lobby call, van call, soundcheck, doors, opener up, headliner up, curfew, hotel, confirmation numbers, settlement terms, merch %, contact, notes, vibes.

**Feature areas.**
- *Create/Invite:* Six people, one link, done. Approval toggle irrelevant at my size but harmless [OBSERVED — invite modal, L3].
- *Places:* Venue + hotel as saved places with the Basecamp anchoring — actually useful for "how far is the club" [OBSERVED — Basecamp concept, ground truth §6].
- *Calendar/Itinerary:* THE feature. The demo's touring trip reads like my day sheet wearing nicer clothes [OBSERVED — desktop-08, Beyoncé demo with touring schedule]. Then I checked what a real Pro trip holds: `schedule: []`, `itinerary: []` [OBSERVED — src/utils/tripConverter.ts:117-120, D7]. So the demo is cosplaying my job and the product can't do it yet. That's the whole review, honestly.
- *Polls:* "Tacos or diner after the show" — sure, that's real. Low stakes.
- *Tasks:* Merch counts, guest-list cutoffs, advance checklists — usable [OBSERVED — §6].
- *Smart Import (what I'd paste):* Venue advance PDFs. This is my #1 want in any product, ever. Forty PDFs a year, each one re-typed. If Chravel parses "Doors 7 / Opener 7:30 / Headliner 8:15 / Curfew 10" into the schedule, I'm a customer for life [HYPOTHESIS — quality on messy venue PDFs untested; pipeline exists with preview/cherry-pick per §6, and replay idempotency is only partially tested per §10.8 — duplicate set times would burn me once and I'd never trust it again].
- *AI Concierge (what I'd ask):* "What's lobby call tomorrow?" — but here's the thing, I don't need to ask, I need the COMEDIAN to ask the app instead of texting me at 2am. Deflection is the product.
- *AI Trust (what breaks it):* Wrong set time, once, in front of a club manager. The confirm-card before AI writes is correct [OBSERVED — §6 pending-action card]; I'd still double-check every write for the first month.
- *Settings priorities:* Per-trip mute when we're between legs [OBSERVED — D11 exists, useTripNotificationMute.ts:26-94 — respect]; notification immediacy when we're on; data export when the tour ends.

**Pro/Events branch.** Professional-grade means: the day sheet is right, updates propagate instantly, and it works in a loading dock with one bar. Control vs automation: automate the assembly (PDF → schedule), let me approve; broadcasts I write myself — tone matters when you're telling a comedian to be in the lobby at 8am. What creates trust: the demo already speaks tour — "Tour Manager" is literally a role chip, the channels are #production and #security, the broadcast says "Showtime in 90 minutes. All crew report to positions NOW." [OBSERVED — desktop-08 roster chips, desktop2-20 channels, desktop2-20 red broadcast]. Whoever wrote the demo data has stood on a loading dock. That's why the empty real trip hurts — you clearly know what the job is, you just haven't built the part that does it [OBSERVED — D7, tripConverter.ts:118-130].

**Money.** Tour floats and tips on Venmo; settlements are checks/wires/cash with the club — no app touches that. The owe/owed split tab [OBSERVED — desktop2-14] fits the party's burrito-run economy fine; the Venmo deeplink settle is actually how we already live [OBSERVED — §6]. Reimbursements: receipts to the business manager monthly. Plan-change comms: morning broadcast + pinned day sheet would replace my iMessage ritual. One planner: extremely yes — me. Hotels: I book; restaurants: democracy via poll, fine. Conversations live in iMessage; the dream is one trip per leg holding everything.

**Willingness to pay.** Per-trip — and here's your problem: Trip Passes exist but they're consumer tiers (Explorer 45d $39.99 / FC 90d $74.99) which DON'T include Pro features like channels/roster/broadcasts [OBSERVED — §7: channels/roles/roster are Pro-tier-only; Trip Passes grant Explorer/FC entitlements]. There's no "Pro leg pass." So my options are Pro Starter $49/mo year-round for a job that's 8 weeks on, 6 off — call it $600/yr — or nothing. I'd do $49/mo during legs IF the PDF import works and kills the grid. I'd much rather pay $99 per leg. Also: I went to start the trial and it opened my email app [OBSERVED — PricingSection.tsx:140, D9 mailto CTA]. On an iPhone, in a van, that's where the journey ended.

**Ratings (1–5).**
- Likelihood next trip: **2** — would pilot chat+broadcasts on a leg; the grid survives until import exists.
- Clarity: **5** — the touring demo explained the product better than any landing page I've seen; it's my job on a screen.
- Time saved: **2** — today: marginal over iMessage. With PDF import: 5, no exaggeration.
- AI trust: **3** — confirm card is right; needs a clean month of correct set times.
- Would invite: **4** — party of six follows me anywhere; that's the job description.
- Mobile usability: **3** — chat is genuinely good one-handed [OBSERVED — mobile-08]; tab strip scrolling and the render-storm jank concern an iPhone-only user [OBSERVED — R1].
- Web usability: **3** — looks great [OBSERVED — desktop-08] but I'll see it twice a year.
- Pricing fit: **2** — no per-tour Pro option; monthly Pro for seasonal work is paying for the off-season.
- NPS sentiment: **3** — closest anyone's come to building my job; furthest gap between demo and delivery.

**Wrap-up.** Change one thing: venue-PDF import that builds the day sheet on a real trip. That's it. That's the product. Recommend when: one leg runs without opening Sheets. Anything else: a "duplicate trip structure for next leg" button would be huge — tours repeat. Follow-up: Yes, from the van.

### E. Web Flow Walkthrough
- **Discovery/landing:** "Touring Crews" in the hero — named, seen, clicked [OBSERVED — desktop-01 copy, L1].
- **Signup/onboarding:** Email/Apple [OBSERVED — desktop-04/05]; I'd Apple-sign on the phone. 10-screen carousel [OBSERVED — D13] — skipped by screen two, I promise.
- **Pro trip exploration (the love letter):** Beyoncé touring demo — "Touring" category badge, 57-member roster with Artists/Performers/Tour Manager/Crew chips, Invite/PDF Recap/Leave [OBSERVED — desktop-08]. Channels #production (25 unread) and #security (20) with an All Messages rollup [OBSERVED — desktop2-20]. Broadcasts: "Showtime in 90 minutes. All crew report to positions NOW." in urgent red [OBSERVED — desktop2-20]; broadcast stream separates announcements from chatter [OBSERVED — desktop2-19]. PDF Recap with section pick-list — that's my end-of-tour record [OBSERVED — desktop2-21]. This demo was written by someone who's advanced a show.
- **Pro trip exploration (the breakup):** Real Pro trips: `itinerary: []`, `roster: []`, `schedule: []`, settlement/medical/compliance stubbed [OBSERVED — tripConverter.ts:117-130, D7]. Evidence-delta says placeholder tabs are now hidden on real trips ("honest surfaces") — honest, but it means the day-sheet machinery I just fell for doesn't exist for me [OBSERVED — D7].
- **Pricing reaction:** Pro Starter $49/mo, no per-tour pass, trial CTA is mailto [OBSERVED — §7; PricingSection.tsx:140]. Consumer Trip Passes tease the per-trip model I want and then exclude the Pro features I need [OBSERVED — §7].
- **Web positives:** Demo authenticity, channel/broadcast architecture, PDF Recap, role chips.
- **Web pain points:** Demo-real gap (terminal), no Pro per-tour SKU, mailto trial, Payments member-load error mid-demo [OBSERVED — desktop2-14, R5].

### F. Mobile / PWA Flow Walkthrough
- **First impression:** Header compresses well — trip name, cities, member count, demo banner [OBSERVED — mobile-08]. Dark theme is correct; everything in my life happens in dark rooms.
- **Navigation:** Horizontal tab strip, no bottom nav [OBSERVED — mobile-08; evidence-delta note]. Nine tabs on a scroll: Chat and Calendar are leftmost (right priorities), but Broadcasts hides inside Chat's subview row, which took me a beat [OBSERVED — mobile-08 shows Messages/Broadcasts/Pinned/Channels subrow].
- **Chat/input:** One-thumb composer, mention hint, dictation mic (dictation-only — fine, that's all I'd use it for [OBSERVED — D8]), attach button [OBSERVED — mobile-08]. The subview pills (Messages/Broadcasts/Pinned/Channels) are small targets in a moving van [SIMULATED RISK grounded in observed pill sizes, mobile-08].
- **Forms/modals:** Roster admin works at phone size — filters, Create Role, Requests [OBSERVED — mobile2-18]. I'd set roles once and never touch it.
- **Invite link flow:** Would send the link in iMessage; not live-testable here [SIMULATED RISK — environment limits]. Six people, one minute, plausible.
- **Perceived speed:** The duplicate-key render storm hits hardest on my exact surfaces — 2,528 warnings during the pro chat-channels step, mobile pass total 5,940, root cause MobileGroupCalendar weekday keys staying mounted across tabs [OBSERVED — R1, MobileGroupCalendar.tsx:525]. iPhone-only user, all-day-every-day usage: battery drain and jank are adoption killers [SIMULATED RISK].
- **Mobile positives:** Chat quality, dark theme, roster-on-phone, dictation input for van use.
- **Mobile pain points:** Render-storm perf, subview pill discoverability/size, no offline story for loading docks and basements [HYPOTHESIS — offline untested].

### H. Emotional Reaction
- **Impressed by:** The demo data's fluency — "Tour Manager" role chips, #production channel, "Showtime in 90 minutes" broadcast. Somebody on this team has done an advance [OBSERVED — desktop-08, desktop2-20].
- **Confused by:** Why Trip Passes exist for consumers but not for Pro, when touring is the most per-leg-shaped business imaginable [OBSERVED — §7].
- **Annoyed by:** Falling for the demo and then reading `schedule: []` [OBSERVED — tripConverter.ts:120]; the trial button opening Mail.app on my phone [OBSERVED — PricingSection.tsx:140].
- **Would abandon when:** Night one of a real leg, when building the day sheet means re-typing the venue PDF into Chravel instead of into Sheets — same work, new app, no.
- **Would invite others?** Instantly, if I adopt — inviting the party is literally my job; six people land in a day.
- **[SYNTHETIC QUOTE]:** "Your demo is my Tuesday. Your product is my Tuesday with all the times deleted. Parse the venue PDF into a day sheet and charge me per leg — I'll sign from the van tonight."

### I. Conversion Scores
- **Activation:** 4/10 — would run chat+broadcasts on a leg as an iMessage upgrade; schedule stays in Sheets.
- **Invite likelihood:** 7/10 — if he runs the pilot, all six are in by soundcheck; that's the role.
- **Day-7 retention:** 4/10 — survives a leg on comms value; the grid's gravity pulls back without import.
- **Paid conversion:** 4/10 — $49/mo during legs is defensible IF import lands; mailto + no per-tour SKU cap it today.
- **NPS-style:** +10 — passive trending promoter; highest variance persona in the batch ("one feature from a 9").
- **Would they pay?** Yes, conditionally and seasonally.
- **What would they pay?** $99 per leg (preferred) or $49/mo on-season only.
- **Feature creating willingness to pay:** Venue-PDF Smart Import that builds the real-trip day sheet.
- **Limit/CTA that triggers upgrade:** Channels/broadcasts being Pro-gated — the moment the leg pilot wants crew/talent separation [OBSERVED — §7].
- **CTA that would annoy them:** `mailto:` trial on an iPhone — "you had me and you opened my email app" [OBSERVED — PricingSection.tsx:140].

### J. Top 5 Fixes for This Persona
1. Make Smart Import parse venue advance PDFs into real Pro trip schedules (populate what `src/utils/tripConverter.ts:117-120` leaves empty), because Jamie's adoption decision is literally "does the PDF become the day sheet" — the single highest-leverage feature for the touring segment, currently a demo-only illusion (D7).
2. Add a Pro Tour Pass (per-leg pricing, ~$99/45-90 days, Pro-tier entitlements), because touring is seasonal, the consumer Trip Pass already proves the model (§7), and $49/mo year-round taxes the off-season — a SKU gap that blocks a willing payer.
3. Ship self-serve Pro checkout (replace `mailto:` at `src/components/conversion/PricingSection.tsx:140`), because an iPhone-only buyer in a van bounced off Mail.app at the moment of maximum intent (D9).
4. Fix the mobile render storm (`src/components/mobile/MobileGroupCalendar.tsx:525` duplicate keys; unmount/stop re-rendering the calendar when off-tab), because R1 shows 5,940 warnings across the mobile pass and Jamie's entire usage is iPhone, all day — battery and jank are churn vectors for his whole party.
5. Add "duplicate trip structure" (clone roles/channels/places/settings into a new leg), because tours repeat their shape every 6-8 weeks and rebuild friction compounds across 6 legs/year — retention mechanic for the highest-invite-velocity persona.

### K. Confidence
- **Level:** High on the demo-vs-real gap and pricing SKU gap (both code/doc-verified); Medium on Smart Import being the conversion trigger (quality untested) and mobile perf impact (warnings observed, battery effect inferred).
- **Directly observed:** Touring demo surfaces (desktop-08, desktop2-19/20/21, mobile-08, mobile2-18), tripConverter.ts:117-130 empty ops, §7 tier/pass structure, mailto CTAs, D8 dictation-only, D11 per-trip mute, R1 render storm.
- **Needs real-user validation:** Smart Import accuracy on real venue advances (the make-or-break); whether comms-only value sustains a full leg; per-leg price elasticity.
- **Beta interview question:** "Here are five real venue advance PDFs from your last leg — watch Chravel import them: how many corrections before you'd trust it to build tomorrow's day sheet, and what would you pay per leg if it got there?"
