## Persona 16: Rosa Delgado-Smith — Pro / Music Artist Tour Manager

### A. Profile
- **Name:** Rosa Delgado-Smith
- **Age range:** 35–45
- **Location/timezone:** Nashville, TN (on tour ~200 days/yr) — CT, but lives in venue-local time
- **Industry/role:** Tour manager for a headlining artist; currently advancing a 25-city arena run
- **Tech comfort:** High-operational — lives in Master Tour, spreadsheets, group texts; not a tinkerer
- **Platform:** iPhone in hand, iPad at the production desk
- **Group size:** 80-person traveling party — band, crew, security, plus local promoter reps per city
- **Planning style:** Advance everything 6 weeks out, then re-plan nightly; the day sheet is law
- **Current tools:** Master Tour (Eventric), Google Sheets rooming lists, WhatsApp per-department threads, email advances, paper settlement folders
- **Main pain points:** Rooming-list churn, crew who never read the day sheet, settlement night chaos, six apps for one show day
- **Budget sensitivity:** Low for tools that work — tour budget absorbs $99/mo without a meeting; zero tolerance for tools that fail on show day
- **Why adopt Chravel:** The Beyoncé demo trip is literally her job on screen — roster with roles, broadcasts, channels, PDF recap [OBSERVED desktop-08]
- **Why reject Chravel:** Creating a real Pro trip and finding the roster/rooms/schedule/settlement surfaces empty — demo promised an ops platform, real trip delivers a group chat [OBSERVED — `src/utils/tripConverter.ts:118-130`]

### B. Jobs-to-Be-Done
1. When I am advancing a 25-city run, I want one place where the day sheet, rooming list, and crew roster live, so I can stop re-sending PDFs every time a hotel changes.
2. When lobby call moves 30 minutes, I want to blast only the people affected (crew, not band), so I can avoid waking the artist over a load-in change.
3. When it's settlement night, I want running per-city expense records, so I can close out with the promoter without digging through a folder of receipts.
4. When a new local hire joins in Dallas, I want to give them schedule visibility without chat-history or money visibility, so I can onboard fast without leaking the tour's internals.
5. When the tour ends, I want a clean export of everything — rooming, schedule, spend — so I can hand accounting a package instead of a shoebox.
6. When I'm side-stage with one bar of signal, I want the day sheet to load anyway, so I can answer "what time is bus call" without walking back to production.

### C. Screener Answers
| Question | Answer |
|---|---|
| Trips last 12 months | 4+ (each tour leg is dozens of city-stops) |
| Typical group size | 16+ (80-person party) |
| Main tools | Master Tour, Google Sheets, WhatsApp, email |
| Primary device | iOS (iPhone + iPad) |
| 45-min call? | Yes — if it might fix my workflow, I'll find 45 minutes on a drive day |
| Role in group | Primary planner |
| Pro-ops responsibility | Yes, I own logistics |

### D. Full Survey Answers

**About you.** Tour manager, 15 years in. I advance the run, build day sheets, manage 80 people who all think their question is the only question, and settle with the promoter every night. My office is a production hallway.

**Most recent group trip.** Current arena run, 25 cities. Kicked off when routing locked. Involved: artist camp, band, 50+ crew, security, management, local promoters. Most frustrating: rooming list changed four times in one week and three different versions were circulating on three threads — a guitar tech showed up to the wrong hotel in Atlanta. What went well: my per-department WhatsApp threads mostly held, and Master Tour kept the schedule of record. Apps used: Master Tour, WhatsApp (6 threads), Google Sheets, email, Venmo for crew per-diem oddities, FlightAware. That's six-plus. After the first plan? The plan is never done — it changes every single night at 11pm.

**Planning workflow.** Idea→booked: routing comes from the agent, I advance each venue and hotel by email, build the master sheet. During: day sheet goes out at midnight, then I spend the day correcting people who didn't read it. Post: settlement reconciliation, expense package to business management. Decisions stick in email threads with promoters; crew non-responders are why broadcasts with delivery tracking matter to me — I need to know WHO hasn't seen the bus-call change. Example doc: my rooming sheet has 80 rows × 25 tabs, one per city.

**Feature areas.**
- *Create/Invite:* The Touring category with its own roster terminology is the right instinct [OBSERVED desktop-08 role chips: Artists, Performers, Tour Manager, Crew]. Invite with approval-required and max-uses is right for local hires [OBSERVED desktop2-11 per evidence log L3].
- *Places:* Basecamp = the hotel, per city. Demo had no basecamp set, which is the one thing I'd set first [OBSERVED desktop2-15]. I need this per-city, not per-trip — a 25-city run has 25 basecamps. That's a real model question.
- *Calendar/Itinerary:* If it can hold load-in / soundcheck / doors / settlement times per day, it's a day sheet. PDF export of it is the artifact I distribute [OBSERVED desktop2-21].
- *Polls:* Cute for the crew dinner. Honestly the demo poll ("Where should we eat before the concert?") is the realistic use [OBSERVED desktop2-16]. Not why I'd pay.
- *Tasks:* The demo tasks say "make sure all clothes are packed" — that's a vacation task, not an ops task [OBSERVED desktop2-17]. Mine would be "advance Kansas City catering rider, due Thursday, assigned to PM."
- *Smart Import:* I'd paste hotel confirmation emails, the routing spreadsheet, and venue advance PDFs. If it can ingest a 25-row routing sheet into calendar entries, that's my setup day saved.
- *AI Concierge:* "Send an urgent broadcast: meet at the lobby at 7pm" is in the suggested prompts — whoever wrote that has been on a bus [OBSERVED desktop2-12]. I'd ask "what time is bus call tomorrow and who hasn't confirmed rooms?"
- *AI Trust:* Broken the first time it tells a crew member the wrong lobby call. One wrong time and I'm back to texting. The "Save to Trip?" confirm card helps [OBSERVED — ground truth §6].
- *Settings priorities:* Per-role notification routing, per-trip mute for the band (exists now — good [OBSERVED — `src/hooks/useTripNotificationMute.ts:26-94`]), and who-can-see-what.

**Pro/Events branch.** Professional-grade means: it does not go down on show day, changes propagate to exactly the right people with receipts (delivery tracking), and money math is auditable. Control vs automation: I want automation drafting and ME sending — no AI auto-blasting my crew. Trust is created by: delivery tracking on broadcasts, role-based visibility that actually enforces, and export I can hand to business management. Trust is destroyed by: demo data that doesn't exist when I build my own tour [OBSERVED — D7, `tripConverter.ts:118-130`], and settlement surfaces that are stubbed. Settlement is money. You don't ship a half-built money feature to touring people [OBSERVED — ground truth §6 "per-diem/compliance/settlement partially stubbed"].

**Money.** Per-diem is cash or Venmo; crew floats get reconciled at settlement. Reimbursement talk is constant and awkward. Plan changes go out via broadcast-style WhatsApp messages today, no read receipts — Chravel's delivery tracking is genuinely better on paper. There is always one planner: me. Hotels are decided by budget + proximity to venue, not by vote. Conversations live in six WhatsApp threads.

**Willingness to pay.** Team plan — Growth $99/mo, tour-budget line item, or Enterprise if QuickBooks export is real. But only after a real trip looks like the demo. Today I'd trial and stall.

**Ratings.**
- Likelihood to use on next trip: 3/5 — I'd pilot a leg, not the tour.
- Clarity: 4/5 — the demo communicates the vision instantly.
- Time saved: 2/5 today, 5/5 if real Pro trips had real ops surfaces.
- AI trust: 3/5 — confirm cards help; one wrong bus call kills it.
- Would invite: 3/5 — inviting 80 people is a commitment I make once.
- Mobile usability: 3/5 — tab strip works but my crew lives on phones; it must be flawless.
- Web usability: 4/5 — production-desk view is solid.
- Pricing fit: 4/5 — $99 is nothing against tour budget IF it delivers.
- NPS-style sentiment: 3/5 — hopeful, burned-cautious.

**Wrap-up.** Change one thing: make a real Pro trip look like the Beyoncé demo — roster, schedule, rooms, settlement, populated and editable. Recommend when: a full leg runs on it without me keeping a shadow spreadsheet. Anything else: rooming-list CSV import/export is table stakes; every hotel sends me Excel. Follow-up: Yes.

## Persona 17: Ben Châu — Pro / Film Production Coordinator

### A. Profile
- **Name:** Ben Châu
- **Age range:** 28–38
- **Location/timezone:** Vancouver, BC — PT; 60-person crew across 3 locations
- **Industry/role:** Production coordinator on an 8-week feature shoot
- **Tech comfort:** High — MacBook + iPhone, fluent in Movie Magic, StudioBinder, Excel macros

- **Current tools:** StudioBinder/Movie Magic for call sheets, Excel for everything else, WhatsApp department threads, email blasts, Dropbox for continuity photos
- **Main pain points:** 11pm schedule revisions fan out across five channels; confirming receipt of a revised call sheet; union turnaround math done by hand; dead zones at remote locations
- **Budget sensitivity:** Production buys tools per show; $49–99/mo is petty cash IF it replaces a line item
- **Why adopt Chravel:** Smart Import of production schedules (PDF/Excel) → calendar could kill his most hated nightly task; role-channels map to departments
- **Why reject Chravel:** No call-sheet construct, no offline guarantee at remote locations, and a real Pro trip ships with empty schedule surfaces [OBSERVED — `src/utils/tripConverter.ts:118-130`]

### B. Jobs-to-Be-Done
1. When the AD locks tomorrow's schedule at 11pm, I want to push the revised day to all 60 crew with proof of receipt, so I can stop chasing "did you see the new call time?"
2. When I get the one-liner schedule as a PDF, I want to import it into a shared calendar in minutes, so I can stop re-typing scenes into three tools.
3. When we company-move between locations, I want maps/directions and parking notes attached to the day, so background actors stop calling the office.
4. When I'm at a remote location with no LTE, I want today's schedule readable offline, so the tool doesn't die exactly when I need it.
5. When continuity needs reference photos, I want a searchable shared media hub per shoot day, so we stop trawling a Dropbox folder named "FINAL_v3".
6. When turnaround is tight, I want the schedule to flag a 10-hour violation before the union rep does, so I can fix it at 11pm instead of 7am.

### D. Full Survey Answers

**About you.** Production coordinator. I'm the person who turns the AD's schedule into 60 people standing in the right parking lot at 6am. I distribute call sheets, manage travel/housing for cast, and absorb every "where do I park" text.

What went well: department WhatsApp threads are fast; StudioBinder distribution is reliable. Apps: StudioBinder, Movie Magic, Excel, WhatsApp, email, Dropbox, Google Maps pins. Seven. After the first plan: the schedule changed 31 times in 8 weeks. That's the job.

**Planning workflow.** Idea→booked: greenlight → location scouts → one-liner schedule → day-out-of-days → crew deal memos. During: daily call sheet cycle — prelim at lunch, final by 10pm, revisions god-willing never. Post: wrap binder. Decisions stick in email with the UPM; non-responders get phone calls because the call sheet is not optional. Example doc: the call sheet itself — one page, sacred, versioned.

**Feature areas.**
- *Create/Invite:* "Productions" is literally a Pro category [OBSERVED — ground truth §4]. Good sign. Invite-with-approval fits day-players [OBSERVED desktop2-11 class, L3].
- *Places:* Three locations means basecamp-per-location; demo shows a single Trip Base Camp, unset [OBSERVED desktop2-15]. Get Directions inline is genuinely useful for company moves [OBSERVED desktop2-15].
- *Calendar/Itinerary:* This is where I map "day sheet" → call sheet. It can hold timed events with locations [OBSERVED — ground truth §6]. But a call sheet is more than events: weather, hospital, parking, walkie channels, advance schedule. As a calendar it works; as a call sheet it's a stretch [SIMULATED RISK — fit gap, no call-sheet construct in feature inventory].
- *Polls:* Crew meal preference, wrap-party venue. Marginal [OBSERVED desktop2-16 renders fine].
- *Tasks:* Per-department checklists with due dates and assignment — actually useful for wrap-out [OBSERVED desktop2-17].
- *Smart Import:* THE feature. I'd paste: the one-liner PDF, location agreements, cast travel itineraries, hotel confirmations. PDF/ICS/CSV/images pipeline with preview + cherry-pick is the right shape [OBSERVED — ground truth §6 Smart Import]. If it round-trips a Movie Magic PDF into calendar days, I'm a customer. If it mangles one call time, I'm gone — and replay idempotency is flagged as only partially tested, so a retried import duplicating shared calendar entries is a live risk [OBSERVED — ground truth §10.8].
- *AI Concierge:* I'd ask "what's tomorrow's earliest call and which department?" and "draft a broadcast: company move to Location B, parking at the church lot." Suggested prompts already lean this way [OBSERVED desktop2-12].
- *AI Trust:* Broken instantly if it states a call time that's one revision stale. Stale data is worse than no data on a film set.
- *Settings priorities:* Notification routing by department/role; quiet hours that respect turnaround (do NOT ping crew during their 10 hours).

**Pro/Events branch.** Professional-grade means versioned truth: one current schedule, visible revision history, receipts on distribution. Control vs automation: automation for ingest and drafting; a human presses send on anything crew-facing. Trust comes from: import accuracy I can verify in a preview screen before commit (the cherry-pick preview is exactly right [OBSERVED — ground truth §6]), delivery tracking on broadcasts, and offline resilience. There IS a real service worker — app-shell precache, offline fallback page, background-sync queue for writes [OBSERVED — `public/sw.js`] — but Supabase reads are network-first, so whether today's schedule is readable in a dead zone depends on what got cached before I lost signal. That's a coin-flip I can't take on set; needs a deliberate "pin this day offline" feature [SIMULATED RISK].

**Money.** Production pays vendors; crew per-diem is accounting's problem, not mine — I'd ignore the Payments tab on a shoot. Plan changes communicate via call sheet + department heads. One planner? The AD owns the schedule, I own distribution — Chravel would need both of us as admins. Hotels are decided by the travel coordinator and budget; nobody votes. Conversations live in WhatsApp and the production office doorway.

**Willingness to pay.** Team plan — Pro Starter $49/mo per show works as a line item; Growth $99 if logistics features mature. Per-show (not per-month) billing would honestly fit production accounting better.

- **Limit/CTA triggering upgrade:** Pro trip creation gate when spinning up the shoot.
- **CTA that would annoy:** Consumer upsell modals ("your trip gets serious") inside a working production.

### J. Top 5 Fixes for This Persona
1. Add idempotency keys to Smart Import commits because a retried import can duplicate shared calendar data (TEST_GAPS via ground truth §10.8) — Ben's single dealbreaker, causing set-wide schedule corruption.
2. Add a "pin this day offline" affordance on top of the existing workbox SW because network-first Supabase reads leave today's schedule uncached exactly at remote locations (`public/sw.js`), causing on-set failure.
3. Build a call-sheet/day-template layer on Calendar for the Productions category because Ben's schedule needs structured blocks (location, parking, hospital, turnaround), not just events, causing him to keep StudioBinder otherwise.
4. Support multiple/per-day basecamps because a 3-location shoot can't express itself in one Trip Base Camp (`desktop2-15`, `BasecampSelector.tsx`), causing the Places tab to be ignored.
5. Ship Pro self-serve checkout (D9) because production accounting can pay instantly but Ben cannot start a paid pilot tonight, causing evaluation momentum loss at 11pm — his actual decision hour.

- **Directly observed:** Demo pro surfaces (desktop-12, desktop2-12..21, mobile-13, mobile2-12), Smart Import pipeline design (ground truth §6), SW/offline scaffolding (public/sw.js), empty real-trip ops (tripConverter.ts:118-130), R1 mobile perf storm.
- **Needs real-user validation:** Import accuracy on Movie Magic/EP exports; offline behavior at real dead-zone locations; whether crews accept a ninth app.
- **Beta interview question:** "Bring last week's one-liner PDF — let's import it live and you tell me the first error you'd fire a tool for."

## Persona 18: Stephanie Müller — Pro / Corporate Offsite Planner

### A. Profile
- **Name:** Stephanie Müller
- **Age range:** 32–42
- **Location/timezone:** San Francisco, CA — PT
- **Industry/role:** Head of People Ops at a 600-person tech company; owns the 150-person annual retreat plus exec offsites
- **Tech comfort:** High — desktop-first Chrome power user, iPhone secondary; lives in Notion, Google Workspace, Slack
- **Group size:** 150 attendees (retreat); 10–20 (exec offsites)
- **Planning style:** Project plan with workback schedule, vendor RFPs, registration forms, comms calendar
- **Current tools:** Google Forms (dietary/flights), Sheets, Slack channel, Eventbrite-ish registration once, TravelPerk for booking, email for vendors
- **Main pain points:** Collecting structured info (dietary, flight numbers, room shares) from 150 people; RSVP tracking; comms that nobody reads; stitching forms→sheets→slack by hand
- **Budget sensitivity:** Medium — needs invoicing and procurement approval, not credit cards; line item must survive finance review
- **Why adopt Chravel:** Broadcasts + calendar + polls in one place per event, with a roster — replaces the Slack-channel-plus-five-sheets sprawl [OBSERVED desktop-12 demo is literally a corporate retreat]
- **Why reject Chravel:** No structured forms/registration, no SSO, vendor security review friction

### B. Jobs-to-Be-Done
1. When I announce the retreat, I want RSVP plus structured intake (dietary, flight info, room-share preference) in one flow, so I can stop reconciling three Google Forms against a roster sheet.
2. When the agenda changes, I want one broadcast that I know people saw, so I can stop posting in Slack, email, AND a printed sign.
3. When execs ask "who hasn't booked flights," I want a live completeness view, so I can chase the 12 stragglers instead of emailing all 150.
4. When procurement reviews a new vendor, I want SOC2-style answers and invoicing, so the tool survives our security and finance gates.
5. When the retreat ends, I want an archive (agenda, photos, decisions) I can hand to next year's planner, so the playbook compounds.
6. When employees use the tool, I want SSO via our IdP, so I'm not managing 150 passwords or personal-Gmail logins.

### C. Screener Answers
| Question | Answer |
|---|---|
| Trips last 12 months | 2–3 (1 retreat + exec offsites) |
| Typical group size | 16+ (150) |
| Main tools | Google Forms/Sheets, Slack, TravelPerk, email |
| Primary device | Desktop-first |
| 45-min call? | Yes — this is my literal job |
| Role in group | Primary planner |
| Pro-ops responsibility | Yes, I own logistics |

### D. Full Survey Answers

**About you.** People Ops. I run the company retreat — 150 people, 3 days, one hotel buyout — plus quarterly exec offsites. I'm the person who knows everyone's dietary restrictions and nobody's gratitude.

**Most recent group trip.** Last retreat: kicked off by exec team picking dates. Involved: me, an EA, a venue, 150 employees with opinions. Most frustrating: collecting flight details — a Google Form, 60% completion, then two weeks of Slack DMs for the rest. What went well: the agenda Notion page; the photographer's shared album. Apps: Google Forms, Sheets, Slack, email, TravelPerk, Notion, a WhatsApp for the planning pod. Seven. After the first plan: three agenda revisions, one venue room swap, and a dietary spreadsheet I updated until the morning of.

**Planning workflow.** Idea→booked: dates → budget approval → venue RFP → contract → registration form → flights → agenda → comms. During: I am a human help desk. Post: survey, photo archive, retro doc. Decisions stick in email with the venue and Slack with execs; non-responders are my whole life — I chase by department head. Example: my "Retreat Master" sheet has 11 tabs.

**Feature areas.**
- *Create/Invite:* The Eli Lilly C-Suite Retreat demo is precisely my exec-offsite shape — Work category, Executives roles, 32 members [OBSERVED desktop-12]. Invite links with approval and expiry work for employees [OBSERVED L3]. For 150 people I'd want domain-restricted or SSO-backed join, not a forwardable link [SIMULATED RISK].
- *Places:* Venue as basecamp, dinner options saved — fine [OBSERVED desktop2-15 class].
- *Calendar/Itinerary:* Agenda blocks with locations — yes. PDF recap of agenda+members is my printed-program replacement [OBSERVED desktop2-21].
- *Polls:* Genuinely useful — session topics, activity sign-ups, dinner choice. Realtime counts with a Leading badge is exactly the engagement bait employees respond to [OBSERVED desktop2-16].
- *Tasks:* Planning-pod workback list with assignments [OBSERVED desktop2-17].
- *Smart Import:* I'd paste the venue BEO PDF, rooming block confirmation, and catering schedule. Useful but not my core gap.
- *AI Concierge:* "Who hasn't RSVPed?" and "summarize dietary restrictions" — except there's no structured intake for it to summarize. The data model is the gap, not the AI.
- *AI Trust:* Broken if it tells an employee the wrong session room. Also: anything AI says to MY employees reflects on ME.
- *Settings priorities:* SSO, admin visibility controls, notification batching (150 people × broadcast = do not melt phones — and the fanout architecture is a documented scale concern [OBSERVED — ground truth §10.4]).

**Pro/Events branch.** Professional-grade means: it survives my security questionnaire, finance can pay an invoice, and admin roles are real. Control vs automation: automation for reminders and summaries; control over anything employee-facing. Trust is created by: role-based permissions that match an org (pro_admin/editor/viewer maps cleanly [OBSERVED — `permissionMatrix.generated.ts:92`]), audit-friendly exports, and — honestly — a sales process. Here's my contrarian take: everyone mocks the mailto-style Pro sales motion [OBSERVED — D9], but for ME a "contact sales" motion is FINE, even preferable — procurement requires a human, a security doc, and an invoice anyway. I was never going to put this on a corporate card. What I can't survive is no SSO and no forms — those aren't sales-motion problems, they're product gaps.

**Money.** I don't collect money from attendees — company pays. The Payments tab is irrelevant for the retreat (maybe exec dinner splits, never). Plan changes go through broadcast + Slack mirror. One planner? Me plus an EA — need 2 admins minimum. Hotels/restaurants are decided by budget and contract, then polls for choice-within-constraints. Conversations live in Slack; Chravel would have to defeat Slack inertia for attendees [SIMULATED RISK — biggest adoption risk].

**Willingness to pay.** Team plan. Growth $99/mo passes without blinking IF security review passes; Enterprise with SSO is the realistic SKU. 150 attendees also exceeds Growth's 100-seat/100-attendee event framing — I'd need the 200-attendee Growth event cap or Enterprise [OBSERVED — ground truth §7].

**Ratings.**
- Likelihood next trip: 3/5 — exec offsite pilot plausible this quarter; retreat needs forms/SSO.
- Clarity: 4/5 — the corporate demo sold the shape immediately.
- Time saved: 3/5 — broadcasts/agenda save real time; forms gap keeps my sheets alive.
- AI trust: 3/5 — fine for summaries, watched closely for employee-facing answers.
- Would invite: 4/5 — inviting employees is my job; the tool just has to not embarrass me.
- Mobile usability: 3/5 — attendees are mobile; tab strip is okay, not great.
- Web usability: 5/5 — desktop planning view is where I live and it's strong.
- Pricing fit: 3/5 — needs an Enterprise conversation, which I'm fine having.
- NPS-style sentiment: 3/5.

**Wrap-up.** Change one thing: structured intake forms (custom fields per attendee, completion tracking). Recommend when: one exec offsite runs end-to-end without my master sheet. Anything else: give me CSV export of the roster + responses; HR systems eat CSV. Follow-up: Yes.

### E. Web Flow Walkthrough
- **Discovery/landing:** "For Teams" nav link exists [OBSERVED desktop-22 per evidence log]; hero mentions Team Travel [OBSERVED desktop-01]. I'd click For Teams first.
- **Signup/onboarding:** Email/Google/Apple only — no SSO/SAML [OBSERVED — ground truth §3]. For a 150-person corporate rollout that's a security-review flag on day one [SIMULATED RISK — procurement reality].
- **Pro creation:** Work category with Executives terminology demoed [OBSERVED desktop-12]. Real Pro trips start with empty roster/ops surfaces [OBSERVED — `tripConverter.ts:118-130`, D7] — for me less fatal than for a tour manager since my "ops" are agenda + comms + intake, and agenda/comms are real features; intake doesn't exist for anyone.
- **Feature usage:** Broadcasts with recipient targeting and delivery tracking is my killer feature [OBSERVED — ground truth §6; desktop-08 class subviews]. Calendar/agenda renders well [OBSERVED desktop-12 class]. Polls realtime [OBSERVED desktop2-16]. PDF Recap with Members section + "emails and phone numbers hidden" — good privacy default for sharing beyond the company [OBSERVED desktop2-21].
- **Forms gap:** Nothing in the feature inventory does structured per-attendee intake (dietary/flight/room-share custom fields with completion tracking) — polls are single-question, tasks aren't data collection [OBSERVED — ground truth §6 feature table has no forms construct]. This is my #1 product gap; today it forces me back to Google Forms + reconciliation.
- **Pricing reaction:** Tiers clear; mailto/contact-sales for Pro is acceptable-to-preferred for procurement [OBSERVED — D9; contrarian]. What's missing from pricing is the word "SSO" and a security/trust page — that's what my CISO will ask for [SIMULATED RISK].
- **Web positives:** Corporate demo realism [OBSERVED desktop-12]; broadcast targeting; recap export; role model fits orgs.
- **Web pain points:** No forms; no SSO; notification fanout at 150-person scale is a documented architectural concern [OBSERVED — §10.4]; attendee adoption vs Slack [SIMULATED RISK].

### F. Mobile / PWA Flow Walkthrough
- **First impression:** The Eli Lilly retreat on mobile is clean — title, venue, Demo Mode banner, chat front and center [OBSERVED mobile-13].
- **Navigation:** Horizontal tab strip; my attendees will find Chat and Calendar, and statistically nothing else [OBSERVED mobile-13; SIMULATED RISK on discovery].
- **Chat/input:** Composer fine; employees know how to chat [OBSERVED mobile-13].
- **Forms/modals:** N/A — the forms I need don't exist; existing modals render fine in demo [OBSERVED mobile2-11 class].
- **Invite link flow:** Forwardable links worry me for a company event — anyone with the link reaches the join gate; approval-required mitigates [OBSERVED L3; leak risk SIMULATED RISK].
- **Perceived speed:** Demo responsive; the documented mobile duplicate-key render storm is the kind of jank employees screenshot and post in Slack [OBSERVED — R1].
- **Thumb reach:** Bottom composer good; nine-tab strip requires horizontal swiping attendees won't do [OBSERVED mobile2-12 class].
- **Mobile positives:** Attendee view is essentially a nice group chat with an agenda — that's 90% of what attendees need.
- **Mobile pain points:** Tab discoverability; no app-store-installed-app expectation management (PWA vs native confusion for non-technical staff) [SIMULATED RISK]; R1 jank risk [OBSERVED].

### H. Emotional Reaction
- **Impressed by:** The corporate retreat demo being a real scenario, not lorem ipsum [OBSERVED desktop-12]; broadcast delivery tracking; PDF recap privacy defaults.
- **Confused by:** Whether "events" tier caps (100/200 attendees) apply to my Pro trip or only Event-type trips; where forms should be.
- **Annoyed by:** Re-explaining to every vendor that I need SSO and an invoice — Chravel's site doesn't preempt either.
- **Would abandon when:** The retreat intake still requires Google Forms — at that point Chravel is a fourth tool, not a consolidation.
- **Would invite others?** Yes — the EA and exec assistants immediately for a pilot offsite; 150 employees only post-security-review.
- **[SYNTHETIC QUOTE]** "Everyone's mad there's no checkout button for Pro. I don't want a checkout button — I want a security questionnaire answered and an invoice. What I can't work around is no forms and no SSO."

### I. Conversion Scores
- **Activation:** 7/10 — exec-offsite pilot is low-friction and the demo maps exactly.
- **Invite likelihood:** 6/10 — planning pod yes; company-wide gated on review.
- **Day-7 retention:** 6/10 — offsite pilot would keep her through an event cycle.
- **Paid conversion:** 6/10 — budget and motion fit; product gaps (forms/SSO) are the blockers, not price.
- **NPS:** +15 — closest-to-buying persona in this batch, with named blockers.
- **Would they pay?** Yes.
- **What:** Growth $99/mo now for pilots; Enterprise (SSO, invoicing) for the retreat.
- **Feature creating WTP:** Broadcasts with delivery tracking + roster, replacing Slack-blast anarchy.
- **Limit/CTA triggering upgrade:** Attendee caps (100 on Starter/FC events) the moment the 150-person retreat loads [OBSERVED — ground truth §7].
- **CTA that would annoy:** Consumer upsell modals ("upgrade when your trip gets serious") in a corporate workspace.

### J. Top 5 Fixes for This Persona
1. Add structured attendee intake forms (custom fields, required/optional, completion dashboard) because Stephanie cannot collect dietary/flight/room-share data in-product, causing her to retain Google Forms and reject consolidation — her stated dealbreaker (no forms construct in `src/` feature inventory).
2. Make notification fanout async with batching before any 150-person broadcast because the current fanout blocks the INSERT transaction at scale (ground truth §10.4), causing exactly the comms moment she buys the product for to be its weakest path.
3. Add domain-restricted/SSO-backed invite joins because a forwardable `/join/{token}` link is a containment risk for a company event (`src/pages/JoinTrip.tsx`), causing security review failure.
4. Publish a security/trust page and invoice billing path for Growth/Enterprise because Stephanie's procurement motion needs collateral, not checkout (D9 — her contrarian acceptance makes collateral the actual bottleneck).
5. Add option-capacity caps to Polls because activity sign-ups (30 spots kayaking) are her real poll use case and unlimited options over-subscribe (`src/components/poll/`), causing manual reconciliation again.

### K. Confidence
- **Level:** High on the forms/SSO gaps and broadcast value (feature inventory + screenshots are unambiguous); Medium on attendee adoption vs Slack.
- **Directly observed:** Corporate demo (desktop-12, mobile-13), polls/tasks/recap surfaces (desktop2-16/17/21), permission model and fanout risk (code/audit docs), absence of forms/SSO (ground truth §3, §6).
- **Needs real-user validation:** Whether attendees adopt a second chat app during a 3-day event; pilot data on broadcast read rates vs Slack.
- **Beta interview question:** "Show me last year's retreat intake form and master sheet — which columns would Chravel have to own before you'd delete the sheet?"


---

## Persona 19: Victoria Ashford-Lee — Pro / Executive Assistant, Confidential Executive Travel

### A. Profile
- **Name:** Victoria Ashford-Lee
- **Age range:** 38–50
- **Location/timezone:** London/NYC split — GMT/ET; plans across both
- **Industry/role:** Executive assistant to a public-company CEO; plans confidential exec travel (board offsites, M&A roadshows, family-adjacent trips)
- **Tech comfort:** High-discretion power user — desktop Outlook/Concur mastery, iPhone always; adopts slowly, vets thoroughly
- **Group size:** 2–8 executives plus security/drivers per leg
- **Planning style:** Need-to-know everything; one immaculate itinerary per principal; redundancy on redundancy
- **Current tools:** Outlook + shared calendar, Word itineraries as locked PDFs, Concur, TripIt Pro (personal), WhatsApp with security lead, phone calls
- **Main pain points:** Itinerary leaks (forwarded PDFs), version drift across principals' copies, coordinating drivers/security without exposing the full picture, after-hours changes
- **Budget sensitivity:** Price-insensitive, trust-sensitive — client-billable/company card; one privacy incident costs more than any subscription
- **Why adopt Chravel:** Role-gated visibility (pro_viewer read-only) + contained guests could replace forwarded PDFs with scoped live access [OBSERVED — `permissionMatrix.generated.ts`]
- **Why reject Chravel:** Any surface where a non-member can see trip names, members, or movements — and any invite link that anyone-with-link can open [OBSERVED/SIMULATED — see E]

### B. Jobs-to-Be-Done
1. When I plan a confidential board offsite, I want each participant to see only their own logistics, so I can prevent the full picture from existing on anyone's phone but mine.
2. When the principal's schedule changes mid-flight, I want drivers and security updated instantly without group-chat chatter, so I can keep movements quiet and current.
3. When I add a local driver for one day, I want read-only, time-boxed access to one pickup, so I can avoid sending an itinerary PDF that lives forever in his WhatsApp.
4. When an exec's spouse or a vendor needs a sliver of info, I want a contained guest state with zero resource access, so containment is the default, not a setting I might miss.
5. When the trip ends, I want to verify and revoke all access, so there's no residue.
6. When anything is shared, I want to know exactly what an outsider with a link can see, so I never discover the answer from a journalist.

### C. Screener Answers
| Question | Answer |
|---|---|
| Trips last 12 months | 4+ (monthly exec travel) |
| Typical group size | 2–4 / 5–8 |
| Main tools | Outlook, Concur, locked PDFs, WhatsApp, TripIt Pro |
| Primary device | Desktop-first, iPhone constant |
| 45-min call? | Maybe — under NDA, no recordings |
| Role in group | Primary planner |
| Pro-ops responsibility | Yes, I own logistics |

### D. Full Survey Answers

**About you.** EA to a chief executive, fifteen years across two continents. I plan travel that occasionally moves markets if it leaks. My job is that nothing surprising ever happens to my principal, including from his own tools.

**Most recent group trip.** A board offsite — 8 principals, 2 security, 3 drivers, 1 venue under NDA. Kicked off by a board-calendar decision. Most frustrating: keeping eleven people's versions of the itinerary current without sending eleven full itineraries — drivers get pickup windows, not the agenda; spouses get dinner time, not the room block. What went well: my color-coded master in Word, and the security lead's discipline. Apps: Outlook, Word/PDF, Concur, WhatsApp, phone. Five, deliberately few. After the first plan: four revisions, each requiring me to re-issue scoped excerpts by hand.

**Planning workflow.** Idea→booked: principal's office decides → I hold everything in my head and one encrypted file until contracts → then scoped distribution. During: I am the single source of truth; changes go out person-by-person. Post: access revocation, file cleanup, debrief with security. Decisions stick in email with me only. Non-responders don't exist at this level — but over-responders (reply-all) do. Example doc: a 14-page master itinerary that exactly three people have ever seen in full.

**Feature areas.**
- *Create/Invite:* Approval-required join, link expiry, max-uses — these are the right primitives [OBSERVED desktop2-11/L3]. But the existence of a shareable link at all is the threat model: anyone holding `/join/{token}` reaches a trip preview showing name, dates, destination, cover, member count before any authentication [OBSERVED — ground truth §5; `src/pages/TripPreview.tsx:13-46` returns name/destination/dates/member_count via the `get-trip-preview` edge function]. For "Project Alpine — Zurich, March 12–14" that preview IS the leak, even without member names. I need an option for zero-preview invites.
- *Places:* Basecamp marked Private ("Only you can see this") for personal location — the instinct exists [OBSERVED desktop2-15 "Personal Base Camp — Private"]. Good sign.
- *Calendar/Itinerary:* Fine as a structure; the question is per-person visibility scoping, which I see no evidence of — everyone in a trip sees the trip calendar [OBSERVED — ground truth §6; per-item visibility absent → gap].
- *Polls:* Never. Executives do not vote in apps.
- *Tasks:* For my own checklist with the second EA, possibly.
- *Smart Import:* I'd paste flight confirmations — but forwarding my principal's PNR through a third-party AI parser requires a data-processing answer first [SIMULATED RISK — vendor trust, not a bug].
- *AI Concierge:* I'd ask logistics ("driving time JFK→venue at 5pm Friday"). I would never let it see the full trip context for a sensitive trip; an AI that "knows your trip, your members" [OBSERVED desktop2-12 caption] is precisely what I need to be able to turn OFF per trip — and a `privacy_mode`/`ai_access_enabled` flag exists in the trip model, defaulting to enabled [OBSERVED — `src/utils/tripConverter.ts:137-138`]. I'd need that surfaced as a first-class setting at creation.
- *AI Trust:* Broken by any indication trip data trains or leaves the tenant; broken by one hallucinated time delivered to a principal.
- *Settings priorities:* Access review (who can see what, one screen), revocation, no emails exposed to other members. The PDF recap's "Emails and phone numbers hidden" default is the single most trust-building line in the product [OBSERVED desktop2-21].

**Pro/Events branch.** Professional-grade means: I can enumerate exactly who can see each datum, prove it, and revoke it. Control vs automation: 95/5 — automation may draft, never send, never share. Trust is created by contained defaults — and here is my contrarian position: `consumer_guest` having ZERO resource access [OBSERVED — `permissionMatrix.generated.ts:44-50`, D15] — which other reviewers will call a bug ("guests get no value") — is a FEATURE for me. Containment-by-default is exactly correct for my use. Likewise `pro_viewer` read-only for drivers [OBSERVED — `permissionMatrix.generated.ts:92`]. What destroys trust: the documented wildcard CORS on 26 edge functions and a demo account holding super-admin [OBSERVED — ground truth §10.3] — if I knew that, and I'd ask, the evaluation ends until fixed.

**Money.** No splitting, ever — company card and invoices. Venmo deeplinks are for other lives. Plan changes are communicated person-to-person by me. One planner: always me. Hotels are decided by security review and the principal's preferences. Conversations live in my Outlook and nowhere else, which is the point.

**Willingness to pay.** Client-billable / team plan — price is irrelevant within reason; Pro Starter $49 or Growth $99 passes without a thought IF the privacy surface passes my audit. I'd happily pay more for a "confidential trip" mode.

**Ratings.**
- Likelihood next trip: 2/5 — not until I can verify the privacy surface end-to-end myself.
- Clarity: 4/5 — the product explains itself well.
- Time saved: 3/5 — scoped live access would genuinely beat re-issuing PDFs.
- AI trust: 2/5 — group-aware AI is a liability until per-trip AI off is a visible control.
- Would invite: 2/5 — each invite is an exposure decision.
- Mobile usability: 3/5 — adequate; I plan on desktop.
- Web usability: 4/5 — clean, professional.
- Pricing fit: 4/5 — price is not the variable.
- NPS-style sentiment: 2/5 — interested, nowhere near trusting.

**Wrap-up.** Change one thing: a confidential-trip mode — no link previews, no member-visible roster beyond admins, AI off, invite by direct named grant only. Recommend when: a security audit I can hand to our CISO exists. Anything else: never show my principal's name in any unauthenticated surface, ever. Follow-up: Maybe — no recording.

### E. Web Flow Walkthrough
- **Discovery/landing:** Consumer-bright marketing ("Group Chat Travel App") makes me assume it's not for me; "Team Travel" keeps me reading [OBSERVED desktop-01, L1].
- **Signup/onboarding:** Standard auth renders [OBSERVED desktop-04/05]. Google/Apple OAuth — I'd use a work identity; no SSO is a gap but tolerable at my party size [OBSERVED — ground truth §3].
- **Privacy surface audit (my real walkthrough):**
  - Trip preview route `/trip/:tripId/preview` serves trip name, destination, dates, cover image, and member count to ANYONE via an edge function, pre-auth — it does NOT expose member names or itinerary items [OBSERVED — `src/pages/TripPreview.tsx:13-46`]. Partial pass: no exec names unless the planner put one in the trip title (which planners do — "Smith Family — Aspen"). I would reject any trip-naming that leaks, and I'd demand a preview-off toggle [SIMULATED RISK].
  - Invite links: expiry, max-uses, approval-required exist [OBSERVED desktop2-11/L3]. Anyone-with-link sees the preview before the approval gate — the gate protects joining, not knowing [OBSERVED — ground truth §5 flow description].
  - Membership enforcement: "trip existence ≠ trip access," RLS-checked membership is an explicit engineering invariant [OBSERVED — ground truth §8] — the right architecture; enforcement quality is unverifiable here [HYPOTHESIS — needs pen test].
  - consumer_guest zero access = containment default [OBSERVED — D15]. Approve.
  - PDF recap hides emails/phones by default and never includes chat/AI history [OBSERVED desktop2-21]. Strongly approve.
  - Known security register: wildcard CORS on 26 functions, demo super-admin account, unauthenticated seed function [OBSERVED — ground truth §10.3]. Disqualifying until remediated for my tier of client.
- **Pro creation:** Work category fits; real trips ops-empty matters little to me — I need chat, calendar, roles, not rooming engines [OBSERVED — D7, low impact for this persona].
- **Pricing reaction:** Contact-sales Pro motion is fine — I'd be asking for a security call anyway [OBSERVED — D9; aligned with Stephanie, opposite of Rosa/Carlos].
- **Web positives:** Role model, containment defaults, recap privacy line, Private personal basecamp [OBSERVED desktop2-15/21].
- **Web pain points:** Link-preview exposure [OBSERVED — TripPreview.tsx]; no per-item visibility scoping; AI-on-by-default with group context [OBSERVED — tripConverter.ts:137-138 defaults]; published security findings [OBSERVED — §10.3].

### H. Emotional Reaction
- **Impressed by:** Containment defaults (guest zero-access, viewer read-only), "Emails and phone numbers hidden" recap default, Private personal basecamp — someone here thinks about exposure [OBSERVED].
- **Confused by:** Why `privacy_mode` and `ai_access_enabled` exist in the data model but nowhere I can see or set them.
- **Annoyed by:** The invite preview showing trip details to anyone holding a link; cheerful consumer chrome on surfaces I'd use for board logistics.
- **Would abandon when:** I see a trip name render on an unauthenticated screen, or read the CORS/super-admin findings — instantly and permanently.
- **Would invite others?** Only after my own red-team pass: a driver as pro_viewer on a dummy trip, verifying every screen he can reach.
- **[SYNTHETIC QUOTE]** "Everyone else complains the guest role can't do anything. That's the first thing this product got right for me. Now turn off the link preview and let me turn off the AI, and we can talk."

### I. Conversion Scores
- **Activation:** 4/10 — would run a dummy-trip audit before any real use.
- **Invite likelihood:** 3/10 — each invite is an exposure decision.
- **Day-7 retention:** 4/10 — survives only as a contained pilot.
- **Paid conversion:** 5/10 — money is no object; trust is the entire object.
- **NPS:** −10 — respects the primitives, cannot yet trust the surface.
- **Would they pay?** Yes, if the privacy audit passes.
- **What:** $49–99/mo client-billable without hesitation; more for a confidential mode.
- **Feature creating WTP:** Scoped live access (viewer roles) replacing forwarded PDFs.
- **Limit/CTA triggering upgrade:** None — she'd enter at Pro directly via sales.
- **CTA that would annoy:** Any upsell modal interrupting a sensitive workflow; growth-hack share prompts ("invite friends!") on a confidential trip.

### J. Top 5 Fixes for This Persona
1. Add a per-trip "no public preview" toggle because `/trip/:id/preview` serves trip name/dates/destination/member-count to anyone unauthenticated (`src/pages/TripPreview.tsx:13-46`), causing confidential trip metadata to leak to anyone holding a forwarded link.
2. Surface `ai_access_enabled`/`privacy_mode` as a visible creation-time control because they exist in the model but default open with no UI (`src/utils/tripConverter.ts:137-138`), causing group-aware AI exposure she cannot decline.
3. Remediate and disclose the security register items (wildcard CORS on 26 edge functions, demo super-admin, unauthenticated seed) because any diligence pass surfaces them (ground truth §10.3), causing immediate disqualification for confidential travel.
4. Add per-event visibility scoping on Calendar because all members currently see the whole itinerary, causing her to keep issuing scoped PDF excerpts by hand — the exact workflow Chravel should replace.
5. Enforce signed URLs + access logging on media storage because quota/access is advisory-only (ground truth §10.7), causing uploaded itinerary documents to be her single riskiest artifact in the product.

### K. Confidence
- **Level:** High on the privacy-surface findings (route code, permission matrix, audit register all read directly); Medium on persona behavior.
- **Directly observed:** TripPreview payload shape (TripPreview.tsx:13-46), permission matrix (44-50, 92), recap privacy defaults (desktop2-21), private basecamp (desktop2-15), security register (§10.3), AI-on defaults (tripConverter.ts:137-138).
- **Needs real-user validation:** Live RLS enforcement under a pro_viewer session; lock-screen push content; whether EAs accept any cloud tool for board travel.
- **Beta interview question:** "Here's a viewer-role login on a dummy trip — spend ten minutes trying to learn things you shouldn't. What did you find, and what would you need to see to trust this with a principal's itinerary?"

## Persona 20: Carlos Mendoza — Pro / Travel Concierge Company Owner

### A. Profile
- **Name:** Carlos Mendoza
- **Age range:** 40–50
- **Location/timezone:** Miami, FL — ET
- **Industry/role:** Owner of a boutique travel concierge firm; 4 staff, ~15 concurrent client itineraries (luxury leisure, incentive groups, bachelor/bachelorette upmarket)
- **Tech comfort:** Medium-high — desktop-first operator; lives in Axus/Travefy trials, Google Workspace, WhatsApp Business
- **Group size:** Per client trip 2–20; portfolio of ~15 active trips at any time
- **Planning style:** White-glove: he builds, clients consume; the deliverable IS the brand
- **Current tools:** Travefy/Axus-style itinerary builders, Canva for branded PDFs, WhatsApp Business, Sheets for trip P&L, Stripe invoices
- **Main pain points:** Itinerary tools that look like the tool's brand instead of his; juggling 15 trips across tabs; clients asking questions answered on page 2; per-client billing chaos
- **Budget sensitivity:** Low-medium — $99+/mo is fine IF it's client-facing polished; he resells the experience at margin
- **Why adopt Chravel:** One workspace per client trip with chat + itinerary + places + a real PDF deliverable [OBSERVED desktop2-21]; multi-trip dashboard
- **Why reject Chravel:** Clients seeing "Chravel" instead of "Mendoza Curated" everywhere; no white-label SKU; 3-active-trip free cap means he can't even evaluate his real workload without paying [OBSERVED — ground truth §7]

### B. Jobs-to-Be-Done
1. When I deliver an itinerary, I want it branded as MY firm, so the client remembers who created the magic — not which software I rent.
2. When I run 15 concurrent client trips, I want a portfolio dashboard with status at a glance, so I can triage the trip that's on fire today.
3. When a client asks "what time is the yacht," I want them self-serving from a beautiful live itinerary, so my team stops answering page-2 questions on WhatsApp.
4. When a trip wraps, I want a keepsake-grade PDF recap, so the deliverable itself markets my next booking.
5. When I onboard a client, I want them in a contained, read-mostly view, so they consume the experience without seeing my vendor notes or margins.
6. When I bill, I want per-client trip costs attributable, so each trip's P&L absorbs its tooling.

### C. Screener Answers
| Question | Answer |
|---|---|
| Trips last 12 months | 4+ (15 concurrent, ~60/year) |
| Typical group size | 5–8 typical; 16+ for incentive groups |
| Main tools | Travefy/Axus-class builders, Canva, WhatsApp Business, Sheets, Stripe |
| Primary device | Desktop-first |
| 45-min call? | Yes — if there's a partnership angle |
| Role in group | Primary planner (professionally) |
| Pro-ops responsibility | Yes, I own logistics |

### D. Full Survey Answers

**About you.** I own a concierge travel firm in Miami. Clients pay us to make trips effortless and gorgeous. My product is the experience plus the artifacts — the itinerary, the recap, the "how did you find that restaurant" moment. Four staff, fifteen live trips on a normal Tuesday.

**Most recent group trip.** A 12-person 40th-birthday villa week in Tulum. Kicked off by one phone call from the host. Involved: host, 11 guests who answer nothing, three vendors, my coordinator. Most frustrating: guests asking my team questions that were in the itinerary — page two, bolded. What went well: the branded PDF got screenshotted to Instagram, which booked me two leads. Apps: our itinerary builder, Canva, WhatsApp Business (two groups), Sheets, Stripe. Five per trip, times fifteen trips. After the first plan: hosts change everything twice; that's why they pay us.

**Planning workflow.** Idea→booked: discovery call → proposal → deposit → build → vendor confirmations → branded itinerary delivery. During: my coordinator runs WhatsApp; I run exceptions. Post: recap deliverable, review request, rebooking nudge. Decisions stick on phone calls with the host. Non-responders: guests, always — the host answers for them. Example: every trip has a one-page branded "Trip Bible" PDF.

**Feature areas.**
- *Create/Invite:* Pro "Celebrations"/"Other" categories fit my trips [OBSERVED — ground truth §4]. Invite links with approval keep plus-ones out [OBSERVED desktop2-11/L3]. I'd create trips on clients' behalf constantly — 15 at a time, which the free tier's 3-active cap can't even demo [OBSERVED — ground truth §7].
- *Places:* Saved places with map + basecamp per villa — useful, client-visible [OBSERVED desktop2-15].
- *Calendar/Itinerary:* The product core for me. Day-by-day with locations works; PDF export is the deliverable [OBSERVED desktop2-21; pipeline real per D1, `ItineraryView.tsx:78-135`].
- *Polls:* Surprisingly useful — "pick Thursday's dinner" run by my coordinator, feels concierge-interactive [OBSERVED desktop2-16].
- *Tasks:* Internal ops checklists per trip; clients never see tasks ideally — visibility control question [SIMULATED RISK].
- *Smart Import:* I'd paste vendor confirmations, charter contracts, restaurant confirmations — bulk-building 15 itineraries faster is direct margin [OBSERVED — ground truth §6 pipeline].
- *AI Concierge:* My clients asking AI instead of my team at 1am is labor savings — IF the answers match my itinerary. "Group-aware — knows your trip" [OBSERVED desktop2-12] is the right promise. But an AI recommending some random restaurant over MY curated pick dilutes my product [SIMULATED RISK — concierge preference-injection behavior is a documented design friction, ground truth §10 design-level].
- *AI Trust:* Broken when it contradicts my curation or hallucinates a time to a paying client. My brand absorbs the damage, not Chravel's.
- *Settings priorities:* Branding controls, client-view permissions, multi-trip overview.

**Pro/Events branch.** Professional-grade means: client-facing surfaces are flawless, my brand is the brand, and I can run a portfolio, not a trip. Control vs automation: automation backstage (import, drafts), control onstage (anything a client sees ships only after my review). Trust comes from: the deliverable. And here's the thing — I checked the PDF: the export pipeline has a customizable footer that defaults to "Made with Chravel," with a code comment literally saying branding stays modest "so client-facing deliverables stay presentable" [OBSERVED — `src/utils/exportPdfClient.ts:1099-1101,1126`]. Someone is thinking about MY use case. But `footerText` customization has no UI — the recap modal offers section checkboxes, no branding controls [OBSERVED desktop2-21]. And the in-app experience my clients touch says Chravel everywhere. White-label — even just logo + footer + accent color — is my top request and a SKU I'd pay real money for. It doesn't exist [OBSERVED — no white-label tier in ground truth §7].

**Money.** Clients pay me by invoice/Stripe; I'd never expose Chravel's split-with-Venmo to a luxury client — that's for their group brunch, not my contract. Per-client billing: I want trip-level cost attribution, or just a flat agency plan I mark up. Plan changes: my coordinator communicates them, white-glove. One planner: my firm IS the planner. Hotels/restaurants: I decide, host approves; guests are told, beautifully. Conversations live in WhatsApp Business today; moving clients into Chravel chat only works if it feels like MY portal.

**Willingness to pay.** Team plan, $99+/mo happily — Growth or an agency/white-label SKU at $149–249/mo if client surfaces carry my brand. The math: one rebooking pays for a year.

**Ratings.**
- Likelihood next trip: 3/5 — I'd pilot one friendly client's trip next month.
- Clarity: 4/5 — I understood the product in ninety seconds of demo.
- Time saved: 4/5 — import + self-serve client Q&A attack my two biggest labor sinks.
- AI trust: 3/5 — useful backstage; onstage it must defer to my curation.
- Would invite: 4/5 — inviting clients is literally my delivery model.
- Mobile usability: 3/5 — clients will live on mobile; tab strip is fine, not luxury.
- Web usability: 4/5 — my build environment is solid.
- Pricing fit: 3/5 — tiers exist but none is shaped like an agency.
- NPS-style sentiment: 3/5 — closest thing to a channel partner you have, unserved.

**Wrap-up.** Change one thing: white-label client view — my logo, my colors, my footer. Recommend when: a client says "your portal is gorgeous" and never learns the word Chravel. Anything else: a multi-trip command dashboard (status, unread, next 48h across 15 trips) would replace my Tuesday-morning tab ritual. Follow-up: Yes.

### E. Web Flow Walkthrough
- **Discovery/landing:** "For Friend & Family trips, Team Travel, Touring Crews… & Anybody Organizing a Group" — I'm "anybody," which means I'm nobody; no agency/concierge positioning [OBSERVED desktop-01, L1].
- **Signup/onboarding:** Standard, fine [OBSERVED desktop-04/05]. Free tier's 3-active-trip cap collides with my evaluation immediately — I can't simulate a week of my business without hitting the wall, which ironically is a decent upgrade trigger aimed at exactly me [OBSERVED — ground truth §7].
- **Pro creation:** Categories fit; Pro purchase still isn't self-serve [OBSERVED — D9]. Unlike the corporate buyer, I'm a 4-person shop — I WANT the checkout button; emailing billing@ to give someone money is friction I don't forgive [OBSERVED — D9; opposite of persona 18].
- **Feature usage:** The Beyoncé/retreat demos prove the multi-role machinery [OBSERVED desktop-08, desktop-12]. PDF Recap modal: section selection, "1 Free Export per trip," Sample link, privacy line [OBSERVED desktop2-21] — as a deliverable engine it's 70% there; as a BRANDED deliverable engine it's 0% exposed (footerText hook exists unexposed [OBSERVED — exportPdfClient.ts:1101]).
- **Portfolio reality:** Dashboard shows trip cards [OBSERVED desktop-06 per L1/L2]; nothing resembling a 15-trip ops console (status rollups, cross-trip alerts) [OBSERVED — absent from route/feature inventory; need = SIMULATED RISK]. `/organizations` route exists — multi-seat machinery is at least scaffolded [OBSERVED — ground truth §2].
- **Pricing reaction:** Growth $99 with 100 seats is dimensionally fine for my team+clients; but no white-label, no agency SKU, no per-client cost view [OBSERVED — ground truth §7]. Real Pro trips shipping with empty ops surfaces matters less to me — my trips are itinerary+chat+places, all real features — but the demo-vs-real gap on Team/roster polish still undercuts the "professional" promise I'd be reselling [OBSERVED — D7, `tripConverter.ts:118-130`].
- **Web positives:** Deliverable-grade PDF pipeline [OBSERVED D1]; categories; invite controls; polls-as-concierge-touch [OBSERVED desktop2-16].
- **Web pain points:** Chravel-branded everything client-facing; no agency dashboard; Pro checkout absent [OBSERVED — D9]; AI may counter-program my curation [SIMULATED RISK].

### F. Mobile / PWA Flow Walkthrough
- **First impression:** Dark-gold aesthetic is genuinely upmarket — closer to my brand language than most tools [OBSERVED mobile-13, mobile2-12].
- **Navigation:** Tab strip works; my clients need exactly Chat + Calendar + Places and will find them [OBSERVED mobile2-12].
- **Chat/input:** Clean composer; clients can handle it [OBSERVED mobile-13].

- **Thumb reach:** Adequate; the broken demo imagery from the CSP issue would be a disaster in a sales demo to a client [OBSERVED — R4].
- **Mobile positives:** Premium visual language; full parity — clients see what I built, exactly.
- **Mobile pain points:** Chravel branding at every client touchpoint; R1 jank; no client-mode simplified view (hide Payments/Tasks from guests) [SIMULATED RISK — visibility controls per tab not in inventory].

### H. Emotional Reaction
- **Impressed by:** The PDF pipeline being real with privacy defaults — and that code comment about client-facing deliverables; the dark-gold aesthetic I could almost pass off as mine.
- **Confused by:** Who the Pro tiers think they're for — crews and companies, apparently, never agencies running trips for OTHER people.
- **Annoyed by:** "Made with Chravel" on my deliverable with the customization hook sitting unexposed in code; 3-trip cap blocking a realistic trial; no checkout for Pro.
- **Would abandon when:** A client asks "what's Chravel?" one too many times — brand dilution is a slow leak I can measure in rebookings.
- **Would invite others?** Yes — inviting clients IS the product for me; that's also why branding matters triple.
- **[SYNTHETIC QUOTE]** "Your own code comment says client deliverables should 'stay presentable' — so you know I exist. Give me my logo on that PDF and a fifteen-trip dashboard, and I'll put every client I have inside this thing at $200 a month."

### I. Conversion Scores
- **Activation:** 6/10 — one pilot client trip is easy; the 3-trip cap stalls realistic evaluation.
- **Invite likelihood:** 7/10 — client invites are his delivery mechanism.
- **Day-7 retention:** 5/10 — survives if the pilot client compliments the portal.
- **Paid conversion:** 6/10 — willing at $99+; blocked by white-label absence and no Pro checkout.
- **NPS:** +10 — sees a near-fit business tool wearing the wrong logo.
- **Would they pay?** Yes.
- **What:** $99/mo now; $149–249/mo for white-label agency tier.
- **Feature creating WTP:** Branded client-facing PDF + portal (white-label).
- **Limit/CTA triggering upgrade:** 3-active-trip cap on day one of a real evaluation [OBSERVED — ground truth §7].
- **CTA that would annoy:** Chravel self-promotion inside client-visible surfaces ("Made with Chravel", upsell banners a client might see).

### J. Top 5 Fixes for This Persona
1. Expose PDF branding controls (logo, accent color, footer text) and grow them into a white-label SKU because the `customization.footerText` hook already exists with no UI (`src/utils/exportPdfClient.ts:1099-1126`), causing Carlos's #1 willingness-to-pay feature to sit unmonetized in the codebase.
2. Build a portfolio dashboard (cross-trip status, unread counts, next-48h events) because Carlos runs 15 concurrent trips through trip cards designed for consumers (`src/pages/Index.tsx`), causing daily triage to stay in browser tabs and Sheets.
3. Ship Pro self-serve checkout because a 4-person agency wants to swipe a card tonight, not email billing@ (D9), causing conversion loss at peak intent — note this is the exact opposite of the corporate buyer's preference; segment both motions.
4. Add an agency trial or evaluation tier (e.g., 10 active trips/14 days) because the 3-active-trip free cap blocks realistic evaluation of his core scenario (ground truth §7 `src/billing/config.ts`), causing the highest-LTV segment to churn pre-purchase.
5. Add a "curator mode" so the AI concierge prefers planner-saved places before generic recommendations because preference-injection behavior is documented (ground truth §10 design frictions), causing the AI to compete with — rather than amplify — the agency's curation.

### K. Confidence
- **Level:** Medium-High — the white-label gap and branding hook are directly observed in code; agency willingness-to-pay is the inference.
- **Directly observed:** PDF recap modal + pipeline (desktop2-21, D1, exportPdfClient.ts:1099-1126), tier table and trip caps (ground truth §7), Pro checkout gap (D9), demo surfaces (desktop-08/12, desktop2-13..17, mobile-13, mobile2-12), CSP demo-image breakage (R4).
- **Needs real-user validation:** Whether agencies will migrate clients off WhatsApp into a portal; price ceiling for white-label; multi-trip dashboard requirements.
- **Beta interview question:** "If your logo replaced ours on the PDF and the trip page tomorrow, how many of your fifteen active clients would you move in the first month — and what's the first thing that would stop you?"

# Batch 5 — Events Segment Personas (21–25) — 2026-06-11 Study

## Persona 21: Megan O'Brien — Events / Professional Wedding Planner

### A. Profile
- **Name:** Megan O'Brien
- **Age range:** 33–43
- **Location/timezone:** Boston, MA / America/New_York
- **Industry/role:** Owner-operator, boutique wedding planning firm (12 weddings/year, 100–200 guests each)
- **Tech comfort:** High — runs her business on Aisle Planner, HoneyBook, Google Workspace
- **Platform:** iPhone 15 Pro in the field, MacBook Air at the desk
- **Group size:** Per wedding: 8–15 vendors + couple + wedding party (~20 "working" people), 100–200 guests downstream
- **Planning style:** Master-timeline perfectionist; everything has an owner and a due date
- **Current tools:** Aisle Planner, HoneyBook (contracts/invoices), Google Sheets timelines, group texts with vendors, email chains with couples
- **Main pain points:** Vendors who don't read email; day-of timeline changes that never reach the band; couples asking "what time is hair again?" for the ninth time
- **Budget sensitivity:** Low for tools that bill to clients; allergic to per-seat pricing for 200 guests
- **Why adopt Chravel:** One link where the couple, the wedding party, and vendors all see the same agenda; broadcasts for day-of changes; Event Recap PDF as a client deliverable
- **Why reject Chravel:** Only two event roles (organizer/attendee) — no vendor/wedding-party/guest tiers; 3 lifetime free events is gone in one quarter; no white-label, so her clients see "ChravelApp," not "O'Brien Events"

### B. Jobs-to-Be-Done
1. When I am building a wedding-day timeline, I want one agenda the couple, vendors, and wedding party all see live, so I can stop re-sending PDF v7 by email.
2. When the ceremony slips 20 minutes, I want to broadcast the change to exactly the people affected (caterer, band — not 180 guests), so I can keep the day on rails without panic.
3. When I onboard a florist or DJ, I want to give them a scoped view — their call time, the loading dock pin, the contact sheet — so I can avoid vendors scrolling guest chatter.
4. When the wedding ends, I want a polished recap artifact with the final timeline and photos, so I can close the file and ask for the referral.
5. When I am pitching a couple, I want the tool to carry my brand, so I can charge for "the O'Brien client portal" instead of advertising someone else's app.
6. When I run 12 of these a year, I want predictable per-event or business pricing, so I can bill it as a line item to each client.

### C. Screener Answers
| Question | Answer |
|---|---|
| Group trips/events last 12 months | 4+ (12 weddings + 2 personal trips) |
| Typical group size | 16+ |
| Main tools today | Aisle Planner, HoneyBook, Google Sheets, group SMS, email |
| Primary device | iOS + MacBook (Both) |
| 45-min call? | Yes — if it might fix my vendor-communication problem |
| Role in group | Primary planner (professionally) |
| Pro-ops responsibility | Yes, I own logistics |

### D. Full Survey Answers

**About you.** I plan weddings for a living — twelve a year, 100 to 200 guests, Boston and the Cape. I'm the person who knows the sunset time, the band's load-in, and which aunt needs a gluten-free meal. My whole job is making sure thirty people who've never met execute one flawless day.

**Most recent event.**
- *What kicked it off:* A 180-guest October wedding at a vineyard in Ipswich — the couple signed 14 months out and the file opened that day.
- *Who was involved:* The couple, both mothers (lord), a 10-person wedding party, and 13 vendors — caterer, florist, band, photographer, videographer, hair/makeup ×2, transport, rentals, officiant, cake, lighting, valet.
- *Most frustrating moment:* The band never opened the final timeline email and showed up planning for a 7pm set that had moved to 6:15.
- *What went well:* My minute-by-minute Google Sheet — once people actually looked at it.
- *Apps used & why:* Aisle Planner (master plan), HoneyBook (contracts), Google Sheets (day-of timeline), three separate group texts (vendors, wedding party, family), email, and Instagram DMs because one florist only answers there.
- *Total app count:* Seven-plus surfaces on a normal week.
- *What happened after the first plan:* It changed eleven times, and every change meant re-broadcasting to three group texts and praying.

**Planning workflow.**
- *Idea→booked:* Contract signing, venue walkthrough, vendor sourcing over 6–10 months.
- *Booked→during:* Timeline drafts, vendor confirmations at 30/14/7/1 days out, then the day-of run sheet.
- *During:* I'm on my phone, on my feet, for 14 hours straight.
- *Post:* Gallery delivery, vendor reviews, recap for my portfolio, referral ask.
- *Where decisions stick:* Email threads. The couple decides things verbally at tastings and I write the "confirming what we agreed" email, or it never happened.
- *Non-responders:* I call them. Vendors respond to calls, not texts.
- *Example thread/doc:* My day-of sheet has 70+ rows — every row is a time, an owner, and a location.

**Feature areas.**
- *Create/Invite:* I'd create one Event per wedding. The invite modal having "require approval to join" and expiry is right for my world — I do NOT want a forwarded link letting a random plus-one into the vendor channel [OBSERVED `desktop2-11`].
- *Places:* Venue pin, loading dock pin, hotel block, after-party. Vendors always get lost at estates with two entrances — pins with notes would genuinely save me calls.
- *Calendar/Itinerary:* The Agenda tab with sessions, times, and venues is exactly the right shape — "Opening Night Gala, 19:00–22:00, The Forum" reads like my run sheet [OBSERVED `desktop-14`, `mobile-15`]. "Upload Schedule" implies I can bring my existing timeline in, which is the only way I'd migrate.
- *Polls:* For the couple choosing between two signature cocktails, cute. For vendors, irrelevant.
- *Tasks:* "Event Tasks — manage event to-dos and assignments" with owners is my language [OBSERVED `desktop2-22`]. I'd need due dates relative to the event ("T-14 days: final counts to caterer").
- *Smart Import:* I'd paste the venue's BEO PDF, the hotel room-block confirmation, and the band's rider. If it can turn a BEO into agenda items, I'd cry.
- *AI Concierge ask:* "Build a getting-ready schedule for 6 bridesmaids with hair starting at 9am and photos at 3pm" or "What's sunset in Ipswich on October 10?"
- *AI trust breaker:* If it invents a vendor call time and a vendor acts on it, that's a career-ending error for me. AI suggestions must be visibly draft-only until I approve.
- *Settings priorities:* Who can see what. Guests must never see vendor chat. Notification controls per event, per role.

**Events branch.**
- *What professional-grade means:* Role separation (vendor vs. wedding party vs. guest), an audit trail of who saw the timeline change, and exports that look client-ready.
- *Control vs. automation:* Control, always. Automate reminders, never decisions.
- *What creates trust:* The broadcast telling me "13 of 13 vendors delivered/read." Delivery tracking is the feature; everything else is decoration.

**Money.**
- *Collecting/tracking payments:* Clients pay me; I pay vendors per contract through HoneyBook. No expense-splitting in my world — Chravel's split-payments tab is for my bachelorette clients, not me.
- *Reimbursement discussion:* Doesn't exist professionally — everything is contracted and invoiced up front.
- *Plan-change communication:* Today it's three group texts and a prayer; that's the exact thing I'm shopping to replace.
- *Is there always one planner:* Yes. Me, contractually, with liability insurance to prove it.
- *How the group decides hotels/restaurants:* The couple decides; I present two or three vetted options and steer gently.
- *Where conversations live:* Email for decisions, SMS for logistics, and whatever app the flakiest vendor prefers that month.

**Willingness to pay.** *Bracket: client-billable / team plan.* I'd pay $49/month as a business expense without blinking IF I get vendor-grade roles and my branding. What I won't do is burn 3 lifetime free events in six weeks and then get pushed to a $19.99 consumer sub that says "Frequent Chraveler" on it — I'm not a chraveler, I'm a vendor-wrangler. Give me an events-business SKU.

**Ratings (1–5).**
- Likelihood to use for next event: **3** — I'd pilot it for a wedding-party-and-vendor layer next to Aisle Planner.
- Clarity: **4** — the event demo is self-explanatory; I knew where everything was in 90 seconds.
- Time saved: **4** — if broadcasts + agenda replace my three group texts, that's hours per wedding.
- AI trust: **2** — nothing AI-written touches my timeline without an approval step.
- Would invite others: **3** — vendors yes; 180 guests no, not with account-required access.
- Mobile usability: **3** — agenda cards are clean but I live on my phone day-of and the tab strip scroll worries me.
- Web usability: **4** — desktop event view is genuinely polished.
- Pricing fit: **2** — no SKU matches "12 events/year, white-label, client-billable."
- NPS-style sentiment: **3** (≈ +10) — right bones, wrong packaging for professionals.

**Wrap-up.**
- *Change one thing:* Vendor-tier roles with scoped visibility — it's the difference between a pilot and a pass.
- *What makes me recommend it:* A couple texting me "this app made your timeline so easy to follow."
- *Anything else:* "Event Recap" could be a client-deliverable goldmine if it's brandable.
- *30-min follow-up:* **Yes.**

### E. Web Flow Walkthrough
- **Discovery/landing:** "The Group Chat Travel App… & Anybody Organizing a Group" — the last clause is the only thing speaking to me; everything else says vacation [OBSERVED `desktop-22`, landing pricing: "Start free. Upgrade when your trip gets serious."]. Nothing on the pricing section mentions events, weddings, or attendee counts — I would not learn the 100/200 attendee caps exist from this page [OBSERVED `desktop-22`].
- **Signup/onboarding:** Auth renders email + Google/Apple [OBSERVED per harvest L4]; completion untestable here, so my real first-run is unverified [SIMULATED RISK].
- **Event creation:** Free tier gives 3 lifetime events (`src/billing/entitlements.ts:296-306` [OBSERVED — code]). I do 12 weddings a year — I hit the paywall during my first quarter's pilot, before I've decided anything. That's the worst possible moment to ask a professional for money [SIMULATED RISK grounded in code].
- **Feature usage:** Demo event shows Admin · Agenda · Calendar · Chat · Line-up · Media · Polls · Tasks tabs, an "Event Team" card, Invite, Event Recap, Leave Trip [OBSERVED `desktop-13`]. Agenda supports Add Session, Upload Schedule, Schedule view, Files (1/5) [OBSERVED `desktop-14`]. Event Team chips show names only — no role labels, unlike the Pro roster's "Tour Manager/Crew" chips — which visually confirms event role granularity is thin: the permission matrix has only event_organizer and event_attendee (`src/types/permissionMatrix.generated.ts` [OBSERVED — code]; vendor/guest tiers absent → [SIMULATED RISK] for my workflow).
- **Pricing reaction:** Consumer tiers up to $19.99, then Pro $49 with a different feature axis (channels/roster). My need (many events, role control, white-label) straddles both and matches neither [OBSERVED `desktop-22` + pricing table in ground truth §7].
- **Web positives:** Agenda structure, Upload Schedule, approval-gated invites, Event Recap button, overall dark-premium polish that I would not be embarrassed to show a client.
- **Web pain points:** No vendor roles; 3-event lifetime cap; Pro contact was historically `mailto:` and Pro self-serve checkout is still pending (delta D9) — a "talk to sales" wall for a 12-event/year solo business [OBSERVED — delta D9].

### F. Mobile / PWA Flow Walkthrough
- **First impression:** Event header is tidy — title, "Los Angeles, CA • 4 attendees," Demo Mode banner, Exit Demo [OBSERVED `mobile-14`].
- **Navigation:** Horizontal tab strip (Agenda · Calendar · Chat · L…) — later tabs are off-screen and require scrolling the strip; on a 14-hour wedding day with one thumb, Tasks being four swipes away matters [OBSERVED `mobile-14`, `mobile2-21`; evidence-delta notes no bottom nav on mobile web].
- **Agenda usability:** Timeline cards with time + venue ("Opening Night Gala, 19:00–22:00, The Forum") are exactly what a vendor needs at a glance — genuinely day-of usable [OBSERVED `mobile-15`].
- **Forms/tasks:** Event Tasks on mobile render numbered cards with edit/delete and a + button; long titles wrap hard in the narrow column ("Pick up your badge at the registration desk" takes four lines) [OBSERVED `mobile2-21`].
- **Chat/input, invite link flow:** Untestable live (backend blocked) [SIMULATED RISK].
- **Perceived speed:** Demo feels fluid, but mobile surfaces fire continuous duplicate-key render warnings from `MobileGroupCalendar.tsx:525` (~150/step, all mobile trip surfaces incl. events) — a perf smell I'd feel on a venue with one bar of LTE [OBSERVED — delta R1].
- **Mobile positives:** Agenda timeline; clean dark theme; readable type.
- **Mobile pain points:** Tab strip overflow; no role labels anywhere on the team card; task-card text wrap; render-storm perf risk on older vendor phones [OBSERVED/SIMULATED as labeled].

### H. Emotional Reaction
- **Impressed by:** The agenda tab — it's her run sheet, live, on every phone [OBSERVED `desktop-14`].
- **Confused by:** Where "trips" end and "events" begin — she has to mentally translate travel language constantly.
- **Annoyed by:** Names-only team chips; "Frequent Chraveler" being the upgrade she's told to buy.
- **Would abandon when:** The 4th event paywall hits mid-pilot, or the first time a guest sees vendor chat.
- **Would invite others?** Vendors and wedding party, yes — that's 20 high-quality professional invites per wedding. Guests, no, while accounts are mandatory.
- **[SYNTHETIC QUOTE]:** "This is the closest anything's come to my day-of binder — but I run twelve weddings a year, and you gave me three, ever, then offered me a travel subscription. Sell me an events business plan and we'll talk."

### I. Conversion Scores
- **Activation:** 7/10 — demo gets her to a real pilot fast.
- **Invite likelihood:** 6/10 — vendors/party yes, guests blocked by account wall.
- **Day-7 retention:** 6/10 — sticks if one real wedding runs through it.
- **Paid conversion:** 5/10 — money is there; the SKU isn't.
- **NPS-style:** +10 — advocate-in-waiting, blocked by packaging.
- **Would they pay?** Yes, as a business expense.
- **What would they pay?** $49–99/mo business plan or ~$15–25 per event, client-billable.
- **Feature creating willingness to pay:** Role-scoped access + broadcast delivery tracking + brandable Event Recap.
- **Limit/CTA that triggers upgrade:** 4th lifetime event — but only if the upgrade path says "events business," not "Chraveler."
- **CTA that would annoy them:** Consumer "Start Free Trial" upsell modal when she needs a Pro conversation; mailto:-only Pro contact [OBSERVED delta D9].

### J. Top 5 Fixes for This Persona
1. Add event sub-roles (vendor / wedding party / guest) with scoped chat+agenda visibility, because Megan failed at "give the florist access without exposing couple chat," causing hard rejection — extend `src/types/permissionMatrix.generated.ts` event roles.
2. Replace the 3-lifetime-event cliff with an events-business SKU or per-event pass, because Megan exhausts the free tier in one quarter mid-evaluation, causing churn at the trust-formation moment (`src/billing/entitlements.ts:296-306`).
3. Add role-scoped invite links to `InviteModal`, because one link granting uniform access fails her "vendors ≠ guests" requirement, causing her to keep three group texts [OBSERVED `desktop2-11`].
4. Ship self-serve Pro/business checkout, because mailto:-gated purchase fails a solo professional ready to pay, causing lost revenue (delta D9).
5. Make Event Recap brandable (logo/name), because unbranded deliverables fail her client-portal job, capping her advocacy — `desktop-13` Event Recap button is the hook.

### K. Confidence
- **Level:** Medium.
- **Directly observed:** Event demo surfaces (agenda/tasks/polls/calendar, both viewports), invite modal controls, pricing page, entitlement code, permission matrix.
- **Needs real-user validation:** Whether a 70-row wedding timeline is usable in Agenda; vendor adoption willingness; actual broadcast delivery UX in events.
- **Beta interview question:** "Walk me through the last day-of timeline change — who had to know, how did you tell them, and how did you confirm they saw it?"
