## Persona 22: Raj Patel — Events / Conference Organizer (1,000-person professional event)

### A. Profile
- **Name:** Raj Patel
- **Age range:** 38–48
- **Location/timezone:** Chicago, IL / America/Chicago
- **Industry/role:** Director of Events at a B2B trade association; owns one 1,000-attendee annual conference + ~8 smaller programs
- **Tech comfort:** High — administers Cvent, has evaluated Whova/Swapcard/Hopin, lives in spreadsheets
- **Platform:** Desktop-first (Windows + Chrome); iPhone secondary
- **Group size:** 1,000 attendees, 60 speakers, 25 sponsors, 12 staff, 40 volunteers
- **Planning style:** RFP-driven, risk-averse, runs everything through a requirements matrix
- **Current tools:** Cvent (reg), Whova (attendee app), Slack (staff), Excel (everything else), Mailchimp (comms)
- **Main pain points:** Attendee-app costs ($8–15k/yr); session-change comms; staff/volunteer coordination split from attendee comms
- **Budget sensitivity:** Medium — has budget, but procurement demands reliability evidence and references
- **Why adopt Chravel:** Could replace Slack+spreadsheets for the staff/speaker/volunteer layer, and run 50-person side events (board retreats, VIP dinners) cheaply
- **Why reject Chravel:** No registration/badge integration, no session-track agenda at scale, notification architecture documented as failing at exactly his attendee count, and advertised attendee caps that aren't actually enforced — a billing-integrity smell procurement would flag

### B. Jobs-to-Be-Done
1. When I am running a 1,000-person conference, I want session changes pushed reliably to affected attendees within a minute, so I can avoid 300 people standing at the wrong ballroom.
2. When I coordinate 40 volunteers and 12 staff, I want role-scoped channels and task assignments, so I can stop bridging Slack and text threads.
3. When I evaluate an event platform, I want documented behavior at my scale (load, delivery, caps), so I can defend the choice to procurement.
4. When I manage 60 speakers, I want each to see their session, room, AV needs, and arrival logistics, so I can kill the 60-thread email ritual.
5. When I run side events (board retreat, VIP dinner, 50 people), I want lightweight coordination without paying Cvent prices, so I can cover the long tail of my calendar.

### C. Screener Answers
| Question | Answer |
|---|---|
| Group trips/events last 12 months | 4+ (1 flagship conference + 8 programs) |
| Typical group size | 16+ (up to 1,000) |
| Main tools today | Cvent, Whova, Slack, Excel, Mailchimp |
| Primary device | Desktop-first |
| 45-min call? | Yes — vendor evaluation is literally my job |
| Role in group | Primary planner |
| Pro-ops responsibility | Yes, I own logistics |

### D. Full Survey Answers

**About you.** I run events for a trade association — one flagship conference, about a thousand registrants, plus a calendar of board retreats, chapter meetups, and VIP dinners. I've bought and deployed Cvent and Whova. I read SLAs for fun. My job is to never be surprised in front of a thousand people.

**Most recent event.**
- *What kicked it off:* Last month's annual conference — 980 registered, 3 days, 4 tracks, 62 sessions, McCormick Place West. Kicked off 11 months prior with venue contracting.
- *Who was involved:* My team of 12, a 40-volunteer corps, 60 speakers, 25 sponsors, AV vendor, decorator, catering.
- *Most frustrating moment:* A keynote room change 40 minutes before doors — Whova push went to everyone (not just keynote RSVPs), the Mailchimp blast landed in spam, and volunteers still fielded 200 confused people.
- *What went well:* The speaker-ready room ran flawlessly off a shared Excel + a dedicated Slack channel.
- *Apps used & why:* Cvent (registration), Whova (attendee app), Slack (staff), Excel (everything else), Mailchimp (attendee email), SMS for floor managers.
- *Total app count:* Seven tools, eight if you count the walkie-talkies. I count the walkie-talkies.
- *What happened after the first plan:* The agenda changed weekly for months — version control was me, manually, in a change log.

**Planning workflow.**
- *Idea→booked:* Budget approval → venue RFP → contract.
- *Booked→during:* Registration build, program committee CFP, speaker confirmations, sponsor fulfillment, the logistics matrix.
- *During:* Command-center mode — radios, Slack, floor walks, hourly stand-ups.
- *Post:* NPS survey, sponsor reports, financial reconciliation, debrief doc.
- *Where decisions stick:* Meeting minutes and my requirements tracker; they die in Slack threads.
- *Non-responders:* Speakers, mostly — escalating cadence: email, then their assistant, then the program chair leans on them.
- *Example thread/doc:* My session-change log — every change, who approved it, which comms went out, timestamped. That log is my audit trail.

**Feature areas.**
- *Create/Invite:* For the conference I would NOT invite 1,000 attendees through `/join/{token}` links — that's reg-system territory. For staff/speakers/volunteers (~115 people), approval-gated links work [OBSERVED `desktop2-11` shows approval/expiry/max-uses].
- *Places:* Venue pins with room-level notes would help volunteers; doubt it does indoor wayfinding.
- *Calendar/Itinerary:* Agenda has sessions with time+venue and an Unscheduled→Schedule flow, Upload Schedule, Add Session [OBSERVED `desktop-14`]. For 62 sessions across 4 tracks I need track/room lanes and filtering — three demo sessions can't tell me if it survives my program [HYPOTHESIS].
- *Polls:* Session Q&A/voting at 1,000 concurrent — unproven; fine for staff decisions.
- *Tasks:* Volunteer assignments with owners — genuinely useful for my 40-person corps [OBSERVED `desktop2-22` shows assignment model].
- *Smart Import:* I'd paste the session grid CSV and speaker confirmations. If Upload Schedule ingests my Excel program, that's the single highest-value feature for me.
- *AI Concierge ask:* "Which sessions changed rooms since Monday and who RSVPed to them?" — answerable only if the data model tracks it.
- *AI trust breaker:* Hallucinated room numbers. One wrong room from an AI answer at my scale equals hundreds of misdirected people.
- *Settings priorities:* Notification reliability and targeting. Delivery evidence. Admin audit logs.

**Events branch.**
- *What professional-grade means:* Documented limits, delivery guarantees, audit trails, role separation, and honest capacity numbers.
- *Control vs. automation:* Automation for fanout, absolute control over what gets sent and to whom.
- *What creates trust:* The vendor telling me their system's breaking points before I find them.
- *And here's my problem:* Your own audit says notification fanout blocks the INSERT at event scale — 4,000 members produced 12,000 rows synchronously, no batching [OBSERVED — NOTIFICATION_AUDIT.md via ground truth §10.4, still open]. And you advertise 100/200 attendee caps by tier that have no enforcement call sites [OBSERVED — ground truth §4]. Unenforced caps cut both ways: today I could exceed what I paid for; tomorrow enforcement arrives suddenly and strands my live event. Procurement calls that billing-integrity risk. I call it disqualifying for the main conference.

**Money.**
- *Collecting/tracking payments:* Association budget, PO + invoice, net-30. Nothing consumer about it.
- *Reimbursement discussion:* Expense reports through finance; expense splitting is irrelevant to my world.
- *Plan-change communication:* Mailchimp + Whova push + printed signage + volunteers repeating themselves.
- *Is there always one planner:* A team, with me accountable for everything that goes wrong.
- *How the group decides hotels/restaurants:* Contracted blocks; the committee decides, procurement signs.
- *Where conversations live:* Slack for staff, email for everyone external, the change log for the truth.

**Willingness to pay.** *Bracket: team plan.* For staff/speaker/volunteer coordination plus side events: $99/mo Growth is defensible if caps and delivery are real. For the attendee-facing layer of the flagship: $0 until there's load evidence, a published cap policy, and reg integration. I pay Whova five figures because it has demonstrably survived events my size.

**Ratings (1–5).**
- Likelihood next event: **3** — yes for the board retreat; no for the flagship.
- Clarity: **4** — surfaces are self-explanatory.
- Time saved: **3** — meaningful for the ops layer only.
- AI trust: **2** — no provenance, no trust at scale.
- Would invite: **3** — staff and speakers; not attendees.
- Mobile usability: **3** — fine for what I saw; my volunteers would live in it, unproven at density.
- Web usability: **4** — desktop event console is clean [OBSERVED `desktop-13`].
- Pricing fit: **2** — caps advertised-but-unenforced undermines the one pricing axis aimed at me.
- NPS sentiment: **2** (≈ −20) — promising ops tool, not a conference platform, and the scale honesty isn't there yet.

**Wrap-up.**
- *Change one thing:* Publish and enforce real attendee capacity with documented fanout behavior.
- *What makes me recommend it:* It survives a 500-person event with verifiable delivery stats.
- *Anything else:* "Side-event tool that grows into the main event" is a credible wedge — say that out loud in marketing instead of implying conference-scale readiness.
- *30-min follow-up:* **Yes.**

### E. Web Flow Walkthrough
- **Discovery/landing:** Travel-consumer framing; "For Teams" nav link is the only B2B signal [OBSERVED `desktop-22`, delta non-defect notes]. Pricing page says nothing about events, attendees, or delivery guarantees — an event buyer can't even start an evaluation from it [OBSERVED `desktop-22`].
- **Signup/onboarding:** Renders fine [OBSERVED L4]; procurement flow (SSO? DPA? SOC2?) — nothing visible [HYPOTHESIS].
- **Event creation:** Demo event console: Admin, Agenda, Calendar, Chat, Line-up, Media, Polls, Tasks; Event Team card; Event Recap [OBSERVED `desktop-13`]. The Admin tab existing at all is a good sign for my world.
- **Agenda at scale:** Add Session, Upload Schedule, Schedule/Unscheduled states, Files (1/5) [OBSERVED `desktop-14`]. Three sessions in demo; 62 sessions × 4 tracks is the real test [HYPOTHESIS]. "Files (1/5)" suggests a 5-file cap — my speaker decks alone are 60 files [OBSERVED UI, SIMULATED RISK for limit].
- **Scale reality:** Fanout architecture documented failing at 4,000 members (12,000 synchronous rows, INSERT-blocking; no batching) [OBSERVED — ground truth §10.4, open]. Hot-trip realtime isolation also open (§10.5) — one big event can saturate realtime for everyone. These two findings end the flagship conversation.
- **Pricing reaction:** FC unlimited events @100 attendees, Pro Starter @100, Growth @200 (ground truth §7) — but zero enforcement call sites for any cap [OBSERVED §4]. Advertised limits that don't exist in code are exactly what a vendor-risk review catches.
- **Web positives:** Event console design, agenda model with scheduled/unscheduled, Upload Schedule, approval-gated invites, Event Recap.
- **Web pain points:** No reg/badge story, no track-level agenda evidence, unenforced caps, fanout risk, Pro self-serve checkout still pending (delta D9).

### F. Mobile / PWA Flow Walkthrough
- **First impression:** Compact event header with attendee count [OBSERVED `mobile-14`]. My volunteers and floor staff are the mobile users; I'm not.
- **Navigation:** Horizontal scrolling tab strip; Tasks/Polls live off-screen right [OBSERVED `mobile-14` vs `mobile2-21`]. A volunteer mid-shift hunting for Tasks behind a strip-scroll is friction at the worst moment.
- **Agenda:** Session cards with time/venue are exactly what floor staff need [OBSERVED `mobile-15`].
- **Tasks:** Assignment cards readable; cramped wrapping on long titles [OBSERVED `mobile2-21`].
- **Chat/input:** Untestable live [SIMULATED RISK].
- **Perceived speed:** Continuous duplicate-key render warnings on every mobile trip surface (`MobileGroupCalendar.tsx:525`; ~150/step, thousands per pass) — on volunteers' mid-range Androids over congested venue Wi-Fi, that's battery and jank I can't afford [OBSERVED — delta R1].
- **Mobile positives:** Agenda cards; legible dark theme; thumb-sized buttons.
- **Mobile pain points:** Tab-strip overflow; render-storm perf; no offline story visible for venues with dead zones [HYPOTHESIS].

### G. Feature-by-Feature Findings

### H. Emotional Reaction
- **Impressed by:** The agenda's scheduled/unscheduled model and Upload Schedule — someone on this team has run an event [OBSERVED `desktop-14`].
- **Confused by:** Why attendee caps appear in pricing but nowhere in enforcement — is the number real or marketing? [OBSERVED §4]
- **Annoyed by:** Having to read audit docs to learn the notification system can't survive his event — the site implies readiness it doesn't have.
- **Would abandon when:** First broadcast to a large event visibly stalls or double-sends; or enforcement of caps arrives mid-event.
- **Would invite others?** His 12 staff for a side-event pilot, yes. 1,000 attendees, no.
- **[SYNTHETIC QUOTE]:** "The bones are right and the demo is slick, but I've read what happens to your notifications at four thousand members. Sell me the board retreat today and the conference in two years — just don't put '200 attendees' on a pricing page your code doesn't enforce."

### I. Conversion Scores
- **Activation:** 5/10 — pilots a side event; flagship blocked.
- **Invite likelihood:** 4/10 — ops layer only.
- **Day-7 retention:** 4/10 — depends on a side event happening that week.
- **Paid conversion:** 3/10 — Growth $99 plausible for the long tail, but caps/fanout doubts stall the PO.
- **NPS-style:** −20 — respectful skeptic; will re-evaluate next cycle.
- **Would they pay?** Eventually, team plan — after scale evidence.
- **What would they pay?** $99/mo Growth for ops + side events; five figures/yr only with conference-grade proof.
- **Feature creating willingness to pay:** Targeted broadcasts with delivery tracking that demonstrably work at 500+.
- **Limit/CTA that triggers upgrade:** Attendee cap — IF it were real and gracefully enforced.
- **CTA that would annoy them:** Consumer upsell modals in an org evaluation; mailto: as the only path to Pro (delta D9).

### J. Top 5 Fixes for This Persona
1. Fix notification fanout (async queue + batching) because Raj's 1,000-attendee event would block INSERTs and stall comms at the highest-stakes moment — NOTIFICATION_AUDIT.md / ground truth §10.4, the single disqualifier.
2. Enforce advertised attendee caps (100/200) with grace-period UX, because pricing promises limits the code never checks (ground truth §4), causing billing-integrity distrust in procurement review.
3. Add a critical-broadcast class that bypasses per-trip mute, because muted attendees missing a room change defeats the product's core event job (`useTripNotificationMute.ts` + §10.4 interaction).
4. Add track/room lanes + filtering to the Agenda, because 62 sessions in a flat list fails his program-management task — `desktop-14` shows the primitives, not the density.
5. Build bulk CSV invite with role pre-assignment, because onboarding 115 staff/speakers one link at a time fails his setup workflow (`desktop2-11` shows single-link model).

### K. Confidence
- **Level:** High for the disqualifiers (code/audit-grounded); Medium for the side-event adoption story.
- **Directly observed:** Event console, agenda primitives, invite controls, cap non-enforcement (§4), fanout audit (§10.4), mute implementation.
- **Needs real-user validation:** Agenda usability at 60+ sessions; volunteer mobile behavior on venue networks; actual broadcast latency at scale.
- **Beta interview question:** "What evidence would your procurement team need to approve an attendee-facing app for your flagship event — and who produced it for Whova?"

## Persona 23: Zoe Carter — Events / Music Festival Attendee Group Lead

### A. Profile
- **Name:** Zoe Carter
- **Age range:** 24–30
- **Location/timezone:** Denver, CO / America/Denver
- **Industry/role:** Marketing coordinator by day; the friend who organizes everything by night
- **Tech comfort:** High — lives in iOS, Instagram, BeReal, Partiful, Spotify
- **Platform:** iPhone 14, exclusively; opens a laptop only at work
- **Group size:** 15 friends at a 3-day music festival (two Airbnbs, one rental van)
- **Planning style:** Vibes-forward but secretly organized — color-coded Notes app, lineup screenshots, pinned Snap map
- **Current tools:** iMessage group (chaos), Instagram DMs, Partiful (pre-parties), Splitwise, shared Apple Note, Spotify blend
- **Main pain points:** "Where ARE you guys" texts at the festival; lineup-clash debates buried in 400 unread messages; photos scattered across 15 camera rolls
- **Budget sensitivity:** High — she'll pay $6 for oat milk but interrogates every subscription
- **Why adopt Chravel:** Line-up tab + polls for set-clash votes + one media pool + a meetup pin = her entire festival problem in one app
- **Why reject Chravel:** If her 15 friends have to create accounts before seeing anything, half of them simply won't — the group lives or dies on zero-friction

### B. Jobs-to-Be-Done
1. When the festival lineup drops, I want the group to vote on set clashes (Doja vs. Odesza), so I can build a day plan that isn't relitigated at the gate.
2. When we split up at the festival, I want a pinned meetup spot everyone can find, so I can stop sending "by the ferris wheel, left side??" texts.
3. When the weekend ends, I want everyone's photos in one pool, so I can make the recap without chasing 15 camera rolls.
4. When I send the invite, I want friends to see the plan instantly with zero signup, so I can get the flaky ones in before they lose interest.
5. When the group chat hits 400 messages, I want decisions pinned and separate from memes, so I can find the van departure time in under ten seconds.

### C. Screener Answers
| Question | Answer |
|---|---|
| Group trips/events last 12 months | 2-3 (festival, bachelorette, ski weekend) |
| Typical group size | 9-15 |
| Main tools today | iMessage, Splitwise, Partiful, Apple Notes, Instagram |
| Primary device | iOS |
| 45-min call? | Maybe — if it's after 6pm |
| Role in group | Primary planner (informally) |
| Pro-ops responsibility | Shared responsibility (but really, her) |

### D. Full Survey Answers

**About you.** I'm the group's unofficial cruise director. If I don't make the plan, fifteen people stand in a parking lot arguing about tacos. This year's big one is a 3-day festival — two Airbnbs, a van, and a lineup that has at least four scheduling fights in it already.

**Most recent/next group trip.** The festival, obviously. Kicked off when tickets dropped and I made the group chat at 10:02am the same day. Who's involved: 15 people, ages 24–31, three of whom have never replied to a poll in their lives. Most frustrating last time: we lost two people for THREE HOURS on day two because "meet at the main stage" means nothing in a crowd of 60,000 — and the photo situation: 2,000 pics across everyone's phones, I got maybe 40. What went well: my Apple Note schedule actually got screenshot and shared, which felt like winning a Grammy. Apps used: iMessage (chat), Splitwise (money), Partiful (pre-party), Notes (plan), Spotify (blend), Find My (sort of). Six apps. After the first plan, the lineup changed and my beautiful Note became a lie nobody re-read.

**Planning workflow.** Idea→booked: tickets first, panic-book Airbnbs same week, van last. Booked→during: the chat just runs hot for two months; decisions happen when I force a poll or threaten to decide myself. During: pure chaos coordination — who's at which stage, when's the van, who has sunscreen. Post: the photo-chase, the Splitwise settle-up, and the "best weekend ever" message. Where decisions stick: they don't — they get re-asked weekly. Non-responders: I @ them twice then decide for them. Example thread: 60 messages about whether to leave Saturday at 11 or noon. The answer was 11:30. Sixty. Messages.

**Feature areas.**
- *Create/Invite:* I'd make the event and blast the link. The invite modal looks right — link, copy, expiry [OBSERVED `desktop2-11`] — but here's the dealbreaker: my friends tap the link and hit an account wall before they can see ANYTHING useful, because guests have zero resource access (`permissionMatrix.generated.ts:44-50`, delta D15 [OBSERVED — code]). Partiful lets you RSVP with a phone number. Half my group will not make an account to see a schedule [SIMULATED RISK].
- *Places:* Meetup pins are THE feature. "Basecamp" = our Airbnb, pins for the van, the medical tent, our flag spot. Yes please.
- *Calendar/Itinerary:* The Agenda with times and venues is literally my Apple Note but alive — "Stand-Up Marathon, 14:00–23:00, Multiple Venues" maps exactly to festival sets [OBSERVED `mobile-15`].
- *Polls/Decisions:* Set-clash votes! "Doja or Odesza 9pm Saturday" with realtime counts ends the 60-message threads. The event demo's polls tab is an empty "create your first poll" state but the consumer demo shows the full poll machinery [OBSERVED `desktop2-23`].
- *Tasks:* "Bring the flag" "Book the van" "Costco run" with names attached. The mobile task cards with assignments look right [OBSERVED `mobile2-21`].
- *Smart Import:* I'd paste the festival's lineup page URL and our Airbnb confirmations. If it builds the schedule from the lineup link, I'd scream (good scream).
- *AI Concierge ask:* "Build us a Saturday plan that hits Doja, the art car at sunset, and food before 8" — fun if it works, fine if it doesn't.
- *AI trust breaker:* Wrong set times. If the AI says 9:15 and the set's at 8:45, we missed it and I'm done asking.
- *Settings priorities:* Mute controls. Fifteen people in one chat is a notification apocalypse — per-event mute existing now matters to me (delta D11 [OBSERVED — code]).

**Events branch.** *Professional-grade means:* nothing, honestly — I need friend-grade. But if you mean "what makes it feel legit": set times that stay synced, pins that load on festival Wi-Fi, and the app not eating my battery. *Control vs. automation:* automate everything except who's in the group. *What creates trust:* the first time the meetup pin actually reunites us, this app becomes religion.

**Money.** Splitwise runs our finances — Airbnbs split 15 ways, van, Costco. The Venmo deeplink settle-up model is exactly how we already live so that's fine [OBSERVED — ground truth §6]. Reimbursement discussion: we're shameless, everyone Venmos within a week or gets roasted. Plan changes: I announce in chat and pray. One planner: me, with two lieutenants. Hotels/restaurants: I propose, polls decide, I book. Conversations live in iMessage, period — which is exactly the problem.

**Willingness to pay.** *Bracket: free only* — with an asterisk. Me personally subscribing monthly for friend trips? No. The 3 free lifetime events covers this year fine [OBSERVED — entitlements.ts:296-306]. But a one-time event pass at like $10–15 that the whole group's covered under, split 15 ways? That's 80 cents each, I'd pay it without asking anyone. The $39.99 Trip Pass framing is too "trip" and too much for a 3-day festival.

**Ratings (1–5).**
- Likelihood next trip: **4** — I want this for the festival, today.
- Clarity: **4** — I understood the event tabs instantly.
- Time saved: **4** — polls + pins + media pool kills my three worst chores.
- AI trust: **3** — fun for plans, not trusted for set times.
- Would invite: **4** — the whole point — IF the join is friction-free.
- Mobile usability: **4** — agenda cards are gorgeous on phone [OBSERVED `mobile-15`]; tab strip scroll is mid.
- Web usability: **3** — looks great but I will never use the desktop version.
- Pricing fit: **3** — free tier genuinely covers me; no group/event pass option though.
- NPS sentiment: **4** (≈ +30) — I'm hype, contingent on my friends actually getting in.

**Wrap-up.** Change one thing: let friends see the event from the invite link without an account — RSVP-light like Partiful, upgrade to full member later. Recommend when: the meetup pin works once in a real crowd. Anything else: the media pool is sneaky-huge — whoever owns the group photo problem owns the group. Follow-up: **Maybe** (text me, don't call).

- **Perceived speed:** Demo feels smooth, but every mobile trip surface logs continuous duplicate-key render storms (`MobileGroupCalendar.tsx:525`) — battery drain at a festival with 8% power is a real betrayal [OBSERVED — delta R1].

- **Mobile positives:** Agenda cards, dark theme (festival night-mode appropriate), readable everything.
- **Mobile pain points:** Tab overflow, render-storm battery risk, account-wall invite flow, unproven offline behavior in a 60,000-person network dead zone [HYPOTHESIS].

### H. Emotional Reaction
- **Impressed by:** A Line-up tab existing at all, and the mobile agenda cards — "this was made by someone who goes to things" [OBSERVED `desktop-13`, `mobile-15`].
- **Confused by:** Why her friends need full accounts to see a schedule she made for them (D15).
- **Annoyed by:** The far tabs hiding behind a strip-scroll; 3-splits free cap on a 15-person trip.
- **Would abandon when:** Three friends text her "it's making me sign up, just screenshot it" — the moment Chravel becomes a second chat instead of the chat.
- **Would invite others?** Emphatically yes — inviting IS her use case — which is exactly why the join wall is existential.
- **[SYNTHETIC QUOTE]:** "I'm fully ready to make this our festival HQ — polls, pins, the photo pool, all of it. But if Maddie has to create an account to see what time the van leaves, Maddie is not creating an account, and then we're back in iMessage."

### I. Conversion Scores
- **Activation:** 8/10 — she'd build the event the night she finds the app.
- **Invite likelihood:** 9/10 — 15 invites, day one; the product's best growth engine.
- **Day-7 retention:** 7/10 — high through the festival; cliff after unless next trip starts.
- **Paid conversion:** 3/10 — free covers her; only a split-able event pass converts her.
- **NPS-style:** +30 — enthusiastic, contingent on friend-join friction.
- **Would they pay?** Personally no; group-split one-time, yes.
- **What would they pay?** $10–15 once per event, split 15 ways.
- **Feature creating willingness to pay:** Bigger media pool + everyone-in-free under one event pass.
- **Limit/CTA that triggers upgrade:** 500 MB media cap mid-festival is the only wall she'd hit emotionally.
- **CTA that would annoy them:** A monthly-subscription modal mid-festival; anything interrupting the group chat.

### J. Top 5 Fixes for This Persona
1. Add a guest/RSVP-light mode (read agenda, pins, polls-view) before account creation, because Zoe's flaky friends abandon at the auth gate, killing the group's adoption — `src/types/permissionMatrix.generated.ts:44-50` consumer_guest zero access (D15).
2. Add an event pass SKU (~$10–15 one-time, covers all members), because no current price maps to "15 friends, one weekend," causing zero paid conversion from her highest-virality segment.
3. Add day filters to the Agenda, because a 3-day festival schedule in one flat timeline fails her "what's today" glance — `desktop-14` primitives support it.
4. Fix the mobile duplicate-key render storm, because continuous re-renders (`MobileGroupCalendar.tsx:525`, delta R1) drain festival-day batteries, causing mid-event abandonment.
5. Offer category-level notification controls per event (decisions/pins only), because all-or-nothing mute (D11) means she either drowns or goes deaf, weakening the chat-replacement promise.

### K. Confidence
- **Level:** Medium-High.
- **Directly observed:** Event tabs incl. Line-up, mobile agenda, tasks, polls empty-state, invite modal, guest permission code, mute code, pricing copy.
- **Needs real-user validation:** Whether friends actually convert at the auth gate; chat usability vs iMessage gravity; pins on congested festival networks.
- **Beta interview question:** "Send this invite link to your three least-responsive friends right now — what do they do, and what do they text you back?"

## Persona 24: Coach Dana Whitfield — Events / Run Club Organizer (Race Weekend)

### A. Profile
- **Name:** Dana Whitfield ("Coach Dana")
- **Age range:** 35–50
- **Location/timezone:** Portland, OR / America/Los_Angeles
- **Industry/role:** Physical therapist by trade; volunteer organizer of a 120-member run club, leading 40 runners to an out-of-town half marathon weekend
- **Tech comfort:** Medium — competent with Strava, Google Forms, Facebook Groups; suspicious of anything that needs a tutorial
- **Platform:** Android (Pixel 7) + desktop at home for "real work"
- **Group size:** 40 runners for race weekend (carpools, one hotel block, three pace groups)
- **Planning style:** Checklists and printed packets; sends one long weekly email nobody fully reads
- **Current tools:** Facebook Group, Google Forms (signups), Google Sheets (carpools/waves), GroupMe, Strava, email
- **Main pain points:** Race-morning chaos — wave times, gear drop, parking; carpool musical chairs; the same five questions asked forty times
- **Budget sensitivity:** Medium-high personally; the club has dues (~$30/yr × 120) and a small treasury
- **Why adopt Chravel:** Broadcasts for race-morning logistics + a calendar everyone actually opens + gear-drop/brunch pins, replacing four tools for one weekend
- **Why reject Chravel:** Android experience is PWA-only (no Play Store app to point members to); and the "who pays — me or the club?" question has no good answer in the pricing

### B. Jobs-to-Be-Done
1. When it's 5:30am on race day, I want to broadcast "Wave 2 gear drop closes 6:40, use the SW gate" to all 40 runners and know it landed, so I can stop doing roll call by text.
2. When runners sign up, I want wave times, pace groups, and carpool assignments visible in one schedule, so I can stop re-answering the same five questions.
3. When we book the hotel block and post-race brunch, I want pins and times in one place, so I can retire the 14-paragraph weekly email.
4. When the club pays for a tool, I want a price that maps to a club (one organizer, many members, a few events a year), so I can justify it to the treasurer in one sentence.
5. When members join, I want it to work the same on every phone — half my club is on Android — so I can avoid being tech support at packet pickup.

### C. Screener Answers
| Question | Answer |
|---|---|
| Group trips/events last 12 months | 2-3 (two race weekends + summer camp-out) |
| Typical group size | 16+ |
| Main tools today | Facebook Group, Google Forms/Sheets, GroupMe, email |
| Primary device | Android + Desktop (Both) |
| 45-min call? | Maybe — evenings only |
| Role in group | Primary planner (volunteer) |

### D. Full Survey Answers

**About you.** I'm a PT and I've run our club for six years. Twice a year I take a big group to a destination race — this fall it's 40 of us going down to the Eugene Half. I handle the hotel block, carpools, pace groups, wave logistics, and the brunch after. Nobody pays me; I do it because someone has to and apparently that someone is me.

**Most recent/next group trip.** Eugene Half Marathon weekend, 40 runners. Kicked off when registration opened and I posted a Google Form in the Facebook Group. Involved: me, two pace-group captains, and 37 adults who read nothing. Most frustrating last time: race morning — three people went to the wrong gear drop, one carpool left a runner at the hotel, and my phone had 31 texts before 6am. What went well: my printed packet — wave times, parking map, brunch address — people photographed it and that photo was the real app. Apps used: Facebook (announcements), Google Forms (signups), Sheets (carpool matrix), GroupMe (day-of), Strava (egos), email (the long one). Six. After the first plan, the race moved our corral assignments and I had to update four places and still got asked.

**Planning workflow.** Idea→booked: pick the race a year out, hotel block within a month, registrations rolling. Booked→during: monthly emails becoming weekly, carpool matrix two weeks out, packet the Tuesday before. During: GroupMe firefighting from 5am. Post: brunch, photo sharing in Facebook comments (terrible), thank-you email, deposit reconciliation with the treasurer. Decisions stick in my Sheet; they get lost in GroupMe within minutes. Non-responders: I call the captains and the captains chase their pace groups — a phone tree, basically. Example doc: the carpool matrix — 40 names, 11 cars, departure times, hotel rooms. It is load-bearing.

**Feature areas.**
- *Create/Invite:* One event for race weekend. The invite link with optional approval is right — our group is privacy-relaxed, I'd leave approval off and just share the link in the Facebook Group [OBSERVED `desktop2-11` shows approval is optional/toggle].
- *Places:* Gear drop pin, parking structure pin, brunch pin, hotel basecamp. This alone replaces my parking-map screenshot.
- *Calendar/Itinerary:* The agenda with times and locations — "Wave 2, 7:10, SW corral" looks exactly like the schedule cards in the demo [OBSERVED `desktop-14`, `mobile-15`]. Add Event on the calendar with month grid covers the training-calendar use too [OBSERVED `desktop2-24`].
- *Polls/Decisions:* Brunch spot vote, carpool departure time. Useful, not essential.
- *Tasks:* "Pick up bibs," "bring the banner," "drive car 6" — assigned tasks with names is my captains system, formalized [OBSERVED `desktop2-22`].
- *Smart Import:* I'd paste the race's confirmation email and the hotel block confirmation. If the wave-time PDF becomes calendar entries, that's an hour of my life back.
- *AI Concierge ask:* "What time should Wave 3 leave the hotel to make a 7:25 corral with 15 minutes for gear drop?" — actually useful math.
- *AI trust breaker:* Wrong race-morning times. If it tells a runner the wrong corral close, that runner misses their race and I hear about it for a year.
- *Settings priorities:* Simple. Big text. Notifications that work on Android without me explaining how to install anything.

**Events branch.** *Professional-grade means:* for a volunteer like me it means "doesn't embarrass me" — links work on every phone, schedule is right, nobody needs help logging in. *Control vs. automation:* I'll take automation for reminders; I keep control of the schedule. *What creates trust:* the first race morning with zero "where do I go" texts. Also: it has to work on Android as well as it does on the organizer's iPhone — I noticed Chravel ships an iOS app but Android is web/PWA only [OBSERVED — ground truth §1: Capacitor iOS wrapper; no Android app listed]. Half my club is Android. If their experience is "open a browser tab," adoption halves.

**Money.** Club dues fund a small treasury; race costs are everyone-pays-their-own, with the club covering the banner and brunch deposit. I collect brunch money via Venmo and track it in the Sheet — so Chravel's log-and-Venmo-deeplink model fits how we already operate [OBSERVED — ground truth §6]. Reimbursement talk is friendly but slow. Plan changes: Facebook post + GroupMe + email, and still. One planner: me, with two captains. Restaurants: I pick two options, the group votes, loudest voice usually wins anyway. Conversations live in GroupMe (day-of) and Facebook (everything else).

**Willingness to pay.** *Bracket: $5-15.* Here's my honest problem: 3 lifetime free events covers about 18 months of club life, then I personally hit a $19.99/mo "Frequent Chraveler" wall for a volunteer job [OBSERVED — entitlements.ts:296-306, ground truth §7]. I will not personally pay $240/year to volunteer. The club COULD pay — the treasury absorbs $50–100/yr without a vote — but there's no "club" SKU: subscriptions are per-person, Pro Starter is $49/mo overkill, and the Trip Pass ($39.99/45d) is framed for one trip, not a club year. If there were a $5–10/mo club plan or a per-event pass the treasurer could approve, I'd have payment sorted in one meeting.

**Ratings (1–5).**
- Likelihood next trip: **4** — I'd genuinely run Eugene weekend on this.
- Clarity: **3** — clear for me; my least-techy members are the test.
- Time saved: **4** — broadcasts + pins + one schedule kill most of my 6am texts.
- AI trust: **3** — useful for logistics math, double-checked by me.
- Would invite: **4** — 40 runners, immediately, if the Android web join is smooth.
- Mobile usability: **3** — demo looks good, but it's a browser tab on Android and that's a harder sell than "download the app."
- Web usability: **4** — desktop is where I'd build everything; it's comfortable.
- Pricing fit: **2** — no SKU a club treasurer can say yes to.
- NPS sentiment: **3** (≈ +10) — wants to love it; pricing-shape and Android parity hold it back.

**Wrap-up.** Change one thing: a club/organization plan where one payer covers the group's events. Recommend when: race morning goes quiet. Anything else: print/PDF export of the schedule matters more than you think — half my club still wants the paper packet, and PDF export needs a paid tier [OBSERVED — ground truth §7: PDF export ✗ on Free]. Follow-up: **Yes** (evenings).

### E. Web Flow Walkthrough
- **Discovery/landing:** "Local Community Clubs" is literally named in the hero copy — that's me, first time an app has said so [OBSERVED — delta L1 hero text]. Pricing page's "Free works forever" reads honest [OBSERVED `desktop-22`].
- **Signup/onboarding:** Email + Google sign-in fine on desktop [OBSERVED L4]. Ten onboarding screens would lose some of my members; skippable helps (delta D13).
- **Event creation:** Desktop event console — Agenda, Calendar, Chat, Tasks, Polls, Media all one click apart; Event Team card with Invite [OBSERVED `desktop-13`]. I'd build the whole weekend here on a Sunday night.
- **Feature usage:** Calendar has Import/Export/Month Grid/Add Event [OBSERVED `desktop2-24`] — Export matters for my paper-packet people, though PDF export is paywalled off Free [OBSERVED — §7]. Tasks with assignments fit the captain system [OBSERVED `desktop2-22`].
- **Pricing reaction:** Free 3 lifetime events → fine for year one, then I'm staring at a personal $19.99/mo for a volunteer role; no club SKU [OBSERVED `desktop-22`, §7]. This is where I stall.
- **Web positives:** Everything in one place; calendar export; clean enough that I trust it with 40 adults.
- **Web pain points:** No price the treasury can approve; no printable one-pager on Free; "Frequent Chraveler" naming feels like it's for jet-setters, not run clubs.

### F. Mobile / PWA Flow Walkthrough
- **First impression:** Compact event header, clear agenda cards with times and venues — my runners could read this at 5:45am with sleep in their eyes [OBSERVED `mobile-14`, `mobile-15`].
- **Navigation:** Horizontal tab strip; Tasks/Polls hidden off-screen right [OBSERVED `mobile2-21`] — my less-techy members won't discover them without me saying "swipe the tabs."
- **Android/PWA reality:** No Android native app — members get mobile web or install-a-PWA, and "add to home screen" is a support burden with this crowd [OBSERVED — ground truth §1 (iOS Capacitor only) / SIMULATED RISK for adoption]. Push notifications on Android PWA require an opt-in flow my members will decline by reflex [SIMULATED RISK].
- **Chat/input:** Untestable live [SIMULATED RISK].
- **Forms/modals:** Task cards readable; text wrap on long titles is cramped but tolerable [OBSERVED `mobile2-21`].
- **Perceived speed:** Demo smooth, but the documented mobile duplicate-key render storm (`MobileGroupCalendar.tsx:525`, ~150 warnings/step on event surfaces too) worries me on members' older Androids [OBSERVED — delta R1].
- **Thumb reach/tap targets:** Fine for me; big-text accessibility unverified [HYPOTHESIS].
- **Mobile positives:** Agenda legibility; clean layout; everything one tap deep once you find the tab.
- **Mobile pain points:** PWA install friction on Android; tab-strip discovery; render-storm perf on old phones; no offline schedule for a start corral with no signal [HYPOTHESIS].

### H. Emotional Reaction
- **Impressed by:** Hero copy naming community clubs, and the calendar Export button — someone thought about people like her [OBSERVED L1, `desktop2-24`].
- **Confused by:** Whether her members on Android "have the app" or "have a website" — she can't explain the difference at packet pickup.
- **Annoyed by:** Being a volunteer staring at a $19.99/mo personal subscription named after frequent travel.
- **Would abandon when:** The third member texts "it won't let me in" on race morning, or event #4 demands her credit card.
- **Would invite others?** Yes — 40 at once; club adoption is all-or-nothing.
- **[SYNTHETIC QUOTE]:** "This could honestly give me my race mornings back — pins, one schedule, blasts that confirm delivery. But I'm a volunteer. Give the club a price the treasury can approve, and make it work on Karen's Android, and I'll move all 120 of us."

### I. Conversion Scores
- **Activation:** 6/10 — would build the event; the 40-member rollout is the gamble.
- **Invite likelihood:** 6/10 — high intent, gated on Android-web join smoothness.
- **Day-7 retention:** 6/10 — strong through race weekend; quiet between events.
- **Paid conversion:** 4/10 — money exists in the treasury; no SKU to spend it on.
- **NPS-style:** +10 — warm, blocked by packaging and platform parity.
- **Would they pay?** The club would; she won't personally.
- **What would they pay?** $50–100/yr club budget, or ~$15 per event pass.
- **Feature creating willingness to pay:** Reliable broadcasts + calendar export + event media pool.
- **Limit/CTA that triggers upgrade:** 4th lifetime event — IF the payer can be the club.
- **CTA that would annoy them:** Personal "Frequent Chraveler" upsell for a volunteer role; PDF export wall when making the paper packet.

### J. Top 5 Fixes for This Persona
1. Add a club/organization SKU (one payer, many members, N events/year), because Dana's treasury can pay but no current plan maps to "volunteer organizer + club funds," stalling conversion at the 4th-event wall (`src/billing/entitlements.ts:296-306`).
2. Build an Android PWA install + push onboarding flow (guided add-to-home-screen, permission explainer), because half her club is Android with no native app (ground truth §1), causing adoption to halve at rollout.
3. Add a basic print/PDF schedule view on Free, because her paper-packet members fail at "photograph the schedule" today and PDF export is paywalled (§7), pushing her back to Google Docs.
4. Fix the mobile duplicate-key render storm (`MobileGroupCalendar.tsx:525`, delta R1), because older Android phones in her club will feel the jank/battery cost, causing "this app is slow" rejection.
5. Add a co-organizer event role, because her two pace-group captains can't share admin under organizer/attendee-only roles (`permissionMatrix.generated.ts`), keeping the phone tree alive.

### K. Confidence
- **Level:** Medium.
- **Directly observed:** Event console, calendar Import/Export, agenda cards, tasks, invite modal toggles, entitlement code, hero club copy, mobile tab strip behavior.
- **Needs real-user validation:** Android PWA join/push completion rates for low-tech members; broadcast capabilities on the event tier; offline behavior at race venues.
- **Beta interview question:** "If the club paid $60 a year for this, what would you need to see at the FIRST race weekend to call it worth it — and what would make you cancel?"

## Persona 25: Hunter Davis — Events / Fraternity Rush Chair

### A. Profile
- **Name:** Hunter Davis
- **Age range:** 19–22
- **Location/timezone:** Tuscaloosa, AL / America/Chicago
- **Industry/role:** Junior, finance major; rush chair running 3 weeks of daily recruitment events
- **Tech comfort:** High — iPhone power user; GroupMe admin of six chats; makes the chapter's Instagram reels
- **Platform:** iPhone 15, exclusively; touches a laptop only for class
- **Group size:** 120 PNMs (potential new members) + 80 active brothers; events daily for ~3 weeks
- **Planning style:** Last-minute but loud — schedules change same-day, everything announced in ALL CAPS
- **Current tools:** GroupMe (three chats), Instagram DMs, Google Sheet (PNM tracker), iMessage, a whiteboard in the house
- **Main pain points:** Daily schedule changes that half the chapter misses; "what time is it at" ×50; knowing who actually saw the announcement; PNM attendance tracking on paper
- **Budget sensitivity:** Personally broke; chapter treasury routinely approves $100–300 for rush tools/supplies
- **Why adopt Chravel:** One event hub for 200 people with broadcasts, daily agenda, and attendance-ish visibility — replacing three GroupMes that brothers have muted into oblivion
- **Why reject Chravel:** If it pings 200 people for everything, everyone mutes it day two and he's back to zero; and a paywall mid-rush would be dead on arrival

### B. Jobs-to-Be-Done
1. When tonight's event moves from the house to the lake at 4pm, I want to blast the change to 200 people and SEE who got it, so I can chase only the ones who didn't.
2. When PNMs ask "what's tomorrow," I want a daily agenda they check themselves, so I can stop answering the same DM fifty times.
3. When brothers have muted three GroupMes, I want important stuff to land differently than memes, so I can keep signal alive during the most important three weeks of the year.
4. When the exec board asks who showed up, I want attendance per event without a paper sheet, so I can rank PNM engagement at vote night.
5. When rush ends, I want the photo pool for the recruitment video, so I can make the reel that wins next year's class.

| Question | Answer |
|---|---|
| Group trips/events last 12 months | 4+ (rush weeks, formal, spring break, game-day blocks) |
| Typical group size | 16+ (up to 200) |

### D. Full Survey Answers

**About you.** Rush chair. Three weeks, an event every single day — house tours, BBQs, lake day, brotherhood nights — 120 PNMs plus 80 brothers who all need to be at the right place at the right time, and the time changes constantly. My whole life is announcements right now.

**Most recent/next group trip.** Fall rush, three weeks out. Kicked off when nationals released the schedule window and I built the Sheet. Involved: me, the exec board, 80 brothers, 120 PNMs whose numbers I collected through a Google Form. Most frustrating: I changed Tuesday's cookout to 7pm and like 40 people showed at 6 because they only saw the FIRST announcement. Also the GroupMe situation — brothers' chat is muted by literally everyone, so "announcements" is me triple-texting and then DMing the group chads to spread the word. What went well: the daily IG story schedule actually got seen — PNMs check stories. Apps: GroupMe ×3, IG, Sheets, iMessage. Call it 4 platforms, 6 surfaces. After the first plan? The plan is a suggestion. It changes daily by 3pm.

**Planning workflow.** Idea→booked: exec sets the calendar in August, venues confirmed week-of. Booked→during: I announce the next day's event each night, re-announce at noon, re-announce the change at 4. During: door duty, name tags, headcount on a clipboard (genuinely a clipboard). Post: exec debrief, attendance into the Sheet, vote night uses my numbers. Where decisions stick: the whiteboard in the house, embarrassingly. Non-responders: I send the group chads after them — peer pressure is my notification system. Example thread: 200+ messages in PNM GroupMe the night the lake day moved. Total chaos, three people still went to the lake.

**Feature areas.**
- *Create/Invite:* One event per rush week, or one for all three weeks. Funny enough the demo's invite modal is LITERALLY a fraternity trip with "Require approval to join — Required" forced on [OBSERVED `desktop2-11`, "Spring Break Cancun 2026 – Fraternity Trip"]. Approval-required is right for PNMs (no randoms), but approving 120 join requests one by one on my phone? I need bulk-approve or I'll die [SIMULATED RISK].
- *Places:* House pin, lake pin, BBQ field pin. PNMs are freshmen — they don't know where anything is. Big.
- *Calendar/Itinerary:* Daily agenda cards with time + location is exactly my IG-story schedule but self-serve [OBSERVED `mobile-15`].
- *Polls:* Brothers voting on theme night, PNM superlatives. Fun, secondary.
- *Tasks:* "Setup crew 4pm," "ice run," "door duty" — assigned tasks replace me yelling in the house chat [OBSERVED `desktop2-22`, `mobile2-21`].
- *Smart Import:* I'd paste the nationals schedule PDF and my Sheet. If it builds three weeks of agenda from that, day one is done.
- *AI Concierge ask:* "Which PNMs haven't been to an event since Tuesday?" — that's vote-night gold if attendance data existed.
- *AI trust breaker:* Wrong event time, one time. My credibility with 200 people IS the product.
- *Settings priorities:* Notification control is everything. If every chat message pings 200 phones, the app is muted by Wednesday and dead by Friday.

**Events branch.** *Professional-grade means:* nothing corporate — it means RELIABLE. The blast goes out, I see who got it, the schedule is always current. *Control vs. automation:* automate reminders ("event in 1 hour" to RSVPs), I control announcements. *What creates trust:* the read counts. GroupMe shows me likes; I need "147 of 200 saw it" so I know who to chase. Here's my fear though, and your own docs back it up: notifications at my scale are the weak spot — the audit says a big event blocks the database writing thousands of notification rows synchronously, like 4,000 members → 12,000 rows, no batching [OBSERVED — ground truth §10.4, still open]. I'm 200 people × 3 announcements a day × 21 days. That's exactly the grind that either lags out or trains everyone to mute. And muting exists per-event now (delta D11 [OBSERVED — code: useTripNotificationMute.ts]) — good for brothers' sanity, but if half the chapter mutes the event, my 4pm venue change dies in the muted pile and there's no "critical" lane that punches through [SIMULATED RISK].

**Money.** Chapter treasury pays for rush — exec approves line items. PNMs pay nothing. Brothers Venmo the social chair for extras; the split-payments thing is more for our spring break trip than rush. Plan changes: announced everywhere, lands nowhere. One planner: me, but exec overrules. How we decide: exec votes, I execute. Conversations live in GroupMe and the house whiteboard.

**Willingness to pay.** *Bracket: per-trip* (chapter-paid). Me personally: $0, I'm a college student. The chapter: $50–100 for rush season is an easy exec vote — we spend more on name tags. The 3 free lifetime events probably covers fall rush, spring rush, and formal… and then I'm out junior year [OBSERVED — entitlements.ts:296-306]. A "rush season pass" the treasury buys once is the move. $19.99/mo "Frequent Chraveler" on MY card is never happening.

**Ratings (1–5).**
- Likelihood next event: **4** — I'd run rush on it tomorrow if joins are smooth.
- Clarity: **4** — took me 30 seconds to get the tabs.
- Time saved: **4** — self-serve agenda kills half my DMs.

- NPS sentiment: **3** (≈ 0) — would push it hard, terrified of the mute-spiral.

**Wrap-up.** Change one thing: bulk-approve joins + read counts on broadcasts. Recommend when: a venue change lands with zero stragglers. Anything else: attendance/check-in per event would make this THE rush app nationally — every chapter has my exact job. Follow-up: **Maybe** (text, never call).

### E. Web Flow Walkthrough

Sketchy either way.

- **Web pain points:** No chapter/org payment path; cap ambiguity; desktop-first flows I'll never touch — if event setup is better on desktop, that's friction for me personally.

### F. Mobile / PWA Flow Walkthrough
- **First impression:** Clean header, attendee count visible, agenda cards readable at a glance — PNM-proof [OBSERVED `mobile-14`, `mobile-15`].
- **Navigation:** Horizontal tab strip scrolls; Tasks/Polls/Media live off-screen [OBSERVED `mobile2-21` vs `mobile-14`]. Freshmen will never find tab #7. No bottom nav on mobile web (delta note).
- **Chat/input:** Couldn't live-test [SIMULATED RISK] — and chat for 200 college kids is a firehose; if it renders like the consumer demo it's fine, but at my volume the open hot-trip realtime issue (§10.5) is the thing that lags us out [SIMULATED RISK grounded in audit].
- **Forms/modals:** Task cards thumb-friendly with edit/delete [OBSERVED `mobile2-21`].
- **Invite link flow:** Link in PNM GroupMe + IG story → preview → account wall → join request → I approve ×120 [SIMULATED RISK per ground truth §5 + D15]. Every step sheds freshmen. The preview is good bait; the account+approval double-gate is the leak.
- **Perceived speed:** Demo is smooth, but the documented duplicate-key render storm on every mobile trip surface (`MobileGroupCalendar.tsx:525`, thousands of warnings per pass) reads like jank waiting for my 200 cheap-case iPhones [OBSERVED — delta R1].
- **Thumb reach/tap targets:** Solid.
- **Mobile positives:** Agenda glanceability; dark mode; everything I need within two taps once tabs are found.
- **Mobile pain points:** Tab discovery; join funnel length ×120; notification fanout/mute spiral risk; render-storm perf [labels as cited].

### G. Feature-by-Feature Findings
| Feature | Expected goal | Tried | What happened | Positive | Friction | Bug/UX issue | Evidence | Severity 1–5 | Revenue impact | Retention impact | Recommended fix |
|---|---|---|---|---|---|---|---|---|---|---|---|
| Marketing/positioning | "Is this for Greek life?" | Landing + demo | Demo invite is literally a fraternity trip | Segment is clearly on the roadmap | No Greek/campus page or campus pricing | — | [OBSERVED] `desktop2-11`, L1 | 2 | Medium | Low | Campus/Greek landing page |

| Settings/notifications | Signal vs meme separation | Mute code + audit | Per-trip mute shipped (D11) | Brothers keep sanity | Mute is binary — critical blasts die with the noise; no priority lane | Mute-spiral kills his core loop | [OBSERVED — code] useTripNotificationMute.ts / [SIMULATED RISK] | 4 | High | High | Priority broadcast class bypassing mute + digest mode |
| Permissions/roles | Exec vs brothers vs PNMs | Permission matrix | organizer/attendee only | Organizer control is real | Can't scope PNMs out of brothers' chat in one event | Forces two parallel events | [OBSERVED — code] permissionMatrix.generated.ts | 4 | Medium | High | Event sub-groups/roles |
| Pricing/upgrade | Chapter-payable, predictable | Pricing + code | 3 lifetime events then personal $19.99/mo; caps advertised not enforced | Free covers ~3 semesters | No org/chapter payment path; cap ambiguity at exactly 200 | Unenforced caps could activate mid-rush | [OBSERVED] §4, §7, entitlements.ts:296-306 | 4 | High | High | Season/event pass purchasable by org treasury |

### H. Emotional Reaction
- **Impressed by:** The agenda cards and the fact that the demo literally ships a fraternity trip with approval-required invites — someone gets my world [OBSERVED `desktop2-11`, `mobile-15`].
- **Confused by:** How 120 join approvals are supposed to work on a phone; whether the 200-attendee number is real or vibes [OBSERVED §4].
- **Annoyed by:** Tab-strip hide-and-seek; no read counts visible in the event demo; the idea of paying $19.99/mo personally.
- **Would abandon when:** The first venue-change blast visibly doesn't land — stragglers at the wrong place ends the experiment same-day; or the mute-spiral makes it GroupMe #4.
- **Would invite others?** 200 people in week one — highest invite velocity in this study — IF the join funnel survives freshmen.
- **[SYNTHETIC QUOTE]:** "I will move all of rush onto this tonight if the blast actually lands and I can see who read it. But if it pings everyone for every meme, the whole chapter mutes it by Wednesday and I'm back to triple-texting like an animal."

### I. Conversion Scores
- **Activation:** 7/10 — builds the event same night; setup tools support him.
- **Invite likelihood:** 8/10 — 200 invites by design; funnel friction is the cap.
- **Day-7 retention:** 5/10 — rush-intense, then cliff until formal; mute-spiral is the in-season risk.
- **Paid conversion:** 5/10 — chapter money is real and approvable; no SKU accepts it.
- **NPS-style:** 0 — maximal enthusiasm, maximal architecture doubt.
- **Would they pay?** Chapter yes; personally never.
- **What would they pay?** $50–100/season from treasury.
- **Feature creating willingness to pay:** Broadcast read counts + bulk approve + attendance check-in.
- **Limit/CTA that triggers upgrade:** 4th lifetime event (junior year) — if payable by the chapter.
- **CTA that would annoy them:** Personal subscription modal mid-rush; any upsell inside the event chat.

### J. Top 5 Fixes for This Persona
1. Ship async/batched notification fanout with a priority-broadcast class, because Hunter's 200-member × 3-announcements/day load hits the documented INSERT-blocking fanout (§10.4 open) and the D11 binary mute kills critical blasts — his trust-breaking moment.
2. Add bulk approve + role pre-assignment to the join-request queue, because approving 120 PNMs one-by-one on a phone fails his onboarding week, causing fallback to GroupMe (`desktop2-11` shows single-approval model).
3. Add broadcast read counts to the event surface ("147 of 200 seen"), because Hunter can't chase stragglers without delivery visibility — pro broadcasts have tracking (`desktop2-19`); events need it surfaced.
4. Add a chapter/org-payable season pass, because treasury money exists but only personal subscriptions are sold, losing a high-velocity 200-seat segment (`src/billing/entitlements.ts:296-306`).
5. Add event sub-groups (brothers vs PNMs) within one event, because organizer/attendee-only roles force him to run two parallel events or expose internal chat (`permissionMatrix.generated.ts`).

### K. Confidence
- **Level:** Medium-High — his core risk (fanout at scale) is audit-documented, and his surfaces were directly observed.
- **Directly observed:** Event agenda/tasks/polls at both viewports, fraternity-themed invite modal with forced approval, mute implementation, fanout audit, cap non-enforcement.
- **Needs real-user validation:** PNM join-funnel completion on iPhones; real broadcast latency/read behavior at 200 members; whether mute-spiral occurs in practice.
- **Beta interview question:** "Last time an event changed same-day, how many people ended up in the wrong place — and what would an app have to show you to trust it instead of triple-texting?"

# Batch 6 — Personas 26–30 (Events/Communities Segment) — 2026-06-11 Study

## Persona 26: Pastor Raymond Hill — Events/Communities / Church & Nonprofit Group Trip Organizer

### A. Profile
- **Name:** Pastor Raymond Hill
- **Age range:** 50–62
- **Location/timezone:** Birmingham, Alabama / America/Chicago (CT)
- **Industry/role:** Senior pastor; organizes an annual mission trip and a youth retreat for his congregation
- **Tech comfort:** LOW — uses email, Facebook, and a flip-through paper binder; texts on Android
- **Platform:** Android phone + church-office Windows desktop
- **Group size:** 45 participants (adults + minors with parental consent requirements)
- **Planning style:** Paper sign-up sheets in the fellowship hall, a church-secretary spreadsheet, Sunday-morning announcements, a group text that only half the group reads
- **Current tools:** Paper forms, Excel, group SMS, Facebook group, church bulletin
- **Main pain points:** Permission slips and medical forms for minors; tracking who has paid what when some families pay in installments and some are subsidized by the scholarship fund; reaching low-tech members
- **Budget sensitivity:** Extreme — the church pays by check or invoice, never a recurring personal credit card; every dollar is congregational money
- **Why adopt Chravel:** One place for the schedule, the announcements, and the photo sharing so the secretary stops fielding forty phone calls
- **Why reject Chravel:** No forms/waivers, payment tracking that can't model partial scholarships and payment plans, and members who can't or won't create an account get nothing

### B. Jobs-to-Be-Done
1. When I am six weeks out from the mission trip, I want every family to see the same schedule and packing list, so I can stop repeating myself from the pulpit and over the phone.
2. When I am collecting permission slips and medical forms for 17 minors, I want to see who has and hasn't turned them in, so I can chase the stragglers before the bus leaves.
3. When I am tracking trip payments, I want to record that the Johnson family paid $50 of $300 and the scholarship fund covered the rest, so the books reconcile for the deacon board.
4. When I am inviting 45 people of all ages and tech levels, I want them to join with one tap and no account hoops, so Sister Mabel (age 78) isn't left out.
5. When something changes mid-trip, I want one announcement that everyone actually sees, so nobody is left standing at the wrong church van.
6. When the trip is over, I want photos and a simple recap to share with the congregation, so the whole church feels part of the mission.

### C. Screener Answers
| Question | Answer |
|---|---|
| Trips last 12 months | 2-3 (mission trip, youth retreat, choir trip) |
| Typical group size | 16+ (45 this year) |
| Main tools | Paper forms, Excel, group SMS, Facebook group |
| Primary device | Android phone + desktop |
| 45-min call? | Yes — "happy to talk if it helps the ministry" |
| Role in group | Primary planner |
| Pro-ops responsibility | Yes, I own logistics (with the church secretary) |

### D. Full Survey Answers
**About you.** I've pastored the same congregation for 23 years. Every summer we take a mission trip — this year it's 45 of us to Guatemala, including 17 youth under 18 — and every fall a youth retreat to Lake Guntersville. I'm not a technology man, but I've learned what I had to learn.

**Most recent/next group trip.**
- *What kicked it off:* The missions committee voted in January. From there it's deposits, passports, forms, fundraisers.
- *Who's involved:* Me, the church secretary (she does the spreadsheet), the youth pastor, 6 chaperones, 45 travelers, and every parent of every minor.
- *Most frustrating:* The forms. Permission slips, medical releases, passport copies. I have a manila folder and a spreadsheet and I still found out at the airport one year that we were missing a notarized form.
- *What went well:* Our people show up. When the announcement is clear, the congregation moves like one body.
- *Apps used & why:* Group SMS (everyone has texting), Facebook group (the over-50s live there), email for documents, Excel for money. None of it talks to each other.
- *Total app count:* 5, counting the paper binder as an app, which it might as well be.
- *After the first plan:* The schedule changed three times and each change meant a Sunday announcement, a text blast, a Facebook post, and still ten phone calls.

**Planning workflow.** Idea comes from the committee → secretary builds the spreadsheet → sign-up sheet in the fellowship hall → deposits collected at the church office → forms chased for two months → final packet handed out the Sunday before. During the trip, I announce things on the bus. After, we do a slideshow on Sunday. Decisions stick in committee meetings; non-responders get a phone call from the secretary — that's our escalation system and it works better than any app.

**Feature areas.**
- *Create/Invite:* I'd need the secretary to set it up. A link people can tap from a text would be a blessing — IF they don't have to make a password. Half my congregation will stop at a password screen.
- *Places:* Less important — we go where the mission board sends us. Marking the hotel and the work site would help the chaperones.
- *Calendar/Itinerary:* This is the heart of it. Day-by-day schedule everyone can see, that updates when plans change.
- *Polls/Decisions:* Maybe for the youth retreat — let the kids vote on the Saturday activity.
- *Tasks:* Assigning chaperone duties, yes. "Brother James — bring the first-aid kit."
- *Smart Import:* I'd paste the flight confirmation email from the travel agency and the bus charter PDF.
- *AI Concierge:* I'd ask "what time do we leave Tuesday?" — honestly the same questions my members would ask me. If it answers them instead of me, that's worth something.
- *AI Trust:* If it ever made up a departure time, I'd never trust it again. Souls and schedules both need the truth.
- *Settings priorities:* Big text, simple screens, and control over who can post — I don't need a 45-person free-for-all chat.

**Money.** The church office collects checks and cash; some families pay $300 over three months; the scholarship fund quietly covers part or all for families that need it — and "quietly" is the important word, it must never show in a group app who got help. I looked at the payments feature: it splits a bill evenly or custom and tracks who owes whom [OBSERVED — mobile2-05 shows equal/custom splits and who-owes-whom]. That's built for ten friends at a restaurant, not for a treasurer tracking partial payments and confidential subsidies [SIMULATED RISK]. There is always one planner — me — but the money runs through the church office, and the church pays vendors by check or invoice. A subscription on my personal card would not pass the deacon board.

**Willingness to pay.** *Free only.* The church could in theory cut a check for a real tool, but there's no invoice option here and the free tier looks like it covers two trips a year. If it asked my card number, that's the end of it.

**Ratings (1–5).**
- Likelihood to use on next trip: **3** — I'd let the youth pastor pilot it on the retreat first.
- Clarity: **3** — the front page shows a busy dashboard before it explains itself; took me a minute to realize those weren't my trips [OBSERVED — desktop-01].
- Time saved: **4** — if my members actually joined, the announcement burden alone would justify it.
- AI trust: **2** — I haven't seen it be wrong, but I haven't seen it be right either.
- Would invite others: **3** — chaperones yes; whole congregation, doubtful.
- Mobile usability: **3** — readable, but small buttons for old thumbs in places.
- Web usability: **4** — the desktop is clearer; the secretary would manage from there.
- Pricing fit: **2** — free tier fits, but anything past it has no church-friendly way to pay.
- NPS-style sentiment: **3** — cautiously hopeful, not converted.

**Wrap-up.** Change one thing: let people join and see the schedule without creating an account. What makes me recommend it: if one trip goes by where nobody calls the church office asking what time the bus leaves. Anything else: a forms feature would make this the only tool a church needs. Follow-up: **Yes**.

### E. Web Flow Walkthrough
- **Discovery/landing:** "The Group Chat Travel App. For Friend & Family trips, Team Travel, Touring Crews, Local Community Clubs, & Anybody Organizing a Group" [OBSERVED — desktop-01]. "Local Community Clubs" is the closest thing to me — churches aren't named, but I can squint and see us in it. The hero is a live-looking dashboard of sample trips; at my tech level I genuinely wasn't sure if I was looking at the product or someone's account [SIMULATED RISK — low-tech users may not parse the interactive-demo hero, desktop-01].
- **Journeys section:** "Built for Every Journey" lists Family Hubs, Touring Artists, Bach Parties [OBSERVED — desktop-20]. No church, mission, or youth-group card — a missed signal for my segment [OBSERVED — desktop-20 shows no faith/nonprofit journey].
- **FAQ/pricing:** The FAQ is plain-spoken ("Why not just use the apps I already have?") which I appreciate [OBSERVED — desktop-23]. Free tier shows 3 active trips, 1 PDF export per trip, 3 events [OBSERVED — desktop-23 sidebar bullets]. Two church trips a year fits inside 3 active trips.
- **Signup/onboarding:** Email or Google sign-in renders fine [OBSERVED — desktop-04/05]; whether my 45 members complete it is the whole ballgame [HYPOTHESIS — needs real users].
- **Trip creation:** Consumer trip with title/dates/timezone [OBSERVED — src/components/CreateTripModal.tsx:55,613-615]. Straightforward enough for the secretary.
- **Feature usage:** Calendar with import/export, tasks with assignment, polls — all present in demo [OBSERVED — desktop2-02/07/08]. Broadcasts — the one-way announcement tool I most need — appear on Pro and Event trips, not consumer trips [OBSERVED — ground truth §6; desktop2-19 is a Pro surface]. A 45-person consumer chat will be noise.
- **Pricing reaction:** Free works. Beyond that, the upgrade is a credit-card subscription; no invoice/check path for organizations like ours [OBSERVED — consumer checkout is Stripe; Pro contact is mailto per ground truth §7 / D9].
- **Web positives:** Plain FAQ language; clear calendar; secretary-friendly desktop.
- **Web pain points:** Demo-as-hero confuses low-tech first-timers [SIMULATED RISK]; no faith/nonprofit positioning [OBSERVED — desktop-20]; no forms feature anywhere in the product [OBSERVED — absence from feature set, ground truth §6].

### F. Mobile / PWA Flow Walkthrough
- **First impression:** Mobile landing is clean and readable — big "Login or Signup" button, "Less Chaos, More Coordination" [OBSERVED — mobile-01]. I understood the mobile page faster than the desktop one.
- **Navigation:** The demo dashboard has a bottom bar (Trips, Search, New, Alerts, Profile) [OBSERVED — mobile-06]; inside a trip it switches to a horizontal strip of tabs you swipe (Calendar, Concierge, Media…) [OBSERVED — mobile2-02; evidence-delta non-defect note]. Two different navigation systems is one more than I'd like to teach my congregation.
- **Chat/input:** Didn't dwell — for my group, chat is the feature I'd restrict, not promote.
- **Forms/modals:** The invite modal is honest and well-labeled — "Require approval to join," expiry, limit uses [OBSERVED — mobile2-11]. Approval-to-join is exactly right for a church trip with minors.
- **Invite link flow:** The link is a tap away, but what happens after the tap requires account creation, and guests without membership have access to nothing [OBSERVED — D15, src/types/permissionMatrix.generated.ts:44-50]. For Sister Mabel, that's a closed door [SIMULATED RISK — account wall will exclude low-tech members].
- **Perceived speed:** Demo felt fine; I'm told the mobile calendar re-renders constantly behind the scenes [OBSERVED — R1, src/components/mobile/MobileGroupCalendar.tsx:525 duplicate-key warnings on every mobile trip surface]. On the cheap Android phones my members carry, that worries me [SIMULATED RISK].
- **Thumb reach/tap targets:** The big trip-card buttons (Recap, Invite, View, Share) are generous [OBSERVED — mobile-06]; the in-trip tab strip and small toggles are fiddlier for arthritic hands [SIMULATED RISK].
- **Mobile positives:** Readable dark theme, big primary buttons, honest demo labeling.
- **Mobile pain points:** Account wall after invite tap; two navigation paradigms; calendar perf smell on low-end Android.

### H. Emotional Reaction
- **Impressed by:** The calendar and the invite approval control — "someone in the trip must approve new members" is church-trip wisdom [OBSERVED — mobile2-11].
- **Confused by:** The landing page opening on a dashboard of strangers' trips before any explanation [OBSERVED — desktop-01].
- **Annoyed by:** Realizing forms — my single biggest burden — simply aren't in here.
- **Would abandon when:** The third elderly member calls saying the link "wants a password."
- **Would invite others?** Chaperones and the youth pastor, yes. The whole congregation, only after a successful retreat pilot.
- **[SYNTHETIC QUOTE]** "This would save my secretary forty phone calls — if my people can get in the door without a password, and if it ever learns what a permission slip is."

### I. Conversion Scores
- **Activation:** 5/10 — he'd set up the retreat, but the forms gap keeps the binder alive.
- **Invite likelihood:** 6/10 — invites are the whole point; sends to chaperones first.
- **Day-7 retention:** 5/10 — depends entirely on member join rate.
- **Paid conversion:** 2/10 — free-only; no church-friendly payment rail.
- **NPS-style:** +5 — warm but conditional.
- **Would they pay?** No (personally); the church might, by invoice only.
- **What would they pay?** $0 personal; church could approve ~$100/yr by check if forms existed.
- **Feature creating willingness to pay:** Forms/waiver tracking with signed-status.
- **Limit/CTA that triggers upgrade:** 500 MB media cap after the mission-trip photo flood.
- **CTA that would annoy them:** Any card-number prompt mid-planning — "we don't put the Lord's work on my Visa."

### J. Top 5 Fixes for This Persona
1. Add a guest/read-only join path (view calendar + announcements via link, no account) because Pastor Hill failed at getting low-tech members in, causing the group to stay on SMS — relax `consumer_guest` zero-access (`src/types/permissionMatrix.generated.ts:44-50`) into scoped read.
2. Add per-member forms/waivers with completion tracking because permission slips and medical releases stay on paper, keeping his most painful workflow outside the app entirely (new feature; nearest hooks: Tasks + Media attachments).
3. Add an organizer-only payment ledger with partial payments because scholarship subsidies must stay confidential and installments are the norm, and `src/components/payments/` splits expose amounts to the whole trip.
4. Add a broadcast/announcement mode to consumer trips because a 45-person chat buries the one message that matters — port the Pro broadcasts surface (`desktop2-19`) down-market with organizer-only posting.
5. Offer invoice/check billing for organizations because churches cannot put subscriptions on personal cards, blocking any paid conversion (billing config `src/billing/config.ts` is card/Stripe-only).

### K. Confidence
- **Level:** Medium.
- **Directly observed:** Landing/journeys/FAQ copy, invite modal controls, payments split model, calendar UI, guest-permission matrix, absence of forms feature, R1 mobile calendar defect.
- **Needs real-user validation:** Whether 45 mixed-age members complete signup from an SMS link; whether the secretary can administer trips solo; AI answer quality on trip-logistics questions.
- **Beta interview question:** "Walk me through exactly what happened the last time you tried to get your congregation to adopt a new app — where did people drop off?"
