## Persona 27: Mrs. Angela Torres — Events/Communities / School Field Trip Coordinator

### A. Profile
- **Name:** Mrs. Angela Torres
- **Age range:** 30–45
- **Location/timezone:** San Antonio, Texas / America/Chicago (CT)
- **Industry/role:** 7th-grade science teacher; coordinates the annual 3-day Austin/state-capitol field trip
- **Tech comfort:** Medium — fluent in Google Classroom, district SIS, Remind; cautious by policy, not by ability
- **Platform:** District-issued Chromebook (desktop-first, locked-down) + personal iPhone
- **Group size:** 60 students + 8 chaperones + ~120 parents in the communication loop
- **Planning style:** District-approved checklists, signed paper permission forms, Remind broadcasts, a chaperone binder
- **Current tools:** Remind, Google Sheets/Forms, district email, paper forms
- **Main pain points:** Reaching parents reliably, chaperone task coordination, schedule changes mid-trip, doing all of it without ever putting student data in an unapproved tool
- **Budget sensitivity:** Absolute — district procurement is a semester-long process; realistically free or nothing
- **Why adopt Chravel:** A single coordination space for the ADULTS — chaperones and parents — with calendar, tasks, and announcements
- **Why reject Chravel:** Anything that requires or even invites student accounts/PII; no education/COPPA-FERPA posture anywhere; no broadcast tool on the free consumer tier

### B. Jobs-to-Be-Done
1. When I am running a field trip with 60 minors, I want a coordination tool that only the adults touch, so I never create a student-data-privacy problem for my district.
2. When the bus is leaving 30 minutes late, I want one broadcast that reaches all 8 chaperones and 120 parents, so my personal phone doesn't become a hotline.
3. When I assign chaperone groups, I want each adult to see their kids' roster, their stops, and their tasks, so nothing depends on the paper binder surviving day two.
4. When parents ask "what time do they get back?", I want them looking at a shared itinerary, so I can teach instead of answering email.
5. When I propose a tool to my district, I want a clear privacy story I can forward to the compliance office, so approval doesn't die in committee.

### C. Screener Answers
| Question | Answer |
|---|---|
| Trips last 12 months | 1 (plus two campus events) |
| Typical group size | 16+ (68 adults+students; ~9 app-eligible adults) |
| Main tools | Remind, Google Forms/Sheets, district email |
| Primary device | Desktop-first (Chromebook) + iPhone |
| 45-min call? | Maybe — after 4pm only |
| Role in group | Primary planner |
| Pro-ops responsibility | Yes, I own logistics |

### D. Full Survey Answers
**About you.** Twelve years teaching, six running the spring field trip. I'm the unofficial logistics department: permission forms, bus contracts, chaperone wrangling, and 120 parents who each believe their question is the first time anyone's asked it.

**Most recent/next group trip.**
- *What kicked it off:* District calendar approval in October for an April trip. Everything downstream of that is me.
- *Who's involved:* Me, my co-teacher, 8 parent chaperones, 60 students, the front office, and every parent.
- *Most frustrating:* Communication fan-out. A schedule change means Remind, email, AND a flyer, because no single channel reaches everyone. Also: chaperones who lose the binder page with their group roster.
- *What went well:* Google Forms for chaperone signup; the kids themselves, honestly.
- *Apps used & why:* Remind (parent broadcast, district-approved), Google Sheets (rosters), Google Forms (signups), district email (official record). Each approved tool does one thing.
- *Total app count:* 4-5, plus paper, which is still the legal system of record for permission slips.
- *After the first plan:* The Alamo slot moved twice and I re-broadcast everything twice. Version control is me, at 9pm.

**Planning workflow.** District approval → vendor quotes → permission forms go home on paper (signatures required) → chaperone recruitment → groups assigned → itinerary finalized → trip → incident-free return is the KPI. Decisions stick in email with the front office CC'd. Non-responders: I call. An example doc: a 7-tab Google Sheet named FIELD_TRIP_MASTER_v4_FINAL_real.

**Feature areas — with my one big caveat up front.** Students will never have accounts. District policy and good sense both say so. So I evaluated this as a tool for adults: me, my co-teacher, 8 chaperones, and ideally parents in a read-only way. That's actually a clean fit — and interestingly, nothing in your marketing says "this is for the adults coordinating," which is exactly how a school would need to hear it.
- *Create/Invite:* I'd create the trip and invite 10 adults. The "require approval to join" toggle is mandatory for me — I must control exactly who's in [OBSERVED — mobile2-11 shows the approval toggle].
- *Places:* Pinning the Capitol, the hotel, the rest stop — useful for chaperones who've never driven it.
- *Calendar/Itinerary:* The core. Day-by-day with times; chaperones check their phones instead of the binder.
- *Polls/Decisions:* Chaperone availability votes, maybe. Low need.
- *Tasks:* Big. "Mrs. Patel — collect EpiPens from nurse Friday." Assignment + due dates is exactly my checklist [OBSERVED — desktop2-08 shows assignment and filters].
- *Smart Import:* I'd paste the charter bus confirmation and the museum group-booking email.
- *AI Concierge:* "Lunch options near the Capitol for 68 people with a nut-allergy kid" — if it answered that well, I'd be impressed. I'd verify everything anyway.
- *AI Trust:* The first hallucinated detail about anything safety-adjacent ends it. I'm accountable to parents; "the AI said so" is not a sentence I can say.
- *Settings priorities:* Privacy controls, who-can-see-what, data deletion. I need to forward a privacy policy to my compliance office and have it survive reading.

**Money.** There's no expense-splitting on a school trip — families pay the school through the district's payment portal; the district pays vendors on POs. I'd use exactly zero payment features, and that's fine; I just need them to stay out of the way. Plan-change communication is THE feature: today it's Remind. Is there always one planner? In schools, painfully yes. Where do conversations live? Remind + email, never group texts with parents — boundaries.

**Willingness to pay.** *Free only.* Not stinginess — structure. A teacher cannot expense a subscription; district procurement takes a semester and requires a data-privacy agreement. If the free tier covers one trip with 10 adults, that's my realistic ceiling. (If you ever built a district SKU with a signed DPA, that's a different conversation — with my principal, not me.)

**Ratings (1–5).**
- Likelihood next trip: **3** — pilot with chaperones only, parents stay on Remind for now.
- Clarity: **4** — the product explains itself well once you're in the demo.
- Time saved: **3** — saves chaperone coordination; the parent fan-out (my biggest cost) needs broadcast, which consumer trips don't have.
- AI trust: **2** — useful for ideas, unusable for anything I'm liable for.
- Would invite: **4** — 8 chaperones, easily.
- Mobile usability: **4** — clean on my iPhone; the tab strip is fine.
- Web usability: **4** — works on the Chromebook, which is non-negotiable.
- Pricing fit: **3** — free tier genuinely covers my use; anything paid is procedurally impossible.
- NPS-style: **3** — would recommend to other teachers with the privacy caveat in bold.

**Wrap-up.** Change one thing: a parent read-only broadcast view with no account required. Recommend when: a chaperone says "I didn't need the binder." Anything else: say the words "for the adults" somewhere — schools will self-select in. Follow-up: **Maybe** — after 4pm.

### E. Web Flow Walkthrough
- **Discovery/landing:** "The Group Chat Travel App" for "Friend & Family trips, Team Travel, Touring Crews, Local Community Clubs" [OBSERVED — desktop-01]. Nothing says school; nothing forbids it either. The "Built for Every Journey" cards cover families, touring artists, and bachelor parties — a field-trip card would have stopped my scroll [OBSERVED — desktop-20].
- **Privacy posture:** Nowhere on the landing or FAQ do I see anything about minors, COPPA, FERPA, or education use [OBSERVED — desktop-23 FAQ topics are trips/limits/AI]. For me that's not a defect of the product so much as a missing market: the product works for adults-only coordination today, and saying so explicitly is free positioning [SIMULATED RISK — schools will bounce without a privacy statement to forward].
- **Signup/onboarding:** Google sign-in matters — my district account is Google [OBSERVED — desktop-04/05 show Google OAuth].
- **Trip creation:** Consumer trip, title/dates — fine for a field trip [OBSERVED — CreateTripModal.tsx]. I'd never touch Pro.
- **Feature usage:** Calendar, tasks with multi-assign, places — all demoed convincingly [OBSERVED — desktop2-02/06/08]. The gap: broadcasts live on Pro/Event trips only [OBSERVED — ground truth §6]; my consumer trip gets a group chat, and a 10-adult chat is survivable but parents can never be in a two-way chat with me.
- **Pricing reaction:** Free = 3 active trips, fine. The FAQ's "What happens when I hit my 3-trip limit?" reads honest [OBSERVED — desktop-23]. Paid tiers are irrelevant to my procurement reality.
- **Web positives:** Chromebook-friendly web app; approval-gated invites; honest free tier.
- **Web pain points:** No education positioning or privacy one-pager [OBSERVED — absence]; no consumer broadcast; demo dashboard hero briefly reads as someone's real data [SIMULATED RISK].

### F. Mobile / PWA Flow Walkthrough
- **First impression:** Mobile landing is tidy; the value line "Plans, photos, places, and payments — one private place for every trip" is clear — "private" is a word I noticed and liked [OBSERVED — mobile-01].
- **Navigation:** Dashboard bottom nav (Trips/Search/New/Alerts/Profile) is conventional [OBSERVED — mobile-06]; in-trip horizontal tab strip means features hide off-screen right — my chaperones will find Calendar but maybe not Tasks without a nudge [OBSERVED — mobile2-02; SIMULATED RISK on discoverability].

- **Perceived speed:** Demo felt responsive; noted the documented mobile calendar render storm [OBSERVED — R1, MobileGroupCalendar.tsx:525] — on chaperones' older phones during the trip, battery drain matters [SIMULATED RISK].
- **Thumb reach/tap targets:** Calendar month-grid dates are small for on-the-bus use [OBSERVED — mobile2-02]; primary buttons are generous.
- **Mobile positives:** Clean hierarchy; approval-gated invites; payments summary I'll never use is at least ignorable.
- **Mobile pain points:** Off-screen tabs; small calendar targets; no broadcast for the consumer tier.

### H. Emotional Reaction
- **Impressed by:** Tasks + calendar matching her checklist mentality almost one-to-one; the approval-gated invite [OBSERVED — mobile2-11, desktop2-08].
- **Confused by:** Whether she's even the intended customer — the marketing never says.
- **Annoyed by:** Realizing the broadcast tool she needs most is on a tier she can never buy.
- **Would abandon when:** The compliance office asks for a student-data answer and there's nothing to forward.
- **Would invite others?** Chaperones yes; parents no (account wall); other teachers yes, with caveats.
- **[SYNTHETIC QUOTE]** "This is genuinely the chaperone binder in app form — but until there's a way for 120 parents to *see* without *joining*, Remind keeps its job."

### I. Conversion Scores
- **Activation:** 6/10 — chaperone pilot is low-risk and high-value.
- **Invite likelihood:** 7/10 — 8 chaperones immediately; that's the whole inner circle.
- **Day-7 retention:** 6/10 — trip-cycle usage; strong during April, dormant otherwise.
- **Paid conversion:** 1/10 — structurally impossible at the individual level.
- **NPS-style:** +10 — recommends to teachers, with the privacy asterisk.
- **Would they pay?** No (personally); district SKU is a multi-year maybe.
- **What would they pay?** $0 personal; district could fund $200-500/yr per school with a DPA.
- **Feature creating willingness to pay:** Parent read-only broadcast portal + signed DPA.
- **Limit/CTA that triggers upgrade:** None — she'd architect around every limit before paying.
- **CTA that would annoy them:** Upsell modals during trip week — "I'm managing 60 children, do not sell to me right now."

### J. Top 5 Fixes for This Persona
1. Add a no-account read-only share view (calendar + announcements) because Angela failed at including 120 parents, causing the highest-value broadcast use case to stay on Remind — relax `consumer_guest` (`src/types/permissionMatrix.generated.ts:44-50`) or add a public itinerary share token.
2. Add an organizer-only announcement channel to consumer trips because two-way chat with parents violates teacher boundaries, capping the tool at chaperone-only scope (port Pro broadcasts, `src/features/chat/`).
3. Publish an education/minors privacy statement ("for the adults coordinating") because the district compliance office has nothing to approve, blocking institutional adoption — landing + FAQ content (`src/components/landing/FullPageLanding.tsx`).
4. Add a read-only consumer member role because all consumer members can edit calendar/tasks, and a chaperone fat-finger during the trip corrupts the schedule of record (`src/types/permissionMatrix.generated.ts`).
5. Fix the mobile calendar duplicate-key render storm because chaperones on older phones will feel the battery/perf cost during the one week it matters (`src/components/mobile/MobileGroupCalendar.tsx:525`, R1).

### K. Confidence
- **Level:** Medium-High for the adults-coordination fit; the persona's constraints are policy facts, not preferences.
- **Directly observed:** Invite approval controls, tasks/calendar surfaces, absence of education positioning, guest permission matrix, R1 defect, free-tier scope.
- **Needs real-user validation:** Whether districts accept "students never touch it" as sufficient; chaperone adoption rates mid-trip; whether parents would use a read-only link.
- **Beta interview question:** "If your compliance office asked one question before approving this app for chaperone use, what would it be?"

## Persona 28: Jake Morrison — Events/Communities / Bachelor Party Planner

### A. Profile
- **Name:** Jake Morrison
- **Age range:** 26–33
- **Location/timezone:** Boston, MA / America/New_York (ET); trip to Montreal

- **Group size:** 11 guys
- **Planning style:** Chaotic-decisive — one giant iMessage thread, a Splitwise board, and Jake fronting deposits then hunting people for months
- **Current tools:** iMessage, Splitwise, Venmo, Google Sheets (abandoned by day 2), Airbnb/OpenTable
- **Main pain points:** Collecting deposits, splitting wildly uneven bills (the steakhouse, the bottle service), and That One Guy who never pays
- **Budget sensitivity:** Price-sensitive personally, but spends freely on the trip itself — software subscriptions are where he gets cheap
- **Why adopt Chravel:** One place where the itinerary, the votes, and the money ledger live, with Venmo a tap away
- **Why reject Chravel:** Hitting a paywall mid-planning for a one-weekend use case priced like a quarterly commitment

### B. Jobs-to-Be-Done
1. When I front $2,200 for the Airbnb deposit, I want every guy's share tracked and nudgeable, so I'm not eating $200 because Derek "forgot."
2. When the steakhouse bill lands at $1,340 with two guys who only had salads, I want uneven splits in 30 seconds, so the math argument doesn't outlive dessert.
3. When 11 guys can't pick a Saturday activity, I want a poll with a deadline, so we book the paintball before it sells out.
4. When the itinerary changes at 1am, I want one source of truth, so nobody shows up at the wrong club.
5. When the trip ends, I want a final who-owes-whom and Venmo links, so settlement takes a day, not a quarter.

### D. Full Survey Answers
**About you.** I'm the guy who gets made best man and discovers the job is actually accounts receivable. I plan two or three group trips a year because apparently competence is a punishment.

**Most recent/next group trip.**
- *What kicked it off:* Matt got engaged in March; I had a Montreal long-weekend skeleton in Notes within 48 hours.
- *Who's involved:* 11 guys, 4 cities, one groom who must know nothing, one guy (Derek) who replies "I'm easy" to every question and disputes every charge.
- *Most frustrating:* Money, full stop. I fronted the Airbnb and the Saturday dinner deposit. Collecting 10 shares took 11 weeks. I have a spreadsheet tab literally named "Derek."
- *What went well:* The poll I ran in iMessage with emoji reactions actually settled the strip-steakhouse-vs-Portuguese-chicken debate. Democracy works when there's a deadline.
- *Apps used & why:* iMessage (the thread IS the trip), Splitwise (money), Venmo (settlement), Google Sheet (died of neglect), Airbnb, OpenTable, a shared Apple Note.
- *Total app count:* 7-ish.
- *After the first plan:* Three guys booked different flight times, one dropped out, his replacement joined, and every plan got re-litigated once. Standard.

Decisions stick when I say "booking at 5pm unless someone objects." Non-responders get the public @-mention. Example thread: 400 messages, of which 9 mattered.

**Willingness to pay.** *Per-trip.* I'd pay **$10–15 per trip** without blinking — call it the "weekend pass." $39.99 is priced for a 45-day European send, not a 3-day Montreal rip. I will never hold a $9.99/mo subscription for something I use 4 weekends a year — that's $120/yr for $50 of value.

- **Invite link flow:** Link → preview → account → join. For 10 guys in their late 20s, fine. Derek will take 6 days [SIMULATED RISK — but that's Derek, not the app].
- **Perceived speed:** Demo felt snappy; the documented mobile duplicate-key render storm (150+/step) is invisible to the eye but smells like battery drain over a weekend of heavy use [OBSERVED — R1, MobileGroupCalendar.tsx:525; SIMULATED RISK on battery].
- **Thumb reach/tap targets:** Payments rows, summary cards, bottom CTA — all thumb-friendly [OBSERVED — mobile2-05]. Calendar month grid dates are small [OBSERVED — mobile2-02].
- **Mobile positives:** Payments tab is best-in-class layout; bottom CTAs; fast demo.
- **Mobile pain points:** Off-screen tabs in the strip; calendar perf smell; PWA-not-native means no share-sheet magic on iPhone for my group.

### G. Feature-by-Feature Findings

### H. Emotional Reaction
- **Impressed by:** The payments tab — summary, pending/settled, per-head splits, Venmo deeplink. "Someone here has personally chased a Derek" [OBSERVED — mobile2-05].
- **Confused by:** Nothing — the demo is self-explanatory to a high-tech user.
- **Annoyed by:** Doing the math on the 3-split cap and realizing it dies Friday night of MY trip, and the fix costs $39.99.
- **Would abandon when:** The split-limit modal appears at the steakhouse and the group reverts to Splitwise in 90 seconds.
- **Would invite others?** Instantly — 10 invites is step one of usage.
- **[SYNTHETIC QUOTE]** "This app understands my job better than my groomsmen do — then it charges forty bucks at the exact moment I'm holding a $1,340 steakhouse bill. Give me a twelve-dollar weekend pass and I'm yours."

### I. Conversion Scores
- **Activation:** 9/10 — creates the trip the night he sees the demo.
- **Invite likelihood:** 9/10 — 10 invites are intrinsic to the workflow.
- **Day-7 retention:** 7/10 — intense around trips, dormant between; that's the category.
- **Paid conversion:** 5/10 — would pay per-trip; bounces off $39.99 for 72 hours of use.
- **NPS-style:** +30 — vocal advocate with a pricing footnote.
- **Would they pay?** Yes — per-trip only.
- **What would they pay?** $10–15/trip; $39.99 only for a 1-2 week trip.
- **Feature creating willingness to pay:** Unlimited splits + AI query top-up bundled in a pass.
- **Limit/CTA that triggers upgrade:** The 3-split wall, currently mistimed to fire mid-trip.
- **CTA that would annoy them:** A monthly-subscription pitch at the split wall — "I am not marrying your app, I'm renting it for a weekend."

### J. Top 5 Fixes for This Persona
1. Add a short-duration trip pass (~$10-15, 7-10 days) because Jake fails at the 3-split cap on expense #4 of an 8-expense weekend, and the only escape is a $39.99/45-day SKU sized for a different trip (pricing in `src/billing/config.ts`; wall copy in `src/billing/entitlements.ts:272-279`).
2. Fire the split-limit warning at split 2 of 3 during pre-trip planning because the wall currently lands mid-trip at peak stress, converting to churn instead of revenue (`src/services/paymentService.ts` + `TripPassModal.tsx`).
3. Diagnose and fix the desktop consumer-trip setState loop because tab interaction throws "maximum update depth exceeded" up to 34×, a freeze risk on the surfaces his group lives in [R2 — desktop-harvest2-log.json steps 3-13].
4. Fix the mobile calendar duplicate-key churn because continuous re-render of a mounted calendar drains battery across a 72-hour heavy-use weekend (`src/components/mobile/MobileGroupCalendar.tsx:525`, R1).
5. Make in-trip tab overflow visible (peek/badge on off-screen tabs) because low-effort members never discover Payments/Polls beyond the fold of the horizontal strip, undermining the group ledger's completeness (mobile trip tab strip, `src/pages/MobileTripDetail.tsx`; mobile2-02).

### K. Confidence
- **Level:** High — this persona's core loop (splits, polls, invites) maps directly onto observed surfaces and verified billing code.
- **Directly observed:** Payments UI and summary math, Venmo deeplink code, enforced split cap + tests, Trip Pass pricing, bach-party landing card, R1/R2 defects.
- **Needs real-user validation:** Actual conversion behavior at the split wall; whether groups dual-wield iMessage + Chravel or abandon one; pass price elasticity.
- **Beta interview question:** "You're at dinner, the app says you've used 3 of 3 free splits — what do you actually do in the next two minutes?"

## Persona 29: Eleanor Vance — Pro / Luxury Travel Advisor

### A. Profile
- **Name:** Eleanor Vance
- **Age range:** 45–60
- **Location/timezone:** Palm Beach, Florida / America/New_York (ET)
- **Industry/role:** Independent luxury travel advisor (Virtuoso-affiliated), ~30 client trips/year, parties of 2–12
- **Tech comfort:** Medium — expert in her tools (AXUS, Travefy, Sabre via host agency), conservative about new ones
- **Platform:** Desktop-first (iMac) + iPhone
- **Group size:** Parties of 2–12; she is the invisible 13th member
- **Planning style:** White-glove — she does everything; clients receive polished deliverables and feel zero machinery
- **Current tools:** AXUS Travel App, Travefy, email, WhatsApp with clients, host-agency booking systems
- **Main pain points:** Multi-generational family trips where 12 people need different views of one itinerary; clients texting questions answered on page 2 of the PDF
- **Budget sensitivity:** Low for tools that touch the client experience; she bills $150k+ in commissions — but the tool must *elevate* the brand, never dilute it
- **Why adopt Chravel:** A live, interactive itinerary clients actually open, replacing static PDFs — with payments-visibility and group chat for family trips
- **Why reject Chravel:** Her clients seeing "The Group Chat Travel App" branding; no white-label; any surface that looks like a fraternity spring break shared a hallway with her Amalfi clients

### B. Jobs-to-Be-Done
1. When I deliver a $90,000 family itinerary, I want it presented under MY brand at the polish level of the trip itself, so the deliverable reinforces why they pay my fee.
2. When a 12-person multi-gen family travels, I want each branch to see the master schedule plus their own activities, so the WhatsApp question volume drops.
3. When plans change mid-trip (they always do), I want to push an update every traveler sees instantly, so I'm not triple-texting three households across time zones.
4. When a client opens anything I send, I want zero consumer-app advertising in their face, so the experience stays mine.
5. When I evaluate AI tools, I want them to draft and summarize under my supervision, so I capture the speed without surrendering the judgment that justifies my existence.

### C. Screener Answers
| Question | Answer |
|---|---|
| Trips last 12 months | 4+ (30 client trips) |
| Typical group size | 2-4 typical; 9-15 for multi-gen |
| Main tools | AXUS, Travefy, email, WhatsApp |
| Primary device | Desktop-first |
| 45-min call? | Yes — she takes meetings professionally |
| Role in group | Primary planner (professional) |
| Pro-ops responsibility | Yes, I own logistics |

### D. Full Survey Answers
**About you.** Twenty-two years in luxury travel, independent for eleven. My clients don't book trips; they commission experiences. My job is judgment, access, and making complexity invisible.

**Most recent/next group trip.**
- *What kicked it off:* A patriarch's 75th — twelve family members, Lake Como, ten days, four villas' worth of opinions.
- *Who's involved:* Me, the family matriarch (decision-maker), three adult children (opinions), a villa broker, two DMCs, and a private chef's agent.
- *Most frustrating:* Distribution. I produce an immaculate itinerary; it dies in four WhatsApp threads. Each household asks me questions the document answers.
- *What went well:* The trip. The trips always go well — that's the product.
- *Apps used & why:* AXUS for client-facing itineraries (mobile app, decent polish), Travefy for proposals, email for record, WhatsApp because clients insist.
- *Total app count:* 6-7 professionally.
- *After the first plan:* Fourteen revisions. Revision distribution is my real workflow.

**Planning workflow.** Discovery call → proposal (Travefy) → booking through host agency → confirmations into AXUS itinerary → pre-trip briefing → live trip support (me, on WhatsApp, at odd hours) → welcome-home gift and debrief. Decisions stick on calls with the matriarch; the family "discusses" in channels I never see, mercifully. Non-responders don't exist — my clients respond to me; I don't respond slowly to them.

**Feature areas.**
- *Create/Invite:* I would create the trip and invite clients with approval ON, always [OBSERVED — invite approval toggle, desktop2-11]. Roles matter enormously: clients must be read-mostly; pro_viewer read-only with partial poll access actually fits "family votes on the Thursday excursion" [OBSERVED — ground truth §8 permission model].
- *Places:* Pinning villas, restaurants, the dock for the Bellagio transfer — with distances from basecamp. Useful, and frankly elegant.
- *Calendar/Itinerary:* The day-sheet equivalent. The demo's Pro calendar is credible [OBSERVED — desktop-10].
- *Polls/Decisions:* Family votes, controlled by me. Anonymous off.
- *Tasks:* Internal — mine and my assistant's. Clients never see tasks; sausage-making is private.
- *Smart Import:* I'd paste DMC confirmations, villa contracts (PDF), and flight records. If extraction is accurate, that's hours saved per trip.
- *AI Concierge:* Here's my honest ambivalence. I'd use it to draft ("summarize the dining reservations for the matriarch"). But the same engine answering my clients' questions directly is a rehearsal for replacing me. I'd want to configure what it can answer — and it cannot be allowed to recommend restaurants to MY clients; that's my cellar, not its [HYPOTHESIS — threat-and-tool dynamic needs real advisor trials].
- *AI Trust:* One wrong dinner recommendation to a client under my brand and the damage is mine, not the model's.
- *Settings priorities:* Branding, client-visible surface control, and what the AI may say to whom.

**Pro/Events branch.** What "professional-grade" means: the client never sees machinery, the advisor controls every surface, and the export looks like it cost money. Control vs automation: automation for assembly, human control over everything client-facing. Trust comes from: my branding on the deliverable, granular roles, and a vendor who answers the phone. On that note — the PDF Recap modal is genuinely impressive in structure: section selection, "Emails and phone numbers hidden. Chat and AI history never included." — that privacy line is exactly the kind of detail my industry notices [OBSERVED — desktop2-21]. But it will export under Chravel's brand, and there is no white-label option at any tier [OBSERVED — ground truth §7 tier table has no white-label row; billing config]. That is THE gap. AXUS exists because advisors need their name on the experience.

**Money.** I don't split bills — the concept is almost vulgar in my segment; the family office wires funds. Payments features would be hidden from my trips entirely if I could. For multi-gen trips where adult children split a villa, the tracking could quietly serve — but client-visible "You Owe $58.20" framing [OBSERVED — mobile2-05] is wrong for people who don't discuss money at dinner. Plan-change communication: broadcasts with delivery tracking [OBSERVED — ground truth §6 Pro broadcasts] is genuinely the right primitive — I'd use it daily mid-trip. One planner? Yes — me, professionally. Where conversations live: WhatsApp, regrettably and permanently.

**Willingness to pay.** *Client-billable / team plan.* I'd pay **$99+/month without negotiation** for a white-labeled client experience — it's a cost of goods, billed into trip fees. Without white-label, I'm at $0, not because of price but because the product as-branded cannot touch my clients. Pro Starter at $49 is cheap *and irrelevant* until the brand problem is solved. Also: there's no self-serve Pro checkout — I'd have to email billing@ to give you money [OBSERVED — D9, Pro checkout still mailto/pending]. In my industry that reads as "not ready."

**Ratings (1–5).**
- Likelihood next trip: **2** — a quiet pilot on a friends-and-family trip, never a client trip yet.
- Clarity: **4** — the product is well-organized; the Pro demo is persuasive.
- Time saved: **3** — import + broadcasts could save real hours; revision distribution remains.
- AI trust: **2** — capable, but ungoverned toward clients.
- Would invite: **2** — inviting clients is the product, and the brand isn't ready for my clients.
- Mobile usability: **3** — fine; my clients are iPhone-native and would find it acceptable.
- Web usability: **4** — the desktop Pro surfaces are strong [OBSERVED — desktop-08..11].
- Pricing fit: **2** — wrong axis; I need a white-label SKU, not a cheaper one.
- NPS-style: **2** — watching with interest, recommending to no one yet.

**Wrap-up.** Change one thing: white-label — my logo, my colors, my domain on the client surface. Recommend when: a client compliments "my" app. Anything else: the dark-gold aesthetic is genuinely close to luxury-appropriate; you're one branding layer away from a segment that expenses software without blinking. Follow-up: **Yes**.

### E. Web Flow Walkthrough
- **Discovery/landing:** "ChravelApp — The Group Chat Travel App. For Friend & Family trips, Team Travel, Touring Crews, Local Community Clubs…" [OBSERVED — desktop-01]. Every word of that is poison for my use case — not because it's bad copy, but because my clients must never see it. "Group Chat" positions downmarket of a $90,000 commission.
- **Journeys:** Touring Artists & Crews, Bach Parties [OBSERVED — desktop-20]. My Amalfi family is not on this page. Travel advisors aren't either — notable, since the Pro tier is presumably for professionals.
- **Pro demo:** The Beyoncé tour trip is operationally impressive — 57-member roster with role chips, channels, broadcasts, PDF Recap in the header [OBSERVED — desktop-08, L2/L3 harvest notes]. A tour manager's tool can be an advisor's tool; the bones are here.
- **PDF Recap:** Section-selectable export with the privacy line and "1 Free Export per trip" with a "Sample it" affordance [OBSERVED — desktop2-21]. Real pipeline now, entitlement-gated [OBSERVED — D1 FIXED, ItineraryView.tsx:78-135]. Chravel-branded output is the dealbreaker [OBSERVED — no white-label tier exists].
- **Pro ops reality check:** Real Pro trips have no structured ops data — the rich roster/schedule surfaces are demo-only; "honest surfaces" now hide the placeholders on real trips [OBSERVED — D7, tripConverter.ts:118-130]. So the Pro demo oversells what my first real trip would look like [SIMULATED RISK — expectation gap at first real use].
- **Pricing reaction:** Pro Starter $49/Growth $99 are trivial sums; the absence of self-serve Pro checkout and of any white-label tier are the actual blockers [OBSERVED — D9; ground truth §7].
- **Web positives:** Premium dark/gold aesthetic; credible Pro information architecture; the recap privacy line.
- **Web pain points:** Consumer-forward branding on every shared surface; demo-vs-real Pro gap (D7); mailto-to-purchase [OBSERVED].

### F. Mobile / PWA Flow Walkthrough
- **First impression:** The mobile landing is handsome — but again leads "The Group Chat Travel App" [OBSERVED — mobile-01]. My evaluation lens is "what does the *client* see on their iPhone," and the answer today is Chravel's brand, everywhere.
- **Navigation:** Dashboard bottom nav is conventional [OBSERVED — mobile-06]; in-trip horizontal tab strip works but eight visible tabs (Chat, Calendar, Media, Payments, Polls, Tasks…) is seven more than a luxury client should face [OBSERVED — mobile2-02; SIMULATED RISK — surface overload for read-mostly clients]. I need to hide tabs per role.
- **Chat/input:** Adequate. My clients would use it if I told them to; they'd prefer WhatsApp.
- **Forms/modals:** Invite modal is clean and the approval requirement is correct [OBSERVED — mobile2-11].
- **Invite link flow:** A `chravel.app/j/…` link [OBSERVED — mobile2-11]. My clients clicking a *chravel.app* URL instead of *vancetravel.com* is the white-label problem in miniature — the brand leak starts at the invitation.
- **Perceived speed:** Demo was smooth; the mobile render-storm defect [OBSERVED — R1] is invisible but the kind of thing that surfaces as warm phones on a yacht with weak signal [SIMULATED RISK].
- **Thumb reach/tap targets:** Fine for my demographic's clients; text sizes are acceptable.
- **Mobile positives:** Aesthetic restraint; the trip cards photograph well — clients would not be embarrassed by the *visual* layer.
- **Mobile pain points:** Payments tab ("You Owe $58.20") visible to clients who do not discuss money [OBSERVED — mobile2-05; SIMULATED RISK]; no per-role tab hiding; brand omnipresence.

### H. Emotional Reaction
- **Impressed by:** The PDF Recap's privacy engineering and the Pro roster/broadcast architecture — "someone built this for real operators" [OBSERVED — desktop2-21, desktop-08].

- **Would invite others?** Not clients, not yet. Possibly two advisor colleagues, framed as "watch this space."

### I. Conversion Scores

- **Invite likelihood:** 4/10 — colleagues maybe; clients are gated on branding.
- **Day-7 retention:** 5/10 — professional evaluation discipline, but no client deployment.
- **Paid conversion:** 7/10 — high WTP parked behind one missing feature.
- **NPS-style:** −10 — professionally respectful, commercially unconverted.
- **Would they pay?** Yes, eagerly — for white-label.
- **What would they pay?** $99–149/mo, client-billable.
- **Feature creating willingness to pay:** White-label client surface + branded PDF export.
- **Limit/CTA that triggers upgrade:** None of the current ones; her trigger is a capability, not a cap.
- **CTA that would annoy them:** Consumer upsell modals ("Start Free Trial") inside a professional workflow [OBSERVED — PlusUpsellModal per ground truth §7].

### J. Top 5 Fixes for This Persona
1. Add white-label branding (logo, accent color, custom invite domain, branded PDF Recap) because Eleanor cannot expose clients to "The Group Chat Travel App," causing a $99+/mo high-WTP segment to stay on AXUS/Travefy (export: `src/components/ItineraryView.tsx:78-135`; invite links: `src/pages/JoinTrip.tsx`).
2. Ship self-serve Pro checkout because a buyer with budget literally cannot purchase without emailing billing@, which signals immaturity to professional buyers (D9; `src/billing/`, mailto CTAs per ground truth §7).
3. Add per-role tab visibility (hide Payments/Tasks from client roles) because read-mostly clients see operational machinery and money framing, breaking the white-glove illusion (`src/types/permissionMatrix.generated.ts`; trip tab config).
4. Add per-role AI governance (what the concierge may answer, to whom) because an ungoverned AI recommending restaurants to her clients under her brand is a trust breach she can't risk (`src/features/concierge/`, toolRegistry).
5. Close the demo-vs-real Pro gap with real data-entry paths for roster/schedule because her first real Pro trip renders far emptier than the Beyoncé demo, an expectation cliff at the exact moment of evaluation (D7; `src/utils/tripConverter.ts:118-130`).

### K. Confidence
- **Level:** Medium — the branding objection is firmly grounded in observed copy and tier structure; the AI threat/tool dynamic and client behavior are hypotheses.
- **Directly observed:** Landing positioning, PDF Recap modal and pipeline, Pro demo surfaces, permission model, absence of white-label SKU, mailto Pro checkout.
- **Needs real-user validation:** Whether affluent clients adopt any third-party app; advisor tolerance for non-custom domains; real Smart Import accuracy on DMC documents.
- **Beta interview question:** "What's the minimum branding control that would let you put a client of yours inside a third-party trip app — and what tool came closest before?"

## Persona 30: Yuki Tanaka-Osei — Events/Communities / International Multi-Country Group Organizer

### A. Profile
- **Name:** Yuki Tanaka-Osei
- **Age range:** 33–45
- **Location/timezone:** Toronto, Canada / America/Toronto (ET)
- **Industry/role:** UX researcher; organizes a triennial family-and-friends reunion trip — 18 people across 5 countries (Canada, Japan, Ghana, UK, Germany), 3 languages (English, Japanese, Twi)
- **Tech comfort:** High — evaluates software professionally
- **Platform:** Android (Pixel) + desktop
- **Group size:** 18 people, ages 9–71
- **Planning style:** Methodical, async-first by necessity — no meeting time works for Tokyo, Accra, and Toronto simultaneously
- **Current tools:** WhatsApp (the incumbent, non-negotiable for elders), Google Sheets, Splitwise, Wise (currency), shared Google Calendar that half the family misreads across timezones
- **Main pain points:** Timezone ambiguity ("7pm WHERE?"), three languages, multi-currency expense chaos, and one app per problem
- **Budget sensitivity:** Medium — happily pays per-trip for something that works; allergic to subscriptions for triennial events
- **Why adopt Chravel:** One coordination home replacing the Sheets+Calendar+Splitwise stack, if it handles timezones and currencies honestly
- **Why reject Chravel:** English-only UI excludes a third of her family; ambiguous event times across 5 timezones is worse than no calendar at all

### B. Jobs-to-Be-Done
1. When I schedule a video call or publish an itinerary across 5 timezones, I want every time shown in each viewer's local time with the zone labeled, so "19:00" stops generating six clarifying messages.
2. When my aunt in Kyoto opens the app, I want her to navigate in Japanese, so participation doesn't depend on her grandson translating.
3. When expenses land in CAD, JPY, GHS, GBP, and EUR, I want them logged in original currency with a sane consolidated view, so settlement isn't a spreadsheet of exchange rates.
4. When my family refuses to leave WhatsApp (they will), I want Chravel to be the plan-of-record layer alongside it, so I'm not fighting a chat-migration war I'll lose.
5. When relatives book flights from 5 countries, I want all arrivals visible on one timeline, so airport pickups in Lisbon don't require a 40-message thread.

### D. Full Survey Answers
**About you.** I'm a UX researcher in Toronto; my family spans Japan, Ghana, the UK, and Germany. Every three years I organize the reunion — Lisbon next summer, 18 people, ages 9 to 71. I am simultaneously the most and least qualified person to evaluate your app.

**Most recent/next group trip.**
- *What kicked it off:* My grandmother turning 90. Within a week: a WhatsApp group, a Sheet, and a Doodle poll that aged me.
- *Who's involved:* 18 family members; effectively me plus a cousin in London as co-planner; the elders as approval layer; teenagers as a chaos layer.
- *Most frustrating:* Time. Not the amount — the *representation* of it. I wrote "call Sunday 19:00 Lisbon time" and got "so 3am for us?" from Japan (correct), "1pm our time?" from Toronto (wrong, it's 2pm), and silence from Accra. Every timestamp needs a footnote.
- *What went well:* WhatsApp's reach — 100% of my family, ages 9 to 71, every country. That's why it can't be replaced, only supplemented.
- *Apps used & why:* WhatsApp (everyone), Sheets (itinerary), Splitwise (money, grudgingly — currency handling is weak), Wise (actual transfers), Google Calendar (timezone disasters), Doodle (scheduling).
- *Total app count:* 6-7.
- *After the first plan:* Flight prices moved, two households changed weeks, and the Sheet forked into "FINAL" and "FINAL(1)". Versioning across languages is its own circle of hell.

**Planning workflow.** Idea → family WhatsApp poll → I build options in Sheets → async voting over two weeks (timezone-fair) → book in waves as each household commits → live coordination during → a shared album after. Decisions stick in a pinned WhatsApp message translated twice. Non-responders: a household-level nudge — culture matters; I message my uncle, not my aunt, and the Ghana side responds to voice notes, never text walls.

**Feature areas.**
- *Create/Invite:* Trip creation has a timezone field, which is more than most apps think to ask [OBSERVED — src/components/CreateTripModal.tsx:55,613-615; though it's collected at creation, the code passes it only for Event-type trips at line 210-211, which makes me wonder where consumer trip timezone goes]. Invite links work for my group IF the join flow is light.
- *Places:* Basecamp + distances is genuinely useful for a villa-centered reunion.
- *Calendar/Itinerary:* The make-or-break feature. The event modal has a timezone picker [OBSERVED — src/features/calendar/components/CalendarEventModal.tsx:26,403-407], which is the right input. The rendering question is what I can't verify from outside: the codebase contains a user-timezone RPC (`get_events_in_user_tz`) that the client deliberately bypasses with a direct query because the RPC "can hang" [OBSERVED — src/services/calendarService.ts:351-358]. All-day dates are handled timezone-invariantly via UTC-midnight, which is correct engineering [OBSERVED — src/utils/dateHelpers.ts:993-1047]. But whether a 19:00 Lisbon dinner renders as 19:00 for everyone or as 14:00 for Toronto viewers — with or without a zone label — I could not confirm, and that ambiguity is precisely my #1 pain [HYPOTHESIS — cross-timezone timed-event rendering needs a live multi-account test].
- *Polls/Decisions:* Async voting with auto-close over a 48h window is timezone-fair by design. Good.
- *Tasks:* Household-level assignment ("Osei household: book Accra–Lisbon legs").
- *Smart Import:* I'd paste flight confirmations in three languages — a JAL email in Japanese, a Lufthansa one in German. If extraction only works on English emails, that's most of my family excluded [HYPOTHESIS — non-English parse quality untested].
- *AI Concierge:* "All 18 arrival times in Lisbon local time, grouped by day" — if it answers that correctly, it has paid for itself. Also "halal and vegetarian group-dinner options near basecamp."
- *AI Trust:* A wrong timezone conversion from the AI would be worse than no answer — confidently wrong times miss flights.
- *Settings priorities:* Language, timezone display rules, date format. On that: I found **no i18n framework at all** — no i18next, react-intl, or any locale library in the dependencies, and no locale modules in src [OBSERVED — package.json has no i18n deps; src grep returns none]. The app is English-only, hardcoded. My Kyoto aunt and my Twi-first uncle are out, full stop. Date formats are US-style ("Mar 15 - Mar 22, 2026") with no locale adaptation [OBSERVED — mobile-06 trip cards].

**Money.** Multi-currency is half-solved, and I want to be fair: there IS a currency model — 10 fiat currencies plus Bitcoin, with per-currency decimal handling (JPY correctly gets 0 decimals) and a CurrencySelector in payment input [OBSERVED — src/constants/currencies.ts:16-28; src/components/payments/CurrencySelector.tsx]. JPY, EUR, GBP, CAD: covered. **GHS (Ghanaian cedi) is absent** — my Accra family logs in… Bitcoin? [OBSERVED — currencies.ts list; the irony of BTC-before-GHS is noted]. And I see no cross-currency consolidation — who-owes-whom across mixed currencies needs an exchange-rate strategy, or the "Net" number is fiction [SIMULATED RISK — mixed-currency settlement math unverified; mobile2-05 shows single-currency USD summaries]. Reimbursement: we settle via Wise transfers between households; Venmo deeplinks are useless internationally — Venmo doesn't exist in Japan, Ghana, the UK, or Germany [OBSERVED — paymentDeeplinks.ts:14 is Venmo-only; SIMULATED RISK for non-US groups]. One planner? Me, with a London deputy. Decisions: household-weighted polls. Conversations: WhatsApp, permanently — Chravel must coexist, not conquer.

**Willingness to pay.** *Per-trip.* The reunion is triennial — a subscription is irrational. I'd pay **$20–40 per trip** for a coordination layer that nails timezones and currencies; the $39.99/45-day Trip Pass is actually shaped right for a reunion (planning crescendo + trip), though I'd want ~90 days of planning runway, which pushes me to the $74.99/90d pass — steep but arguable for 18 people if I split it.

**Ratings (1–5).**
- Likelihood next trip: **3** — pilot with the English-speaking half; that asterisk is the whole story.
- Clarity: **4** — information architecture is professional; I evaluate UIs for a living and this one is competently built.
- Time saved: **3** — calendar+places+polls consolidates three tools; language gap claws half of it back.
- AI trust: **3** — confirm-before-write cards are the right pattern [OBSERVED — ground truth §6 pending-action confirm]; timezone math trust is unearned until demonstrated.
- Would invite: **3** — the anglophone 60%; inviting my aunt into an English-only app is unkind.
- Mobile usability: **4** — solid on the Pixel; tab strip is manageable.
- Web usability: **4** — desktop is where I'd plan.
- Pricing fit: **3** — per-trip passes exist (correct model for me); sized a bit long/expensive for my cadence.
- NPS-style: **3** — impressed professionally, blocked practically.

**Wrap-up.** Change one thing: i18n — even just UI-string localization for 5 languages changes my answer from "pilot" to "adopt." Recommend when: a JST-timezone relative sees an event time and doesn't ask "whose 7pm?" Anything else: your currency file's comment says "can expand based on usage" — usage will never come from countries whose currencies aren't listed; chicken, meet egg. Follow-up: **Yes** — and I'll bring annotated screenshots, it's my job.

### E. Web Flow Walkthrough
- **Discovery/landing:** Demo-dashboard hero is effective for a high-tech evaluator — I immediately understood the product [OBSERVED — desktop-01]. Copy is US-centric: journeys are bach parties and touring crews; international/diaspora reunions are absent, though "Friend & Family trips" technically includes us [OBSERVED — desktop-20].
- **FAQ/pricing:** Honest free-tier framing; "What happens when I hit my 3-trip limit?" answered up-front builds trust [OBSERVED — desktop-23].
- **Signup/onboarding:** Standard OAuth/email [OBSERVED — desktop-04/05]. English-only onboarding carousel (10 screens, skippable) [OBSERVED — D13; OnboardingCarousel.tsx] — fine for me, a wall for a third of my invitees.
- **Trip creation:** Timezone field present at creation [OBSERVED — CreateTripModal.tsx:613-615]; defaults to creator's zone via `Intl.DateTimeFormat().resolvedOptions().timeZone` [OBSERVED — :55]. Good default; the question is whether viewers in other zones get conversion or just my zone's wall-clock [HYPOTHESIS].
- **Feature usage:** Calendar import/export visible [OBSERVED — mobile2-02 buttons]; ICS export across timezones is exactly the kind of thing that silently shifts events by 5 hours if done naively — the codebase shows real care in dateHelpers (UTC-midnight invariance, explicit timezone-bug comments) [OBSERVED — dateHelpers.ts:4-18,993-1047], which raises my confidence without settling the timed-event question.
- **Pricing reaction:** Per-trip passes are the right shape for triennial organizers; 45/90-day windows map to reunion planning arcs [OBSERVED — ground truth §7].
- **Web positives:** Professional IA; timezone-aware inputs; honest pricing copy; visible engineering care in date handling.
- **Web pain points:** English-only everything [OBSERVED — no i18n framework]; US date formats unlocalized [OBSERVED — mobile-06]; no international positioning [OBSERVED — desktop-20].

### F. Mobile / PWA Flow Walkthrough
- **First impression:** Clean, fast on the Pixel; dark theme reads well [OBSERVED — mobile-01].
- **Navigation:** Bottom nav on dashboard, horizontal tab strip in-trip — a hybrid my 71-year-old mother would find inconsistent; she learns ONE navigation scheme per app, maximum [OBSERVED — mobile-06 vs mobile2-02; SIMULATED RISK for elder users].
- **Chat/input:** Competent, but it's competing with WhatsApp's 100% family penetration; it will lose that fight and should be positioned as the plans layer [SIMULATED RISK — chat-migration resistance].
- **Forms/modals:** Calendar's Import/Export/Add row is well-placed [OBSERVED — mobile2-02]; "No events for this day" empty state is clear.
- **Invite link flow:** Link + preview + approval toggle is solid [OBSERVED — mobile2-11]; the join wall (account required, guests get nothing) multiplied by a language barrier is a steep entry ramp for elders [OBSERVED — D15; SIMULATED RISK compounded].
- **Perceived speed:** Good — but the duplicate-key render storm fires on every mobile trip surface, ~150 warnings/step, and the calendar re-renders even while on other tabs [OBSERVED — R1, MobileGroupCalendar.tsx:525]. On the mid-range Androids common in my Accra family, that's real jank and battery cost [SIMULATED RISK].
- **Thumb reach/tap targets:** Month-grid dates are small for older thumbs [OBSERVED — mobile2-02]; primary buttons are fine.
- **Mobile positives:** Performance-conscious feel, good empty states, payments layout is excellent in single-currency contexts [OBSERVED — mobile2-05].
- **Mobile pain points:** R1 perf on budget Androids; small calendar targets; navigation paradigm split; everything in English.

### H. Emotional Reaction
- **Impressed by:** The visible engineering care in date handling — the UTC-midnight invariance comments read like someone got burned and learned [OBSERVED — dateHelpers.ts:4-18]; the currency model handling JPY decimals correctly.
- **Confused by:** A currency list that includes Bitcoin but not the cedi; a timezone RPC that exists but is deliberately routed around.
- **Annoyed by:** Realizing there is no i18n layer at all — not incomplete, absent. As a UX researcher I know exactly how expensive that is to retrofit.
- **Would abandon when:** The first cross-timezone event renders ambiguously and her family's trust in the calendar dies in one WhatsApp message.
- **Would invite others?** The anglophone 60% for a pilot; the full family only after localization.
- **[SYNTHETIC QUOTE]** "This app asks for my timezone and my currency — genuinely rare — and then speaks to my family in one language and settles up in an app that doesn't exist in four of our five countries. It's eighty percent of the way to being the only tool I need, and the missing twenty percent is exactly my family."

### I. Conversion Scores
- **Activation:** 7/10 — she'll build the Lisbon trip this month as a pilot.
- **Invite likelihood:** 6/10 — 10-11 anglophone members now; rest blocked on i18n.
- **Day-7 retention:** 6/10 — planning-arc usage is sustained for a reunion organizer.
- **Paid conversion:** 5/10 — would buy a 90-day pass if the timezone test passes.
- **NPS-style:** +15 — professionally generous, practically conditional.
- **Would they pay?** Yes — per-trip.
- **What would they pay?** $20–40/trip comfortably; $74.99 split across households at a stretch.
- **Feature creating willingness to pay:** Verified viewer-local time rendering + multi-currency consolidation.
- **Limit/CTA that triggers upgrade:** 3-split cap (18 people generate splits fast) and the 90-day planning window.
- **CTA that would annoy them:** An English-only upsell modal interrupting her aunt's first session — compounding exclusion with a sales pitch.

### J. Top 5 Fixes for This Persona
1. Add UI-string internationalization because Yuki failed at inviting a third of her family, capping group adoption at 60% — no i18n framework exists anywhere in the dependency tree (package.json; retrofit cost grows with every new component).
2. Render calendar event times in the viewer's timezone with an explicit zone chip (and verify, since `get_events_in_user_tz` was bypassed) because ambiguous times are her #1 pain and a single wrong rendering destroys calendar trust (`src/services/calendarService.ts:351-358`, `src/features/calendar/components/CalendarEventModal.tsx:403`).
3. Expand the currency list beyond top-10+BTC and define mixed-currency consolidation because her Accra household literally cannot log expenses in their currency and the cross-currency "Net" is undefined (`src/constants/currencies.ts:16-28`, `src/components/payments/`).
4. Add international settle-up deeplinks (Wise, PayPal, Revolut) because the Venmo-only deeplink serves exactly one of her five countries (`src/utils/paymentDeeplinks.ts:14`).
5. Fix the mobile calendar duplicate-key render storm and unmount inactive tab content because budget Android devices in her family will pay the jank/battery tax continuously (`src/components/mobile/MobileGroupCalendar.tsx:525`, R1).

### K. Confidence
- **Level:** High on the i18n/currency/deeplink gaps (directly code-verified); Medium overall because the central timezone-rendering question could not be live-tested.
- **Directly observed:** Absence of i18n framework, currency model contents and GHS gap, Venmo-only deeplink, timezone fields at trip/event creation, bypassed user-TZ RPC, TZ-invariant date helpers, R1 defect, US date formats in UI.
- **Needs real-user validation:** Cross-timezone timed-event rendering with two real accounts in different zones; non-English Smart Import extraction; elder onboarding completion rates.
- **Beta interview question:** "Open the trip calendar with me — your cousin in Kyoto added 'Dinner 19:00' — tell me what time you believe that dinner is, and how confident you are."
